I kissed her again and again, assured her that we should meet hereafter, and that in the meanwhile I should be ever mindful of her kindness. I gave her two of the buttons off my coat and a lock of my hair as a keepsake, taking a goodly curl from her own beautiful head in return: and so, having said good-bye a hundred times, till I was fairly overcome with her great sweetness and her sorrow, I tore myself away from her and got down-stairs to the caleche which was in waiting. How thankful I was when it was all over, and I was driven away and out of sight. Would that I could have felt that it was out of mind also! Pray heaven that it is so now, and that she is married happily among her own people, and has forgotten me!
第二天早上醒来时，我好多了。我决定乘坐一辆交通工具出发，该交通工具将于十一点左右等待我。对变化的期待让我心情很好，即使是伊拉姆泪流满面的脸也无法完全扰乱我的心情。我一次又一次地吻她，向她保证我们以后一定会见面，同时我应该永远铭记她的善意。我把我外套上的两颗扣子和一绺头发送给她作为纪念品，并从她美丽的头上剪下一缕漂亮的卷发作为回报：就这样，说了一百次再见，直到我完全被面对她的甜蜜和悲伤，我挣脱了她的束缚，下了楼，走向等候着的马车。当一切都结束时，我是多么庆幸，我被赶走了，消失在人们的视线中。要是我也能感觉到它是心不在焉就好了！祈求上天保佑她现在能和自己的人民幸福地结婚，并把我忘记了！

And now began a long and tedious journey with which I should hardly trouble the reader if I could. He is safe, however, for the simple reason that I was blindfolded during the greater part of the time. A bandage was put upon my eyes every morning, and was only removed at night when I reached the inn at which we were to pass the night. We travelled slowly, although the roads were good. We drove but one horse, which took us our day’s journey from morning till evening, about six hours, exclusive of two hours’ rest in the middle of the day. I do not suppose we made above thirty or thirty-five miles on an average. Each day we had a fresh horse. As I have said already, I could see nothing of the country. I only know that it was level, and that several times we had to cross large rivers in ferry-boats. The inns were clean and comfortable. In one or two of the larger towns they were quite sumptuous, and the food was good and well cooked. The same wonderful health and grace and beauty prevailed everywhere.
现在开始了漫长而乏味的旅程，如果可以的话，我不会打扰读者。然而，他很安全，原因很简单，因为我大部分时间都被蒙住眼睛。每天早上，我的眼睛上都会缠上绷带，直到晚上，当我到达我们过夜的旅馆时，才将绷带取下。尽管路况很好，但我们还是走得很慢。我们只骑了一匹马，一天的行程从早到晚，大约需要六个小时，还不包括中午的两个小时休息时间。我认为我们的平均行驶里程不会超过三十或三十五英里。每天我们都有一匹新鲜的马。正如我已经说过的，我看不到这个国家的任何东西。我只知道那里是水平的，有几次我们不得不乘渡船渡过大河。旅馆干净舒适。在一两个较大的城镇里，食物相当丰盛，食物很好，煮得很好。同样美妙的健康、优雅和美丽到处都盛行。

I found myself an object of great interest; so much so, that the driver told me he had to keep our route secret, and at times to go to places that were not directly on our road, in order to avoid the press that would otherwise have awaited us. Every evening I had a reception, and grew heartily tired of having to say the same things over and over again in answer to the same questions, but it was impossible to be angry with people whose manners were so delightful. They never once asked after my health, or even whether I was fatigued with my journey; but their first question was almost invariably an inquiry after my temper, the naivete of which astonished me till I became used to it. One day, being tired and cold, and weary of saying the same thing over and over again, I turned a little brusquely on my questioner and said that I was exceedingly cross, and that I could hardly feel in a worse humour with myself and every one else than at that moment. To my surprise, I was met with the kindest expressions of condolence, and heard it buzzed about the room that I was in an ill temper; whereon people began to give me nice things to smell and to eat, which really did seem to have some temper-mending quality about them, for I soon felt pleased and was at once congratulated upon being better. The next morning two or three people sent their servants to the hotel with sweetmeats, and inquiries whether I had quite recovered from my ill humour. On receiving the good things I felt in half a mind to be ill-tempered every evening; but I disliked the condolences and the inquiries, and found it most comfortable to keep my natural temper, which is smooth enough generally.
我发现自己是一个非常有趣的对象；以至于司机告诉我，他必须对我们的路线保密，有时还要去一些不直接在我们路上的地方，以避免等待我们的媒体。每天晚上我都要参加招待会，不得不一遍又一遍地说同样的话来回答同样的问题，我对此感到非常厌倦，但我不可能对那些举止如此令人愉快的人生气。他们从来没有问过我的健康状况，甚至没有问过我旅途是否疲劳；但他们的第一个问题几乎总是询问我的脾气，这种天真让我感到惊讶，直到我习惯了。有一天，我又累又冷，又厌倦了一遍又一遍地说同样的话，我有点粗鲁地转向提问者，说我非常生气，而且我对自己和每个人都没有比这更糟糕的幽默感了。除了那一刻之外还有另外一个。令我惊讶的是，我得到了最善意的哀悼，并听到房间里嗡嗡作响，说我脾气不好；于是人们开始给我一些好闻的东西和好吃的东西，这似乎确实具有某种治愈脾气的品质，因为我很快就感到高兴，并立即祝贺我变得更好了。第二天一早，有两三个人派仆人带着甜食来到旅馆，询问我的坏心情是否已经好转了。收到好东西后，我每天晚上都觉得心情不好；但我不喜欢哀悼和询问，我觉得保持我的自然脾气最舒服，一般来说，我的脾气很平稳。

Among those who came to visit me were some who had received a liberal education at the Colleges of Unreason, and taken the highest degrees in hypothetics, which are their principal study. These gentlemen had now settled down to various employments in the country, as straighteners, managers and cashiers of the Musical Banks, priests of religion, or what not, and carrying their education with them they diffused a leaven of culture throughout the country. I naturally questioned them about many of the things which had puzzled me since my arrival. I inquired what was the object and meaning of the statues which I had seen upon the plateau of the pass. I was told that they dated from a very remote period, and that there were several other such groups in the country, but none so remarkable as the one which I had seen. They had a religious origin, having been designed to propitiate the gods of deformity and disease. In former times it had been the custom to make expeditions over the ranges, and capture the ugliest of Chowbok’s ancestors whom they could find, in order to sacrifice them in the presence of these deities, and thus avert ugliness and disease from the Erewhonians themselves. It had been whispered (but my informant assured me untruly) that centuries ago they had even offered up some of their own people who were ugly or out of health, in order to make examples of them; these detestable customs, however, had been long discontinued; neither was there any present observance of the statues.
在那些来拜访我的人中，有些人在非理性学院接受过文科教育，并获得了假设学的最高学位，这是他们的主要研究领域。这些先生们现在已经在这个国家定居下来，从事各种工作，比如音乐银行的矫直师、经理和出纳员、宗教牧师等等，他们带着他们所受的教育，在全国各地传播了文化的酵母。我很自然地向他们询问了许多自从我到达以来一直困扰我的事情。我询问我在山口高原上看到的雕像的目的和意义是什么。有人告诉我，他们的历史可以追溯到非常遥远的时期，国内还有其他几个这样的团体，但没有一个比我所见过的那个团体更引人注目。它们具有宗教起源，旨在安抚畸形和疾病之神。从前，人们有一种习俗，就是对山脉进行探险，捕获他们能找到的最丑陋的乔博克祖先，以便在这些神灵面前将他们献祭，从而避免埃雷洪人本身的丑陋和疾病。有人私下传言（但我的线人向我保证不真实），几个世纪前，他们甚至牺牲了一些丑陋或不健康的自己的人民，以便为他们树立榜样。然而，这些令人憎恶的习俗早已停止。目前也没有对这些雕像进行任何纪念活动。

I had the curiosity to inquire what would be done to any of Chowbok’s tribe if they crossed over into Erewhon. I was told that nobody knew, inasmuch as such a thing had not happened for ages. They would be too ugly to be allowed to go at large, but not so much so as to be criminally liable. Their offence in having come would be a moral one; but they would be beyond the straightener’s art. Possibly they would be consigned to the Hospital for Incurable Bores, and made to work at being bored for so many hours a day by the Erewhonian inhabitants of the hospital, who are extremely impatient of one another’s boredom, but would soon die if they had no one whom they might bore—in fact, that they would be kept as professional borees. When I heard this, it occurred to me that some rumours of its substance might perhaps have become current among Chowbok’s people; for the agony of his fear had been too great to have been inspired by the mere dread of being burnt alive before the statues.
我很好奇，想知道如果乔博克的部落的任何一个人越过埃里翁，他们会怎么做。有人告诉我，没有人知道，因为这样的事情已经很久没有发生了。他们长得太丑，不能逍遥法外，但也不会严重到要承担刑事责任。他们的到来是一种道德上的冒犯。但它们超出了矫直器的技术范围。他们可能会被送往无法治愈的无聊医院，并被医院里的埃雷洪尼亚居民每天强迫工作好几个小时，他们对彼此的无聊极其不耐烦，但如果他们没有无聊，他们很快就会死去他们可能会讨厌的人——事实上，他们会被当作职业的讨厌者。当我听到这个消息时，我突然想到，关于其实质内容的一些谣言可能已经在乔博克的人民中流传开来。因为他的恐惧带来的痛苦太大了，不可能仅仅因为害怕在雕像前被活活烧死而受到启发。

I also questioned them about the museum of old machines, and the cause of the apparent retrogression in all arts, sciences, and inventions. I learnt that about four hundred years previously, the state of mechanical knowledge was far beyond our own, and was advancing with prodigious rapidity, until one of the most learned professors of hypothetics wrote an extraordinary book (from which I propose to give extracts later on), proving that the machines were ultimately destined to supplant the race of man, and to become instinct with a vitality as different from, and superior to, that of animals, as animal to vegetable life. So convincing was his reasoning, or unreasoning, to this effect, that he carried the country with him; and they made a clean sweep of all machinery that had not been in use for more than two hundred and seventy-one years (which period was arrived at after a series of compromises), and strictly forbade all further improvements and inventions under pain of being considered in the eye of the law to be labouring under typhus fever, which they regard as one of the worst of all crimes.
我还向他们询问了旧机器博物馆的情况，以及所有艺术、科学和发明明显倒退的原因。我了解到，大约四百年前，机械知识的水平远远超出了我们的水平，并且正在以惊人的速度前进，直到一位最博学的假设学教授写了一本非凡的书（我打算稍后提供其中的摘录） ），证明机器最终注定要取代人类，并成为本能，其生命力不同于动物，但又优于动物，就像动物与植物的生命一样。就这一点而言，他的推理或不推理是如此令人信服，以至于他赢得了国家的支持。他们对所有已经超过两百七十一年（这一时期是经过一系列妥协之后才达到的）不再使用的机器进行了彻底的清理，并严格禁止一切进一步的改进和发明，否则将被处以死刑。从法律的角度来看，他们被认为患有斑疹伤寒，他们认为斑疹伤寒是所有罪行中最严重的罪行之一。

This is the only case in which they have confounded mental and physical diseases, and they do it even here as by an avowed legal fiction. I became uneasy when I remembered about my watch; but they comforted me with the assurance that transgression in this matter was now so unheard of, that the law could afford to be lenient towards an utter stranger, especially towards one who had such a good character (they meant physique), and such beautiful light hair. Moreover the watch was a real curiosity, and would be a welcome addition to the metropolitan collection; so they did not think I need let it trouble me seriously.
这是他们将精神疾病和身体疾病混为一谈的唯一案例，即使在这里，他们也是通过公开的法律虚构来做到这一点的。当我想起我的手表时，我感到不安。但他们安慰我，保证这件事上的违法行为现在已经闻所未闻，法律可以对一个完全陌生的人宽大处理，特别是对一个性格如此好的人（他们指的是体格）和如此美丽的光芒的人头发。此外，这款手表确实是一件令人好奇的事情，并且将成为大都会收藏中受欢迎的补充。所以他们认为我不需要让它严重困扰我。

I will write, however, more fully upon this subject when I deal with the Colleges of Unreason, and the Book of the Machines.
然而，当我讨论《非理性学院》和《机器之书》时，我将更全面地讨论这个主题。

In about a month from the time of our starting I was told that our journey was nearly over. The bandage was now dispensed with, for it seemed impossible that I should ever be able to find my way back without being captured. Then we rolled merrily along through the streets of a handsome town, and got on to a long, broad, and level road, with poplar trees on either side. The road was raised slightly above the surrounding country, and had formerly been a railway; the fields on either side were in the highest conceivable cultivation, but the harvest and also the vintage had been already gathered. The weather had got cooler more rapidly than could be quite accounted for by the progress of the season; so I rather thought that we must have been making away from the sun, and were some degrees farther from the equator than when we started. Even here the vegetation showed that the climate was a hot one, yet there was no lack of vigour among the people; on the contrary, they were a very hardy race, and capable of great endurance. For the hundredth time I thought that, take them all round, I had never seen their equals in respect of physique, and they looked as good- natured as they were robust. The flowers were for the most part over, but their absence was in some measure compensated for by a profusion of delicious fruit, closely resembling the figs, peaches, and pears of Italy and France. I saw no wild animals, but birds were plentiful and much as in Europe, but not tame as they had been on the other side the ranges. They were shot at with the cross-bow and with arrows, gunpowder being unknown, or at any rate not in use.
从我们出发大约一个月后，我被告知我们的旅程即将结束。现在绷带已经被去掉了，因为我似乎不可能在不被抓获的情况下找到回去的路。然后我们欢快地穿过一座美丽小镇的街道，走上一条又长又宽又平坦的路，路两旁都是白杨树。这条路略高于周围的乡村，以前是一条铁路。两边的田地都处于可以想象的最高耕种状态，但庄稼和葡萄已经收完了。天气变冷的速度比季节的进展所能完全解释的要快。所以我宁愿认为我们一定是在远离太阳，并且距离赤道比我们开始时更远了一些。即使这里的植被显示出气候炎热，但人们却并不缺乏活力；相反，他们是一个非常吃苦耐劳的种族，具有很强的耐力。我第一百次想到，放眼望去，我从未见过他们的体格能与他们相媲美，而且他们看起来脾气很好，而且很强壮。花朵大部分已经开放，但它们的缺席在某种程度上被大量美味的水果所弥补，这些水果与意大利和法国的无花果、桃子和梨非常相似。我没有看到野生动物，但鸟类数量很多，和欧洲一样，但不像山脉另一边那样驯服。他们被十字弓和箭射杀，火药不明，或者至少没有使用过。

We were now nearing the metropolis and I could see great towers and fortifications, and lofty buildings that looked like palaces. I began to be nervous as to my reception; but I had got on very well so far, and resolved to continue upon the same plan as hitherto— namely, to behave just as though I were in England until I saw that I was making a blunder, and then to say nothing till I could gather how the land lay. We drew nearer and nearer. The news of my approach had got abroad, and there was a great crowd collected on either side the road, who greeted me with marks of most respectful curiosity, keeping me bowing constantly in acknowledgement from side to side.
我们现在已经接近大都市了，我可以看到巨大的塔楼和防御工事，以及看起来像宫殿的高耸建筑。我开始对自己的接待感到紧张。但到目前为止，我相处得很好，并决定继续执行迄今为止的相同计划——即，表现得就像我在英国一样，直到我发现自己犯了一个错误，然后什么也不说，直到我可以收集土地的分布情况。我们越来越近了。我即将到来的消息已经传到了国外，路两边都聚集了一大群人，他们用最恭敬的好奇心向我打招呼，让我不停地鞠躬致谢。

When we were about a mile off, we were met by the Mayor and several Councillors, among whom was a venerable old man, who was introduced to me by the Mayor (for so I suppose I should call him) as the gentleman who had invited me to his house. I bowed deeply and told him how grateful I felt to him, and how gladly I would accept his hospitality. He forbade me to say more, and pointing to his carriage, which was close at hand, he motioned me to a seat therein. I again bowed profoundly to the Mayor and Councillors, and drove off with my entertainer, whose name was Senoj Nosnibor. After about half a mile the carriage turned off the main road, and we drove under the walls of the town till we reached a palazzo on a slight eminence, and just on the outskirts of the city. This was Senoj Nosnibor’s house, and nothing can be imagined finer. It was situated near the magnificent and venerable ruins of the old railway station, which formed an imposing feature from the gardens of the house. The grounds, some ten or a dozen acres in extent, were laid out in terraced gardens, one above the other, with flights of broad steps ascending and descending the declivity of the garden. On these steps there were statues of most exquisite workmanship. Besides the statues there were vases filled with various shrubs that were new to me; and on either side the flights of steps there were rows of old cypresses and cedars, with grassy alleys between them. Then came choice vineyards and orchards of fruit-trees in full bearing.
当我们离我们大约一英里时，市长和几位议员迎接了我们，其中有一位德高望重的老人，市长（我想我应该这么称呼他）向我介绍了他，他是邀请我们的绅士。我去他家。我深深地鞠了一躬，告诉他我是多么感激他，并且我多么高兴接受他的盛情款待。他不许我多说，指着近在咫尺的马车，示意我坐下。我再次向市长和议员深深鞠了一躬，然后和我的艺人一起开车离开了，他的名字叫Senoj Nosnibor。大约半英里后，马车驶离主干道，我们在城墙下行驶，直到到达一座位于城市郊区稍高处的宫殿。这是 Senoj Nosnibor 的房子，没有什么比这更好的了。它坐落在宏伟而古老的旧火车站遗址附近，与房子的花园形成了一道壮丽的风景。占地约十英亩或十几英亩的土地被布置在梯田花园中，一个在另一个之上，一段宽阔的台阶沿着花园的斜坡上升和下降。这些台阶上矗立着做工最精美的雕像。除了雕像之外，还有花瓶，里面装满了对我来说很陌生的各种灌木。台阶两边长着一排排老柏树和雪松，它们之间有长满青草的小巷。然后是精选的葡萄园和果树丰收的果园。

The house itself was approached by a court-yard, and round it was a corridor on to which rooms opened, as at Pompeii. In the middle of the court there was a bath and a fountain. Having passed the court we came to the main body of the house, which was two stories in height. The rooms were large and lofty; perhaps at first they looked rather bare of furniture, but in hot climates people generally keep their rooms more bare than they do in colder ones. I missed also the sight of a grand piano or some similar instrument, there being no means of producing music in any of the rooms save the larger drawing-room, where there were half a dozen large bronze gongs, which the ladies used occasionally to beat about at random. It was not pleasant to hear them, but I have heard quite as unpleasant music both before and since.
房子本身有一个庭院，周围有一条走廊，房间通向走廊，就像庞贝古城一样。庭院中央有一个浴室和一个喷泉。穿过庭院，我们来到了两层楼高的房屋主体。房间又大又高。也许一开始他们看起来相当空荡荡的家具，但在炎热的气候下，人们通常比在寒冷的气候下更空荡荡的房间。我还错过了三角钢琴或类似乐器的景象，除了较大的客厅外，任何房间都没有办法演奏音乐，客厅里有六个大青铜锣，女士们偶尔会用它们来敲击大约是随机的。听到这些声音并不令人愉快，但我之前和之后都听到过同样令人不愉快的音乐。

Mr. Nosnibor took me through several spacious rooms till we reached a boudoir where were his wife and daughters, of whom I had heard from the interpreter. Mrs. Nosnibor was about forty years old, and still handsome, but she had grown very stout: her daughters were in the prime of youth and exquisitely beautiful. I gave the preference almost at once to the younger, whose name was Arowhena; for the elder sister was haughty, while the younger had a very winning manner. Mrs. Nosnibor received me with the perfection of courtesy, so that I must have indeed been shy and nervous if I had not at once felt welcome. Scarcely was the ceremony of my introduction well completed before a servant announced that dinner was ready in the next room. I was exceedingly hungry, and the dinner was beyond all praise. Can the reader wonder that I began to consider myself in excellent quarters? ‘That man embezzle money?’ thought I to myself; ‘impossible.’
诺斯尼博尔先生带我穿过几个宽敞的房间，直到我们到达一间闺房，那里住着他的妻子和女儿，我是从翻译那里听到她们的消息的。诺斯尼博尔夫人四十岁左右，依然英俊潇洒，但已经变得很胖了：她的女儿们正值青春年华，非常美丽。我几乎立刻就优先选择了较年轻的，她的名字叫阿罗维纳（Arowhena）。因为姐姐很傲慢，而妹妹则很有征服欲。诺斯尼博尔夫人以完美的礼貌接待了我，因此，如果我没有立即感受到受欢迎的话，我一定会感到害羞和紧张。我的介绍仪式刚结束，仆人就宣布隔壁房间准备好了晚餐。我实在是太饿了，晚餐真是太棒了。读者是否会好奇我开始认为自己处于优秀的地位？ “那个人贪污了钱？”我心里想。 '不可能的。'

But I noticed that my host was uneasy during the whole meal, and that he ate nothing but a little bread and milk; towards the end of dinner there came a tall lean man with a black beard, to whom Mr. Nosnibor and the whole family paid great attention: he was the family straightener. With this gentleman Mr. Nosnibor retired into another room, from which there presently proceeded a sound of weeping and wailing. I could hardly believe my ears, but in a few minutes I got to know for a certainty that they came from Mr. Nosnibor himself.
但我注意到主人整顿饭都很不安，只吃了一点面包和牛奶；晚饭快结束时，来了一个高高瘦瘦、留着黑胡子的男人，诺斯尼博尔先生和全家人都对他十分关注：他是家里的矫正者。诺斯尼博尔先生和这位先生一起退到了另一个房间，那里立刻传来哭泣和哀号的声音。我简直不敢相信自己的耳朵，但几分钟后我就确信这些声音来自诺斯尼伯先生本人。

‘Poor papa,’ said Arowhena, as she helped herself composedly to the salt, ‘how terribly he has suffered.’
“可怜的爸爸，”阿罗维娜一边平静地取盐，一边说道，“他受了多么可怕的痛苦啊。”

‘Yes,’ answered her mother; ‘but I think he is quite out of danger now.’
“是的，”她母亲回答道。 “但我认为他现在已经脱离危险了。”

Then they went on to explain to me the circumstances of the case, and the treatment which the straightener had prescribed, and how successful he had been—all which I will reserve for another chapter, and put rather in the form of a general summary of the opinions current upon these subjects than in the exact words in which the facts were delivered to me; the reader, however, is earnestly requested to believe that both in this next chapter and in those that follow it I have endeavoured to adhere most conscientiously to the strictest accuracy, and that I have never willingly misrepresented, though I may have sometimes failed to understand all the bearings of an opinion or custom.
然后他们继续向我解释案件的情况、矫直器规定的治疗方法以及他的治疗效果如何——所有这些我将在另一章中保留，并以一般总结的形式提出。关于这些主题的当前观点，而不是向我传达事实的确切文字；然而，恳请读者相信，无论是在下一章还是在其后的章节中，我都尽力严格遵守最严格的准确性，并且我从未故意歪曲，尽管有时我可能无法理解意见或习俗的所有方位。

CHAPTER X: CURRENT OPINIONS
第十章：当前观点

This is what I gathered. That in that country if a man falls into ill health, or catches any disorder, or fails bodily in any way before he is seventy years old, he is tried before a jury of his countrymen, and if convicted is held up to public scorn and sentenced more or less severely as the case may be. There are subdivisions of illnesses into crimes and misdemeanours as with offences amongst ourselves—a man being punished very heavily for serious illness, while failure of eyes or hearing in one over sixty-five, who has had good health hitherto, is dealt with by fine only, or imprisonment in default of payment. But if a man forges a cheque, or sets his house on fire, or robs with violence from the person, or does any other such things as are criminal in our own country, he is either taken to a hospital and most carefully tended at the public expense, or if he is in good circumstances, he lets it be known to all his friends that he is suffering from a severe fit of immorality, just as we do when we are ill, and they come and visit him with great solicitude, and inquire with interest how it all came about, what symptoms first showed themselves, and so forth,—questions which he will answer with perfect unreserve; for bad conduct, though considered no less deplorable than illness with ourselves, and as unquestionably indicating something seriously wrong with the individual who misbehaves, is nevertheless held to be the result of either pre-natal or post-natal misfortune.
这是我收集到的。在那个国家，如果一个人在七十岁之前健康状况不佳，或者患上任何疾病，或者身体出现任何问题，他就会在他的同胞组成的陪审团面前接受审判，如果被定罪，他就会受到公众的蔑视和嘲笑。根据具体情况，判处较重或较轻的刑罚。疾病分为犯罪和轻罪，就像我们之间的犯罪行为一样——一个人因重病而受到严厉的惩罚，而六十五岁以上的人，如果迄今为止健康状况良好，则眼睛或听力丧失，将受到罚款或因拖欠付款而被监禁。但是，如果一个人伪造支票，或者放火烧毁他的房子，或者暴力抢劫，或者做出任何其他在我们国家属于犯罪的行为，那么他要么被送往医院，要么在医院接受最仔细的治疗。公共开支，或者如果他状况良好，他会让所有朋友都知道他患有严重的不道德行为，就像我们生病时一样，他们会非常关心地来看望他，并饶有兴趣地询问这一切是如何发生的，首先出现什么症状，等等，他会毫无保留地回答这些问题；因为不良行为虽然被认为与我们自己的疾病一样令人遗憾，并且毫无疑问地表明行为不端的人存在严重问题，但仍然被认为是产前或产后不幸的结果。

The strange part of the story, however, is that though they ascribe moral defects to the effect of misfortune either in character or surroundings, they will not listen to the plea of misfortune in cases that in England meet with sympathy and commiseration only. Ill luck of any kind, or even ill treatment at the hands of others, is considered an offence against society, inasmuch as it makes people uncomfortable to hear of it. Loss of fortune, therefore, or loss of some dear friend on whom another was much dependent, is punished hardly less severely than physical delinquency.
然而，这个故事的奇怪之处在于，尽管他们将道德缺陷归咎于性格或环境的不幸，但在英国只得到同情和怜悯的情况下，他们却不会倾听不幸的恳求。任何形式的厄运，甚至受到他人的虐待，都被认为是对社会的冒犯，因为这会让人们听到它感到不舒服。因此，失去财富，或者失去另一个人非常依赖的亲密朋友，所受到的惩罚几乎不亚于身体犯罪。

Foreign, indeed, as such ideas are to our own, traces of somewhat similar opinions can be found even in nineteenth-century England. If a person has an abscess, the medical man will say that it contains ‘peccant’ matter, and people say that they have a ‘bad’ arm or finger, or that they are very ‘bad’ all over, when they only mean ‘diseased.’ Among foreign nations Erewhonian opinions may be still more clearly noted. The Mahommedans, for example, to this day, send their female prisoners to hospitals, and the New Zealand Maories visit any misfortune with forcible entry into the house of the offender, and the breaking up and burning of all his goods. The Italians, again, use the same word for ‘disgrace’ and ‘misfortune.’ I once heard an Italian lady speak of a young friend whom she described as endowed with every virtue under heaven, ‘ma,’ she exclaimed, ‘povero disgraziato, ha ammazzato suo zio.’ (“Poor unfortunate fellow, he has murdered his uncle.’)
事实上，虽然这些观念对我们来说是陌生的，但即使在十九世纪的英国也能找到多少类似观点的痕迹。如果一个人有脓肿，医生会说它含有“腐败”物质，人们会说他们的手臂或手指“不好”，或者全身都很“不好”，而他们的意思只是“在外国中，埃雷洪尼亚的观点可能更容易被注意到。例如，伊斯兰教徒至今仍将女囚犯送往医院，而新西兰毛利人则强行进入罪犯的家中，并打碎并烧毁他的所有物品，以应对任何不幸。意大利人再次使用同一个词来表示“耻辱”和“不幸”。我曾经听到一位意大利女士谈到一位年轻的朋友，她形容他拥有天下所有的美德，“妈”，她惊呼道，“povero disgraziato” , ha ammazzato suo zio。”（“可怜的不幸的家伙，他谋杀了他的叔叔。”）

On mentioning this, which I heard when taken to Italy as a boy by my father, the person to whom I told it showed no surprise. He said that he had been driven for two or three years in a certain city by a young Sicilian cabdriver of prepossessing manners and appearance, but then lost sight of him. On asking what had become of him, he was told that he was in prison for having shot at his father with intent to kill him—happily without serious result. Some years later my informant again found himself warmly accosted by the prepossessing young cabdriver. ‘Ah, caro signore,’ he exclaimed, ‘sono cinque anni che non lo vedo—tre anni di militare, e due anni di disgrazia,’ &c. (“My dear sir, it is five years since I saw you—three years of military service, and two of misfortune’)—during which last the poor fellow had been in prison. Of moral sense he showed not so much as a trace. He and his father were now on excellent terms, and were likely to remain so unless either of them should again have the misfortune mortally to offend the other.
当我还是个孩子的时候，我被父亲带去意大利时听到了这件事，听我讲述这件事的人并没有表现出任何惊讶。他说，他曾在某个城市被一位举止和外表都很讨人喜欢的西西里年轻出租车司机开车了两三年，但后来就再也见不到他了。在询问他的情况时，他被告知他因向父亲开枪意图杀死他而入狱——幸运的是没有造成严重后果。几年后，我的线人再次发现自己受到了那位迷人的年轻出租车司机的热情搭讪。 “啊，卡罗先生，”他喊道，“sono cinque anni che non lo vedo——tre anni di militare，e due anni di disgrazia，”等等。 （“亲爱的先生，自从我见到你以来，已经五年了——三年的兵役，两年的不幸”）——最后这个可怜的家伙一直在监狱里。他没有表现出任何道德感。他和他的父亲现在关系很好，而且很可能会一直如此，除非他们中的任何一个再次不幸得罪对方。

In the following chapter I will give a few examples of the way in which what we should call misfortune, hardship, or disease are dealt with by the Erewhonians, but for the moment will return to their treatment of cases that with us are criminal. As I have already said, these, though not judicially punishable, are recognised as requiring correction. Accordingly, there exists a class of men trained in soul-craft, whom they call straighteners, as nearly as I can translate a word which literally means ‘one who bends back the crooked.’ These men practise much as medical men in England, and receive a quasi-surreptitious fee on every visit. They are treated with the same unreserve, and obeyed as readily, as our own doctors—that is to say, on the whole sufficiently—because people know that it is their interest to get well as soon as they can, and that they will not be scouted as they would be if their bodies were out of order, even though they may have to undergo a very painful course of treatment.
在下一章中，我将举几个例子，说明埃雷洪人处理我们所谓的不幸、困难或疾病的方式，但现在我们将回到他们对我们来说是犯罪案件的处理方式。正如我已经说过的，这些虽然不会受到司法惩罚，但被认为需要纠正。因此，存在着一类受过灵魂技艺训练的人，他们称之为矫直者，我可以翻译一个词，字面意思是“使弯曲的人弯曲。”这些人在英国的实践就像医生一样，并且每次访问都会收取准秘密费用。他们受到与我们自己的医生一样的毫无保留的对待，并且像我们自己的医生一样乐意服从——也就是说，总体上足够了——因为人们知道尽快康复是他们的利益，而且他们不会即使他们可能必须经历非常痛苦的治疗过程，但如果他们的身体出了问题，他们也会被侦察。

When I say that they will not be scouted, I do not mean that an Erewhonian will suffer no social inconvenience in consequence, we will say, of having committed fraud. Friends will fall away from him because of his being less pleasant company, just as we ourselves are disinclined to make companions of those who are either poor or poorly. No one with any sense of self-respect will place himself on an equality in the matter of affection with those who are less lucky than himself in birth, health, money, good looks, capacity, or anything else. Indeed, that dislike and even disgust should be felt by the fortunate for the unfortunate, or at any rate for those who have been discovered to have met with any of the more serious and less familiar misfortunes, is not only natural, but desirable for any society, whether of man or brute.
当我说他们不会被侦察时，我并不是说埃雷洪人不会因为我们所说的欺诈行为而遭受社会不便。朋友会因为他不那么令人愉快而远离他，就像我们自己不愿意与那些贫穷或贫穷的人做朋友一样。任何一个有自尊心的人都不会在感情问题上与那些在出身、健康、金钱、美貌、能力或其他方面不如自己幸运的人平等对待。事实上，幸运者对不幸者，或者至少是那些被发现遭遇过更严重和不太熟悉的不幸的人，应该感到不喜欢甚至厌恶，这不仅是自然的，而且对任何人来说都是可取的。社会，无论是人社会还是畜生社会。

The fact, therefore, that the Erewhonians attach none of that guilt to crime which they do to physical ailments, does not prevent the more selfish among them from neglecting a friend who has robbed a bank, for instance, till he has fully recovered; but it does prevent them from even thinking of treating criminals with that contemptuous tone which would seem to say, ‘I, if I were you, should be a better man than you are,’ a tone which is held quite reasonable in regard to physical ailment. Hence, though they conceal ill health by every cunning and hypocrisy and artifice which they can devise, they are quite open about the most flagrant mental diseases, should they happen to exist, which to do the people justice is not often. Indeed, there are some who are, so to speak, spiritual valetudinarians, and who make themselves exceedingly ridiculous by their nervous supposition that they are wicked, while they are very tolerable people all the time. This however is exceptional; and on the whole they use much the same reserve or unreserve about the state of their moral welfare as we do about our health.
因此，事实上，埃雷洪人并不像对待身体疾病那样将罪责归咎于犯罪，但这并不能阻止他们中更自私的人忽视一个抢劫银行的朋友，例如，直到他完全康复为止；但它确实阻止他们想到用那种轻蔑的语气对待罪犯，这种语气似乎是在说，“如果我是你，我应该是一个比你更好的人”，这种语气在身体方面是相当合理的。病痛。因此，尽管他们用一切狡猾、虚伪和诡计来掩盖健康状况不佳，但他们却对最明目张胆的精神疾病（如果碰巧存在的话）持开放态度，而为人民伸张正义并不常见。确实，有些人可以说是精神上的衰弱者，他们因紧张地认为自己是邪恶的而使自己变得极其可笑，而实际上他们一直都是非常可以容忍的人。然而，这是例外的；总体而言，他们对自己的道德福利状况的保留或不保留与我们对健康的保留或无保留几乎相同。

Hence all the ordinary greetings among ourselves, such as, How do you do? and the like, are considered signs of gross ill-breeding; nor do the politer classes tolerate even such a common complimentary remark as telling a man that he is looking well. They salute each other with, ‘I hope you are good this morning;’ or ‘I hope you have recovered from the snappishness from which you were suffering when I last saw you;’ and if the person saluted has not been good, or is still snappish, he says so at once and is condoled with accordingly. Indeed, the straighteners have gone so far as to give names from the hypothetical language (as taught at the Colleges of Unreason), to all known forms of mental indisposition, and to classify them according to a system of their own, which, though I could not understand it, seemed to work well in practice; for they are always able to tell a man what is the matter with him as soon as they have heard his story, and their familiarity with the long names assures him that they thoroughly understand his case.
因此，我们之间所有的普通问候都是如此，例如，你好吗？等等，被认为是严重不良教养的迹象；礼貌阶层也不会容忍像告诉一个男人他看起来很好这样常见的赞美之词。他们互相打招呼，“我希望你今天早上一切都好”；或者“我希望你已经从我上次见到你时所遭受的暴躁中恢复过来了；”如果打招呼的人表现不好，或者是他仍然脾气暴躁，立刻这么说了，并得到了相应的哀悼。事实上，矫正者们甚至用假设的语言（如非理性学院所教授的）给所有已知的精神不适形式命名，并根据他们自己的系统对它们进行分类，尽管我看不懂，实践起来好像效果很好；因为他们总是能够在听完一个人的故事后立即告诉他发生了什么事，而且他们对长名字的熟悉使他确信他们完全了解他的情况。

The reader will have no difficulty in believing that the laws regarding ill health were frequently evaded by the help of recognised fictions, which every one understood, but which it would be considered gross ill-breeding to even seem to understand. Thus, a day or two after my arrival at the Nosnibors’, one of the many ladies who called on me made excuses for her husband’s only sending his card, on the ground that when going through the public market- place that morning he had stolen a pair of socks. I had already been warned that I should never show surprise, so I merely expressed my sympathy, and said that though I had only been in the capital so short a time, I had already had a very narrow escape from stealing a clothes-brush, and that though I had resisted temptation so far, I was sadly afraid that if I saw any object of special interest that was neither too hot nor too heavy, I should have to put myself in the straightener’s hands.
读者会毫不费力地相信，关于健康不良的法律经常借助公认的虚构作品来逃避，这些虚构作品每个人都理解，但即使看起来理解，也会被认为是严重的无教养。因此，在我到达诺斯尼伯斯家一两天后，拜访我的众多女士中的一位为她丈夫只寄了他的名片找借口，理由是那天早上他经过公共市场时偷了东西。一双袜子。我已经被警告过不要表现出惊讶，所以我只是表达了我的同情，并说我虽然来京城的时间很短，但我已经九死一生地偷了一把衣刷，虽然到目前为止我已经抵制住了诱惑，但我很遗憾地担心，如果我看到任何特别感兴趣的物体，既不太热也不太重，我就不得不把自己放在直发器的手中。

Mrs. Nosnibor, who had been keeping an ear on all that I had been saying, praised me when the lady had gone. Nothing, she said, could have been more polite according to Erewhonian etiquette. She then explained that to have stolen a pair of socks, or ‘to have the socks’ (in more colloquial language), was a recognised way of saying that the person in question was slightly indisposed.
诺斯尼伯夫人一直在倾听我所说的一切，当那位女士走后，她称赞了我。她说，根据埃雷洪尼亚礼仪，没有什么比这更礼貌的了。然后她解释说，“偷了一双袜子”，或者“拥有袜子”（用更通俗的语言），是一种公认​​的表达方式，表示该人有点不舒服。

In spite of all this they have a keen sense of the enjoyment consequent upon what they call being ‘well.’ They admire mental health and love it in other people, and take all the pains they can (consistently with their other duties) to secure it for themselves. They have an extreme dislike to marrying into what they consider unhealthy families. They send for the straightener at once whenever they have been guilty of anything seriously flagitious— often even if they think that they are on the point of committing it; and though his remedies are sometimes exceedingly painful, involving close confinement for weeks, and in some cases the most cruel physical tortures, I never heard of a reasonable Erewhonian refusing to do what his straightener told him, any more than of a reasonable Englishman refusing to undergo even the most frightful operation, if his doctors told him it was necessary.
尽管如此，他们对他们所说的“健康”所带来的享受有着敏锐的感觉。他们钦佩并热爱其他人的心理健康，并尽一切努力（与他们的其他职责一致）来确保心理健康。为他们自己。他们非常不喜欢嫁给他们认为不健康的家庭。每当他们犯下严重的罪行时，他们就会立即派人去矫正——通常即使他们认为自己即将犯下这种罪行；尽管他的治疗方法有时非常痛苦，包括数周的严密监禁，有时甚至是最残酷的肉体折磨，但我从未听说过一个理智的埃雷洪人拒绝做他的矫正器告诉他的事情，就像一个理智的英国人拒绝做他的矫直师告诉他的那样。如果医生告诉他有必要的话，他甚至可以接受最可怕的手术。

We in England never shrink from telling our doctor what is the matter with us merely through the fear that he will hurt us. We let him do his worst upon us, and stand it without a murmur, because we are not scouted for being ill, and because we know that the doctor is doing his best to cure us, and that he can judge of our case better than we can; but we should conceal all illness if we were treated as the Erewhonians are when they have anything the matter with them; we should do the same as with moral and intellectual diseases,—we should feign health with the most consummate art, till we were found out, and should hate a single flogging given in the way of mere punishment more than the amputation of a limb, if it were kindly and courteously performed from a wish to help us out of our difficulty, and with the full consciousness on the part of the doctor that it was only by an accident of constitution that he was not in the like plight himself. So the Erewhonians take a flogging once a week, and a diet of bread and water for two or three months together, whenever their straightener recommends it.
我们英国人从来不会仅仅因为担心医生会伤害我们而不敢告诉医生我们出了什么问题。我们让他对我们做最坏的事，并且毫无怨言地忍受着，因为我们没有因为生病而被发现，因为我们知道医生正在尽最大努力治愈我们，而且他比其他人更能判断我们的情况。我们可以;但是，如果我们像埃瑞洪人一样，在他们有任何问题时受到对待，我们就应该隐瞒所有疾病。我们应该像对待道德和智力疾病那样做，——我们应该用最完美的艺术假装健康，直到我们被发现，并且应该憎恨仅仅以惩罚方式给予的鞭打，而不是截肢，如果这是出于帮助我们摆脱困境的愿望而仁慈而礼貌地进行的，并且医生充分意识到，他自己没有陷入同样的​​困境只是由于体质的意外。因此，埃雷洪人每周接受一次鞭打，并在两三个月内以面包和水为食，只要直发师建议这样做即可。

I do not suppose that even my host, on having swindled a confiding widow out of the whole of her property, was put to more actual suffering than a man will readily undergo at the hands of an English doctor. And yet he must have had a very bad time of it. The sounds I heard were sufficient to show that his pain was exquisite, but he never shrank from undergoing it. He was quite sure that it did him good; and I think he was right. I cannot believe that that man will ever embezzle money again. He may—but it will be a long time before he does so.
我不认为，即使是我的主人，在骗取了一位心腹的寡妇的全部财产后，所遭受的实际痛苦也不会比一个男人在英国医生手中所承受的痛苦还要多。但他一定过得很糟糕。我听到的声音足以表明他的痛苦是剧烈的，但他却从不退缩。他确信这对他有好处；我认为他是对的。我不敢相信那个人会再次贪污钱财。他可能会——但他需要很长时间才能这样做。

During my confinement in prison, and on my journey, I had already discovered a great deal of the above; but it still seemed surpassingly strange, and I was in constant fear of committing some piece of rudeness, through my inability to look at things from the same stand-point as my neighbours; but after a few weeks’ stay with the Nosnibors, I got to understand things better, especially on having heard all about my host’s illness, of which he told me fully and repeatedly.
在我入狱期间和旅途中，我已经发现了很多上述内容；但这似乎仍然非常奇怪，我一直担心自己会做出一些无礼的举动，因为我无法从与邻居相同的角度来看待事物。但在诺斯尼伯一家待了几周后，我对事情有了更好的了解，尤其是在听了我的主人的病情的全部信息之后，他向我详细地、反复地讲述了这些事情。

It seemed that he had been on the Stock Exchange of the city for many years and had amassed enormous wealth, without exceeding the limits of what was generally considered justifiable, or at any rate, permissible dealing; but at length on several occasions he had become aware of a desire to make money by fraudulent representations, and had actually dealt with two or three sums in a way which had made him rather uncomfortable. He had unfortunately made light of it and pooh-poohed the ailment, until circumstances eventually presented themselves which enabled him to cheat upon a very considerable scale;—he told me what they were, and they were about as bad as anything could be, but I need not detail them;—he seized the opportunity, and became aware, when it was too late, that he must be seriously out of order. He had neglected himself too long.
看来他在这座城市的证券交易所工作了很多年，积累了巨大的财富，但没有超出一般认为合理的限度，或者至少没有超出允许的交易限度；但最终有几次他意识到自己想通过欺诈性陈述来赚钱，并且实际上以一种让他感到相当不舒服的方式处理了两三笔钱。不幸的是，他对此轻描淡写，对这种疾病嗤之以鼻，直到情况最终出现，使他能够在相当大的范围内作弊；——他告诉我它们是什么，它们几乎是最糟糕的，但是我不需要详细说明它们；——他抓住了这个机会，并意识到，当为时已晚时，他一定是严重失常了。他已经忽视自己太久了。

He drove home at once, broke the news to his wife and daughters as gently as he could, and sent off for one of the most celebrated straighteners of the kingdom to a consultation with the family practitioner, for the case was plainly serious. On the arrival of the straightener he told his story, and expressed his fear that his morals must be permanently impaired.
他立即开车回家，尽可能温和地将这个消息告诉了他的妻子和女儿，并派人请王国最著名的直发师之一去咨询家庭医生，因为案件显然很严重。矫直机到来后，他讲述了自己的故事，并表示担心自己的道德将永远受到损害。

The eminent man reassured him with a few cheering words, and then proceeded to make a more careful diagnosis of the case. He inquired concerning Mr. Nosnibor’s parents—had their moral health been good? He was answered that there had not been anything seriously amiss with them, but that his maternal grandfather, whom he was supposed to resemble somewhat in person, had been a consummate scoundrel and had ended his days in a hospital,—while a brother of his father’s, after having led a most flagitious life for many years, had been at last cured by a philosopher of a new school, which as far as I could understand it bore much the same relation to the old as homoeopathy to allopathy. The straightener shook his head at this, and laughingly replied that the cure must have been due to nature. After a few more questions he wrote a prescription and departed.
这位知名人士用几句鼓励的话安抚了他，然后开始对这个病例进行更仔细的诊断。他询问了诺斯尼博尔先生的父母——他们的道德健康状况良好吗？他得到的答复是，他们并没有什么严重的问题，但是他的外祖父，他应该与外祖父有几分相似，是一个完美的恶棍，在医院结束了他的日子，而他的一个兄弟父亲的病情在经历了多年最恶劣的生活之后，终于被一位新学派的哲学家治愈了，据我所知，新学派与旧学派的关系就像顺势疗法与对抗疗法一样。直人闻言摇了摇头，笑道，这一定是自然的治愈。又问了几个问题后，他开了一张处方就离开了。

I saw the prescription. It ordered a fine to the State of double the money embezzled; no food but bread and milk for six months, and a severe flogging once a month for twelve. I was surprised to see that no part of the fine was to be paid to the poor woman whose money had been embezzled, but on inquiry I learned that she would have been prosecuted in the Misplaced Confidence Court, if she had not escaped its clutches by dying shortly after she had discovered her loss.
我看到了处方。它下令对州政府处以所贪污金额双倍的罚款；六个月内除了面包和牛奶外没有食物，十二个月内每月会受到一次严厉的鞭打。我很惊讶地发现，罚款的一部分没有支付给那个钱被挪用的可怜的女人，但经过询问，我得知，如果她没有逃脱法庭的魔掌，她就会在失信法庭受到起诉。她发现自己失去亲人后不久就去世了。

As for Mr. Nosnibor, he had received his eleventh flogging on the day of my arrival. I saw him later on the same afternoon, and he was still twinged; but there had been no escape from following out the straightener’s prescription, for the so-called sanitary laws of Erewhon are very rigorous, and unless the straightener was satisfied that his orders had been obeyed, the patient would have been taken to a hospital (as the poor are), and would have been much worse off. Such at least is the law, but it is never necessary to enforce it.
至于诺斯尼博尔先生，我到达的那天，他已经受到了第十一次鞭打。当天下午晚些时候，我见到了他，但他仍然感到刺痛。但必须遵守矫直师的处方，因为埃里洪所谓的卫生法非常严格，除非矫直师确信他的命令得到了遵守，否则病人就会被送往医院（如穷人），而且情况会更糟。至少法律是这样，但没有必要强制执行。

On a subsequent occasion I was present at an interview between Mr. Nosnibor and the family straightener, who was considered competent to watch the completion of the cure. I was struck with the delicacy with which he avoided even the remotest semblance of inquiry after the physical well-being of his patient, though there was a certain yellowness about my host’s eyes which argued a bilious habit of body. To have taken notice of this would have been a gross breach of professional etiquette. I was told, however, that a straightener sometimes thinks it right to glance at the possibility of some slight physical disorder if he finds it important in order to assist him in his diagnosis; but the answers which he gets are generally untrue or evasive, and he forms his own conclusions upon the matter as well as he can. Sensible men have been known to say that the straightener should in strict confidence be told of every physical ailment that is likely to bear upon the case; but people are naturally shy of doing this, for they do not like lowering themselves in the opinion of the straightener, and his ignorance of medical science is supreme. I heard of one lady, indeed, who had the hardihood to confess that a furious outbreak of ill-humour and extravagant fancies for which she was seeking advice was possibly the result of indisposition. ‘You should resist that,’ said the straightener, in a kind, but grave voice; ‘we can do nothing for the bodies of our patients; such matters are beyond our province, and I desire that I may hear no further particulars.’ The lady burst into tears, and promised faithfully that she would never be unwell again.
在随后的一次场合中，我参加了诺斯尼博尔先生和家庭矫正师的会面，他被认为有能力监督治疗的完成。令我震惊的是，他对病人的身体健康状况避而不谈，哪怕是最细微的询问，尽管我的主人的眼睛有些发黄，这说明他的身体习惯很坏。如果注意到这一点，那就严重违反了职业礼仪。然而，有人告诉我，矫直师有时会认为，如果他认为某种轻微的身体疾病的可能性对帮助他的诊断很重要，那么他就应该检查一下。但他得到的答案通常是不真实的或含糊其辞的，他尽可能地根据此事得出自己的结论。据了解，明智的人会说，应该严格保密地将可能影响案件的每一种身体疾病告知矫直师。但人们自然不愿意这样做，因为他们不喜欢在矫正者的意见中贬低自己，而他对医学的无知是至高无上的。事实上，我听说过一位女士，她勇敢地承认，她正在寻求建议的暴怒和奢侈的幻想可能是身体不适的结果。 “你应该抵制这种行为，”矫直师用一种友善但严肃的声音说道。 “我们对病人的身体无能为力；这些事情不属于我们的管辖范围，我希望不要再听到更多细节。”这位女士泪流满面，并忠实地保证她再也不会感到不适。

But to return to Mr. Nosnibor. As the afternoon wore on many carriages drove up with callers to inquire how he had stood his flogging. It had been very severe, but the kind inquiries upon every side gave him great pleasure, and he assured me that he felt almost tempted to do wrong again by the solicitude with which his friends had treated him during his recovery: in this I need hardly say that he was not serious.
回到诺斯尼博尔先生。下午过去了，许多马车开过来，来电者询问他是如何忍受鞭打的。虽然情况非常严峻，但各方的善意询问让他感到非常高兴，他向我保证，他的朋友们在他康复期间对他的关心让他几乎想再次做错事：在这一点上，我几乎不需要说他不认真。

During the remainder of my stay in the country Mr. Nosnibor was constantly attentive to his business, and largely increased his already great possessions; but I never heard a whisper to the effect of his having been indisposed a second time, or made money by other than the most strictly honourable means. I did hear afterwards in confidence that there had been reason to believe that his health had been not a little affected by the straightener’s treatment, but his friends did not choose to be over-curious upon the subject, and on his return to his affairs it was by common consent passed over as hardly criminal in one who was otherwise so much afflicted. For they regard bodily ailments as the more venial in proportion as they have been produced by causes independent of the constitution. Thus if a person ruin his health by excessive indulgence at the table or by drinking, they count it to be almost a part of the mental disease which brought it about, and so it goes for little, but they have no mercy on such illnesses as fevers or catarrhs or lung diseases, which to us appear to be beyond the control of the individual. They are only more lenient towards the diseases of the young—such as measles, which they think to be like sowing one’s wild oats—and look over them as pardonable indiscretions if they have not been too serious, and if they are atoned for by complete subsequent recovery.
在我留在该国的剩余时间里，诺斯尼博尔先生一直专注于他的生意，并大大增加了他本已庞大的财产。但我从来没有听到过任何关于他第二次身体不适的传言，或者说他除了最严格的光荣手段之外还通过其他方式赚钱。后来我确实私下听说，有理由相信他的健康受到直发器治疗的影响不小，但他的朋友们并没有选择对这个问题过度好奇，当他回到自己的事务中时，对于一个原本饱受折磨的人来说，这种行为被普遍认为不算犯罪。因为他们认为，身体疾病越是由独立于体质的原因引起的，就越是轻微的。因此，如果一个人因在餐桌上过度放纵或酗酒而损害了自己的健康，他们认为这几乎是造成这种疾病的精神疾病的一部分，所以这没什么关系，但他们对诸如此类的疾病却毫不怜悯。发烧、卡他或肺部疾病，在我们看来，这些似乎超出了个人的控制范围。他们只是对年轻人的疾病更加宽容，比如麻疹，他们认为这就像播种野燕麦一样，并且将其视为可以原谅的轻率行为，如果它们不是太严重的话，如果它们可以通过彻底的补救来弥补的话。随后的恢复。

It is hardly necessary to say that the office of straightener is one which requires long and special training. It stands to reason that he who would cure a moral ailment must be practically acquainted with it in all its bearings. The student for the profession of straightener is required to set apart certain seasons for the practice of each vice in turn, as a religious duty. These seasons are called ‘fasts,’ and are continued by the student until he finds that he really can subdue all the more usual vices in his own person, and hence can advise his patients from the results of his own experience.
毋庸置疑，矫直师的职位是一个需要长期、特殊培训的职位。按理说，想要治愈道德疾病的人必须实际上熟悉它的所有方面。作为一项宗教义务，矫直师专业的学生必须在特定的季节里轮流练习每种恶习。这些季节被称为“禁食”，并由学生继续进行，直到他发现自己确实可以克服自己身上所有更常见的恶习，因此可以根据自己的经验为患者提供建议。

Those who intend to be specialists, rather than general practitioners, devote themselves more particularly to the branch in which their practice will mainly lie. Some students have been obliged to continue their exercises during their whole lives, and some devoted men have actually died as martyrs to the drink, or gluttony, or whatever branch of vice they may have chosen for their especial study. The greater number, however, take no harm by the excursions into the various departments of vice which it is incumbent upon them to study.
那些想要成为专家而不是全科医生的人，会更加专注于他们主要从事的领域。有些学生一生都被迫继续锻炼，有些虔诚的人实际上因酗酒、暴食或他们为特殊学习而选择的任何恶习而殉道。然而，大多数人并没有因为涉足他们有责任研究的恶行的各个部门而受到伤害。

For the Erewhonians hold that unalloyed virtue is not a thing to be immoderately indulged in. I was shown more than one case in which the real or supposed virtues of parents were visited upon the children to the third and fourth generation. The straighteners say that the most that can be truly said for virtue is that there is a considerable balance in its favour, and that it is on the whole a good deal better to be on its side than against it; but they urge that there is much pseudo-virtue going about, which is apt to let people in very badly before they find it out. Those men, they say, are best who are not remarkable either for vice or virtue. I told them about Hogarth’s idle and industrious apprentices, but they did not seem to think that the industrious apprentice was a very nice person.
因为埃雷洪派认为，纯粹的美德并不是一件可以无节制地沉迷的事情。我蒙指示看到不止一个案例，在这些案例中，父母真正的或假定的美德一直传到第三代和第四代的孩子身上。矫正者们说，对于美德来说，最真实的说法是，在很大程度上有利于它，而且总体来说，站在它一边比反对它要好得多。但他们认为，存在着许多虚假的美德，这很容易让人们在发现之前就陷入非常糟糕的境地。他们说，那些在恶行或美德方面都不引人注目的人是最优秀的。我给他们讲了霍加斯的那些游手好闲又勤劳的学徒，但他们似乎并不认为那个勤劳的学徒是一个很好的人。

CHAPTER XI: SOME EREWHONIAN TRIALS
第十一章：一些埃雷霍尼亚的审判

In Erewhon as in other countries there are some courts of justice that deal with special subjects. Misfortune generally, as I have above explained, is considered more or less criminal, but it admits of classification, and a court is assigned to each of the main heads under which it can be supposed to fall. Not very long after I had reached the capital I strolled into the Personal Bereavement Court, and was much both interested and pained by listening to the trial of a man who was accused of having just lost a wife to whom he had been tenderly attached, and who had left him with three little children, of whom the eldest was only three years old.
与其他国家一样，埃里洪也有一些法院处理特殊问题。正如我上面所解释的，一般来说，不幸或多或少被认为是犯罪，但它允许分类，并且为每个主要类别分配了一个法院，可以认为它属于这些类别。到达首都后不久，我漫步走进个人丧亲法庭，聆听对一名男子的审判，既感兴趣又痛苦，这名男子被指控刚刚失去了他一直深爱的妻子。他给他留下了三个小孩，其中最大的只有三岁。

The defence which the prisoner’s counsel endeavoured to establish was, that the prisoner had never really loved his wife; but it broke down completely, for the public prosecutor called witness after witness who deposed to the fact that the couple had been devoted to one another, and the prisoner repeatedly wept as incidents were put in evidence that reminded him of the irreparable nature of the loss he had sustained. The jury returned a verdict of guilty after very little deliberation, but recommended the prisoner to mercy on the ground that he had but recently insured his wife’s life for a considerable sum, and might be deemed lucky inasmuch as he had received the money without demur from the insurance company, though he had only paid two premiums.
囚犯律师极力提出的辩护是，囚犯从未真正爱过他的妻子；但它完全崩溃了，因为检察官传唤了一个又一个证人，证人证明了这对夫妇彼此忠诚，而囚犯在事件被作为证据时不断哭泣，提醒他损失的不可挽回性他坚持了下来。陪审团在没有经过深思熟虑后就做出了有罪判决，但建议囚犯宽大处理，理由是他最近才为妻子投了一笔相当大的生命保险，而且可能被认为是幸运的，因为他毫无异议地收到了这笔钱。保险公司，尽管他只支付了两笔保费。

I have just said that the jury found the prisoner guilty. When the judge passed sentence, I was struck with the way in which the prisoner’s counsel was rebuked for having referred to a work in which the guilt of such misfortunes as the prisoner’s was extenuated to a degree that roused the indignation of the court.
我刚才说过，陪审团判定犯人有罪。当法官宣判时，令我震惊的是，囚犯的律师因提及一部作品而受到谴责，在该作品中，囚犯所遭受的不幸的罪责被减轻到了引起法庭愤慨的程度。

‘We shall have,’ said the judge, ‘these crude and subversionary books from time to time until it is recognised as an axiom of morality that luck is the only fit object of human veneration. How far a man has any right to be more lucky and hence more venerable than his neighbours, is a point that always has been, and always will be, settled proximately by a kind of higgling and haggling of the market, and ultimately by brute force; but however this may be, it stands to reason that no man should be allowed to be unlucky to more than a very moderate extent.’
法官说：“我们将时不时地拥有这些粗俗和颠覆性的书籍，直到人们承认运气是人类崇拜的唯一合适的对象这一道德公理为止。”一个人在多大程度上有权利比他的邻居更幸运并因此更受人尊敬，这个问题始终是、也将永远是通过市场的讨价还价，并最终通过蛮力来解决的。 ;但无论情况如何，按理说，任何人都不应该允许超过一定程度的不幸。”

Then, turning to the prisoner, the judge continued:- ‘You have suffered a great loss. Nature attaches a severe penalty to such offences, and human law must emphasise the decrees of nature. But for the recommendation of the jury I should have given you six months’ hard labour. I will, however, commute your sentence to one of three months, with the option of a fine of twenty-five per cent. of the money you have received from the insurance company.’
然后，法官转向囚犯继续说道：“你遭受了巨大的损失。”大自然对此类罪行给予严厉的惩罚，人类的法律必须强调大自然的法令。要不是陪审团的推荐，我应该给你六个月的苦役。不过，我会将你的刑期减为三个月，并可以选择处以百分之二十五的罚款。您从保险公司收到的钱。

The prisoner thanked the judge, and said that as he had no one to look after his children if he was sent to prison, he would embrace the option mercifully permitted him by his lordship, and pay the sum he had named. He was then removed from the dock.
囚犯感谢法官，并表示，如果他被送进监狱，就没有人照顾他的孩子，他会接受勋爵大人仁慈地允许他的选择，并支付他指定的金额。随后他被带离被告席。

The next case was that of a youth barely arrived at man’s estate, who was charged with having been swindled out of large property during his minority by his guardian, who was also one of his nearest relations. His father had been long dead, and it was for this reason that his offence came on for trial in the Personal Bereavement Court. The lad, who was undefended, pleaded that he was young, inexperienced, greatly in awe of his guardian, and without independent professional advice. ‘Young man,’ said the judge sternly, ‘do not talk nonsense. People have no right to be young, inexperienced, greatly in awe of their guardians, and without independent professional advice. If by such indiscretions they outrage the moral sense of their friends, they must expect to suffer accordingly.’ He then ordered the prisoner to apologise to his guardian, and to receive twelve strokes with a cat-of-nine- tails.
下一个案件是一名刚刚抵达男子庄园的年轻人，他被指控在未成年时被他的监护人（也是他最亲近的亲戚之一）骗取了大笔财产。他的父亲早已去世，正因如此，他的罪行才在个人丧亲法庭接受审判。这名小伙子毫无防备，他辩称自己年轻、缺乏经验，对监护人非常敬畏，也没有得到独立的专业建议。 “年轻人，”法官严厉地说，“别胡说八道。”人们没有权利年轻、缺乏经验、对监护人充满敬畏，并且没有独立的专业建议。如果他们的轻率行为触犯了朋友的道德感，他们必然会受到相应的痛苦。”然后他命令囚犯向他的监护人道歉，并用九尾猫打十二下。

But I shall perhaps best convey to the reader an idea of the entire perversion of thought which exists among this extraordinary people, by describing the public trial of a man who was accused of pulmonary consumption—an offence which was punished with death until quite recently. It did not occur till I had been some months in the country, and I am deviating from chronological order in giving it here; but I had perhaps better do so in order that I may exhaust this subject before proceeding to others. Moreover I should never come to an end were I to keep to a strictly narrative form, and detail the infinite absurdities with which I daily came in contact.
但我也许应该通过描述对一名被指控患有肺结核的人的公开审判（直到最近才被判处死刑的罪行）的公开审判，向读者传达这一非凡人物中存在的整个思想扭曲的想法。直到我在乡下呆了几个月后，这件事才发生，而我在这里讲述它时偏离了时间顺序；但我也许最好这样做，以便在继续讨论其他主题之前先把这个主题讲完。此外，如果我坚持严格的叙述形式，并详细描述我每天接触到的无限荒谬的事情，我就永远不会结束。

The prisoner was placed in the dock, and the jury were sworn much as in Europe; almost all our own modes of procedure were reproduced, even to the requiring the prisoner to plead guilty or not guilty. He pleaded not guilty, and the case proceeded. The evidence for the prosecution was very strong; but I must do the court the justice to observe that the trial was absolutely impartial. Counsel for the prisoner was allowed to urge everything that could be said in his defence: the line taken was that the prisoner was simulating consumption in order to defraud an insurance company, from which he was about to buy an annuity, and that he hoped thus to obtain it on more advantageous terms. If this could have been shown to be the case he would have escaped a criminal prosecution, and been sent to a hospital as for a moral ailment. The view, however, was one which could not be reasonably sustained, in spite of all the ingenuity and eloquence of one of the most celebrated advocates of the country. The case was only too clear, for the prisoner was almost at the point of death, and it was astonishing that he had not been tried and convicted long previously. His coughing was incessant during the whole trial, and it was all that the two jailors in charge of him could do to keep him on his legs until it was over.
囚犯被送上被告席，陪审团像在欧洲一样宣誓。几乎所有我们自己的程序模式都被复制，甚至要求囚犯认罪或不认罪。他不认罪，案件继续审理。控方的证据非常有力；但我必须公正地对待法庭，确保审判绝对公正。犯人的律师被允许提出一切可以为他辩护的内容：采取的说法是，犯人正在模拟消费，以诈骗一家保险公司，他正要从该公司购买年金，他希望这样以更有利的条件获得它。如果事实确实如此，他就可以逃脱刑事起诉，并因精神疾病而被送往医院。然而，尽管该国最著名的倡导者之一具有独创性和雄辩能力，但这种观点是无法合理维持的。案情再清楚不过了，犯人已经快要死了，而且令人惊讶的是他早就没有受到审判和定罪。在整个审判过程中，他一直在咳嗽，看守他的两名狱卒也竭尽全力让他保持站立状态，直到审判结束。

The summing up of the judge was admirable. He dwelt upon every point that could be construed in favour of the prisoner, but as he proceeded it became clear that the evidence was too convincing to admit of doubt, and there was but one opinion in the court as to the impending verdict when the jury retired from the box. They were absent for about ten minutes, and on their return the foreman pronounced the prisoner guilty. There was a faint murmur of applause, but it was instantly repressed. The judge then proceeded to pronounce sentence in words which I can never forget, and which I copied out into a note-book next day from the report that was published in the leading newspaper. I must condense it somewhat, and nothing which I could say would give more than a faint idea of the solemn, not to say majestic, severity with which it was delivered. The sentence was as follows:-
法官的总结令人钦佩。他仔细考虑了每一个可以被解释为有利于囚犯的观点，但随着他的继续，很明显，证据太有说服力，不容怀疑，当陪审团做出裁决时，法庭上对于即将做出的判决只有一种意见。从盒子里退休了。他们缺席了大约十分钟，回来后工头宣布囚犯有罪。一阵轻微的掌声响起，但立刻就被压下去了。然后，法官用我永远不会忘记的话语宣判，第二天我把主要报纸上发表的报道抄到笔记本上。我必须把它稍微浓缩一下，我所能说的任何一句话都只能隐约地让人感受到它的庄严，更不用说庄严，严肃了。判决如下：-

‘Prisoner at the bar, you have been accused of the great crime of labouring under pulmonary consumption, and after an impartial trial before a jury of your countrymen, you have been found guilty. Against the justice of the verdict I can say nothing: the evidence against you was conclusive, and it only remains for me to pass such a sentence upon you, as shall satisfy the ends of the law. That sentence must be a very severe one. It pains me much to see one who is yet so young, and whose prospects in life were otherwise so excellent, brought to this distressing condition by a constitution which I can only regard as radically vicious; but yours is no case for compassion: this is not your first offence: you have led a career of crime, and have only profited by the leniency shown you upon past occasions, to offend yet more seriously against the laws and institutions of your country. You were convicted of aggravated bronchitis last year: and I find that though you are now only twenty-three years old, you have been imprisoned on no less than fourteen occasions for illnesses of a more or less hateful character; in fact, it is not too much to say that you have spent the greater part of your life in a jail.
‘酒吧里的囚犯，你被指控犯有肺消耗劳动的重罪，经过你的同胞陪审团的公正审判，你被判有罪。对于判决的公正性，我无话可说：对你不利的证据是确凿的，我只需对你作出这样的判决，以满足法律的目的。这句话一定是非常严厉的。看到一个如此年轻的人，原本生活前景如此美好的人，却被一种我只能认为是极其邪恶的体质导致了这种令人痛苦的境地，我感到非常痛苦。但你的行为不值得同情：这不是你的第一次犯罪：你领导了犯罪生涯，并且只是从过去对你表现出的宽大处理中获利，更严重地违反了你的国家的法律和制度。去年你因严重支气管炎被判有罪：我发现，尽管你现在只有二十三岁，但你已经因或多或少可恶的疾病而被监禁了不下十四次；事实上，说你一生的大部分时间都是在监狱里度过的，并不过分。

‘It is all very well for you to say that you came of unhealthy parents, and had a severe accident in your childhood which permanently undermined your constitution; excuses such as these are the ordinary refuge of the criminal; but they cannot for one moment be listened to by the ear of justice. I am not here to enter upon curious metaphysical questions as to the origin of this or that— questions to which there would be no end were their introduction once tolerated, and which would result in throwing the only guilt on the tissues of the primordial cell, or on the elementary gases. There is no question of how you came to be wicked, but only this— namely, are you wicked or not? This has been decided in the affirmative, neither can I hesitate for a single moment to say that it has been decided justly. You are a bad and dangerous person, and stand branded in the eyes of your fellow-countrymen with one of the most heinous known offences.
“你可以这么说，你的父母身体不好，童年时遭遇过一场严重的事故，永久损害了你的体质；诸如此类的借口是罪犯通常的避难所；但正义的耳朵一刻也听不到他们的声音。我来这里并不是要讨论关于这个或那个的起源的好奇的形而上学问题——如果它们的引入一旦被容忍，这些问题将没有尽头，并且这将导致将唯一的罪责加在原始细胞的组织上，或基本气体。不问你是怎么邪恶的，只有一个问题，就是你邪恶不邪恶？这是肯定的决定，我也毫不犹豫地说，这是公正的决定。你是一个坏人和危险的人，在你的同胞眼中被打上了已知的最令人发指的罪行之一的烙印。

‘It is not my business to justify the law: the law may in some cases have its inevitable hardships, and I may feel regret at times that I have not the option of passing a less severe sentence than I am compelled to do. But yours is no such case; on the contrary, had not the capital punishment for consumption been abolished, I should certainly inflict it now.
“为法律辩护不是我的事：法律在某些情况下可能有其不可避免的困难，有时我可能会感到遗憾，因为我无法选择比我被迫做的更轻的判决。但你的情况并非如此；相反，如果消费的死刑没有被废除，我现在肯定应该判处它。

‘It is intolerable that an example of such terrible enormity should be allowed to go at large unpunished. Your presence in the society of respectable people would lead the less able-bodied to think more lightly of all forms of illness; neither can it be permitted that you should have the chance of corrupting unborn beings who might hereafter pester you. The unborn must not be allowed to come near you: and this not so much for their protection (for they are our natural enemies), as for our own; for since they will not be utterly gainsaid, it must be seen to that they shall be quartered upon those who are least likely to corrupt them.
“令人无法容忍的是，如此可怕的罪行却逍遥法外而不受惩罚。你出现在受人尊敬的社会中，会让身体较弱的人更加轻视各种形式的疾病；也不能让你有机会败坏未来可能困扰你的未出生的众生。绝对不允许未出生的孩子靠近你：这与其说是为了保护他们（因为他们是我们的天敌），不如说是为了我们自己；因为既然他们不会被完全否定，那么就必须注意，他们将被分到那些最不可能腐蚀他们的人身上。

‘But independently of this consideration, and independently of the physical guilt which attaches itself to a crime so great as yours, there is yet another reason why we should be unable to show you mercy, even if we were inclined to do so. I refer to the existence of a class of men who lie hidden among us, and who are called physicians. Were the severity of the law or the current feeling of the country to be relaxed never so slightly, these abandoned persons, who are now compelled to practise secretly and who can be consulted only at the greatest risk, would become frequent visitors in every household; their organisation and their intimate acquaintance with all family secrets would give them a power, both social and political, which nothing could resist. The head of the household would become subordinate to the family doctor, who would interfere between man and wife, between master and servant, until the doctors should be the only depositaries of power in the nation, and have all that we hold precious at their mercy. A time of universal dephysicalisation would ensue; medicine-vendors of all kinds would abound in our streets and advertise in all our newspapers. There is one remedy for this, and one only. It is that which the laws of this country have long received and acted upon, and consists in the sternest repression of all diseases whatsoever, as soon as their existence is made manifest to the eye of the law. Would that that eye were far more piercing than it is.
“但是，抛开这种考虑，抛开像你这样严重的罪行所带来的身体罪责，还有另一个原因说明我们不能对你表示怜悯，即使我们愿意这样做。我指的是隐藏在我们中间的一类人的存在，他们被称为医生。如果法律的严厉性或者国家目前的情绪能够稍微放松一些，那么这些被迫秘密行医、只有在冒着最大风险才能得到咨询的被遗弃者就会成为家家户户的常客。他们的组织以及对所有家庭秘密的熟悉将赋予他们一种任何人都无法抗拒的社会和政治权力。一家之主将成为家庭医生的下属，家庭医生会干涉夫妻之间、主仆之间，直到医生成为国家唯一的权力保管者，我们所珍视的一切都由他们摆布。 。一个普遍的非物质化时代将会随之而来。各种各样的药品供应商在我们的街道上随处可见，并在我们所有的报纸上做广告。对此有一种补救办法，而且只有一种。这是这个国家的法律长期以来所接受和执行的法律，它包括对所有疾病的最严厉镇压，只要它们的存在在法律上得到体现。如果那双眼睛比现在更加锐利就好了。

‘But I will enlarge no further upon things that are themselves so obvious. You may say that it is not your fault. The answer is ready enough at hand, and it amounts to this—that if you had been born of healthy and well-to-do parents, and been well taken care of when you were a child, you would never have offended against the laws of your country, nor found yourself in your present disgraceful position. If you tell me that you had no hand in your parentage and education, and that it is therefore unjust to lay these things to your charge, I answer that whether your being in a consumption is your fault or no, it is a fault in you, and it is my duty to see that against such faults as this the commonwealth shall be protected. You may say that it is your misfortune to be criminal; I answer that it is your crime to be unfortunate.
“但我不会进一步阐述那些本身如此明显的事情。你可能会说这不是你的错。答案已经唾手可得，大致就是这样的——如果你出生于健康富裕的父母，并且在你还是个孩子的时候受到很好的照顾，你就永远不会触犯法律。你的国家，也没有发现自己处于目前不光彩的境地。如果你告诉我，你的出身和教育与你无关，因此将这些事情归咎于你是不公正的，我的回答是，无论你是否患有肺病，都是你的错，这都是你的错。 ，我有责任确保联邦免受此类过失的侵害。你可能会说，犯罪是你的不幸；我的回答是，你的不幸就是你的罪过。

‘Lastly, I should point out that even though the jury had acquitted you—a supposition that I cannot seriously entertain—I should have felt it my duty to inflict a sentence hardly less severe than that which I must pass at present; for the more you had been found guiltless of the crime imputed to you, the more you would have been found guilty of one hardly less heinous—I mean the crime of having been maligned unjustly.
“最后，我应该指出，即使陪审团宣判你无罪——我不能认真考虑这一假设——我应该感到有责任判处比我目前必须通过的判决更严厉的判决；因为你越是被判无罪，你就越会被判犯有同样令人发指的罪行——我指的是受到不公正的诽谤。

‘I do not hesitate therefore to sentence you to imprisonment, with hard labour, for the rest of your miserable existence. During that period I would earnestly entreat you to repent of the wrongs you have done already, and to entirely reform the constitution of your whole body. I entertain but little hope that you will pay attention to my advice; you are already far too abandoned. Did it rest with myself, I should add nothing in mitigation of the sentence which I have passed, but it is the merciful provision of the law that even the most hardened criminal shall be allowed some one of the three official remedies, which is to be prescribed at the time of his conviction. I shall therefore order that you receive two tablespoonfuls of castor oil daily, until the pleasure of the court be further known.’
“因此，我毫不犹豫地判你入狱，并进行苦役，度过你悲惨的余生。在此期间我恳切地恳请你们悔改自己已经犯下的错误，彻底改造你们整个身体的体质。我不太希望你会注意我的建议；你已经被抛弃太多了。如果我自己决定的话，我不应该在减轻我已经通过的判决方面添加任何内容，但法律的仁慈规定是，即使是最顽固的罪犯也应被允许采取三种官方补救措施中的一种，即在他被定罪时规定的。因此，我将命令您每天接受两汤匙蓖麻油，直到法庭进一步了解为止。

When the sentence was concluded the prisoner acknowledged in a few scarcely audible words that he was justly punished, and that he had had a fair trial. He was then removed to the prison from which he was never to return. There was a second attempt at applause when the judge had finished speaking, but as before it was at once repressed; and though the feeling of the court was strongly against the prisoner, there was no show of any violence against him, if one may except a little hooting from the bystanders when he was being removed in the prisoners’ van. Indeed, nothing struck me more during my whole sojourn in the country, than the general respect for law and order.
判决结束后，囚犯用几句话几乎听不见的声音承认，他受到了公正的惩罚，他受到了公正的审判。然后他被转移到监狱，再也没有回来过。法官讲完后，有人再次鼓掌，但和之前一样，掌声立即被压制住了。尽管法庭对囚犯的态度是强烈反对的，但除了当他被押上囚犯的货车时，旁观者发出了一点小叫声之外，没有表现出任何针对他的暴力行为。事实上，在这个国家的整个逗留期间，没有什么比对法律和秩序的普遍尊重更让我印象深刻的了。

CHAPTER XII: MALCONTENTS
第十二章：恶意内容

I confess that I felt rather unhappy when I got home, and thought more closely over the trial that I had just witnessed. For the time I was carried away by the opinion of those among whom I was. They had no misgivings about what they were doing. There did not seem to be a person in the whole court who had the smallest doubt but that all was exactly as it should be. This universal unsuspecting confidence was imparted by sympathy to myself, in spite of all my training in opinions so widely different. So it is with most of us: that which we observe to be taken as a matter of course by those around us, we take as a matter of course ourselves. And after all, it is our duty to do this, save upon grave occasion.
我承认，当我回到家时，我感到相当不高兴，并且更加仔细地思考了我刚刚目睹的审判。有一段时间，我被那些与我同在的人的意见所左右。他们对自己所做的事情没有任何疑虑。整个朝廷里似乎没有一个人有半点怀疑，但一切都是理所应当的。这种普遍的、毫无戒心的信心是由对我自己的同情所赋予的，尽管我所受的训练所持的观点差异如此之大。我们大多数人都是如此：我们观察到周围人认为理所当然的事情，我们自己也认为是理所当然的。毕竟，除非有特殊情况，否则我们有责任这样做。

But when I was alone, and began to think the trial over, it certainly did strike me as betraying a strange and untenable position. Had the judge said that he acknowledged the probable truth, namely, that the prisoner was born of unhealthy parents, or had been starved in infancy, or had met with some accidents which had developed consumption; and had he then gone on to say that though he knew all this, and bitterly regretted that the protection of society obliged him to inflict additional pain on one who had suffered so much already, yet that there was no help for it, I could have understood the position, however mistaken I might have thought it. The judge was fully persuaded that the infliction of pain upon the weak and sickly was the only means of preventing weakness and sickliness from spreading, and that ten times the suffering now inflicted upon the accused was eventually warded off from others by the present apparent severity. I could therefore perfectly understand his inflicting whatever pain he might consider necessary in order to prevent so bad an example from spreading further and lowering the Erewhonian standard; but it seemed almost childish to tell the prisoner that he could have been in good health, if he had been more fortunate in his constitution, and been exposed to less hardships when he was a boy.
但当我独自一人并开始思考审判时，我确实觉得它背叛了一种奇怪且站不住脚的立场。如果法官说他承认可能的事实，即囚犯是由不健康的父母所生，或者在婴儿时期挨饿过，或者遇到了一些事故而发展为肺病，那么他是否承认了这一事实？如果他接着说，尽管他知道这一切，并且对社会的保护迫使他对一个已经遭受了如此多痛苦的人施加额外的痛苦而深感遗憾，但又没有任何帮助，我可以理解这个立场，无论我的想法多么错误。法官完全相信，对弱者和病人施加痛苦是防止虚弱和疾病蔓延的唯一方法，而现在对被告造成的十倍的痛苦最终通过目前明显的严厉程度而避免了其他人的痛苦。因此，我完全可以理解他会造成他认为必要的任何痛苦，以防止如此糟糕的例子进一步蔓延并降低埃雷洪尼亚的标准；但是告诉囚犯，如果他的体质比较幸运，并且在他还是个孩子的时候受到较少的苦难，他本来可以身体健康，这似乎有点幼稚。

I write with great diffidence, but it seems to me that there is no unfairness in punishing people for their misfortunes, or rewarding them for their sheer good luck: it is the normal condition of human life that this should be done, and no right-minded person will complain of being subjected to the common treatment. There is no alternative open to us. It is idle to say that men are not responsible for their misfortunes. What is responsibility? Surely to be responsible means to be liable to have to give an answer should it be demanded, and all things which live are responsible for their lives and actions should society see fit to question them through the mouth of its authorised agent.
我怀着极大的信心写下这篇文章，但在我看来，惩罚人们的不幸，或奖励他们的纯粹好运并没有什么不公平：这是人类生活的正常状况，应该这样做，没有权利——有头脑的人会抱怨受到普通待遇。我们别无选择。说男人不对自己的不幸负责是毫无意义的。什么是责任？当然，负责任意味着如果有人要求的话，有责任必须给出答案，并且如果社会认为适合通过其授权代理人的嘴提出质疑，所有生物都对其生命和行为负责。

What is the offence of a lamb that we should rear it, and tend it, and lull it into security, for the express purpose of killing it? Its offence is the misfortune of being something which society wants to eat, and which cannot defend itself. This is ample. Who shall limit the right of society except society itself? And what consideration for the individual is tolerable unless society be the gainer thereby? Wherefore should a man be so richly rewarded for having been son to a millionaire, were it not clearly provable that the common welfare is thus better furthered? We cannot seriously detract from a man’s merit in having been the son of a rich father without imperilling our own tenure of things which we do not wish to jeopardise; if this were otherwise we should not let him keep his money for a single hour; we would have it ourselves at once. For property is robbery, but then, we are all robbers or would-be robbers together, and have found it essential to organise our thieving, as we have found it necessary to organise our lust and our revenge. Property, marriage, the law; as the bed to the river, so rule and convention to the instinct; and woe to him who tampers with the banks while the flood is flowing.
我们养育一只羔羊，照料它，安抚它，使其处于安全状态，而只是为了杀死它，这有什么罪过呢？它的罪行是不幸地成为社会想要吃的东西，却无法保卫自己。这已经足够了。除了社会本身之外谁能限制社会的权利？除非社会因此成为受益者，否则对个人的什么考虑是可以容忍的？如果一个人是百万富翁的儿子，为什么会得到如此丰厚的回报，如果没有清楚地证明公共福利因此得到了更好的促进呢？我们不能严重贬低一个人作为一个富有父亲的儿子的优点，而不危及我们自己所不想危及的事物的保有权；如果不是这样，我们就不应该让他把钱保留一个小时；我们自己马上就能得到它。因为财产就是抢劫，但是，我们都是强盗或潜在的强盗，并且发现有必要组织我们的盗窃行为，就像我们发现有必要组织我们的欲望和复仇一样。财产、婚姻、法律；正如河床之于河床，规则与习俗之于本能；洪水泛滥时擅自破坏堤岸的人有祸了。

But to return. Even in England a man on board a ship with yellow fever is held responsible for his mischance, no matter what his being kept in quarantine may cost him. He may catch the fever and die; we cannot help it; he must take his chance as other people do; but surely it would be desperate unkindness to add contumely to our self-protection, unless, indeed, we believe that contumely is one of our best means of self-protection. Again, take the case of maniacs. We say that they are irresponsible for their actions, but we take good care, or ought to take good care, that they shall answer to us for their insanity, and we imprison them in what we call an asylum (that modern sanctuary!) if we do not like their answers. This is a strange kind of irresponsibility. What we ought to say is that we can afford to be satisfied with a less satisfactory answer from a lunatic than from one who is not mad, because lunacy is less infectious than crime.
但要回来。即使在英国，船上患有黄热病的男子也要对自己的不幸负责，无论他被隔离可能会付出什么代价。他可能会发烧而死；我们无能为力；他必须像其他人一样抓住机会；但是，如果我们确实认为侮辱是我们最好的自我保护手段之一，那么如果我们确实认为侮辱是我们最好的自我保护手段之一，那么在我们的自我保护中加入侮辱无疑是极其不仁慈的。再次以疯子为例。我们说他们对自己的行为不负责任，但我们会好好照顾，或者应该好好照顾，让他们为自己的疯狂行为向我们负责，并且我们将他们囚禁在我们所谓的庇护所（现代避难所！）中，如果我们不喜欢他们的答案。这是一种奇怪的不负责任。我们应该说的是，我们可以接受一个疯子的回答，而不是一个没有疯子的回答，因为疯子的传染性比犯罪小。

We kill a serpent if we go in danger by it, simply for being such and such a serpent in such and such a place; but we never say that the serpent has only itself to blame for not having been a harmless creature. Its crime is that of being the thing which it is: but this is a capital offence, and we are right in killing it out of the way, unless we think it more danger to do so than to let it escape; nevertheless we pity the creature, even though we kill it.
如果我们遇到危险，我们就会杀死一条蛇，仅仅因为在某个地方是这样那样的蛇；但我们从来没有说蛇不是无害的生物，这只能归咎于它自己。它的罪行在于它本来就是这样的东西：但这是一种死罪，我们把它杀掉是正确的，除非我们认为这样做比让它逃跑更危险；尽管如此，我们还是怜悯这个生物，尽管我们杀死了它。

But in the case of him whose trial I have described above, it was impossible that any one in the court should not have known that it was but by an accident of birth and circumstances that he was not himself also in a consumption; and yet none thought that it disgraced them to hear the judge give vent to the most cruel truisms about him. The judge himself was a kind and thoughtful person. He was a man of magnificent and benign presence. He was evidently of an iron constitution, and his face wore an expression of the maturest wisdom and experience; yet for all this, old and learned as he was, he could not see things which one would have thought would have been apparent even to a child. He could not emancipate himself from, nay, it did not even occur to him to feel, the bondage of the ideas in which he had been born and bred.
但就我上面所描述的对他的审判而言，法庭上的任何人都不可能不知道，他本人也患有肺痨病，这只是由于出生和环境的意外。然而，没有人认为听到法官说出有关他的最残酷的老话是让他们感到羞耻的。法官本人是一个善良、体贴的人。他是一个气度高尚、和蔼可亲的人。他的体格显然是钢铁般的，脸上带着最成熟的智慧和经验的表情。然而，尽管如此，尽管他年纪大了，学识渊博，但他却看不到人们认为即使是一个孩子也会明白的事情。他无法将自己从他出生和成长的观念的束缚中解放出来，不，他甚至没有想到去感受。

So was it also with the jury and bystanders; and—most wonderful of all—so was it even with the prisoner. Throughout he seemed fully impressed with the notion that he was being dealt with justly: he saw nothing wanton in his being told by the judge that he was to be punished, not so much as a necessary protection to society (although this was not entirely lost sight of), as because he had not been better born and bred than he was. But this led me to hope that he suffered less than he would have done if he had seen the matter in the same light that I did. And, after all, justice is relative.
陪审团和旁观者也是如此。而且——最美妙的是——即使是囚犯也是如此。在整个过程中，他似乎对自己受到公正对待的想法印象深刻：他认为法官告诉他要受到惩罚并没有任何肆意的地方，而不是对社会的必要保护（尽管这并没有完全丧失）看到），因为他没有比他更好的出生和教养。但这让我希望，如果他以与我相同的眼光看待这件事，他所遭受的痛苦会比他所承受的要少。毕竟，正义是相对的。

I may here mention that only a few years before my arrival in the country, the treatment of all convicted invalids had been much more barbarous than now, for no physical remedy was provided, and prisoners were put to the severest labour in all sorts of weather, so that most of them soon succumbed to the extreme hardships which they suffered; this was supposed to be beneficial in some ways, inasmuch as it put the country to less expense for the maintenance of its criminal class; but the growth of luxury had induced a relaxation of the old severity, and a sensitive age would no longer tolerate what appeared to be an excess of rigour, even towards the most guilty; moreover, it was found that juries were less willing to convict, and justice was often cheated because there was no alternative between virtually condemning a man to death and letting him go free; it was also held that the country paid in recommittals for its over-severity; for those who had been imprisoned even for trifling ailments were often permanently disabled by their imprisonment; and when a man had been once convicted, it was probable that he would seldom afterwards be off the hands of the country.
我可以在这里提到，就在我到达这个国家的前几年，所有被定罪的残疾人所受到的待遇比现在要野蛮得多，因为没有提供任何物理治疗，囚犯在各种天气条件下都被投入最艰苦的劳动。 ，因此他们中的大多数人很快就屈服于所遭受的极端苦难；这在某些方面被认为是有益的，因为它可以减少国家维持犯罪阶层的开支；但奢侈的增长导致了旧有严厉的放松，敏感的时代不再容忍看似过度的严格，即使是对最有罪的人也是如此。此外，人们发现，陪审团不太愿意定罪，正义常常受到欺骗，因为除了实际上判处一个人死刑和释放他之外，别无选择；还认为该国因其过分严重的行为而付出了重新承诺的代价；因为那些即使是因为小病而被监禁的人也常常因监禁而永久残疾；一个人一旦被定罪，很可能此后就很少会脱离国家的控制。

These evils had long been apparent and recognised; yet people were too indolent, and too indifferent to suffering not their own, to bestir themselves about putting an end to them, until at last a benevolent reformer devoted his whole life to effecting the necessary changes. He divided all illnesses into three classes— those affecting the head, the trunk, and the lower limbs—and obtained an enactment that all diseases of the head, whether internal or external, should be treated with laudanum, those of the body with castor-oil, and those of the lower limbs with an embrocation of strong sulphuric acid and water.
这些罪恶早已显而易见并为人们所认识。然而，人们太懒惰，对不属于他们自己的苦难太漠不关心，以至于没有鼓起勇气去结束它们，直到最后一位仁慈的改革者毕生致力于实现必要的改变。他把所有的疾病分为三类——影响头部、躯干和下肢的疾病——并制定了一个规定：所有头部的疾病，无论是内部的还是外部的，都应该用鸦片酊治疗，身体的疾病应该用蓖麻子治疗。油，下肢用浓硫酸和水擦洗。

It may be said that the classification was not sufficiently careful, and that the remedies were ill chosen; but it is a hard thing to initiate any reform, and it was necessary to familiarise the public mind with the principle, by inserting the thin end of the wedge first: it is not, therefore, to be wondered at that among so practical a people there should still be some room for improvement. The mass of the nation are well pleased with existing arrangements, and believe that their treatment of criminals leaves little or nothing to be desired; but there is an energetic minority who hold what are considered to be extreme opinions, and who are not at all disposed to rest contented until the principle lately admitted has been carried further.
可以说分类不够仔细，补救措施选择不当；但发起任何改革都是一件困难的事情，有必要通过首先插入楔子的细端来让公众熟悉这一原则：因此，在如此务实的人民中，这一点并不奇怪。应该还有一些改进的空间。全国人民对现有的安排感到非常满意，并相信他们对罪犯的对待几乎没有什么可改进的地方；但是，也有一小部分精力充沛的人持有被认为是极端的观点，并且在最近承认的原则得到进一步贯彻之前，他们根本不会满足。

I was at some pains to discover the opinions of these men, and their reasons for entertaining them. They are held in great odium by the generality of the public, and are considered as subverters of all morality whatever. The malcontents, on the other hand, assert that illness is the inevitable result of certain antecedent causes, which, in the great majority of cases, were beyond the control of the individual, and that therefore a man is only guilty for being in a consumption in the same way as rotten fruit is guilty for having gone rotten. True, the fruit must be thrown on one side as unfit for man’s use, and the man in a consumption must be put in prison for the protection of his fellow-citizens; but these radicals would not punish him further than by loss of liberty and a strict surveillance. So long as he was prevented from injuring society, they would allow him to make himself useful by supplying whatever of society’s wants he could supply. If he succeeded in thus earning money, they would have him made as comfortable in prison as possible, and would in no way interfere with his liberty more than was necessary to prevent him from escaping, or from becoming more severely indisposed within the prison walls; but they would deduct from his earnings the expenses of his board, lodging, surveillance, and half those of his conviction. If he was too ill to do anything for his support in prison, they would allow him nothing but bread and water, and very little of that.
我煞费苦心地想了解这些人的观点，以及他们招待他们的理由。他们受到公众的极大厌恶，并被认为是所有道德的颠覆者。另一方面，不满者则断言，疾病是某些先因的不可避免的结果，而在大多数情况下，这些先因是个人无法控制的，因此，一个人只有在患有肺病时才有罪。就像腐烂的水果因腐烂而有罪一样。诚然，这些水果必须被扔到一边，因为不适合人类使用，而为了保护他的同胞，患有肺病的人必须被关进监狱。但这些激进分子除了失去自由和严格监视之外不会对他进行进一步的惩罚。只要他不伤害社会，他们就会允许他通过满足社会的任何需求来使自己变得有用。如果他成功地赚到了钱，他们就会让他在监狱里过得尽可能舒服，并且不会以任何方式干涉他的自由，除非有必要阻止他越狱，或者防止他在监狱围墙内变得更加严重。但他们会从他的收入中扣除他的食宿、监视费用以及他定罪费用的一半。如果他病得太重，无法在监狱里做任何事情来维持生活，他们只会给他面包和水，而且很少。

They say that society is foolish in refusing to allow itself to be benefited by a man merely because he has done it harm hitherto, and that objection to the labour of the diseased classes is only protection in another form. It is an attempt to raise the natural price of a commodity by saying that such and such persons, who are able and willing to produce it, shall not do so, whereby every one has to pay more for it.
他们说，社会愚蠢地拒绝让自己受益于一个人，仅仅因为他迄今为止对社会造成了伤害，而反对病态阶级的劳动只是另一种形式的保护。它试图通过规定有能力并愿意生产该商品的人不得生产该商品，从而提高商品的自然价格，从而使每个人都必须为此付出更多的代价。

Besides, so long as a man has not been actually killed he is our fellow-creature, though perhaps a very unpleasant one. It is in a great degree the doing of others that he is what he is, or in other words, the society which now condemns him is partly answerable concerning him. They say that there is no fear of any increase of disease under these circumstances; for the loss of liberty, the surveillance, the considerable and compulsory deduction from the prisoner’s earnings, the very sparing use of stimulants (of which they would allow but little to any, and none to those who did not earn them), the enforced celibacy, and above all, the loss of reputation among friends, are in their opinion as ample safeguards to society against a general neglect of health as those now resorted to.
