A man, therefore, (so they say) should carry his profession or trade into prison with him if possible; if not, he must earn his living by the nearest thing to it that he can; but if he be a gentleman born and bred to no profession, he must pick oakum, or write art criticisms for a newspaper.
此外，只要一个人没有被真正杀死，他就是我们的同胞，尽管这可能是一个非常令人不愉快的同胞。在很大程度上，他之所以成为现在的他，是因为别人的所作所为，或者换句话说，现在谴责他的社会对他负有部分责任。他们说，在这种情况下，不必担心疾病会增加；失去自由、监视、从囚犯的收入中强制扣除大量费用、极少使用兴奋剂（他们只允许任何人使用兴奋剂，对于那些没有获得兴奋剂的人则不允许使用）、强迫独身最重要的是，在他们看来，在朋友中名誉的损失是社会防止普遍忽视健康的充分保障，就像现在所采取的那样。因此，（人们这么说）一个人如果可能的话，应该把他的职业或行业带进监狱。如果没有，他就必须靠尽可能接近的东西来谋生。但如果他是一位天生无业的绅士，他就必须选择奥库姆，或者为报纸撰写艺术评论。

These people say further, that the greater part of the illness which exists in their country is brought about by the insane manner in which it is treated.
这些人进一步说，他们国家存在的大部分疾病都是由疯狂的治疗方式造成的。

They believe that illness is in many cases just as curable as the moral diseases which they see daily cured around them, but that a great reform is impossible till men learn to take a juster view of what physical obliquity proceeds from. Men will hide their illnesses as long as they are scouted on its becoming known that they are ill; it is the scouting, not the physic, which produces the concealment; and if a man felt that the news of his being in ill-health would be received by his neighbours as a deplorable fact, but one as much the result of necessary antecedent causes as though he had broken into a jeweller’s shop and stolen a valuable diamond necklace—as a fact which might just as easily have happened to themselves, only that they had the luck to be better born or reared; and if they also felt that they would not be made more uncomfortable in the prison than the protection of society against infection and the proper treatment of their own disease actually demanded, men would give themselves up to the police as readily on perceiving that they had taken small-pox, as they go now to the straightener when they feel that they are on the point of forging a will, or running away with somebody else’s wife.
他们相信，在许多情况下，疾病就像他们周围每天看到的道德疾病一样可以治愈，但除非人们学会更公正地看待身体倾斜的根源，否则伟大的改革是不可能的。只要人们发现自己有病，人们就会隐藏自己的疾病。产生隐蔽的是侦察，而不是物理；如果一个人认为他健康状况不佳的消息会被邻居视为可悲的事实，但这就像他闯入珠宝店并偷走了一颗珍贵的钻石一样是必要的先因原因的结果项链——这一事实很可能发生在他们自己身上，只是他们有幸出生或成长得更好；如果他们还认为，他们在监狱里不会比保护社会免受感染和适当治疗自己的疾病实际上需要的更不舒服，那么男人在意识到他们已经采取了行动时，也会很容易地向警察投案自首。天花，当他们觉得自己即将立下遗嘱，或者与别人的妻子私奔时，他们就会去矫正。

But the main argument on which they rely is that of economy: for they know that they will sooner gain their end by appealing to men’s pockets, in which they have generally something of their own, than to their heads, which contain for the most part little but borrowed or stolen property; and also, they believe it to be the readiest test and the one which has most to show for itself. If a course of conduct can be shown to cost a country less, and this by no dishonourable saving and with no indirectly increased expenditure in other ways, they hold that it requires a good deal to upset the arguments in favour of its being adopted, and whether rightly or wrongly I cannot pretend to say, they think that the more medicinal and humane treatment of the diseased of which they are the advocates would in the long run be much cheaper to the country: but I did not gather that these reformers were opposed to meeting some of the more violent forms of illness with the cat-of- nine-tails, or with death; for they saw no so effectual way of checking them; they would therefore both flog and hang, but they would do so pitifully.
但他们所依赖的主要论据是经济论据：因为他们知道，通过诉诸人们的口袋，他们通常拥有自己的东西，而不是诉诸他们的头脑，他们会更快地达到目的，而头脑中的大部分内容都包含着自己的东西。除了借来或偷来的财产外，几乎没有什么；而且，他们相信这是最容易进行的测试，也是最能展示其本身的测试。如果一项行为可以证明可以减少一个国家的成本，并且没有不光彩的储蓄，也没有以其他方式间接增加支出，那么他们认为需要做很多事情来推翻支持其被采用的论点，并且无论正确还是错误，我都不能假装说，他们认为，从长远来看，他们所倡导的对病人进行更加医学和人道的治疗对国家来说会便宜得多：但我没有想到这些改革者会反对用九尾猫或死亡来应对一些更严重的疾病；因为他们没有看到如此有效的方法来检查他们。因此，他们要么被鞭打，要么被绞死，但他们这样做的方式很可怜。

I have perhaps dwelt too long upon opinions which can have no possible bearing upon our own, but I have not said the tenth part of what these would-be reformers urged upon me. I feel, however, that I have sufficiently trespassed upon the attention of the reader.
也许我在那些可能与我们自己的观点没有任何关系的观点上讨论得太久了，但我还没有说出这些潜在的改革者敦促我的内容的第十部分。然而，我觉得我已经充分地侵犯了读者的注意力。

CHAPTER XIII: THE VIEWS OF THE EREWHONIANS CONCERNING DEATH
第十三章：埃雷霍尼安派关于死亡的观点

The Erewhonians regard death with less abhorrence than disease. If it is an offence at all, it is one beyond the reach of the law, which is therefore silent on the subject; but they insist that the greater number of those who are commonly said to die, have never yet been born—not, at least, into that unseen world which is alone worthy of consideration. As regards this unseen world I understand them to say that some miscarry in respect to it before they have even reached the seen, and some after, while few are ever truly born into it at all—the greater part of all the men and women over the whole country miscarrying before they reach it. And they say that this does not matter so much as we think it does.
埃雷洪人对死亡的憎恶程度远低于对疾病的憎恶程度。如果这确实构成犯罪，那么它就超出了法律的管辖范围，因此法律对这个问题保持沉默；但他们坚持认为，大多数通常所说的死亡者实际上还没有出生——至少没有出生到那个单独值得考虑的看不见的世界。至于这个看不见的世界，我理解他们的意思是，有些人甚至在到达看得见的世界之前就流产了，有些人则在到达看得见的世界之前就流产了，而很少有人真正出生在这个世界上——大多数男人和女人都出生在这个世界上。整个国家在到达之前就流产了。他们说这并不像我们想象的那么重要。

As for what we call death, they argue that too much has been made of it. The mere knowledge that we shall one day die does not make us very unhappy; no one thinks that he or she will escape, so that none are disappointed. We do not care greatly even though we know that we have not long to live; the only thing that would seriously affect us would be the knowing—or rather thinking that we know— the precise moment at which the blow will fall. Happily no one can ever certainly know this, though many try to make themselves miserable by endeavouring to find it out. It seems as though there were some power somewhere which mercifully stays us from putting that sting into the tail of death, which we would put there if we could, and which ensures that though death must always be a bugbear, it shall never under any conceivable circumstances be more than a bugbear.
至于我们所谓的死亡，他们认为人们对它的理解太多了。仅仅知道我们有一天会死去并不会让我们感到非常不快乐；相反，我们会感到高兴。没有人认为他或她会逃脱，因此没有人感到失望。尽管我们知道自己的寿命不长，但我们并不在意；唯一会严重影响我们的事情就是知道——或者更确切地说，认为我们知道——打击将会发生的确切时刻。值得庆幸的是，没有人能够确切地知道这一点，尽管许多人试图通过努力找出这一点而让自己感到痛苦。似乎有某种力量仁慈地阻止我们将那刺刺入死亡的尾巴，如果可以的话，我们会把它放在那里，并确保尽管死亡总是令人烦恼，但它永远不会在任何可以想象的情况下发生。情况不仅仅是令人烦恼的。

For even though a man is condemned to die in a week’s time and is shut up in a prison from which it is certain that he cannot escape, he will always hope that a reprieve may come before the week is over. Besides, the prison may catch fire, and he may be suffocated not with a rope, but with common ordinary smoke; or he may be struck dead by lightning while exercising in the prison yards. When the morning is come on which the poor wretch is to be hanged, he may choke at his breakfast, or die from failure of the heart’s action before the drop has fallen; and even though it has fallen, he cannot be quite certain that he is going to die, for he cannot know this till his death has actually taken place, and it will be too late then for him to discover that he was going to die at the appointed hour after all. The Erewhonians, therefore, hold that death, like life, is an affair of being more frightened than hurt.
因为，即使一个人被判处一周后死亡，并被关在监狱里，他肯定无法逃脱，但他总是希望在一周结束之前能得到缓刑。此外，监狱可能着火，他可能不是被绳子，而是被普通的烟雾窒息；或者他可能在监狱院子里锻炼时被闪电击中身亡。当这个可怜的可怜人被绞死的早晨来临的时候，他可能会被早餐噎住，或者在水滴落下之前因心脏衰竭而死亡。即使它已经掉下来，他也不能完全确定自己会死，因为直到他的死亡真正发生之前他无法知道这一点，而那时他发现自己将要死的时候就为时已晚了。毕竟是约定的时间。因此，埃雷洪主义者认为，死亡就像生命一样，是一种更多的恐惧而不是伤害。

They burn their dead, and the ashes are presently scattered over any piece of ground which the deceased may himself have chosen. No one is permitted to refuse this hospitality to the dead: people, therefore, generally choose some garden or orchard which they may have known and been fond of when they were young. The superstitious hold that those whose ashes are scattered over any land become its jealous guardians from that time forward; and the living like to think that they shall become identified with this or that locality where they have once been happy.
他们焚烧死者，然后将骨灰撒在死者自己选择的任何一块地上。任何人都不允许拒绝对死者的这种款待：因此，人们通常会选择一些他们年轻时可能知道并喜欢的花园或果园。迷信认为，那些骨灰撒在任何土地上的人，从那时起就成为该土地的嫉妒守护者。活着的人喜欢认为他们会认同他们曾经幸福过的这个或那个地方。

They do not put up monuments, nor write epitaphs, for their dead, though in former ages their practice was much as ours, but they have a custom which comes to much the same thing, for the instinct of preserving the name alive after the death of the body seems to be common to all mankind. They have statues of themselves made while they are still alive (those, that is, who can afford it), and write inscriptions under them, which are often quite as untruthful as are our own epitaphs—only in another way. For they do not hesitate to describe themselves as victims to ill temper, jealousy, covetousness, and the like, but almost always lay claim to personal beauty, whether they have it or not, and, often, to the possession of a large sum in the funded debt of the country. If a person is ugly he does not sit as a model for his own statue, although it bears his name. He gets the handsomest of his friends to sit for him, and one of the ways of paying a compliment to another is to ask him to sit for such a statue. Women generally sit for their own statues, from a natural disinclination to admit the superior beauty of a friend, but they expect to be idealised. I understood that the multitude of these statues was beginning to be felt as an encumbrance in almost every family, and that the custom would probably before long fall into desuetude.
他们不为死者立碑，也不写墓志铭，尽管在过去的时代他们的做法与我们的做法很相似，但他们有一个几乎相同的习俗，因为在死后保留名字的本能身体的特征似乎是全人类共有的。他们在活着的时候为自己制作雕像（即那些买得起的人），并在雕像下面写下铭文，这些铭文往往和我们自己的墓志铭一样不真实——只是以另一种方式。因为他们毫不犹豫地将自己描述为脾气暴躁、嫉妒、贪婪等的受害者，但几乎总是声称自己拥有个人美貌，无论他们是否拥有美貌，而且常常声称拥有一大笔财产。该国的融资债务。如果一个人长得很丑，他就不会坐在自己的雕像上作为模型，尽管雕像上有他的名字。他让他的朋友中最帅的一个为他坐，向另一个人致意的方式之一就是请他为这样的雕像坐。女性通常会为自己的雕像而坐，因为她们天生不愿意承认朋友的美貌，但她们希望自己被理想化。我明白，几乎每个家庭都开始觉得大量的雕像是一种负担，而且这种习俗可能很快就会被废除。

Indeed, this has already come about to the satisfaction of every one, as regards the statues of public men—not more than three of which can be found in the whole capital. I expressed my surprise at this, and was told that some five hundred years before my visit, the city had been so overrun with these pests, that there was no getting about, and people were worried beyond endurance by having their attention called at every touch and turn to something, which, when they had attended to it, they found not to concern them. Most of these statues were mere attempts to do for some man or woman what an animal-stuffer does more successfully for a dog, or bird, or pike. They were generally foisted on the public by some coterie that was trying to exalt itself in exalting some one else, and not unfrequently they had no other inception than desire on the part of some member of the coterie to find a job for a young sculptor to whom his daughter was engaged. Statues so begotten could never be anything but deformities, and this is the way in which they are sure to be begotten, as soon as the art of making them at all has become widely practised.
事实上，这已经让所有人都满意了，就公共人物的雕像而言——整个首都的雕像不超过三座。我对此表示惊讶，并被告知，在我访问之前大约五百年，这座城市已经被这些害虫淹没了，以至于无法走动，人们担心得无法忍受，因为每次接触都会引起他们的注意然后转向某件事，当他们注意到这件事时，他们发现与他们无关。大多数这些雕像只是尝试为某些男人或女人做一些动物填充者为狗、鸟或梭子鱼所做的更成功的事情。它们通常是由某些小圈子强加给公众的，这些小圈子试图通过抬高别人来抬高自己，而这种情况并不少见，除了小圈子中的某些成员希望为年轻的雕塑家找到一份工作之外，他们没有其他的出发点。他的女儿已经订婚了。这样产生的雕像除了畸形之外永远不会是什么，而一旦制作它们的艺术得到广泛应用，它们就一定会以这种方式产生。

I know not why, but all the noblest arts hold in perfection but for a very little moment. They soon reach a height from which they begin to decline, and when they have begun to decline it is a pity that they cannot be knocked on the head; for an art is like a living organism—better dead than dying. There is no way of making an aged art young again; it must be born anew and grow up from infancy as a new thing, working out its own salvation from effort to effort in all fear and trembling.
我不知道为什么，但所有最高尚的艺术都保持着完美，但只维持了很短的时间。他们很快就会达到一个高度，然后开始下降，当他们开始下降时，可惜的是，不能敲他们的头；因为艺术就像一个活的有机体——死了总比死了好。没有办法让古老的艺术重新焕发青春；它必须重生，从婴儿时期就成长为一个新事物，在恐惧和颤抖中不断努力，努力实现自己的救赎。

The Erewhonians five hundred years ago understood nothing of all this—I doubt whether they even do so now. They wanted to get the nearest thing they could to a stuffed man whose stuffing should not grow mouldy. They should have had some such an establishment as our Madame Tussaud’s, where the figures wear real clothes, and are painted up to nature. Such an institution might have been made self-supporting, for people might have been made to pay before going in. As it was, they had let their poor cold grimy colourless heroes and heroines loaf about in squares and in corners of streets in all weathers, without any attempt at artistic sanitation—for there was no provision for burying their dead works of art out of their sight—no drainage, so to speak, whereby statues that had been sufficiently assimilated, so as to form part of the residuary impression of the country, might be carried away out of the system. Hence they put them up with a light heart on the cackling of their coteries, and they and their children had to live, often enough, with some wordy windbag whose cowardice had cost the country untold loss in blood and money.
五百年前的埃瑞洪人对这一切一无所知——我怀疑他们现在是否还明白。他们想找到最接近毛绒玩具的东西，而且里面的填充物不会发霉。他们应该有像我们的杜莎夫人蜡像馆这样的场所，里面的人物穿着真衣服，而且画得很自然。这样的机构本来可以是自给自足的，因为人们在进去之前可能会被要求付钱。 事实上，他们让可怜的、寒冷的、肮脏的、无色的英雄和女英雄在任何天气条件下在广场和街道的角落里闲逛。 ，没有任何艺术卫生的尝试——因为没有规定将死去的艺术品掩埋在他们的视线之外——可以说，没有排水，已经被充分同化的雕像，从而形成了残留印象的一部分国家，可能会被排除在体制之外。因此，他们对他们的小圈子的咯咯笑声感到轻松，而他们和他们的孩子常常不得不与一些多嘴的空谈者一起生活，他们的懦弱使国家付出了无数的鲜血和金钱损失。

At last the evil reached such a pitch that the people rose, and with indiscriminate fury destroyed good and bad alike. Most of what was destroyed was bad, but some few works were good, and the sculptors of to-day wring their hands over some of the fragments that have been preserved in museums up and down the country. For a couple of hundred years or so, not a statue was made from one end of the kingdom to the other, but the instinct for having stuffed men and women was so strong, that people at length again began to try to make them. Not knowing how to make them, and having no academics to mislead them, the earliest sculptors of this period thought things out for themselves, and again produced works that were full of interest, so that in three or four generations they reached a perfection hardly if at all inferior to that of several hundred years earlier.
最后，邪恶达到了如此程度，人们起来了，用不分青红皂白的愤怒摧毁了善人和恶人。大多数被毁坏的东西都是坏的，但也有少数作品是好的，今天的雕塑家们对一些保存在全国各地博物馆中的碎片绞尽脑汁。在大约几百年的时间里，从王国的一端到另一端，没有建造一座雕像，但填充男人和女人的本能如此强烈，以至于人们终于再次开始尝试制作它们。这一时期最早的雕塑家们不知道如何制作，又没有学术界的误导，他们自己思考，又创作出了充满趣味的作品，以至于三四代人几乎都达到了完美。与数百年前相比，根本不逊色。

On this the same evils recurred. Sculptors obtained high prices— the art became a trade—schools arose which professed to sell the holy spirit of art for money; pupils flocked from far and near to buy it, in the hopes of selling it later on, and were struck purblind as a punishment for the sin of those who sent them. Before long a second iconoclastic fury would infallibly have followed, but for the prescience of a statesman who succeeded in passing an Act to the effect that no statue of any public man or woman should be allowed to remain unbroken for more than fifty years, unless at the end of that time a jury of twenty-four men taken at random from the street pronounced in favour of its being allowed a second fifty years of life. Every fifty years this reconsideration was to be repeated, and unless there was a majority of eighteen in favour of the retention of the statue, it was to be destroyed.
在此过程中，同样的罪恶再次发生。雕塑家获得了高价——艺术成为一种贸易——学校兴起，声称以出售艺术的神圣精神来换取金钱；学生们从四面八方涌来购买它，希望以后能卖掉它，但他们却被打得失明，作为对送他们的人的罪孽的惩罚。不久之后，第二次反传统的愤怒肯定会随之而来，但由于一位政治家的先见之明，他成功地通过了一项法案，该法案的大意是，任何公众人物的雕像不得在五十年以上保持完好无损，除非最后，由从街上随机抽取的二十四人组成的陪审团宣布支持给予其第二个五十年的寿命。每五十年就要重复一次这种重新考虑，除非有十八人的多数赞成保留雕像，否则它将被摧毁。

Perhaps a simpler plan would have been to forbid the erection of a statue to any public man or woman till he or she had been dead at least one hundred years, and even then to insist on reconsideration of the claims of the deceased and the merit of the statue every fifty years—but the working of the Act brought about results that on the whole were satisfactory. For in the first place, many public statues that would have been voted under the old system, were not ordered, when it was known that they would be almost certainly broken up after fifty years, and in the second, public sculptors knowing their work to be so ephemeral, scamped it to an extent that made it offensive even to the most uncultured eye. Hence before long subscribers took to paying the sculptor for the statue of their dead statesmen, on condition that he did not make it. The tribute of respect was thus paid to the deceased, the public sculptors were not mulcted, and the rest of the public suffered no inconvenience.
也许一个更简单的计划是禁止为任何公众人物竖立雕像，直到他或她去世至少一百年，即便如此，仍坚持重新考虑死者的主张和其功绩。每五十年建造一次雕像——但该法案的实施带来的结果总体上是令人满意的。因为首先，许多在旧制度下本应投票的公共雕像没有被订购，因为人们知道它们几乎肯定会在五十年后被拆除；其次，公共雕塑家知道他们的作品将被拆除。如此短暂，以至于即使在最没有文化的人看来也令人反感。因此，不久之后，订阅者就开始向雕塑家支付费用，购买他们已故政治家的雕像，条件是他不能成功。因此，人们向死者表示了敬意，公共雕塑家没有受到影响，其他公众也没有受到任何不便。

I was told, however, that an abuse of this custom is growing up, inasmuch as the competition for the commission not to make a statue is so keen, that sculptors have been known to return a considerable part of the purchase money to the subscribers, by an arrangement made with them beforehand. Such transactions, however, are always clandestine. A small inscription is let into the pavement, where the public statue would have stood, which informs the reader that such a statue has been ordered for the person, whoever he or she may be, but that as yet the sculptor has not been able to complete it. There has been no Act to repress statues that are intended for private consumption, but as I have said, the custom is falling into desuetude.
然而，有人告诉我，滥用这种习俗的现象正在增多，因为不制作雕像的委托竞争非常激烈，众所周知，雕塑家会将相当一部分购买资金返还给订阅者，通过事先与他们做出的安排。然而，此类交易始终是秘密的。人行道上刻有一个小铭文，公共雕像本来应该矗立在那里，它告诉读者，已经为这个人订购了这样一个雕像，无论他或她是谁，但到目前为止，雕塑家还无法完成它。目前还没有任何法案禁止私人消费的雕像，但正如我所说，这种习俗正在逐渐废弃。

Returning to Erewhonian customs in connection with death, there is one which I can hardly pass over. When any one dies, the friends of the family write no letters of condolence, neither do they attend the scattering, nor wear mourning, but they send little boxes filled with artificial tears, and with the name of the sender painted neatly upon the outside of the lid. The tears vary in number from two to fifteen or sixteen, according to degree of intimacy or relationship; and people sometimes find it a nice point of etiquette to know the exact number which they ought to send. Strange as it may appear, this attention is highly valued, and its omission by those from whom it might be expected is keenly felt. These tears were formerly stuck with adhesive plaster to the cheeks of the bereaved, and were worn in public for a few months after the death of a relative; they were then banished to the hat or bonnet, and are now no longer worn.
回到埃鲁洪尼亚与死亡有关的习俗，有一个我很难忽视。当有人去世时，亲朋好友不写吊唁信，也不参加追悼会，也不穿丧服，只是寄来装满人工泪液的小盒子，盒子外面工整地写着寄件人的名字。盖子。根据亲密程度或关系的不同，眼泪的数量从两滴到十五滴或十六滴不等；人们有时发现知道他们应该发送的确切号码是一种很好的礼仪。尽管看起来很奇怪，但这种关注受到高度重视，而那些可能期待这种关注的人却敏锐地感受到了它的忽视。这些眼泪以前是用橡皮膏贴在死者家属的脸颊上的，在亲人去世后在公共场合佩戴了几个月；然后它们被放逐到帽子或软帽上，现在不再佩戴。

The birth of a child is looked upon as a painful subject on which it is kinder not to touch: the illness of the mother is carefully concealed until the necessity for signing the birth-formula (of which hereafter) renders further secrecy impossible, and for some months before the event the family live in retirement, seeing very little company. When the offence is over and done with, it is condoned by the common want of logic; for this merciful provision of nature, this buffer against collisions, this friction which upsets our calculations but without which existence would be intolerable, this crowning glory of human invention whereby we can be blind and see at one and the same moment, this blessed inconsistency, exists here as elsewhere; and though the strictest writers on morality have maintained that it is wicked for a woman to have children at all, inasmuch as it is wrong to be out of health that good may come, yet the necessity of the case has caused a general feeling in favour of passing over such events in silence, and of assuming their non-existence except in such flagrant cases as force themselves on the public notice. Against these the condemnation of society is inexorable, and if it is believed that the illness has been dangerous and protracted, it is almost impossible for a woman to recover her former position in society.
孩子的出生被视为一个痛苦的话题，最好不要触及：母亲的病被小心地隐瞒，直到需要签署出生公式（此后）使进一步的保密变得不可能。活动举行前几个月，一家人过着退休生活，很少有人陪伴。当冒犯结束后，由于普遍缺乏逻辑，它被宽恕了。因为大自然的这种仁慈的规定，这种对碰撞的缓冲，这种扰乱我们的计算但没有它的存在将是无法忍受的摩擦，这种人类发明的至高无上的荣耀，使我们可以盲目地同时看到这种神圣的不一致，这里和其他地方一样存在；尽管最严格的道德作家们都坚持认为，女人生孩子根本就是邪恶的，因为健康状况不佳是错误的，但这种情况的必要性却引起了普遍的支持。对此类事件保持沉默，并假设这些事件不存在，除非是那些迫使公众注意的公然案件。社会对这些的谴责是无情的，如果人们认为这种疾病是危险的和长期的，那么妇女几乎不可能恢复以前的社会地位。

The above conventions struck me as arbitrary and cruel, but they put a stop to many fancied ailments; for the situation, so far from being considered interesting, is looked upon as savouring more or less distinctly of a very reprehensible condition of things, and the ladies take care to conceal it as long as they can even from their own husbands, in anticipation of a severe scolding as soon as the misdemeanour is discovered. Also the baby is kept out of sight, except on the day of signing the birth-formula, until it can walk and talk. Should the child unhappily die, a coroner’s inquest is inevitable, but in order to avoid disgracing a family which may have been hitherto respected, it is almost invariably found that the child was over seventy-five years old, and died from the decay of nature.
上述惯例给我的印象是武断和残酷，但它们阻止了许多想象中的疾病。因为这种情况远非被认为是有趣的，而是被认为或多或少明显是一种非常应受谴责的情况，而女士们则小心翼翼地向自己的丈夫隐瞒这一情况，甚至不让自己的丈夫知道，因为她们预计会发生这样的事情。一旦发现违法行为，立即严厉批评。此外，除了在签署配方奶的那天外，婴儿也不会被人看到，直到他能走路和说话。如果孩子不幸死亡，验尸官的调查是不可避免的，但为了避免让一个迄今为止可能受到尊重的家庭蒙羞，几乎总是发现孩子已经超过七十五岁，死于自然腐烂。 。

CHAPTER XIV: MAHAINA
第十四章：玛海娜

I continued my sojourn with the Nosnibors. In a few days Mr. Nosnibor had recovered from his flogging, and was looking forward with glee to the fact that the next would be the last. I did not think that there seemed any occasion even for this; but he said it was better to be on the safe side, and he would make up the dozen. He now went to his business as usual; and I understood that he was never more prosperous, in spite of his heavy fine. He was unable to give me much of his time during the day; for he was one of those valuable men who are paid, not by the year, month, week, or day, but by the minute. His wife and daughters, however, made much of me, and introduced me to their friends, who came in shoals to call upon me.
我继续在诺斯尼伯家族逗留。几天后，诺斯尼博尔先生从鞭打中恢复过来，并高兴地期待着下一次将是最后一次。我认为似乎没有任何必要这样做；但他说保险起见比较好，他会补上十几个。现在他像往常一样去干自己的事了。我明白，尽管他受到了巨额罚款，但他从未像现在这样富裕过。他白天无法给我太多时间。因为他是那些有价值的人之一，他们的报酬不是按年、月、周或日计算，而是按分钟计算。然而，他的妻子和女儿们很看重我，把我介绍给她们的朋友，他们纷纷前来拜访我。

One of these persons was a lady called Mahaina. Zulora (the elder of my host’s daughters) ran up to her and embraced her as soon as she entered the room, at the same time inquiring tenderly after her ‘poor dipsomania.’ Mahaina answered that it was just as bad as ever; she was a perfect martyr to it, and her excellent health was the only thing which consoled her under her affliction.
其中一位名叫玛海娜的女士。她一进房间，祖洛拉（我主人的女儿中的长辈）就跑到她面前拥抱了她，同时温柔地询问她“可怜的酗酒狂”的情况。她是一个完美的殉道者，而她良好的健康状况是在她的痛苦中唯一安慰她的东西。

Then the other ladies joined in with condolences and the never- failing suggestions which they had ready for every mental malady. They recommended their own straightener and disparaged Mahaina’s. Mrs. Nosnibor had a favourite nostrum, but I could catch little of its nature. I heard the words ‘full confidence that the desire to drink will cease when the formula has been repeated * * * this confidence is EVERYTHING * * * far from undervaluing a thorough determination never to touch spirits again * * * fail too often * * * formula a CERTAIN CURE (with great emphasis) * * * prescribed form * * * full conviction.’ The conversation then became more audible, and was carried on at considerable length. I should perplex myself and the reader by endeavouring to follow the ingenious perversity of all they said; enough, that in the course of time the visit came to an end, and Mahaina took her leave receiving affectionate embraces from all the ladies. I had remained in the background after the first ceremony of introduction, for I did not like the looks of Mahaina, and the conversation displeased me. When she left the room I had some consolation in the remarks called forth by her departure.
然后其他女士也加入了哀悼，并提出了她们为每一种精神疾病准备的永不失败的建议。他们推荐了自己的直发器，并贬低了 Mahaina 的直发器。诺斯尼伯夫人有一个最喜欢的秘方，但我对它的本质知之甚少。我听到这样一句话：“完全有信心，重复这个公式后，喝酒的欲望就会停止 * * * 这种信心就是一切 * * * 远非低估了不再接触烈酒的彻底决心 * * * 经常失败 * * *公式“一定治愈”（特别强调）* * * 规定形式 * * * 完全确信。然后谈话变得更加清晰，并且持续了相当长的时间。我试图追随他们所说的一切巧妙而反常的观点，这会让我自己和读者感到困惑。就这样，随着时间的推移，访问结束了，马海娜在所有女士们深情的拥抱下离开了。在第一次介绍仪式之后，我一直处于幕后，因为我不喜欢马海娜的长相，而且谈话也让我不高兴。当她离开房间时，我从她的离开引起的言论中得到了一些安慰。

At first they fell to praising her very demurely. She was all this that and the other, till I disliked her more and more at every word, and inquired how it was that the straighteners had not been able to cure her as they had cured Mr. Nosnibor.
起初，他们非常拘谨地称赞她。她就是这样又那样，直到我每说一句话都越来越不喜欢她，并询问直发器为什么不能像治愈诺斯尼伯先生那样治愈她。

There was a shade of significance on Mrs. Nosnibor’s face as I said this, which seemed to imply that she did not consider Mahaina’s case to be quite one for a straightener. It flashed across me that perhaps the poor woman did not drink at all. I knew that I ought not to have inquired, but I could not help it, and asked point blank whether she did or not.
当我说这句话时，诺斯尼博尔夫人的脸上流露出一丝严肃的神色，这似乎暗示着她并不认为马海娜的情况适合直发器。我突然想到，也许这个可怜的女人根本就没有喝酒。我知道我不应该问，但我忍不住，直截了当地问她到底问了没有。

‘We can none of us judge of the condition of other people,’ said Mrs. Nosnibor in a gravely charitable tone and with a look towards Zulora.
“我们谁也无法判断别人的处境，”诺斯尼博尔夫人用严肃而仁慈的语气说道，目光看向祖洛拉。

‘Oh, mamma,’ answered Zulora, pretending to be half angry but rejoiced at being able to say out what she was already longing to insinuate; ‘I don’t believe a word of it. It’s all indigestion. I remember staying in the house with her for a whole month last summer, and I am sure she never once touched a drop of wine or spirits. The fact is, Mahaina is a very weakly girl, and she pretends to get tipsy in order to win a forbearance from her friends to which she is not entitled. She is not strong enough for her calisthenic exercises, and she knows she would be made to do them unless her inability was referred to moral causes.’
“哦，妈妈，”祖洛拉回答道，假装半生气，但很高兴能够说出她已经渴望暗示的话； ‘我一个字也不信。都是消化不良。我记得去年夏天和她一起在家里待了整整一个月，我确信她从来没有碰过一滴酒或烈酒。事实上，玛海娜是一个非常虚弱的女孩，她假装喝醉了，以博得朋友们的宽容，而她没有资格这样做。她的体力不足以进行健美操练习，她知道除非她的无能是出于道德原因，否则她将被迫进行这些练习。

Here the younger sister, who was ever sweet and kind, remarked that she thought Mahaina did tipple occasionally. ‘I also think,’ she added, ‘that she sometimes takes poppy juice.’
妹妹一向和蔼可亲，她说她认为马海娜偶尔会喝醉。 “我还认为，”她补充道，“她有时会喝罂粟汁。”

‘Well, then, perhaps she does drink sometimes,’ said Zulora; ‘but she would make us all think that she does it much oftener in order to hide her weakness.’
“那么，也许她有时确实会喝酒，”祖洛拉说。 “但她会让我们所有人认为她更频繁地这样做是为了隐藏自己的弱点。”

And so they went on for half an hour and more, bandying about the question as to how far their late visitor’s intemperance was real or no. Every now and then they would join in some charitable commonplace, and would pretend to be all of one mind that Mahaina was a person whose bodily health would be excellent if it were not for her unfortunate inability to refrain from excessive drinking; but as soon as this appeared to be fairly settled they began to be uncomfortable until they had undone their work and left some serious imputation upon her constitution. At last, seeing that the debate had assumed the character of a cyclone or circular storm, going round and round and round and round till one could never say where it began nor where it ended, I made some apology for an abrupt departure and retired to my own room.
就这样，他们持续了半个多小时，不断地讨论着这个问题：这位已故访客的放纵行为到底是真是假。他们时不时地参加一些慈善活动，假装全心全意地认为，如果不是玛海娜不幸无法克制过度饮酒，她的身体健康状况将会非常好；但一旦事情似乎得到了相当的解决，他们就开始感到不舒服，直到他们取消了他们的工作，并对她的体质留下了一些严重的指责。最后，看到这场争论已经呈现出旋风或循环风暴的特征，一圈又一圈，一圈又一圈，直到人们无法说出它从哪里开始，也无法说出它在哪里结束，我为突然离开表示歉意，然后退休了。我自己的房间。

Here at least I was alone, but I was very unhappy. I had fallen upon a set of people who, in spite of their high civilisation and many excellences, had been so warped by the mistaken views presented to them during childhood from generation to generation, that it was impossible to see how they could ever clear themselves. Was there nothing which I could say to make them feel that the constitution of a person’s body was a thing over which he or she had had at any rate no initial control whatever, while the mind was a perfectly different thing, and capable of being created anew and directed according to the pleasure of its possessor? Could I never bring them to see that while habits of mind and character were entirely independent of initial mental force and early education, the body was so much a creature of parentage and circumstances, that no punishment for ill-health should be ever tolerated save as a protection from contagion, and that even where punishment was inevitable it should be attended with compassion? Surely, if the unfortunate Mahaina were to feel that she could avow her bodily weakness without fear of being despised for her infirmities, and if there were medical men to whom she could fairly state her case, she would not hesitate about doing so through the fear of taking nasty medicine. It was possible that her malady was incurable (for I had heard enough to convince me that her dipsomania was only a pretence and that she was temperate in all her habits); in that case she might perhaps be justly subject to annoyances or even to restraint; but who could say whether she was curable or not, until she was able to make a clean breast of her symptoms instead of concealing them? In their eagerness to stamp out disease, these people overshot their mark; for people had become so clever at dissembling—they painted their faces with such consummate skill— they repaired the decay of time and the effects of mischance with such profound dissimulation—that it was really impossible to say whether any one was well or ill till after an intimate acquaintance of months or years. Even then the shrewdest were constantly mistaken in their judgements, and marriages were often contracted with most deplorable results, owing to the art with which infirmity had been concealed.
这里至少只有我一个人，但我很不高兴。我遇到了一群人，尽管他们有很高的文明程度和许多优秀的品质，但他们却被童年时期一代又一代的错误观点所扭曲，以致于他们根本无法看清自己的清白。 。难道我没有什么可以说的，让他们觉得一个人的身体的构成是一个他或她无论如何都无法最初控制的东西，而心灵是一个完全不同的东西，并且能够被创造重新并根据其拥有者的喜好进行引导？难道我永远不能让他们明白，虽然思想和性格的习惯完全独立于最初的精神力量和早期教育，但身体在很大程度上是出身和环境的产物，任何对健康不良的惩罚都是不应该容忍的，除非防止传染，即使惩罚不可避免，也应该充满同情心？当然，如果不幸的玛海娜觉得她可以承认自己身体上的弱点，而不必担心因她的虚弱而受到鄙视，并且如果有医生可以公平地向她陈述自己的情况，那么她会毫不犹豫地这样做，因为她害怕服用难吃的药。她的病可能无法治愈（因为我听到的足够多的信息使我确信她的酗酒只是一种假象，而且她在所有习惯上都很节制）；在这种情况下，她也许会理所应当地受到烦恼，甚至受到限制。但在她能够坦白而不是隐瞒自己的症状之前，谁能说她是否可以治愈呢？ 由于渴望消灭疾病，这些人超出了他们的目标。因为人们已经变得如此善于掩饰——他们用如此高超的技巧来描绘自己的脸——他们用如此深刻的掩饰来修复时间的腐烂和不幸的影响——以至于直到后来才真正不可能说一个人是好是坏。数月或数年的亲密相识。即使在那时，最精明的人也经常做出错误的判断，而且由于掩盖虚弱的艺术，婚姻往往会带来最悲惨的结果。

It appeared to me that the first step towards the cure of disease should be the announcement of the fact to a person’s near relations and friends. If any one had a headache, he ought to be permitted within reasonable limits to say so at once, and to retire to his own bedroom and take a pill, without every one’s looking grave and tears being shed and all the rest of it. As it was, even upon hearing it whispered that somebody else was subject to headaches, a whole company must look as though they had never had a headache in their lives. It is true they were not very prevalent, for the people were the healthiest and most comely imaginable, owing to the severity with which ill health was treated; still, even the best were liable to be out of sorts sometimes, and there were few families that had not a medicine-chest in a cupboard somewhere.
在我看来，治愈疾病的第一步应该是向一个人的近亲和朋友宣布这一事实。如果有人头痛，应该允许他在合理的范围内立即说出来，然后回到自己的卧室吃药，而不是每个人都显得严肃，流泪等等。事实上，即使听到有人低声说别人患有头痛，整个公司的人也一定看起来好像他们一生中从未患过头痛一样。确实，这种病并不普遍，因为人们对疾病的治疗非常严格，是可以想象到的最健康、最漂亮的人。尽管如此，即使是最好的人有时也会感到不舒服，而且几乎每个家庭的橱柜里都没有放着一个药箱。

CHAPTER XV: THE MUSICAL BANKS
第十五章：音乐库

On my return to the drawing-room, I found that the Mahaina current had expended itself. The ladies were just putting away their work and preparing to go out. I asked them where they were going. They answered with a certain air of reserve that they were going to the bank to get some money.
当我回到客厅时，我发现马海纳电流已经耗尽了。女士们刚刚放下手中的工作，准备出去。我问他们要去哪里。他们带着某种矜持的态度回答说，他们要去银行取点钱。

Now I had already collected that the mercantile affairs of the Erewhonians were conducted on a totally different system from our own; I had, however, gathered little hitherto, except that they had two distinct commercial systems, of which the one appealed more strongly to the imagination than anything to which we are accustomed in Europe, inasmuch as the banks that were conducted upon this system were decorated in the most profuse fashion, and all mercantile transactions were accompanied with music, so that they were called Musical Banks, though the music was hideous to a European ear.
现在我已经了解到，埃雷洪尼亚人的商业事务是按照与我们完全不同的制度进行的。然而，到目前为止，我所知甚少，只知道他们有两种不同的商业系统，其中一种比我们在欧洲习惯的任何系统都更能激发人们的想象力，因为在该系统上进行操作的银行都是装饰性的。以最丰富的方式进行，所有商业交易都伴随着音乐，因此它们被称为音乐银行，尽管音乐对欧洲人来说是可怕的。

As for the system itself I never understood it, neither can I do so now: they have a code in connection with it, which I have not the slightest doubt that they understand, but no foreigner can hope to do so. One rule runs into, and against, another as in a most complicated grammar, or as in Chinese pronunciation, wherein I am told that the slightest change in accentuation or tone of voice alters the meaning of a whole sentence. Whatever is incoherent in my description must be referred to the fact of my never having attained to a full comprehension of the subject.
至于这个系统本身，我从来没有理解过，现在也不能理解：他们有一个与之相关的代码，我毫不怀疑他们理解这个代码，但没有外国人能希望这样做。一条规则与另一条规则相冲突，或者相反，就像在最复杂的语法中，或者在中文发音中，我被告知，重音或语调的最轻微的变化都会改变整个句子的含义。我的描述中任何不连贯的地方都必须涉及到我从未完全理解该主题的事实。

So far, however, as I could collect anything certain, I gathered that they have two distinct currencies, each under the control of its own banks and mercantile codes. One of these (the one with the Musical Banks) was supposed to be THE system, and to give out the currency in which all monetary transactions should be carried on; and as far as I could see, all who wished to be considered respectable, kept a larger or smaller balance at these banks. On the other hand, if there is one thing of which I am more sure than another, it is that the amount so kept had no direct commercial value in the outside world; I am sure that the managers and cashiers of the Musical Banks were not paid in their own currency. Mr. Nosnibor used to go to these banks, or rather to the great mother bank of the city, sometimes but not very often. He was a pillar of one of the other kind of banks, though he appeared to hold some minor office also in the musical ones. The ladies generally went alone; as indeed was the case in most families, except on state occasions.
然而，到目前为止，由于我能收集到任何确定的信息，我推测它们有两种不同的货币，每种货币都受自己的银行和商业代码的控制。其中之一（音乐银行的那个）应该是系统，并发行所有货币交易应使用的货币；据我所知，所有希望被视为受人尊敬的人都在这些银行保留了或多或少的余额。另一方面，如果说有一件事我比另一件事更确定的话，那就是如此保留的数量在外界没有直接的商业价值；我确信音乐银行的经理和出纳员的工资不是用本国货币支付的。诺斯尼博尔先生过去常常去这些银行，或者更确切地说，去这座城市伟大的母银行，有时但不是经常去。他是另一种银行的支柱，尽管他似乎也在音乐银行中担任过一些次要职位。女士们一般都是单独前往。大多数家庭的情况确实如此，除了国家场合。

I had long wanted to know more of this strange system, and had the greatest desire to accompany my hostess and her daughters. I had seen them go out almost every morning since my arrival and had noticed that they carried their purses in their hands, not exactly ostentatiously, yet just so as that those who met them should see whither they were going. I had never, however, yet been asked to go with them myself.
我早就想更多地了解这个奇怪的系统，最渴望的是陪伴女主人和她的女儿们。自从我到达以来，我几乎每天早上都看到他们出去，并注意到他们手里拿着钱包，并不完全是招摇的，但只是为了让见到他们的人知道他们要去哪里。然而，我从来没有被要求亲自和他们一起去。

It is not easy to convey a person’s manner by words, and I can hardly give any idea of the peculiar feeling that came upon me when I saw the ladies on the point of starting for the bank. There was a something of regret, a something as though they would wish to take me with them, but did not like to ask me, and yet as though I were hardly to ask to be taken. I was determined, however, to bring matters to an issue with my hostess about my going with them, and after a little parleying, and many inquiries as to whether I was perfectly sure that I myself wished to go, it was decided that I might do so.
用言语来表达一个人的举止并不容易，当我看到女士们正要出发去银行时，我几乎无法想象那种奇特的感觉。有一种遗憾，好像他们想带我一起去，但又不愿意邀请我，但又好像我很难要求被带去。然而，我决心向我的女主人提出关于我和他们一起去的问题，经过一番谈判，并多次询问我是否完全确定我自己想去，最后决定我可以这样做。

We passed through several streets of more or less considerable houses, and at last turning round a corner we came upon a large piazza, at the end of which was a magnificent building, of a strange but noble architecture and of great antiquity. It did not open directly on to the piazza, there being a screen, through which was an archway, between the piazza and the actual precincts of the bank. On passing under the archway we entered upon a green sward, round which there ran an arcade or cloister, while in front of us uprose the majestic towers of the bank and its venerable front, which was divided into three deep recesses and adorned with all sorts of marbles and many sculptures. On either side there were beautiful old trees wherein the birds were busy by the hundred, and a number of quaint but substantial houses of singularly comfortable appearance; they were situated in the midst of orchards and gardens, and gave me an impression of great peace and plenty.
我们穿过几条街道，两边都是或多或少相当大的房子，最后拐过一个街角，我们来到了一个大广场，广场的尽头是一座宏伟的建筑，建筑风格奇怪但高贵，而且非常古老。它并没有直接通向广场，在广场和银行的实际区域之间有一个屏风，通过屏风是一个拱门。穿过拱门下方，我们进入了一片绿色的草地，周围有一个拱廊或回廊，而在我们面前，矗立着银行的雄伟塔楼及其庄严的正面，正面分为三个深凹处，装饰着各种各样的东西。大理石和许多雕塑。两边都是美丽的古树，成百上千的鸟儿在忙碌，还有许多古色古香但坚固的房屋，外观异常舒适。它们坐落在果园和花园中间，给我一种非常和平和富足的印象。

Indeed it had been no error to say that this building was one that appealed to the imagination; it did more—it carried both imagination and judgement by storm. It was an epic in stone and marble, and so powerful was the effect it produced on me, that as I beheld it I was charmed and melted. I felt more conscious of the existence of a remote past. One knows of this always, but the knowledge is never so living as in the actual presence of some witness to the life of bygone ages. I felt how short a space of human life was the period of our own existence. I was more impressed with my own littleness, and much more inclinable to believe that the people whose sense of the fitness of things was equal to the upraising of so serene a handiwork, were hardly likely to be wrong in the conclusions they might come to upon any subject. My feeling certainly was that the currency of this bank must be the right one.
事实上，说这座建筑是一座充满想象力的建筑并没有错。它做得更多——它承载着强烈的想象力和判断力。这是一部石头和大理石的史诗，它对我产生的影响是如此强大，以至于当我看到它时，我被迷住了，融化了。我更加意识到遥远过去的存在。人们总是知道这一点，但这种知识从来没有像过去时代生活的某些见证人的实际存在那样生动。我感到人类的生命空间对于我们自己存在的时期来说是多么短暂。我对自己的渺小印象更深刻，更倾向于相信，那些对事物的适宜性的感觉等同于提升如此宁静的工艺品的人，他们得出的结论几乎不可能是错误的。任何主题。我的感觉当然是这家银行的货币一定是正确的。

We crossed the sward and entered the building. If the outside had been impressive the inside was even more so. It was very lofty and divided into several parts by walls which rested upon massive pillars; the windows were filled with stained glass descriptive of the principal commercial incidents of the bank for many ages. In a remote part of the building there were men and boys singing; this was the only disturbing feature, for as the gamut was still unknown, there was no music in the country which could be agreeable to a European ear. The singers seemed to have derived their inspirations from the songs of birds and the wailing of the wind, which last they tried to imitate in melancholy cadences that at times degenerated into a howl. To my thinking the noise was hideous, but it produced a great effect upon my companions, who professed themselves much moved. As soon as the singing was over, the ladies requested me to stay where I was while they went inside the place from which it had seemed to come.
我们穿过草地，进入大楼。如果说外部令人印象深刻，那么内部更是如此。它非常高大，被由巨大柱子支撑的墙壁分成几个部分。窗户上贴满了彩色玻璃，描述了多年来银行的主要商业事件。在大楼的一个偏僻的地方，男人和男孩们在唱歌。这是唯一令人不安的特征，因为由于音域仍然未知，该国没有适合欧洲人耳朵的音乐。歌手们的灵感似乎来自鸟儿的歌声和风的哀号，最后他们试图以忧郁的节奏模仿，有时甚至退化为嚎叫。在我看来，这种噪音是可怕的，但它对我的同伴产生了很大的影响，他们声称自己很感动。歌声一结束，女士们就要求我留在原地，而她们则走进了歌声似乎来自的地方。

During their absence certain reflections forced themselves upon me.
他们不在的时候，我突然产生了一些思考。

In the first place, it struck me as strange that the building should be so nearly empty; I was almost alone, and the few besides myself had been led by curiosity, and had no intention of doing business with the bank. But there might be more inside. I stole up to the curtain, and ventured to draw the extreme edge of it on one side. No, there was hardly any one there. I saw a large number of cashiers, all at their desks ready to pay cheques, and one or two who seemed to be the managing partners. I also saw my hostess and her daughters and two or three other ladies; also three or four old women and the boys from one of the neighbouring Colleges of Unreason; but there was no one else. This did not look as though the bank was doing a very large business; and yet I had always been told that every one in the city dealt with this establishment.
首先，这栋建筑几乎空无一人，这让我感到很奇怪。几乎只有我一个人，除了我之外的几个人都被好奇心所引导，无意与银行做生意。但里面可能还有更多。我偷偷走到窗帘前，大胆地把窗帘的边缘拉到一侧。不，那里几乎没有人。我看到很多收银员，都在办公桌前准备支付支票，还有一两个似乎是管理合伙人。我还看到了我的女主人和她的女儿们以及另外两三位女士。还有来自邻近一所非理性学院的三四个老妇人和男孩；但没有其他人。这看起来不像银行正在做一项非常大的业务；然而我一直被告知，城里的每个人都与这个机构打交道。

I cannot describe all that took place in these inner precincts, for a sinister-looking person in a black gown came and made unpleasant gestures at me for peeping. I happened to have in my pocket one of the Musical Bank pieces, which had been given me by Mrs. Nosnibor, so I tried to tip him with it; but having seen what it was, he became so angry that I had to give him a piece of the other kind of money to pacify him. When I had done this he became civil directly. As soon as he was gone I ventured to take a second look, and saw Zulora in the very act of giving a piece of paper which looked like a cheque to one of the cashiers. He did not examine it, but putting his hand into an antique coffer hard by, he pulled out a quantity of metal pieces apparently at random, and handed them over without counting them; neither did Zulora count them, but put them into her purse and went back to her seat after dropping a few pieces of the other coinage into an alms box that stood by the cashier’s side. Mrs. Nosnibor and Arowhena then did likewise, but a little later they gave all (so far as I could see) that they had received from the cashier back to a verger, who I have no doubt put it back into the coffer from which it had been taken. They then began making towards the curtain; whereon I let it drop and retreated to a reasonable distance.
我无法描述在这些内部区域发生的一切，因为一个穿着黑袍、面容阴险的人走过来，对我偷看做出了令人不快的手势。我的口袋里碰巧有一张音乐银行的碎片，是诺斯尼伯夫人给我的，所以我想用它给他小费；但他没有得到任何回报。但看到那是什么后，他非常生气，我不得不给他一块另一种钱来安抚他。当我这样做时，他直接变得文明了。他一走，我就大胆地再看了一眼，看到祖洛拉正在把一张看起来像支票的纸交给一名收银员。他没有细看，而是把手伸进了旁边的一个古董保险箱里，显然是随意地掏出了一些金属件，没有数数就递了过去；祖洛拉也没有数，而是将它们放入钱包中，然后将其他硬币的几枚放入收银员旁边的施舍箱中，然后返回座位。诺斯尼博尔夫人和阿罗维纳夫人也做了同样的事，但过了一会儿，他们把从收银员那里收到的所有钱（据我所知）都还给了司事，我毫不怀疑他又把钱放回了保险箱。已被采取。然后他们开始走向幕布。然后我让它掉下来，退到一个合理的距离。

They soon joined me. For some few minutes we all kept silence, but at last I ventured to remark that the bank was not so busy to-day as it probably often was. On this Mrs. Nosnibor said that it was indeed melancholy to see what little heed people paid to the most precious of all institutions. I could say nothing in reply, but I have ever been of opinion that the greater part of mankind do approximately know where they get that which does them good.
他们很快就加入了我。我们都保持沉默了几分钟，但最后我大胆地说，银行今天不像往常那么忙。对此，诺斯尼博尔夫人表示，看到人们对最宝贵的机构如此漠不关心，确实令人感到悲伤。我无话可说，但我一直认为，大多数人大约知道他们从哪里得到对他们有好处的东西。

Mrs. Nosnibor went on to say that I must not think there was any want of confidence in the bank because I had seen so few people there; the heart of the country was thoroughly devoted to these establishments, and any sign of their being in danger would bring in support from the most unexpected quarters. It was only because people knew them to be so very safe, that in some cases (as she lamented to say in Mr. Nosnibor’s) they felt that their support was unnecessary. Moreover these institutions never departed from the safest and most approved banking principles. Thus they never allowed interest on deposit, a thing now frequently done by certain bubble companies, which by doing an illegitimate trade had drawn many customers away; and even the shareholders were fewer than formerly, owing to the innovations of these unscrupulous persons, for the Musical Banks paid little or no dividend, but divided their profits by way of bonus on the original shares once in every thirty thousand years; and as it was now only two thousand years since there had been one of these distributions, people felt that they could not hope for another in their own time and preferred investments whereby they got some more tangible return; all which, she said, was very melancholy to think of.
诺斯尼博尔夫人接着说，我一定不会认为人们对银行缺乏信心，因为我在那里见过的人太少了；国家的心脏完全投入到这些机构中，任何它们处于危险之中的迹象都会带来最意想不到的方面的支持。只是因为人们知道他们非常安全，所以在某些情况下（正如她在诺斯尼伯先生的故事中哀叹地说的那样），他们觉得他们的支持是不必要的。此外，这些机构从未偏离最安全和最受认可的银行原则。因此，他们从不允许存款利息，而现在某些泡沫公司经常这样做，通过非法交易吸引了许多客户；由于这些不法分子的创新，甚至股东也比以前少了，因为音乐银行很少或根本不支付股息，而是以每三万年一次的原始股份红利的方式分配利润；由于这种分配方式距今只有两千多年的时间了，人们觉得他们不能指望在自己的时代再有另一种分配方式，而更愿意进行投资，从而获得更切实的回报；她说，想到这一切就感到非常忧郁。

Having made these last admissions, she returned to her original statement, namely, that every one in the country really supported these banks. As to the fewness of the people, and the absence of the able-bodied, she pointed out to me with some justice that this was exactly what we ought to expect. The men who were most conversant about the stability of human institutions, such as the lawyers, men of science, doctors, statesmen, painters, and the like, were just those who were most likely to be misled by their own fancied accomplishments, and to be made unduly suspicious by their licentious desire for greater present return, which was at the root of nine-tenths of the opposition; by their vanity, which would prompt them to affect superiority to the prejudices of the vulgar; and by the stings of their own conscience, which was constantly upbraiding them in the most cruel manner on account of their bodies, which were generally diseased.
在做出最后的承认之后，她回到了最初的声明，即该国每个人都真正支持这些银行。至于人少、壮士少的问题，她颇有正义感地向我指出，这正是我们应该期待的。最熟悉人类制度稳定性的人，如律师、科学家、医生、政治家、画家等，正是那些最有可能被自己幻想的成就所误导的人，并由于他们对当前更大回报的放荡渴望而引起过度怀疑，这是十分之九的反对派的根源；由于他们的虚荣心，这会促使他们对庸俗的偏见表现出优越感；他们的良心不断地以最残酷的方式责备他们，因为他们的身体普遍患病。

Let a person’s intellect (she continued) be never so sound, unless his body is in absolute health, he can form no judgement worth having on matters of this kind. The body is everything: it need not perhaps be such a strong body (she said this because she saw that I was thinking of the old and infirm-looking folks whom I had seen in the bank), but it must be in perfect health; in this case, the less active strength it had the more free would be the working of the intellect, and therefore the sounder the conclusion. The people, then, whom I had seen at the bank were in reality the very ones whose opinions were most worth having; they declared its advantages to be incalculable, and even professed to consider the immediate return to be far larger than they were entitled to; and so she ran on, nor did she leave off till we had got back to the house.
一个人的智力（她继续说）永远不要那么健全，除非他的身体绝对健康，否则他无法对这类事情做出任何值得做出的判断。身体就是一切：也许不需要那么强壮的身体（她这么说是因为她看到我想起了我在银行里看到的那些年老体弱的人），但它必须非常健康；在这种情况下，它的积极力量越少，智力的运作就越自由，因此得出的结论就越合理。那么，我在银行见过的那些人实际上是那些最值得听取意见的人；他们的观点是正确的。他们宣称它的好处是无法估量的，甚至声称认为立即的回报远远大于他们应得的回报；于是她继续跑，直到我们回到家才停下来。

She might say what she pleased, but her manner carried no conviction, and later on I saw signs of general indifference to these banks that were not to be mistaken. Their supporters often denied it, but the denial was generally so couched as to add another proof of its existence. In commercial panics, and in times of general distress, the people as a mass did not so much as even think of turning to these banks. A few might do so, some from habit and early training, some from the instinct that prompts us to catch at any straw when we think ourselves drowning, but few from a genuine belief that the Musical Banks could save them from financial ruin, if they were unable to meet their engagements in the other kind of currency.
她可以说她想说的话，但她的态度没有说服力，后来我看到了对这些银行普遍漠不关心的迹象，这一点是不容误解的。他们的支持者经常否认这一点，但这种否认的措辞通常是为了证明其存在。在商业恐慌和普遍困难时期，广大人民甚至没有想过求助于这些银行。有些人可能会这样做，有些是出于习惯和早期训练，有些是出于本能，当我们认为自己快要淹死时，促使我们抓住任何一根稻草，但很少有人真正相信音乐银行可以使他们免于财务破产，如果他们无法用另一种货币履行其约定。

In conversation with one of the Musical Bank managers I ventured to hint this as plainly as politeness would allow. He said that it had been more or less true till lately; but that now they had put fresh stained glass windows into all the banks in the country, and repaired the buildings, and enlarged the organs; the presidents, moreover, had taken to riding in omnibuses and talking nicely to people in the streets, and to remembering the ages of their children, and giving them things when they were naughty, so that all would henceforth go smoothly.
在与音乐银行的一位经理交谈时，我冒昧地在礼貌允许的范围内尽可能简单地暗示了这一点。他说，直到最近，这或多或少都是正确的。但现在他们已经为全国所有银行安装了新的彩色玻璃窗，修复了建筑物，扩大了机关；此外，总统们还习惯于乘坐公共汽车，在街上与人们亲切交谈，记住孩子的年龄，在他们顽皮时给他们东西，以便今后一切顺利。

‘But haven’t you done anything to the money itself?’ said I, timidly.
“但是你没有对钱本身做任何事吗？”我胆怯地说。

‘It is not necessary,’ he rejoined; ‘not in the least necessary, I assure you.’
“没有必要，”他回答道。 “我向你保证，完全没有必要。”

And yet any one could see that the money given out at these banks was not that with which people bought their bread, meat, and clothing. It was like it at a first glance, and was stamped with designs that were often of great beauty; it was not, again, a spurious coinage, made with the intention that it should be mistaken for the money in actual use; it was more like a toy money, or the counters used for certain games at cards; for, notwithstanding the beauty of the designs, the material on which they were stamped was as nearly valueless as possible. Some were covered with tin foil, but the greater part were frankly of a cheap base metal the exact nature of which I was not able to determine. Indeed they were made of a great variety of metals, or, perhaps more accurately, alloys, some of which were hard, while others would bend easily and assume almost any form which their possessor might desire at the moment.
然而任何人都可以看出，这些银行发放的钱并不是人们用来购买面包、肉类和衣服的钱。乍一看就像它一样，并且印有通常非常美丽的图案。再说一次，它并不是一种伪造的货币，其目的是为了被误认为是实际使用的货币；它更像是一种玩具钱，或者是用于某些纸牌游戏的计数器；因为，尽管设计很美，但印在其上的材料却几乎毫无价值。有些是用锡箔覆盖的，但坦率地说，大部分是廉价的贱金属，我无法确定其确切性质。事实上，它们是由各种各样的金属制成的，或者更准确地说，是合金制成的，其中一些很硬，而另一些则很容易弯曲，并呈现出它们的拥有者当时可能想要的几乎任何形状。

Of course every one knew that their commercial value was nil, but all those who wished to be considered respectable thought it incumbent upon them to retain a few coins in their possession, and to let them be seen from time to time in their hands and purses. Not only this, but they would stick to it that the current coin of the realm was dross in comparison with the Musical Bank coinage. Perhaps, however, the strangest thing of all was that these very people would at times make fun in small ways of the whole system; indeed, there was hardly any insinuation against it which they would not tolerate and even applaud in their daily newspapers if written anonymously, while if the same thing were said without ambiguity to their faces—nominative case verb and accusative being all in their right places, and doubt impossible—they would consider themselves very seriously and justly outraged, and accuse the speaker of being unwell.
当然，每个人都知道它们的商业价值为零，但所有希望被视为受人尊敬的人都认为他们有责任保留几枚硬币，并让人们时不时地在他们的手中和钱包中看到它们。 。不仅如此，他们还坚持认为，与音乐银行的硬币相比，现在的王国硬币就是渣滓。然而，也许最奇怪的是，这些人有时会以整个系统的小方式取笑；事实上，如果是匿名写的，他们的日报上几乎没有他们不会容忍甚至鼓掌的任何反对它的暗示，而如果同样的事情当着他们的面毫不含糊地说出来——主格动词和宾格都在正确的位置，怀疑是不可能的——他们会认为自己非常严肃、公正地感到愤怒，并指责说话者身体不适。

I never could understand (neither can I quite do so now, though I begin to see better what they mean) why a single currency should not suffice them; it would seem to me as though all their dealings would have been thus greatly simplified; but I was met with a look of horror if ever I dared to hint at it. Even those who to my certain knowledge kept only just enough money at the Musical Banks to swear by, would call the other banks (where their securities really lay) cold, deadening, paralysing, and the like.
我永远无法理解（我现在也不能完全理解它们的含义，尽管我开始更好地理解它们的含义）为什么单一货币不能满足它们；在我看来，他们所有的交易都会因此而大大简化。但如果我敢暗示这一点，我就会遭到惊恐的表情。据我所知，即使是那些在音乐银行只存了足够发誓的钱的人，也会称其他银行（他们的证券真正存放在那里）冷漠、麻木、瘫痪等等。

I noticed another thing, moreover, which struck me greatly. I was taken to the opening of one of these banks in a neighbouring town, and saw a large assemblage of cashiers and managers. I sat opposite them and scanned their faces attentively. They did not please me; they lacked, with few exceptions, the true Erewhonian frankness; and an equal number from any other class would have looked happier and better men. When I met them in the streets they did not seem like other people, but had, as a general rule, a cramped expression upon their faces which pained and depressed me.
此外，我还注意到另一件事，令我印象深刻。我被带到邻近城镇的其中一家银行的开业处，看到一大群出纳员和经理。我坐在他们对面，仔细地扫视他们的脸。他们不让我高兴；除了少数例外，他们缺乏真正的埃雷洪人的坦率。同等数量的其他阶级的人看起来会更快乐、更优秀。当我在街上遇见他们时，他们看起来不像其他人，但一般来说，他们的脸上都有一种局促的表情，这让我感到痛苦和沮丧。

Those who came from the country were better; they seemed to have lived less as a separate class, and to be freer and healthier; but in spite of my seeing not a few whose looks were benign and noble, I could not help asking myself concerning the greater number of those whom I met, whether Erewhon would be a better country if their expression were to be transferred to the people in general. I answered myself emphatically, no. The expression on the faces of the high Ydgrunites was that which one would wish to diffuse, and not that of the cashiers.
来自乡下的人更好；他们似乎不再像一个独立的阶级那样生活，而且更加自由和健康。但是，尽管我看到了不少看上去善良而高贵的人，但我还是忍不住问自己，对于我所遇到的更多人来说，如果将他们的表达转移到当地人民身上，埃里洪是否会成为一个更好的国家？一般的。我斩钉截铁地回答自己，不。伊古鲁人的高层脸上的表情是人们希望散布的表情，而不是收银员的表情。

A man’s expression is his sacrament; it is the outward and visible sign of his inward and spiritual grace, or want of grace; and as I looked at the a majority of these men, I could not help feeling that there must be a something in their lives which had stunted their natural development, and that they would have been more healthily minded in any other profession. I was always sorry for them, for in nine cases out of ten they were well-meaning persons; they were in the main very poorly paid; their constitutions were as a rule above suspicion; and there were recorded numberless instances of their self-sacrifice and generosity; but they had had the misfortune to have been betrayed into a false position at an age for the most part when their judgement was not matured, and after having been kept in studied ignorance of the real difficulties of the system. But this did not make their position the less a false one, and its bad effects upon themselves were unmistakable.
一个人的表达是他的圣礼；这是他内在和精神上的恩典或缺乏恩典的外在和可见的标志；当我看到这些人中的大多数时，我不禁感到他们的生活中一定有什么东西阻碍了他们的自然发展，而且他们在任何其他职业中都会有更健康的心态。我一直为他们感到难过，因为十有八九他们都是好心人；他们的工资大体上很低；他们的宪法通常是不容怀疑的。他们的自我牺牲和慷慨的事例被记录下来。但他们不幸的是，在他们的判断力尚未成熟的年龄，并且在对体制的真正困难一无所知之后，他们就被出卖到了一个错误的位置。但这并没有使他们的立场变得不那么虚假，而且这对他们自己造成的不良影响是显而易见的。

Few people would speak quite openly and freely before them, which struck me as a very bad sign. When they were in the room every one would talk as though all currency save that of the Musical Banks should be abolished; and yet they knew perfectly well that even the cashiers themselves hardly used the Musical Bank money more than other people. It was expected of them that they should appear to do so, but this was all. The less thoughtful of them did not seem particularly unhappy, but many were plainly sick at heart, though perhaps they hardly knew it, and would not have owned to being so. Some few were opponents of the whole system; but these were liable to be dismissed from their employment at any moment, and this rendered them very careful, for a man who had once been cashier at a Musical Bank was out of the field for other employment, and was generally unfitted for it by reason of that course of treatment which was commonly called his education. In fact it was a career from which retreat was virtually impossible, and into which young men were generally induced to enter before they could be reasonably expected, considering their training, to have formed any opinions of their own. Not unfrequently, indeed, they were induced, by what we in England should call undue influence, concealment, and fraud. Few indeed were those who had the courage to insist on seeing both sides of the question before they committed themselves to what was practically a leap in the dark. One would have thought that caution in this respect was an elementary principle,—one of the first things that an honourable man would teach his boy to understand; but in practice it was not so.
很少有人会在他们面前公开、自由地讲话，这对我来说是一个非常糟糕的迹象。当他们在房间里时，每个人都会谈论好像除了音乐银行之外的所有货币都应该被废除；然而他们非常清楚，即使是出纳员自己也并不比其他人更多地使用音乐银行的钱。人们期望他们会这样做，但仅此而已。他们中不太体贴的人似乎并没有特别不高兴，但许多人显然心里不舒服，尽管他们可能几乎不知道这一点，也不会承认自己是这样。有些人是整个体系的反对者；有些人是整个体系的反对者。但这些人随时都有可能被解雇，这让他们非常小心，因为曾经在音乐银行当过出纳员的人现在已经不再从事其他工作了，而且通常由于某种原因不适合做这份工作。那个治疗过程通常被称为他的教育。事实上，这是一个几乎不可能退出的职业，考虑到他们所受的训练，年轻人通常在可以合理地预期他们形成自己的观点之前就被诱导进入了这个职业。事实上，这种情况并不少见，是由我们英国人所谓的不当影响、隐瞒和欺诈所诱发的。确实很少有人有勇气坚持看到问题的两面，然后才做出实际上是在黑暗中跳跃的决定。人们可能会认为，在这方面的谨慎是一项基本原则，这是一个正直的人会教他的孩子首先要理解的事情之一；但实际上并非如此。

I even saw cases in which parents bought the right of presenting to the office of cashier at one of these banks, with the fixed determination that some one of their sons (perhaps a mere child) should fill it. There was the lad himself—growing up with every promise of becoming a good and honourable man—but utterly without warning concerning the iron shoe which his natural protector was providing for him. Who could say that the whole thing would not end in a life-long lie, and vain chafing to escape? I confess that there were few things in Erewhon which shocked me more than this.
我什至看到这样的案例，父母购买了这些银行之一出纳办公室的出纳权，并坚定地认为他们的某个儿子（也许只是一个孩子）应该担任这一职务。还有那个小伙子本人——在成长过程中，他满怀成为一个善良而值得尊​​敬的人的承诺——但完全没有警告过他的天然保护者为他提供的铁鞋。谁能说这一切不会以终生的谎言和徒劳的逃避而告终呢？我承认，在埃里洪，没有什么比这更让我震惊的了。

Yet we do something not so very different from this even in England, and as regards the dual commercial system, all countries have, and have had, a law of the land, and also another law, which, though professedly more sacred, has far less effect on their daily life and actions. It seems as though the need for some law over and above, and sometimes even conflicting with, the law of the land, must spring from something that lies deep down in man’s nature; indeed, it is hard to think that man could ever have become man at all, but for the gradual evolution of a perception that though this world looms so large when we are in it, it may seem a little thing when we have got away from it.
然而，即使在英国，我们所做的事情也与此没有太大不同，并且就双重商业制度而言，所有国家都拥有并且曾经拥有一项土地法，以及另一项法律，尽管该法律自称更神圣，但远非如此。对他们的日常生活和行动的影响较小。似乎对某种超越当地法律、有时甚至与当地法律相冲突的法律的需要，必定源于人类本性深处的某些东西；事实上，很难想象人能成为人，但随着人们逐渐形成这样一种观念，即虽然当我们身处其中时，这个世界显得如此巨大，但当我们远离这个世界时，它可能显得微不足道。它。

When man had grown to the perception that in the everlasting Is- and-Is-Not of nature, the world and all that it contains, including man, is at the same time both seen and unseen, he felt the need of two rules of life, one for the seen, and the other for the unseen side of things. For the laws affecting the seen world he claimed the sanction of seen powers; for the unseen (of which he knows nothing save that it exists and is powerful) he appealed to the unseen power (of which, again, he knows nothing save that it exists and is powerful) to which he gives the name of God.
当人类逐渐认识到，在自然界永恒的“是与非”中，世界及其所包含的一切，包括人类，同时既是可见的又是不可见的，他感到需要两条规则：生活，一个是为了看得见的一面，另一个是为了看不见的一面。对于影响可见世界的法律，他要求可见权力的认可。对于看不见的力量（除了它的存在和强大之外，他一无所知），他诉诸于看不见的力量（除了它的存在和强大之外，他一无所知），他将这种力量称为上帝。

Some Erewhonian opinions concerning the intelligence of the unborn embryo, that I regret my space will not permit me to lay before the reader, have led me to conclude that the Erewhonian Musical Banks, and perhaps the religious systems of all countries, are now more or less of an attempt to uphold the unfathomable and unconscious instinctive wisdom of millions of past generations, against the comparatively shallow, consciously reasoning, and ephemeral conclusions drawn from that of the last thirty or forty.
一些关于未出生胚胎的智力的埃雷洪尼亚观点，我很遗憾我的篇幅不允许我向读者展示，这些观点使我得出这样的结论：埃雷洪尼亚音乐库，也许还有所有国家的宗教体系，现在或多或少都已经存在了。更不是试图维护过去数百万代人深不可测和无意识的本能智慧，反对过去三十或四十代人得出的相对肤浅的、有意识的推理和短暂的结论。

The saving feature of the Erewhonian Musical Bank system (as distinct from the quasi-idolatrous views which coexist with it, and on which I will touch later) was that while it bore witness to the existence of a kingdom that is not of this world, it made no attempt to pierce the veil that hides it from human eyes. It is here that almost all religions go wrong. Their priests try to make us believe that they know more about the unseen world than those whose eyes are still blinded by the seen, can ever know—forgetting that while to deny the existence of an unseen kingdom is bad, to pretend that we know more about it than its bare existence is no better.
埃雷洪尼亚音乐银行系统的拯救特征（与与之共存的准偶像崇拜观点不同，我稍后会谈到）是，虽然它见证了一个不属于这个世界的王国的存在，它并没有试图刺破人类眼睛看不见的面纱。正是在这里，几乎所有的宗教都出了问题。他们的祭司试图让我们相信，他们对看不见的世界的了解比那些眼睛仍然被看得见的东西蒙蔽的人所能知道的要多——忘记了，虽然否认看不见的王国的存在是不好的，但假装我们知道得更多关于它，并不比它的存在好多少。

This chapter is already longer than I intended, but I should like to say that in spite of the saving feature of which I have just spoken, I cannot help thinking that the Erewhonians are on the eve of some great change in their religious opinions, or at any rate in that part of them which finds expression through their Musical Banks. So far as I could see, fully ninety per cent. of the population of the metropolis looked upon these banks with something not far removed from contempt. If this is so, any such startling event as is sure to arise sooner or later, may serve as nucleus to a new order of things that will be more in harmony with both the heads and hearts of the people.
本章已经比我预想的要长了，但我想说的是，尽管我刚才谈到了拯救的特点，我还是忍不住想，埃雷洪尼亚人正处于他们的宗教观念发生重大变化的前夕，或者无论如何，他们的那部分通过他们的音乐库得到表达。据我所知，百分之九十。这座大都市的居民以近乎蔑视的目光看待这些银行。如果真是这样，那么任何迟早肯定会发生的令人震惊的事件都可能成为新秩序的核心，而新秩序将更加符合人们的头脑和心灵。

CHAPTER XVI: AROWHENA
第十六章：阿罗维娜

The reader will perhaps have learned by this time a thing which I had myself suspected before I had been twenty-four hours in Mr. Nosnibor’s house—I mean, that though the Nosnibors showed me every attention, I could not cordially like them, with the exception of Arowhena who was quite different from the rest. They were not fair samples of Erewhonians. I saw many families with whom they were on visiting terms, whose manners charmed me more than I know how to say, but I never could get over my original prejudice against Mr. Nosnibor for having embezzled the money. Mrs. Nosnibor, too, was a very worldly woman, yet to hear her talk one would have thought that she was singularly the reverse; neither could I endure Zulora; Arowhena however was perfection.
读者此时也许已经了解到一件事，在我在诺斯尼伯先生家里待了二十四小时之前，我自己就曾怀疑过这一点——我的意思是，尽管诺斯尼伯一家对我表现出极大的关注，但我无法真诚地喜欢他们，因为阿罗菲娜是个例外，她与其他人截然不同。他们不是埃雷洪人的公平样本。我见到了许多与他们有过往往来的家庭，他们的举止让我着迷得难以言喻，但我始终无法克服对诺斯尼博尔先生贪污钱财的最初偏见。诺斯尼伯夫人也是一位非常世俗的女人，但听她说话，人们会认为她恰恰相反；我也无法忍受祖洛拉；然而，Arowhena 却是完美的。

She it was who ran all the little errands for her mother and Mr. Nosnibor and Zulora, and gave those thousand proofs of sweetness and unselfishness which some one member of a family is generally required to give. All day long it was Arowhena this, and Arowhena that; but she never seemed to know that she was being put upon, and was always bright and willing from morning till evening. Zulora certainly was very handsome, but Arowhena was infinitely the more graceful of the two and was the very ne plus ultra of youth and beauty. I will not attempt to describe her, for anything that I could say would fall so far short of the reality as only to mislead the reader. Let him think of the very loveliest that he can imagine, and he will still be below the truth. Having said this much, I need hardly say that I had fallen in love with her.
正是她为她的母亲、诺斯尼博尔先生和祖罗拉跑了所有的小差事，并提供了成千上万的甜蜜和无私的证明，而这些是一个家庭中的某个成员通常需要提供的。整天都是阿罗时那这个，阿罗时那那个；但她似乎从来不知道自己被欺骗了，从早到晚总是神采奕奕、心甘情愿。祖洛拉确实非常英俊，但阿罗维娜在两人中更加优雅，而且是最年轻和最美丽的一个。我不会试图描述她，因为我能说的任何话都与现实相去甚远，只会误导读者。让他去想他能想象到的最可爱的事情，他仍然会低于事实。说了这么多，不用说我已经爱上她了。

She must have seen what I felt for her, but I tried my hardest not to let it appear even by the slightest sign. I had many reasons for this. I had no idea what Mr. and Mrs. Nosnibor would say to it; and I knew that Arowhena would not look at me (at any rate not yet) if her father and mother disapproved, which they probably would, considering that I had nothing except the pension of about a pound a day of our money which the King had granted me. I did not yet know of a more serious obstacle.
她一定看出了我对她的感情，但我尽力不让它表现出来，哪怕是最轻微的迹象。我这样做有很多原因。我不知道诺斯尼博尔先生和诺斯尼博尔夫人会对它说什么；我知道，如果她的父母不同意，阿罗维娜不会看我（至少现在还不会），他们很可能会的，考虑到我除了国王每天大约一英镑的养老金之外一无所有。授予我。我还不知道还有什么更严重的障碍。

In the meantime, I may say that I had been presented at court, and was told that my reception had been considered as singularly gracious; indeed, I had several interviews both with the King and Queen, at which from time to time the Queen got everything from me that I had in the world, clothes and all, except the two buttons I had given to Yram, the loss of which seemed to annoy her a good deal. I was presented with a court suit, and her Majesty had my old clothes put upon a wooden dummy, on which they probably remain, unless they have been removed in consequence of my subsequent downfall. His Majesty’s manners were those of a cultivated English gentleman. He was much pleased at hearing that our government was monarchical, and that the mass of the people were resolute that it should not be changed; indeed, I was so much encouraged by the evident pleasure with which he heard me, that I ventured to quote to him those beautiful lines of Shakespeare’s -
与此同时，我可以说，我已经被带到法庭，并被告知我的接待被认为是异常亲切的。事实上，我与国王和王后进行了几次会面，王后时不时地从我那里得到了我在世界上拥有的一切，衣服等等，除了我给伊拉姆的两颗纽扣，这颗纽扣丢失了。似乎让她很恼火。我收到了一份法庭诉讼，女王陛下把我的旧衣服放在一个木制假人身上，它们可能会留在上面，除非它们因我随后的垮台而被移走。国王陛下的举止是一位有教养的英国绅士的举止。当他听说我们的政府是君主制的，而且人民群众坚决不应该改变它时，他感到非常高兴。事实上，他听到我讲话时的明显愉悦使我深受鼓舞，以至于我斗胆向他引用莎士比亚的那些美丽的台词——

‘There’s a divinity doth hedge a king, Rough hew him how we may;.’
“有一位神灵围困着一位国王，我们可以如何粗暴地砍伐他；”

but I was sorry I had done so afterwards, for I do not think his Majesty admired the lines as much as I could have wished.
但事后我很遗憾自己这样做了，因为我认为国王陛下并不像我所希望的那样欣赏这些诗句。

There is no occasion for me to dwell further upon my experience of the court, but I ought perhaps to allude to one of my conversations with the King, inasmuch as it was pregnant with the most important consequences.
我没有机会进一步详述我在法庭上的经历，但我也许应该提及我与国王的一次谈话，因为它孕育着最重要的后果。

He had been asking me about my watch, and enquiring whether such dangerous inventions were tolerated in the country from which I came. I owned with some confusion that watches were not uncommon; but observing the gravity which came over his Majesty’s face I presumed to say that they were fast dying out, and that we had few if any other mechanical contrivances of which he was likely to disapprove. Upon his asking me to name some of our most advanced machines, I did not dare to tell him of our steam-engines and railroads and electric telegraphs, and was puzzling my brains to think what I could say, when, of all things in the world, balloons suggested themselves, and I gave him an account of a very remarkable ascent which was made some years ago. The King was too polite to contradict, but I felt sure that he did not believe me, and from that day forward though he always showed me the attention which was due to my genius (for in this light was my complexion regarded), he never questioned me about the manners and customs of my country.
他一直在问我手表的事，并询问我的祖国是否容忍这种危险的发明。我有些困惑地承认，手表并不罕见。但是，观察国王陛下脸上的严肃表情，我猜想它们正在迅速消失，而且我们几乎没有任何其他机械发明，他可能会不赞成。当他让我说出一些我们最先进的机器时，我不敢告诉他我们的蒸汽机、铁路和电报，我绞尽脑汁地想，在世界上的所有事物中，我能说些什么呢？我向他讲述了几年前一次非常了不起的攀登。国王很有礼貌，没有反驳，但我确信他不相信我，从那天起，尽管他总是对我表现出由于我的天才而引起的关注（因为从这个角度来看我的肤色），他从来没有问我有关我国的风俗习惯。

To return, however, to Arowhena. I soon gathered that neither Mr. nor Mrs. Nosnibor would have any objection to my marrying into the family; a physical excellence is considered in Erewhon as a set off against almost any other disqualification, and my light hair was sufficient to make me an eligible match. But along with this welcome fact I gathered another which filled me with dismay: I was expected to marry Zulora, for whom I had already conceived a great aversion. At first I hardly noticed the little hints and the artifices which were resorted to in order to bring us together, but after a time they became too plain. Zulora, whether she was in love with me or not, was bent on marrying me, and I gathered in talking with a young gentleman of my acquaintance who frequently visited the house and whom I greatly disliked, that it was considered a sacred and inviolable rule that whoever married into a family must marry the eldest daughter at that time unmarried. The young gentleman urged this upon me so frequently that I at last saw he was in love with Arowhena himself, and wanted me to get Zulora out of the way; but others told me the same story as to the custom of the country, and I saw there was a serious difficulty. My only comfort was that Arowhena snubbed my rival and would not look at him. Neither would she look at me; nevertheless there was a difference in the manner of her disregard; this was all I could get from her.
然而，我们还是要回到阿罗维纳。我很快就发现，诺斯尼伯先生和诺斯尼伯太太都不会反对我嫁入这个家族。在埃里洪，出色的身体素质被认为是对抗几乎所有其他取消资格的条件，而我的浅色头发足以使我成为合格的比赛对象。但除了这个令人欣喜的事实之外，我还发现了另一个令我沮丧的事实：我本来已经对祖罗拉产生了极大的厌恶，但我却被期望嫁给他。起初，我几乎没有注意到为了让我们走到一起而采取的小暗示和技巧，但过了一段时间，它们就变得太简单了。祖罗拉，无论她是否爱我，都一心要嫁给我，我和一位经常来我家拜访、我非常不喜欢的熟人年轻绅士交谈时，我认为这是一条神圣不可侵犯的规则。凡嫁入一个家庭的，必须娶当时未婚的长女。这位年轻的绅士如此频繁地向我提出这一点，以至于我终于看出他爱上了阿罗维纳本人，并希望我把祖洛拉让开。但其他人告诉我同样的故事，关于这个国家的习俗，我看到了一个严重的困难。唯一让我感到安慰的是，阿罗维娜冷落了我的对手，连看都不看他一眼。她也不肯看我；然而，她的漠视方式却有所不同。这是我能从她那里得到的一切。

Not that she avoided me; on the contrary I had many a tete-a-tete with her, for her mother and sister were anxious for me to deposit some part of my pension in the Musical Banks, this being in accordance with the dictates of their goddess Ydgrun, of whom both Mrs. Nosnibor and Zulora were great devotees. I was not sure whether I had kept my secret from being perceived by Arowhena herself, but none of the others suspected me, so she was set upon me to get me to open an account, at any rate pro forma, with the Musical Banks; and I need hardly say that she succeeded. But I did not yield at once; I enjoyed the process of being argued with too keenly to lose it by a prompt concession; besides, a little hesitation rendered the concession itself more valuable. It was in the course of conversations on this subject that I learned the more defined religious opinions of the Erewhonians, that coexist with the Musical Bank system, but are not recognised by those curious institutions. I will describe them as briefly as possible in the following chapters before I return to the personal adventures of Arowhena and myself.
并不是说她回避了我；而是她回避了我。相反，我与她进行了多次面对面的交谈，因为她的母亲和姐姐急于让我将部分养老金存入音乐银行，这是按照她们的女神伊德格林的指示进行的，其中诺斯尼伯夫人和祖洛拉夫人都是伟大的奉献者。我不确定我是否保守了秘密，不让阿罗希娜本人发现，但其他人都没有怀疑我，所以她决定让我在音乐银行开一个账户，至少是形式上的；我几乎不用说她成功了。但我并没有立刻屈服；我很享受与人激烈争论的过程，我不会因为迅速让步而失去它。此外，一点点的犹豫就使让步本身变得更有价值。正是在关于这个主题的对话过程中，我了解到埃雷洪人更明确的宗教观点，这些观点与音乐银行系统共存，但不被那些好奇的机构认可。在我回到 Arowhena 和我自己的个人冒险之前，我将在接下来的章节中尽可能简要地描述它们。

They were idolaters, though of a comparatively enlightened kind; but here, as in other things, there was a discrepancy between their professed and actual belief, for they had a genuine and potent faith which existed without recognition alongside of their idol worship.
他们是偶像崇拜者，尽管属于比较开明的那种。但在这里，就像在其他事情上一样，他们所宣称的信仰和实际的信仰之间存在着差异，因为他们有一种真正而有力的信仰，这种信仰与他们的偶像崇拜并存，但没有得到承认。

The gods whom they worship openly are personifications of human qualities, as justice, strength, hope, fear, love, &c., &c. The people think that prototypes of these have a real objective existence in a region far beyond the clouds, holding, as did the ancients, that they are like men and women both in body and passion, except that they are even comelier and more powerful, and also that they can render themselves invisible to human eyesight. They are capable of being propitiated by mankind and of coming to the assistance of those who ask their aid. Their interest in human affairs is keen, and on the whole beneficent; but they become very angry if neglected, and punish rather the first they come upon, than the actual person who has offended them; their fury being blind when it is raised, though never raised without reason. They will not punish with any less severity when people sin against them from ignorance, and without the chance of having had knowledge; they will take no excuses of this kind, but are even as the English law, which assumes itself to be known to every one.
他们公开崇拜的神是人类品质的化身，如正义、力量、希望、恐惧、爱等等。人们认为它们的原型在遥远的云层之外真实客观存在，认为它们和古人一样，无论是肉体还是情欲，都像男人和女人一样，只是更加美丽、更加强大，而且它们可以使自己对人类的视力来说是不可见的。他们能够得到人类的安抚，并能够向那些向他们求助的人提供帮助。他们对人类事务非常感兴趣，而且总体上是仁慈的。但如果受到忽视，他们就会非常生气，并且会惩罚他们第一个遇到的人，而不是真正冒犯他们的人。他们的愤怒在爆发时是盲目的，尽管从来不会无缘无故地爆发。当人们因无知而没有获得知识的机会而得罪他们时，他们不会以更严厉的方式惩罚他们；他们不会采取此类借口，而是就像英国法律一样，它假定自己是人人都知道的。

Thus they have a law that two pieces of matter may not occupy the same space at the same moment, which law is presided over and administered by the gods of time and space jointly, so that if a flying stone and a man’s head attempt to outrage these gods, by ‘arrogating a right which they do not possess’ (for so it is written in one of their books), and to occupy the same space simultaneously, a severe punishment, sometimes even death itself, is sure to follow, without any regard to whether the stone knew that the man’s head was there, or the head the stone; this at least is their view of the common accidents of life. Moreover, they hold their deities to be quite regardless of motives. With them it is the thing done which is everything, and the motive goes for nothing.
因此他们有一个法则，即两块物质不能同时占据同一个空间，这个法则是由时空诸神共同主持和管理的，因此，如果一块飞石和一个人头试图激怒这些神通过“剥夺他们不拥有的权利”（因为他们的一本书中是这么写的），并同时占据同一个空间，严厉的惩罚，有时甚至是死亡本身，肯定会随之而来，而无需担心。是否考虑到石头是否知道那个人的头在那里，或者石头是否知道头在那里；这至少是他们对生活中常见事故的看法。此外，无论动机如何，他们都认为自己的神是完全独立的。对他们来说，所做的事情就是一切，动机毫无意义。

Thus they hold it strictly forbidden for a man to go without common air in his lungs for more than a very few minutes; and if by any chance he gets into the water, the air-god is very angry, and will not suffer it; no matter whether the man got into the water by accident or on purpose, whether through the attempt to save a child or through presumptuous contempt of the air-god, the air-god will kill him, unless he keeps his head high enough out of the water, and thus gives the air-god his due.
因此，他们严格禁止一个人在肺部没有空气的情况下行走超过几分钟。如果他万一掉进水里，空气之神就会非常生气，不会容忍。无论这个人是偶然还是故意落入水中，无论是为了拯救一个孩子还是出于对空气之神的傲慢蔑视，空气之神都会杀死他，除非他把头保持得足够高，以免被水淹没。水，从而给予空气神应得的。

This with regard to the deities who manage physical affairs. Over and above these they personify hope, fear, love, and so forth, giving them temples and priests, and carving likenesses of them in stone, which they verily believe to be faithful representations of living beings who are only not human in being more than human. If any one denies the objective existence of these divinities, and says that there is really no such being as a beautiful woman called Justice, with her eyes blinded and a pair of scales, positively living and moving in a remote and ethereal region, but that justice is only the personified expression of certain modes of human thought and action—they say that he denies the existence of justice in denying her personality, and that he is a wanton disturber of men’s religious convictions. They detest nothing so much as any attempt to lead them to higher spiritual conceptions of the deities whom they profess to worship. Arowhena and I had a pitched battle on this point, and should have had many more but for my prudence in allowing her to get the better of me.
这是关于管理物质事务的神灵。除此之外，他们将希望、恐惧、爱等等人格化，为他们提供寺庙和祭司，并在石头上雕刻他们的肖像，他们坚信这些是生物的忠实代表，而这些生物只是在本质上不是人类而已。人类。如果有人否认这些神祇的客观存在，并说确实不存在一位名叫正义的美丽女子，双目失明，长着一对鳞片，在遥远而空灵的地方积极地生活和活动，但那正义只是人类某些思想和行为模式的拟人化表达——他们说他否认了正义的存在，就否定了她的人格，说他是对人类宗教信仰的肆意扰乱者。他们最讨厌任何试图引导他们对他们自称崇拜的神明产生更高精神观念的行为。阿罗维娜和我在这一点上发生了一场激烈的争斗，如果不是我谨慎地让她占了上风，本来应该有更多的争斗。

I am sure that in her heart she was suspicious of her own position for she returned more than once to the subject. ‘Can you not see,’ I had exclaimed, ‘that the fact of justice being admirable will not be affected by the absence of a belief in her being also a living agent? Can you really think that men will be one whit less hopeful, because they no longer believe that hope is an actual person?’ She shook her head, and said that with men’s belief in the personality all incentive to the reverence of the thing itself, as justice or hope, would cease; men from that hour would never be either just or hopeful again.
我相信她心里对自己的立场有所怀疑，因为她不止一次回到这个话题。 “你难道看不出来吗，”我大声说道，“正义令人钦佩的事实不会因为不相信她也是一个活着的代理人而受到影响吗？”你真的认为男人会因为不再相信希望是一个真实的人而变得不那么有希望吗？”她摇了摇头，说男人对人格的信仰都会激发对事物本身的敬畏，正义或希望都会消失；从那时起，人们就再也不会公正或充满希望了。

I could not move her, nor, indeed, did I seriously wish to do so. She deferred to me in most things, but she never shrank from maintaining her opinions if they were put in question; nor does she to this day abate one jot of her belief in the religion of her childhood, though in compliance with my repeated entreaties she has allowed herself to be baptized into the English Church. She has, however, made a gloss upon her original faith to the effect that her baby and I are the only human beings exempt from the vengeance of the deities for not believing in their personality. She is quite clear that we are exempted. She should never have so strong a conviction of it otherwise. How it has come about she does not know, neither does she wish to know; there are things which it is better not to know and this is one of them; but when I tell her that I believe in her deities as much as she does—and that it is a difference about words, not things, she becomes silent with a slight emphasis.
我无法感动她，事实上，我也不想这么做。她在大多数事情上都听从我的意见，但如果有人质疑她的观点，她也毫不犹豫地坚持自己的观点。尽管在我一再的恳求下，她接受了英国教会的洗礼，但直到今天，她对童年时所信奉的宗教的信仰也没有丝毫减弱。然而，她对她最初的信仰进行了粉饰，大意是她的孩子和我是唯一可以免受神灵报复的人类，因为他们不相信他们的人格。她很清楚我们是豁免的。否则她不应该有如此强烈的信念。她不知道，也不想知道这是怎么发生的。有些事情最好不要知道，这就是其中之一；但当我告诉她我和她一样相信她的神灵时——而且区别在于言语，而不是事物，她变得沉默了，并略微加重了语气。
