I own that she very nearly conquered me once; for she asked me what I should think if she were to tell me that my God, whose nature and attributes I had been explaining to her, was but the expression for man’s highest conception of goodness, wisdom, and power; that in order to generate a more vivid conception of so great and glorious a thought, man had personified it and called it by a name; that it was an unworthy conception of the Deity to hold Him personal, inasmuch as escape from human contingencies became thus impossible; that the real thing men should worship was the Divine, whereinsoever they could find it; that ‘God’ was but man’s way of expressing his sense of the Divine; that as justice, hope, wisdom, &c., were all parts of goodness, so God was the expression which embraced all goodness and all good power; that people would no more cease to love God on ceasing to believe in His objective personality, than they had ceased to love justice on discovering that she was not really personal; nay, that they would never truly love Him till they saw Him thus.
我承认她有一次差一点就征服了我。因为她问我，如果她告诉我，我向她解释过的上帝的本性和属性，只是人类对善良、智慧和力量的最高概念的表达，我会怎么想？为了对如此伟大和光荣的思想产生更生动的概念，人类将其拟人化并为其命名；将他视为个人是一种不值得的神性观念，因为这样就不可能逃脱人类的意外事件；人们应该崇拜的真正事物是神，无论他们能在哪里找到它； “上帝”不过是人表达其神圣感的方式；正如正义、希望、智慧等都是良善的组成部分一样，上帝也是包含所有良善和所有良善力量的表达；人们不会因为不再相信上帝的客观人格而不再爱上帝，就像他们不会因为发现正义并非真正的人格而不再热爱正义一样；不仅如此，他们永远不会真正爱他，直到他们看到他这样。

She said all this in her artless way, and with none of the coherence with which I have here written it; her face kindled, and she felt sure that she had convinced me that I was wrong, and that justice was a living person. Indeed I did wince a little; but I recovered myself immediately, and pointed out to her that we had books whose genuineness was beyond all possibility of doubt, as they were certainly none of them less than 1800 years old; that in these there were the most authentic accounts of men who had been spoken to by the Deity Himself, and of one prophet who had been allowed to see the back parts of God through the hand that was laid over his face.
她以一种天真无邪的方式说出了这一切，而且完全不像我在这里写的那样连贯。她的脸红了，她确信她已经让我相信我错了，正义是活生生的。事实上，我确实有点畏缩了；但我立刻恢复了平静，并向她指出我们拥有的书籍的真实性是不容置疑的，因为它们的历史肯定不低于 1800 年。其中有关于神亲自与人类交谈的最真实的记载，以及一位先知被允许通过放在神的脸上的手看到他的背部的故事。

This was conclusive; and I spoke with such solemnity that she was a little frightened, and only answered that they too had their books, in which their ancestors had seen the gods; on which I saw that further argument was not at all likely to convince her; and fearing that she might tell her mother what I had been saying, and that I might lose the hold upon her affections which I was beginning to feel pretty sure that I was obtaining, I began to let her have her own way, and to convince me; neither till after we were safely married did I show the cloven hoof again.
这是决定性的；我说话的语气如此严肃，让她有点害怕，只是回答说他们也有他们的书，他们的祖先在书里见过众神。我发现进一步的争论根本不可能说服她。我担心她会把我刚才说的话告诉她母亲，而我可能会失去对她的感情的控制，而我开始确信我已经获得了她的感情，我开始让她按照自己的方式行事，并说服她我;直到我们安全结婚后，我才再次露出偶蹄子。

Nevertheless, her remarks have haunted me, and I have since met with many very godly people who have had a great knowledge of divinity, but no sense of the divine: and again, I have seen a radiance upon the face of those who were worshipping the divine either in art or nature—in picture or statue—in field or cloud or sea—in man, woman, or child—which I have never seen kindled by any talking about the nature and attributes of God. Mention but the word divinity, and our sense of the divine is clouded.
尽管如此，她的言论一直困扰着我，从那以后我遇到了许多非常敬虔的人，他们对神性有丰富的知识，但对神性却没有任何感觉：我再次看到那些正在敬拜的人脸上焕发出光彩无论是在艺术中还是在自然中——在图画或雕像中——在田野、云彩或海洋中——在男人、女人或孩子中——我从未见过任何谈论上帝的本质和属性而点燃这种神圣感。只要提到“神性”这个词，我们对神的感觉就会变得模糊。

CHAPTER XVII: YDGRUN AND THE YDGRUNITES
第十七章：YDGRUN 和 YDGRUNITES

In spite of all the to-do they make about their idols, and the temples they build, and the priests and priestesses whom they support, I could never think that their professed religion was more than skin-deep; but they had another which they carried with them into all their actions; and although no one from the outside of things would suspect it to have any existence at all, it was in reality their great guide, the mariner’s compass of their lives; so that there were very few things which they ever either did, or refrained from doing, without reference to its precepts.
尽管他们对自己的偶像、他们建造的寺庙、他们支持的祭司和女祭司做了很多事情，但我从来不认为他们所宣称的宗教不仅仅是肤浅的；他们的宗教信仰只是表面上的。但他们还有另外一个东西，他们将其带入他们所有的行动中。尽管外界根本不会怀疑它的存在，但它实际上是他们伟大的指南，是航海者生活的指南针。因此，他们做或不做的事情很少是不参考其戒律的。

Now I suspected that their professed faith had no great hold upon them—firstly, because I often heard the priests complain of the prevailing indifference, and they would hardly have done so without reason; secondly, because of the show which was made, for there was none of this about the worship of the goddess Ydgrun, in whom they really did believe; thirdly, because though the priests were constantly abusing Ydgrun as being the great enemy of the gods, it was well known that she had no more devoted worshippers in the whole country than these very persons, who were often priests of Ydgrun rather than of their own deities. Neither am I by any means sure that these were not the best of the priests.
现在我怀疑他们所宣称的信仰对他们没有太大的吸引力——首先，因为我经常听到牧师抱怨普遍的冷漠态度，他们几乎不会毫无理由地这样做；其次，因为所进行的表演，因为没有任何关于对伊德格伦女神的崇拜的内容，而他们确实相信伊德格伦女神。第三，因为尽管祭司们不断地辱骂伊德古伦，称其为众神的大敌，但众所周知，在整个国家，她没有比这些人更忠实的崇拜者了，他们往往是伊德古伦的祭司，而不是他们自己的祭司。神灵。我也不能肯定这些人不是最好的牧师。

Ydgrun certainly occupied a very anomalous position; she was held to be both omnipresent and omnipotent, but she was not an elevated conception, and was sometimes both cruel and absurd. Even her most devoted worshippers were a little ashamed of her, and served her more with heart and in deed than with their tongues. Theirs was no lip service; on the contrary, even when worshipping her most devoutly, they would often deny her. Take her all in all, however, she was a beneficent and useful deity, who did not care how much she was denied so long as she was obeyed and feared, and who kept hundreds of thousands in those paths which make life tolerably happy, who would never have been kept there otherwise, and over whom a higher and more spiritual ideal would have had no power.
伊格伦无疑占据了一个非常不寻常的位置；她被认为是无所不在、无所不能的，但她并不是一个崇高的概念，有时甚至是残酷和荒谬的。即使是她最忠实的崇拜者也对她感到有点羞耻，他们更多地用心和行动来侍奉她，而不是用舌头。他们的言论并非口头上的承诺。相反，即使他们最虔诚地崇拜她，他们也常常否认她。然而，总而言之，她是一位仁慈而有用的神灵，只要人们服从和敬畏她，她就不在乎自己被拒绝多少，她让成千上万的人走在那些让生活过上幸福的道路上，她否则，他们永远不会被留在那里，更高、更精神的理想也无法对他们产生影响。

I greatly doubt whether the Erewhonians are yet prepared for any better religion, and though (considering my gradually strengthened conviction that they were the representatives of the lost tribes of Israel) I would have set about converting them at all hazards had I seen the remotest prospect of success, I could hardly contemplate the displacement of Ydgrun as the great central object of their regard without admitting that it would be attended with frightful consequences; in fact were I a mere philosopher, I should say that the gradual raising of the popular conception of Ydgrun would be the greatest spiritual boon which could be conferred upon them, and that nothing could effect this except example. I generally found that those who complained most loudly that Ydgrun was not high enough for them had hardly as yet come up to the Ydgrun standard, and I often met with a class of men whom I called to myself ‘high Ydgrunites’ (the rest being Ydgrunites, and low Ydgrunites), who, in the matter of human conduct and the affairs of life, appeared to me to have got about as far as it is in the right nature of man to go.
我非常怀疑埃瑞洪人是否已经准备好接受任何更好的宗教，尽管如此（考虑到我逐渐坚定的信念，他们是以色列失落部落的代表），如果我看到最遥远的前景，我会不惜一切危险开始改变他们的信仰成功之后，我几乎无法想象伊格伦被取代，成为他们关注的伟大中心目标，而不承认这会带来可怕的后果。事实上，如果我只是一个哲学家，我应该说，伊德格林的普遍观念的逐渐提高将是可以赋予​​他们的最大的精神恩惠，除了榜样之外，没有什么可以影响这一点。我通常发现那些大声抱怨伊德格林对他们来说不够高的人几乎还没有达到伊德格林的标准，而且我经常遇到一类人，我称他们自己为“高伊德格林人”（其余的是在我看来，他们在人类行为和生活事务方面已经做到了人类正确本性所能做到的程度。

They were gentlemen in the full sense of the word; and what has one not said in saying this? They seldom spoke of Ydgrun, or even alluded to her, but would never run counter to her dictates without ample reason for doing so: in such cases they would override her with due self-reliance, and the goddess seldom punished them; for they are brave, and Ydgrun is not. They had most of them a smattering of the hypothetical language, and some few more than this, but only a few. I do not think that this language has had much hand in making them what they are; but rather that the fact of their being generally possessed of its rudiments was one great reason for the reverence paid to the hypothetical language itself.
他们是真正意义上的绅士。这句话还有什么没有说的呢？他们很少谈论伊格伦，甚至很少提及她，但如果没有充分的理由，他们绝不会违背她的命令：在这种情况下，他们会以应有的自力更生凌驾于她之上，女神很少惩罚他们;因为他们很勇敢，而伊格伦则不然。他们中的大多数人都掌握了一些假设性的语言，也有一些比这更多，但也只是少数。我不认为这种语言对它们的形成有多大作用；相反，它们普遍具备基本语言这一事实​​是人们对假想语言本身表示敬意的一个重要原因。

Being inured from youth to exercises and athletics of all sorts, and living fearlessly under the eye of their peers, among whom there exists a high standard of courage, generosity, honour, and every good and manly quality—what wonder that they should have become, so to speak, a law unto themselves; and, while taking an elevated view of the goddess Ydgrun, they should have gradually lost all faith in the recognised deities of the country? These they do not openly disregard, for conformity until absolutely intolerable is a law of Ydgrun, yet they have no real belief in the objective existence of beings which so readily explain themselves as abstractions, and whose personality demands a quasi-materialism which it baffles the imagination to realise. They keep their opinions, however, greatly to themselves, inasmuch as most of their countrymen feel strongly about the gods, and they hold it wrong to give pain, unless for some greater good than seems likely to arise from their plain speaking.
从年轻时起就习惯了各种锻炼和运动，在同龄人的注视下无所畏惧地生活，在同龄人中存在着高标准的勇气、慷慨、荣誉以及一切善良和男子气概的品质——他们应该成为什么样的人，这有什么奇怪的？可以说，这是一条自成一体的法则；而且，在崇高地崇拜伊格伦女神的同时，他们应该逐渐失去对该国公认的神祇的所有信仰吗？他们并没有公开忽视这些，因为除非绝对不能容忍，否则从众是伊德格林的法则，但他们并不真正相信存在者的客观存在，这些存在者很容易将自己解释为抽象，其个性要求一种准唯物主义，这让他们感到困惑。想象来实现。然而，他们非常保守自己的观点，因为他们的大多数同胞对诸神都有强烈的感情，他们认为给予痛苦是错误的，除非是为了一些比他们的直言不讳可能产生的更大的利益。

On the other hand, surely those whose own minds are clear about any given matter (even though it be only that there is little certainty) should go so far towards imparting that clearness to others, as to say openly what they think and why they think it, whenever they can properly do so; for they may be sure that they owe their own clearness almost entirely to the fact that others have done this by them: after all, they may be mistaken, and if so, it is for their own and the general well-being that they should let their error be seen as distinctly as possible, so that it may be more easily refuted. I own, therefore, that on this one point I disapproved of the practice even of the highest Ydgrunites, and objected to it all the more because I knew that I should find my own future task more easy if the high Ydgrunites had already undermined the belief which is supposed to prevail at present.
另一方面，那些自己的头脑对任何特定问题都清楚的人（即使只是没有什么确定性）当然应该将这种清晰性传递给他人，公开说出他们的想法以及他们为什么这么想只要他们能够适当地这样做；因为他们可能确信，他们自己的清晰几乎完全归功于其他人已经通过他们做到了这一点：毕竟，他们可能是错误的，如果是这样，那么为了他们自己和普遍的福祉，他们应该让他们的错误尽可能清晰地被看到，这样就更容易被驳斥。因此，我承认，在这一点上，我什至不赞成最高级别的伊格鲁尼派的做法，并且更加反对它，因为我知道，如果高级伊格鲁尼派已经破坏了这一信仰，我会发现自己未来的任务会更容易。目前应该盛行。

In other respects they were more like the best class of Englishmen than any whom I have seen in other countries. I should have liked to have persuaded half-a-dozen of them to come over to England and go upon the stage, for they had most of them a keen sense of humour and a taste for acting: they would be of great use to us. The example of a real gentleman is, if I may say so without profanity, the best of all gospels; such a man upon the stage becomes a potent humanising influence, an Ideal which all may look upon for a shilling.
在其他方面，他们比我在其他国家见过的任何人都更像是最优秀的英国人。我本想说服他们中的六个人来英国登上舞台，因为他们中的大多数人都有敏锐的幽默感和表演品味：他们对我们很有用。如果我可以不带脏话地这么说的话，真正绅士的榜样是最好的福音书。这样的一个人在舞台上会成为一种强大的人性化影响力，一种所有人都可以用一先令来看待的理想。

I always liked and admired these men, and although I could not help deeply regretting their certain ultimate perdition (for they had no sense of a hereafter, and their only religion was that of self- respect and consideration for other people), I never dared to take so great a liberty with them as to attempt to put them in possession of my own religious convictions, in spite of my knowing that they were the only ones which could make them really good and happy, either here or hereafter. I did try sometimes, being impelled to do so by a strong sense of duty, and by my deep regret that so much that was admirable should be doomed to ages if not eternity of torture; but the words stuck in my throat as soon as I began.
我一直喜欢和钦佩这些人，虽然我不禁对他们的最终灭亡深感遗憾（因为他们没有来世的意识，他们唯一的宗教就是自尊和为他人着想），但我从来不敢我对他们采取如此大的自由，试图让他们拥有我自己的宗教信仰，尽管我知道他们是唯一能让他们真正善良和幸福的信仰，无论是现在还是将来。有时我确实尝试过这样做，是出于强烈的责任感，也出于深深的遗憾，因为如此令人钦佩的事情注定要遭受多年甚至永恒的折磨；但话刚开始，我就卡在了喉咙里。

Whether a professional missionary might have a better chance I know not; such persons must doubtless know more about the science of conversion: for myself, I could only be thankful that I was in the right path, and was obliged to let others take their chance as yet. If the plan fails by which I propose to convert them myself, I would gladly contribute my mite towards the sending two or three trained missionaries, who have been known as successful converters of Jews and Mahometans; but such have seldom much to glory in the flesh, and when I think of the high Ydgrunites, and of the figure which a missionary would probably cut among them, I cannot feel sanguine that much good would be arrived at. Still the attempt is worth making, and the worst danger to the missionaries themselves would be that of being sent to the hospital where Chowbok would have been sent had he come with me into Erewhon.
我不知道职业传教士是否有更好的机会；这些人无疑必须更多地了解皈依的科学：对我自己来说，我只能庆幸自己走在正确的道路上，并且不得不让其他人抓住机会。如果我提议亲自让他们皈依的计划失败了，我会很乐意为派遣两到三名受过训练的传教士出一份力，他们被认为是犹太人和伊斯兰教徒的成功皈依者；但这样的人在肉体上很少有什么值得夸耀的，当我想到那些高尚的伊格鲁尼人，以及传教士可能在他们中间塑造的形象时，我对会取得多大的好处感到乐观。尽管如此，这种尝试还是值得的，对传教士来说，最严重的危险就是被送往医院，如果乔博克和我一起进入埃瑞洪的话，他就会被送往医院。

Taking then their religious opinions as a whole, I must own that the Erewhonians are superstitious, on account of the views which they hold of their professed gods, and their entirely anomalous and inexplicable worship of Ydgrun, a worship at once the most powerful, yet most devoid of formalism, that I ever met with; but in practice things worked better than might have been expected, and the conflicting claims of Ydgrun and the gods were arranged by unwritten compromises (for the most part in Ydgrun’s favour), which in ninety-nine cases out of a hundred were very well understood.
考虑到他们的宗教观点作为一个整体，我必须承认埃雷洪人是迷信的，因为他们对自称的神所持有的观点，以及他们对伊德格林的完全反常和莫名其妙的崇拜，这种崇拜曾经是最强大的，但我所见过的最没有形式主义的；但在实践中，事情比预期的要好，伊古伦和众神的相互冲突的主张是通过不成文的妥协安排的（大部分对伊古伦有利），在一百个案例中，九十九个都很好理解。

I could not conceive why they should not openly acknowledge high Ydgrunism, and discard the objective personality of hope, justice, &c.; but whenever I so much as hinted at this, I found that I was on dangerous ground. They would never have it; returning constantly to the assertion that ages ago the divinities were frequently seen, and that the moment their personality was disbelieved in, men would leave off practising even those ordinary virtues which the common experience of mankind has agreed on as being the greatest secret of happiness. ‘Who ever heard,’ they asked, indignantly, ‘of such things as kindly training, a good example, and an enlightened regard to one’s own welfare, being able to keep men straight?’ In my hurry, forgetting things which I ought to have remembered, I answered that if a person could not be kept straight by these things, there was nothing that could straighten him, and that if he were not ruled by the love and fear of men whom he had seen, neither would he be so by that of the gods whom he had not seen.
我无法理解为什么他们不应该公开承认高度的Ydgrunism，并放弃希望、正义等客观人格；但每当我暗示这一点时，我就发现自己处于危险的境地。他们永远不会拥有它；不断地回到这样的断言，即很久以前，人们经常看到神灵，一旦他们的人格不被相信，人们就会放弃实践那些普通的美德，而人类的共同经验已经认为这些美德是幸福的最大秘密。 “谁听说过，”他们愤怒地问道，“诸如仁慈的训练、良好的榜样、开明地关心自己的福利以及能够使人保持正直这样的事情？”在我的匆忙中，忘记了我应该做的事情我记得，我回答说，如果一个人不能被这些事情保持正直，那么没有什么可以使他正直，如果他不是被他所见过的人的爱和恐惧所统治，他也不会如此是由他未曾见过的众神所赐予的。

At one time indeed I came upon a small but growing sect who believed, after a fashion, in the immortality of the soul and the resurrection from the dead; they taught that those who had been born with feeble and diseased bodies and had passed their lives in ailing, would be tortured eternally hereafter; but that those who had been born strong and healthy and handsome would be rewarded for ever and ever. Of moral qualities or conduct they made no mention.
确实有一次，我遇到了一个规模虽小但正在不断壮大的教派，他们在某种程度上相信灵魂不朽和死里复活。他们教导说，那些出生时身体虚弱多病、在病痛中度过一生的人，将在来世遭受永恒的折磨。但那些生来强壮、健康、英俊的人将永远得到奖赏。他们没有提及道德品质或行为。

Bad as this was, it was a step in advance, inasmuch as they did hold out a future state of some sort, and I was shocked to find that for the most part they met with opposition, on the score that their doctrine was based upon no sort of foundation, also that it was immoral in its tendency, and not to be desired by any reasonable beings.
尽管这很糟糕，但它还是提前了一步，因为他们确实提出了某种未来状态，而我惊讶地发现，他们在很大程度上遭到了反对，因为他们的学说是基于这一点的。没有任何基础，而且它的倾向是不道德的，任何理性的人都不希望看到它。

When I asked how it could be immoral, I was answered, that if firmly held, it would lead people to cheapen this present life, making it appear to be an affair of only secondary importance; that it would thus distract men’s minds from the perfecting of this world’s economy, and was an impatient cutting, so to speak, of the Gordian knot of life’s problems, whereby some people might gain present satisfaction to themselves at the cost of infinite damage to others; that the doctrine tended to encourage the poor in their improvidence, and in a debasing acquiescence in ills which they might well remedy; that the rewards were illusory and the result, after all, of luck, whose empire should be bounded by the grave; that its terrors were enervating and unjust; and that even the most blessed rising would be but the disturbing of a still more blessed slumber.
当我问它怎么可能是不道德的时候，我得到的回答是，如果坚持下去，它会导致人们贬低今生，使它显得只是次要的事情;因此，它会分散人们对完善世界经济的注意力，可以说，它是对生活问题的棘手解决方案的不耐烦的切割，通过这种方式，一些人可能会以对他人造成无限伤害为代价来获得眼前的满足。 ;这种学说倾向于鼓励穷人的短视，以及对他们本可以很好补救的弊病的可耻默许；奖励是虚幻的，归根结底是运气的结果，运气的帝国应该以坟墓为界；它的恐怖令人衰弱且不公正；即使是最幸福的起床也只会扰乱更幸福的睡眠。

To all which I could only say that the thing had been actually known to happen, and that there were several well-authenticated instances of people having died and come to life again—instances which no man in his senses could doubt.
对于这一切，我只能说，人们确实知道这件事发生过，而且有几个经过充分证实的人死而复生的例子——任何有理智的人都不会怀疑这些例子。

‘If this be so,’ said my opponent, ‘we must bear it as best we may.’
“既然如此，”我的对手说，“我们就必须尽力忍受。”

I then translated for him, as well as I could, the noble speech of Hamlet in which he says that it is the fear lest worse evils may befall us after death which alone prevents us from rushing into death’s arms.
然后，我尽我所能为他翻译了哈姆雷特的高贵演讲，他在演讲中说，正是担心死后更糟糕的邪恶降临到我们身上，才阻止我们冲入死亡的怀抱。

‘Nonsense,’ he answered, ‘no man was ever yet stopped from cutting his throat by any such fears as your poet ascribes to him—and your poet probably knew this perfectly well. If a man cuts his throat he is at bay, and thinks of nothing but escape, no matter whither, provided he can shuffle off his present. No. Men are kept at their posts, not by the fear that if they quit them they may quit a frying-pan for a fire, but by the hope that if they hold on, the fire may burn less fiercely. ‘The respect,’ to quote your poet, ‘that makes calamity of so long a life,’ is the consideration that though calamity may live long, the sufferer may live longer still.’
“胡说，”他回答道，“从来没有人因为你们的诗人所描述的那种恐惧而阻止过割断自己的喉咙——你们的诗人可能非常清楚这一点。如果一个人割断了自己的喉咙，他就陷入了困境，除了逃跑之外别无他法，无论去往何处，只要他能摆脱他的礼物。不。人们坚守在自己的岗位上，不是因为担心一旦放弃，他们可能会放弃煎锅，而是希望，如果他们坚持下去，火会烧得不那么猛烈。引用你的诗人的话说，“尊重使灾难得以长久存在”，就是考虑到尽管灾难可能会持续很长时间，但受难者可能会活得更久。

On this, seeing that there was little probability of our coming to an agreement, I let the argument drop, and my opponent presently left me with as much disapprobation as he could show without being overtly rude.
在这一点上，看到我们达成协议的可能性很小，我放弃了争论，而我的对手很快就在不显得粗鲁的情况下对我表示了尽可能多的不满。

CHAPTER XVIII: BIRTH FORMULAE
第十八章：出生公式

I heard what follows not from Arowhena, but from Mr. Nosnibor and some of the gentlemen who occasionally dined at the house: they told me that the Erewhonians believe in pre-existence; and not only this (of which I will write more fully in the next chapter), but they believe that it is of their own free act and deed in a previous state that they come to be born into this world at all. They hold that the unborn are perpetually plaguing and tormenting the married of both sexes, fluttering about them incessantly, and giving them no peace either of mind or body until they have consented to take them under their protection. If this were not so (this at least is what they urge), it would be a monstrous freedom for one man to take with another, to say that he should undergo the chances and changes of this mortal life without any option in the matter. No man would have any right to get married at all, inasmuch as he can never tell what frightful misery his doing so may entail forcibly upon a being who cannot be unhappy as long as he does not exist. They feel this so strongly that they are resolved to shift the blame on to other shoulders; and have fashioned a long mythology as to the world in which the unborn people live, and what they do, and the arts and machinations to which they have recourse in order to get themselves into our own world. But of this more anon: what I would relate here is their manner of dealing with those who do come.
我不是从阿罗维纳那里听到的，而是从诺斯尼博尔先生和一些偶尔在家里吃饭的绅士那里听到的：他们告诉我，埃雷洪人相信前世；他们相信前世；他们相信前世。不仅如此（我将在下一章更详细地写到），他们还相信，他们降生到这个世界上完全是由于他们自己在先前状态下的自由行为和行为。他们认为，未出生的孩子永远困扰和折磨已婚的男女，不断地在他们周围扑腾，使他们的身心得不到安宁，直到他们同意将他们置于他们的保护之下。如果情况并非如此（至少他们是这么要求的），那么一个人与另一个人说他应该在没有任何选择的情况下经历今生的机会和变化，这将是一种巨大的自由。没有人有权利结婚，因为他永远无法知道他的结婚可能会给一个只要他不存在就不会不快乐的人带来多么可怕的痛苦。他们如此强烈地感受到这一点，以至于他们决心将责任推到别人的肩上；并塑造了一个漫长的神话，涉及未出生的人们所生活的世界，他们所做的事情，以及他们为了进入我们自己的世界而求助的艺术和阴谋。但稍后再说：我在这里要讲的是他们对待那些来的人的方式。

It is a distinguishing peculiarity of the Erewhonians that when they profess themselves to be quite certain about any matter, and avow it as a base on which they are to build a system of practice, they seldom quite believe in it. If they smell a rat about the precincts of a cherished institution, they will always stop their noses to it if they can.
埃雷洪人的一个显着特点是，当他们声称自己对任何事情非常确定，并承认它是他们建立实践体系的基础时，他们很少完全相信它。如果他们在某个珍贵机构的范围内闻到了老鼠的味道，他们总是会尽可能地阻止它。

This is what most of them did in this matter of the unborn, for I cannot (and never could) think that they seriously believed in their mythology concerning pre-existence: they did and they did not; they did not know themselves what they believed; all they did know was that it was a disease not to believe as they did. The only thing of which they were quite sure was that it was the pestering of the unborn which caused them to be brought into this world, and that they would not have been here if they would have only let peaceable people alone.
这就是他们中的大多数人在未出生的问题上所做的，因为我不能（也永远不能）认为他们认真地相信他们关于前世的神话：他们相信了，他们没有；他们相信了，他们没有；他们相信了，也没有相信过。他们不知道自己相信什么；他们只知道，不相信自己的信仰是一种病。他们唯一确信的是，正是未出生的人的纠缠才把他们带到这个世界上，如果他们只放过和平的人，他们就不会来到这里。

It would be hard to disprove this position, and they might have a good case if they would only leave it as it stands. But this they will not do; they must have assurance doubly sure; they must have the written word of the child itself as soon as it is born, giving the parents indemnity from all responsibility on the score of its birth, and asserting its own pre-existence. They have therefore devised something which they call a birth formula—a document which varies in words according to the caution of parents, but is much the same practically in all cases; for it has been the business of the Erewhonian lawyers during many ages to exercise their skill in perfecting it and providing for every contingency.
很难反驳这一立场，如果他们只保持现状，他们可能会有一个很好的理由。但他们不会这样做；他们必须有双重保证；他们必须在孩子出生后立即获得孩子本人的书面证明，免除父母因孩子出生而承担的所有责任，并主张孩子本身的存在。因此，他们设计了一种被他们称为出生公式的东西——一份根据父母的谨慎而在文字上有所不同的文件，但实际上在所有情况下都是相同的。因为多年来，埃鲁洪尼亚律师的职责就是锻炼他们的技能，完善它并为每一种意外情况做好准备。

These formulae are printed on common paper at a moderate cost for the poor; but the rich have them written on parchment and handsomely bound, so that the getting up of a person’s birth formula is a test of his social position. They commence by setting forth, That whereas A. B. was a member of the kingdom of the unborn, where he was well provided for in every way, and had no cause of discontent, &c., &c., he did of his own wanton depravity and restlessness conceive a desire to enter into this present world; that thereon having taken the necessary steps as set forth in laws of the unborn kingdom, he did with malice aforethought set himself to plague and pester two unfortunate people who had never wronged him, and who were quite contented and happy until he conceived this base design against their peace; for which wrong he now humbly entreats their pardon.
这些公式印在普通纸上，价格适中，适合穷人使用；但富人则把它们写在羊皮纸上，并装订得精美，因此一个人的出生公式的起落是对他社会地位的考验。他们首先指出，虽然 A.B. 是未出生王国的一员，在那里他在各方面都得到了充分的供应，并且没有任何不满的理由，等等，但他却因自己的肆意堕落和焦躁不安，渴望进入现世；于是，在按照未出生王国的法律规定采取了必要的步骤之后，他怀着恶意，预先让自己去折磨和纠缠两个不幸的人，他们从未冤枉过他，而且他们非常满足和快乐，直到他构思出这个卑鄙的设计。破坏他们的和平；对于这一错误，他现在谦卑地恳求他们的原谅。

He acknowledges that he is responsible for all physical blemishes and deficiencies which may render him answerable to the laws of his country; that his parents have nothing whatever to do with any of these things; and that they have a right to kill him at once if they be so minded, though he entreats them to show their marvellous goodness and clemency by sparing his life. If they will do this, he promises to be their most obedient and abject creature during his earlier years, and indeed all his life, unless they should see fit in their abundant generosity to remit some portion of his service hereafter. And so the formula continues, going sometimes into very minute details, according to the fancies of family lawyers, who will not make it any shorter than they can help.
他承认他对所有身体缺陷和缺陷负有责任，这些缺陷和缺陷可能使他对其国家的法律负责；他的父母与这些事情没有任何关系；尽管他恳求他们饶恕他的生命，以显示他们非凡的善良和仁慈，但如果他们有这样的想法，他们就有权立即杀死他。如果他们愿意这样做，他承诺在他的早年乃至一生中成为他们最顺从和最卑微的生物，除非他们认为以后可以慷慨地免除他的部分服务。就这样，这个公式继续下去，有时会根据家庭律师的想法深入到非常微小的细节，他们不会把它说得比他们力所能及的更短。

The deed being thus prepared, on the third or fourth day after the birth of the child, or as they call it, the ‘final importunity,’ the friends gather together, and there is a feast held, where they are all very melancholy—as a general rule, I believe, quite truly so—and make presents to the father and mother of the child in order to console them for the injury which has just been done them by the unborn.
事情就这样准备好了，在孩子出生后的第三天或第四天，或者按他们所说的“最后的催促”，朋友们聚集在一起，举行了一场宴会，他们都非常忧郁——我相信，一般来说，确实如此——向孩子的父母赠送礼物，以安慰他们刚刚受到未出生婴儿的伤害。

By-and-by the child himself is brought down by his nurse, and the company begin to rail upon him, upbraiding him for his impertinence, and asking him what amends he proposes to make for the wrong that he has committed, and how he can look for care and nourishment from those who have perhaps already been injured by the unborn on some ten or twelve occasions; for they say of people with large families, that they have suffered terrible injuries from the unborn; till at last, when this has been carried far enough, some one suggests the formula, which is brought out and solemnly read to the child by the family straightener. This gentleman is always invited on these occasions, for the very fact of intrusion into a peaceful family shows a depravity on the part of the child which requires his professional services.
渐渐地，孩子自己被保姆放倒了，大家开始责备他，责备他的无礼，并询问他打算对自己所犯下的错误做出怎样的弥补，以及如何弥补。可以向那些可能已经被胎儿伤害过十到十二次的人寻求照顾和滋养；因为他们说，拥有大家庭的人，他们遭受了未出生的可怕伤害。直到最后，当这已经进行得足够深入时，有人提出了这个公式，然后由家庭矫治师拿出来并郑重地读给孩子听。在这些场合，这位绅士总是受到邀请，因为闯入一个平静的家庭这一事实本身就表明了孩子的堕落，需要他的专业服务。

On being teased by the reading and tweaked by the nurse, the child will commonly begin to cry, which is reckoned a good sign, as showing a consciousness of guilt. He is thereon asked, Does he assent to the formula? on which, as he still continues crying and can obviously make no answer, some one of the friends comes forward and undertakes to sign the document on his behalf, feeling sure (so he says) that the child would do it if he only knew how, and that he will release the present signer from his engagement on arriving at maturity. The friend then inscribes the signature of the child at the foot of the parchment, which is held to bind the child as much as though he had signed it himself.
在被读物逗弄和被护士扭捏时，孩子通常会开始哭泣，这被认为是一个好兆头，因为表现出内疚感。于是有人问他，他同意这个公式吗？当他仍在继续哭泣并且显然无法回答时，其中一位朋友站出来并承诺代表他签署文件，他确信（他是这样说的）如果孩子知道如何做，他就会这样做。 ，并且他将在成熟时解除当前签名者的订婚。然后，朋友将孩子的签名写在羊皮纸的底部，拿着羊皮纸来约束孩子，就像他自己签名一样。

Even this, however, does not fully content them, for they feel a little uneasy until they have got the child’s own signature after all. So when he is about fourteen, these good people partly bribe him by promises of greater liberty and good things, and partly intimidate him through their great power of making themselves actively unpleasant to him, so that though there is a show of freedom made, there is really none; they also use the offices of the teachers in the Colleges of Unreason, till at last, in one way or another, they take very good care that he shall sign the paper by which he professes to have been a free agent in coming into the world, and to take all the responsibility of having done so on to his own shoulders. And yet, though this document is obviously the most important which any one can sign in his whole life, they will have him do so at an age when neither they nor the law will for many a year allow any one else to bind him to the smallest obligation, no matter how righteously he may owe it, because they hold him too young to know what he is about, and do not consider it fair that he should commit himself to anything that may prejudice him in after years.
然而，即便如此，他们还是不能完全满意，因为在最终得到孩子自己的签名之前，他们还是感到有些不安。因此，当他大约十四岁的时候，这些好人部分地通过许诺更大的自由和美好事物来贿赂他，部分地通过他们的强大力量来恐吓他，使自己主动地让他不愉快，因此，尽管他们表现得自由，但实际上确实没有；他们还使用非理性学院教师的办公室，直到最后，以这样或那样的方式，他们非常小心地让他签署一份文件，通过该文件他声称自己是来到这个世界的自由人。 ，并把这样做的所有责任都扛在自己的肩上。然而，尽管这份文件显然是任何人一生中都可以签署的最重要的文件，但他们会让他在这样的年龄签署：他们和法律在很多年里都不会允许任何其他人将他约束在这份文件上。最小的义务，无论他负有多么正义，因为他们认为他太年轻，不知道自己在做什么，并且认为他应该承担任何可能在以后的岁月里损害他的事情，这是不公平的。

I own that all this seemed rather hard, and not of a piece with the many admirable institutions existing among them. I once ventured to say a part of what I thought about it to one of the Professors of Unreason. I did it very tenderly, but his justification of the system was quite out of my comprehension. I remember asking him whether he did not think it would do harm to a lad’s principles, by weakening his sense of the sanctity of his word and of truth generally, that he should be led into entering upon a solemn declaration as to the truth of things about which all that he can certainly know is that he knows nothing—whether, in fact, the teachers who so led him, or who taught anything as a certainty of which they were themselves uncertain, were not earning their living by impairing the truth-sense of their pupils (a delicate organisation mostly), and by vitiating one of their most sacred instincts.
我承认这一切看起来相当困难，而且与其中存在的许多令人钦佩的机构格格不入。我曾经大胆地向一位非理性教授说出了我对此的部分想法。我做得非常温柔，但他对这个系统的合理性完全超出了我的理解范围。我记得我曾问过他，如果他被引导对事物的真实性做出庄严的声明，是否会削弱他对自己的话语和真理的神圣感，从而损害他的原则？对此，他所能肯定知道的就是他一无所知——事实上，那些如此引导他的老师，或者那些将他们自己不确定的东西作为确定性教授的老师，是否不是通过损害真理来谋生的——学生的意识（主要是一个微妙的组织），并损害了他们最神圣的本能之一。

The Professor, who was a delightful person, seemed greatly surprised at the view which I took, but it had no influence with him whatsoever. No one, he answered, expected that the boy either would or could know all that he said he knew; but the world was full of compromises; and there was hardly any affirmation which would bear being interpreted literally. Human language was too gross a vehicle of thought—thought being incapable of absolute translation. He added, that as there can be no translation from one language into another which shall not scant the meaning somewhat, or enlarge upon it, so there is no language which can render thought without a jarring and a harshness somewhere—and so forth; all of which seemed to come to this in the end, that it was the custom of the country, and that the Erewhonians were a conservative people; that the boy would have to begin compromising sooner or later, and this was part of his education in the art. It was perhaps to be regretted that compromise should be as necessary as it was; still it was necessary, and the sooner the boy got to understand it the better for himself. But they never tell this to the boy.
教授是个和蔼可亲的人，他对我的观点似乎感到非常惊讶，但这对他没有任何影响。他回答说，没有人期望这个男孩会或能够知道他所说的一切。但这个世界充满了妥协；几乎没有任何断言可以按字面解释。人类语言作为思想的载体太粗糙了——思想无法绝对翻译。他补充说，正如从一种语言翻译成另一种语言时，如果不忽略或扩大其含义，就不可能有任何语言能够使思想在某处不产生不和谐和刺耳的感觉，等等。所有这一切似乎最终都得出这样的结果：这是这个国家的习俗，而埃雷洪尼亚人是一个保守的民族。这个男孩迟早要开始妥协，这是他接受的艺术教育的一部分。也许令人遗憾的是，妥协是必要的。但这仍然是必要的，男孩越早理解这一点对自己越好。但他们从未将此事告诉男孩。

From the book of their mythology about the unborn I made the extracts which will form the following chapter.
我从他们关于胎儿的神话书中摘录了一些内容，这些内容将构成下一章。

CHAPTER XIX: THE WORLD OF THE UNBORN
第十九章：未出生的世界

The Erewhonians say that we are drawn through life backwards; or again, that we go onwards into the future as into a dark corridor. Time walks beside us and flings back shutters as we advance; but the light thus given often dazzles us, and deepens the darkness which is in front. We can see but little at a time, and heed that little far less than our apprehension of what we shall see next; ever peering curiously through the glare of the present into the gloom of the future, we presage the leading lines of that which is before us, by faintly reflected lights from dull mirrors that are behind, and stumble on as we may till the trap-door opens beneath us and we are gone.
埃雷洪人说，我们的生活是在倒退中度过的。又或者，我们继续走向未来，就像走进一条黑暗的走廊一样。时间在我们身边行走，随着我们前进，时间将百叶窗拉开；但这样发出的光常常使我们眼花缭乱，并加深了前面的黑暗。我们一次只能看到很少的东西，而且我们对这一点的关注远远少于我们对接下来将看到的东西的担忧。我们总是好奇地透过现在的眩光窥视未来的阴暗，通过背后暗淡的镜子微弱反射的光线，我们预示着前方的引导线，然后跌跌撞撞地走下去，直到活板门。在我们脚下打开，我们就消失了。

They say at other times that the future and the past are as a panorama upon two rollers; that which is on the roller of the future unwraps itself on to the roller of the past; we cannot hasten it, and we may not stay it; we must see all that is unfolded to us whether it be good or ill; and what we have seen once we may see again no more. It is ever unwinding and being wound; we catch it in transition for a moment, and call it present; our flustered senses gather what impression they can, and we guess at what is coming by the tenor of that which we have seen. The same hand has painted the whole picture, and the incidents vary little—rivers, woods, plains, mountains, towns and peoples, love, sorrow, and death: yet the interest never flags, and we look hopefully for some good fortune, or fearfully lest our own faces be shown us as figuring in something terrible. When the scene is past we think we know it, though there is so much to see, and so little time to see it, that our conceit of knowledge as regards the past is for the most part poorly founded; neither do we care about it greatly, save in so far as it may affect the future, wherein our interest mainly lies.
他们有时说，未来和过去就像两个滚筒上的全景；未来的滚轴上的东西将自己展开到过去的滚轴上；我们不能加速它，也不能阻止它；我们必须看到展现在我们面前的一切，无论是好还是坏；我们曾经见过的东西可能再也见不到了。它总是在松开和上紧；我们暂时抓住了它的转变，并称之为现在；我们慌乱的感官尽可能地收集印象，并根据我们所看到的内容猜测即将发生的事情。同一只手描绘了整个画面，事件变化不大——河流、树林、平原、山脉、城镇和人民、爱情、悲伤和死亡：但兴趣从未减弱，我们满怀希望地寻找一些好运，或者害怕我们自己的脸被认为正在策划一些可怕的事情。当场景过去时，我们认为我们知道它，尽管有太多可看的东西，而看它的时间却很少，以至于我们对过去的知识的自负在很大程度上是没有根据的；我们也不太关心它，除非它可能影响我们的主要利益所在的未来。

The Erewhonians say it was by chance only that the earth and stars and all the heavenly worlds began to roll from east to west, and not from west to east, and in like manner they say it is by chance that man is drawn through life with his face to the past instead of to the future. For the future is there as much as the past, only that we may not see it. Is it not in the loins of the past, and must not the past alter before the future can do so?
埃雷洪人说，地球、星星和所有天堂世界开始从东向西滚动，而不是从西向东滚动，只是偶然的；同样，他们说，人类在生命中被吸引，也是出于偶然。他面对过去而不是未来。因为未来和过去一样都存在，只是我们可能看不到它。难道它不是过去的产物吗？在未来改变之前，过去一定不能改变吗？

Sometimes, again, they say that there was a race of men tried upon the earth once, who knew the future better than the past, but that they died in a twelvemonth from the misery which their knowledge caused them; and if any were to be born too prescient now, he would be culled out by natural selection, before he had time to transmit so peace-destroying a faculty to his descendants.
有时，他们又说，有一个人类种族曾经在地球上受过考验，他们比过去更了解未来，但他们在十二个月内就死于他们的知识给他们带来的痛苦；如果现在有一个人出生得太有先见之明，那么在他有时间将这种破坏和平的能力传给他的后代之前，他就会被自然选择淘汰掉。

Strange fate for man! He must perish if he get that, which he must perish if he strive not after. If he strive not after it he is no better than the brutes, if he get it he is more miserable than the devils.
人类的奇怪命运！如果他得到了这个，他就一定会灭亡；如果他不努力去追求，他就一定会灭亡。如果他不去追求它，那么他并不比畜生更好；如果他得到了它，他比魔鬼还悲惨。

Having waded through many chapters like the above, I came at last to the unborn themselves, and found that they were held to be souls pure and simple, having no actual bodies, but living in a sort of gaseous yet more or less anthropomorphic existence, like that of a ghost; they have thus neither flesh nor blood nor warmth. Nevertheless they are supposed to have local habitations and cities wherein they dwell, though these are as unsubstantial as their inhabitants; they are even thought to eat and drink some thin ambrosial sustenance, and generally to be capable of doing whatever mankind can do, only after a visionary ghostly fashion as in a dream. On the other hand, as long as they remain where they are they never die—the only form of death in the unborn world being the leaving it for our own. They are believed to be extremely numerous, far more so than mankind. They arrive from unknown planets, full grown, in large batches at a time; but they can only leave the unborn world by taking the steps necessary for their arrival here—which is, in fact, by suicide.
费力地读完上述许多章节后，我终于来到了未出生的人本身，发现他们被认为是纯粹而简单的灵魂，没有实际的身体，而是生活在一种气态但或多或少拟人化的存在中，像幽灵一样；因此，他们既没有血肉，也没有温度。然而，他们应该有当地的住所和居住的城市，尽管这些和他们的居民一样不真实。他们甚至被认为可以吃喝一些稀薄的食物，并且通常能够做人类能做的任何事情，只有在像梦一样的幻象幽灵般的时尚之后。另一方面，只要它们留在原地，它们就永远不会死亡——未出生的世界中唯一的死亡形式就是把它留给我们自己的世界。据信它们的数量极其庞大，远远超过人类。它们来自未知的星球，已经完全成熟，一次大批地到达；但他们只能通过采取到达这里所需的步骤来离开未出生的世界——事实上，就是自杀。

They ought to be an exceedingly happy people, for they have no extremes of good or ill fortune; never marrying, but living in a state much like that fabled by the poets as the primitive condition of mankind. In spite of this, however, they are incessantly complaining; they know that we in this world have bodies, and indeed they know everything else about us, for they move among us whithersoever they will, and can read our thoughts, as well as survey our actions at pleasure. One would think that this should be enough for them; and most of them are indeed alive to the desperate risk which they will run by indulging themselves in that body with ‘sensible warm motion’ which they so much desire; nevertheless, there are some to whom the ennui of a disembodied existence is so intolerable that they will venture anything for a change; so they resolve to quit. The conditions which they must accept are so uncertain, that none but the most foolish of the unborn will consent to them; and it is from these, and these only, that our own ranks are recruited.
他们应该是一个非常幸福的民族，因为他们没有极端的好运或厄运。从未结婚，但生活在一种很像诗人所寓言的人类原始状态的状态。尽管如此，他们还是不断地抱怨；他们知道我们在这个世界上有身体，事实上他们知道关于我们的一切，因为他们在我们中间移动，无论他们想去哪里，可以读懂我们的思想，也可以随意观察我们的行为。人们会认为这对他们来说应该足够了；但事实上，这对他们来说已经足够了。他们中的大多数人确实意识到，如果他们将自己沉浸在他们如此渴望的“明显的温暖运动”的身体中，他们将冒着绝望的风险。然而，有些人却无法忍受脱离肉体的存在所带来的厌倦，以至于为了改变他们愿意冒险做任何事。所以他们决定戒烟。他们必须接受的条件是如此不确定，除了最愚蠢的胎儿之外，没有人会同意他们。我们自己的队伍正是从这些人中招募的。

When they have finally made up their minds to leave, they must go before the magistrate of the nearest town, and sign an affidavit of their desire to quit their then existence. On their having done this, the magistrate reads them the conditions which they must accept, and which are so long that I can only extract some of the principal points, which are mainly the following:-
当他们最终决定离开时，他们必须去最近城镇的地方法官面前，并签署一份宣誓书，表明他们希望退出当时的存在。他们这样做后，地方法官向他们宣读了他们必须接受的条件，这些条件太长了，我只能摘录一些要点，主要是以下几点：-

First, they must take a potion which will destroy their memory and sense of identity; they must go into the world helpless, and without a will of their own; they must draw lots for their dispositions before they go, and take them, such as they are, for better or worse—neither are they to be allowed any choice in the matter of the body which they so much desire; they are simply allotted by chance, and without appeal, to two people whom it is their business to find and pester until they adopt them. Who these are to be, whether rich or poor, kind or unkind, healthy or diseased, there is no knowing; they have, in fact, to entrust themselves for many years to the care of those for whose good constitution and good sense they have no sort of guarantee.
首先，他们必须服用一种会摧毁他们的记忆和身份感的药剂；他们必须无助地、没有自己意愿地来到这个世界上。他们在出发前必须抽签决定自己的性情，无论好坏，都按其本来面目接受——在他们如此渴望的身体问题上，他们也不允许有任何选择；他们只是偶然地、毫无吸引力地分配给了两个人，他们的职责就是找到并纠缠他们，直到他们收养他们为止。这些人是谁，无论富有还是贫穷，善良还是不善良，健康还是患病，我们都不得而知；事实上，他们多年来必须将自己托付给那些他们无法保证其良好体质和良好判断力的人。

It is curious to read the lectures which the wiser heads give to those who are meditating a change. They talk with them as we talk with a spendthrift, and with about as much success.
阅读明智的头脑为那些正在思考改变的人提供的讲座是很有趣的。他们与他们交谈就像我们与挥霍无度的人交谈一样，并且取得了同样的成功。

‘To be born,’ they say, ‘is a felony—it is a capital crime, for which sentence may be executed at any moment after the commission of the offence. You may perhaps happen to live for some seventy or eighty years, but what is that, compared with the eternity you now enjoy? And even though the sentence were commuted, and you were allowed to live on for ever, you would in time become so terribly weary of life that execution would be the greatest mercy to you.
他们说，“出生是重罪——是死罪，犯罪后随时可以执行判决。”也许你碰巧活了七十年或八十岁，但与你现在享受的永恒相比，那又算什么呢？即使减刑，并且允许你永远活着，但随着时间的推移，你也会对生活感到非常厌倦，以至于处决对你来说就是最大的仁慈。

‘Consider the infinite risk; to be born of wicked parents and trained in vice! to be born of silly parents, and trained to unrealities! of parents who regard you as a sort of chattel or property, belonging more to them than to yourself! Again, you may draw utterly unsympathetic parents, who will never be able to understand you, and who will do their best to thwart you (as a hen when she has hatched a duckling), and then call you ungrateful because you do not love them; or, again, you may draw parents who look upon you as a thing to be cowed while it is still young, lest it should give them trouble hereafter by having wishes and feelings of its own.
‘考虑无限的风险；出生于邪恶的父母，并受过恶行的训练！出生于愚蠢的父母，并被训练成不切实际的人！父母把你视为一种动产或财产，更多地属于他们而不是你自己！再一次，你可能会画出完全没有同情心的父母，他们永远无法理解你，他们会尽最大努力阻止你（就像母鸡孵出小鸭一样），然后说你忘恩负义，因为你不爱他们;或者，你可能会画出父母，他们在你还年轻的时候就将你视为令人畏惧的东西，以免你的愿望和感情在以后给他们带来麻烦。

‘In later life, when you have been finally allowed to pass muster as a full member of the world, you will yourself become liable to the pesterings of the unborn—and a very happy life you may be led in consequence! For we solicit so strongly that a few only—nor these the best—can refuse us; and yet not to refuse is much the same as going into partnership with half-a-dozen different people about whom one can know absolutely nothing beforehand—not even whether one is going into partnership with men or women, nor with how many of either. Delude not yourself with thinking that you will be wiser than your parents. You may be an age in advance of those whom you have pestered, but unless you are one of the great ones you will still be an age behind those who will in their turn pester you.
“在以后的生活中，当你最终被允许作为世界上的正式成员通过考验时，你自己就会容易受到未出生的人的纠缠——结果你可能会过上非常幸福的生活！因为我们如此强烈地恳求，以至于只有少数人——而且不是最好的——可以拒绝我们；然而，不拒绝就等于与六个不同的人建立伙伴关系，而你事先对这些人一无所知——甚至不知道一个人是与男人还是女人建立伙伴关系，也不知道与其中的多少人建立伙伴关系。不要欺骗自己，以为自己会比父母更聪明。你可能比那些被你纠缠的人早一个时代，但除非你是伟大的人之一，否则你仍然比那些反过来纠缠你的人落后一个时代。

‘Imagine what it must be to have an unborn quartered upon you, who is of an entirely different temperament and disposition to your own; nay, half-a-dozen such, who will not love you though you have stinted yourself in a thousand ways to provide for their comfort and well-being,—who will forget all your self-sacrifice, and of whom you may never be sure that they are not bearing a grudge against you for errors of judgement into which you may have fallen, though you had hoped that such had been long since atoned for. Ingratitude such as this is not uncommon, yet fancy what it must be to bear! It is hard upon the duckling to have been hatched by a hen, but is it not also hard upon the hen to have hatched the duckling?
“想象一下，如果有一个未出生的孩子对着你，他的性情和性情与你完全不同，那会是什么感觉？不仅如此，还有六六个这样的人，他们不会爱你，尽管你已经千方百计地为他们提供舒适和幸福，他们会忘记你所有的自我牺牲，而你可能永远不会成为他们中的一员。确保他们不会因为你可能犯下的判断错误而对你怀恨在心，尽管你曾希望这种错误早已得到弥补。像这样的忘恩负义并不少见，但想象一下必须忍受什么！母鸡孵小鸭难，母鸡孵小鸭不也难吗？

‘Consider it again, we pray you, not for our sake but for your own. Your initial character you must draw by lot; but whatever it is, it can only come to a tolerably successful development after long training; remember that over that training you will have no control. It is possible, and even probable, that whatever you may get in after life which is of real pleasure and service to you, will have to be won in spite of, rather than by the help of, those whom you are now about to pester, and that you will only win your freedom after years of a painful struggle in which it will be hard to say whether you have suffered most injury, or inflicted it.
“我们请求您再考虑一下，不是为了我们，而是为了您自己。”你必须通过抽签抽出你的初始角色；但无论是什么，都需要经过长期的训练才能获得比较成功的发展。请记住，在训练过程中您将无法控制。有可能，甚至很可能，无论你在来世获得真正的快乐和对你有用的东西，都必须不顾那些你现在要纠缠的人，而不是通过他们的帮助来赢得。 ，只有经过多年的痛苦斗争，你才能赢得自由，在这场斗争中，很难说你是否遭受了最大的伤害，或者造成了伤害。

‘Remember also, that if you go into the world you will have free will; that you will be obliged to have it; that there is no escaping it; that you will be fettered to it during your whole life, and must on every occasion do that which on the whole seems best to you at any given time, no matter whether you are right or wrong in choosing it. Your mind will be a balance for considerations, and your action will go with the heavier scale. How it shall fall will depend upon the kind of scales which you may have drawn at birth, the bias which they will have obtained by use, and the weight of the immediate considerations. If the scales were good to start with, and if they have not been outrageously tampered with in childhood, and if the combinations into which you enter are average ones, you may come off well; but there are too many ‘ifs’ in this, and with the failure of any one of them your misery is assured. Reflect on this, and remember that should the ill come upon you, you will have yourself to thank, for it is your own choice to be born, and there is no compulsion in the matter.
‘还要记住，如果你进入这个世界，你将拥有自由意志；您将有义务拥有它；无法逃避它；你一生都会被它束缚，并且在任何时候都必须做对你来说总体上最好的事情，无论你的选择是对还是错。你的头脑将是一个平衡的考虑，你的行动将伴随着更重的尺度。它将如何下降取决于你在出生时所使用的天平的种类、通过使用它们将获得的偏见以及直接考虑因素的权重。如果天平一开始就很好，如果它们在童年时期没有被无耻地篡改，如果你输入的组合是普通的，你可能会得到很好的结果；但这其中有太多的“如果”，只要其中任何一个失败，你的痛苦就注定了。想一想，如果不幸降临到你身上，你要感谢你自己，因为出生是你自己的选择，没有什么强迫的。

‘Not that we deny the existence of pleasures among mankind; there is a certain show of sundry phases of contentment which may even amount to very considerable happiness; but mark how they are distributed over a man’s life, belonging, all the keenest of them, to the fore part, and few indeed to the after. Can there be any pleasure worth purchasing with the miseries of a decrepit age? If you are good, strong, and handsome, you have a fine fortune indeed at twenty, but how much of it will be left at sixty? For you must live on your capital; there is no investing your powers so that you may get a small annuity of life for ever: you must eat up your principal bit by bit, and be tortured by seeing it grow continually smaller and smaller, even though you happen to escape being rudely robbed of it by crime or casualty.
“并不是说我们否认人类快乐的存在；而是说我们否认快乐的存在。”存在一定程度的满足感，甚至可能构成非常可观的幸福；但请注意它们在一个人的一生中是如何分布的，所有最敏锐的人都属于前面的部分，很少有属于后面的部分。在衰老的岁月中，还有什么值得购买的快乐吗？如果你善良、强壮、英俊，二十岁确实是一笔好财富，但六十岁还能剩下多少呢？因为你必须靠你的资本生活；投资你的权力是不可能永远得到一小笔生命年金的：你必须一点一点地吃掉你的本金，并看着它越来越小而受到折磨，即使你碰巧逃脱了被粗暴地抢劫。犯罪或伤亡。

‘Remember, too, that there never yet was a man of forty who would not come back into the world of the unborn if he could do so with decency and honour. Being in the world he will as a general rule stay till he is forced to go; but do you think that he would consent to be born again, and re-live his life, if he had the offer of doing so? Do not think it. If he could so alter the past as that he should never have come into being at all, do you not think that he would do it very gladly?
“还要记住，如果四十岁的男人能够体面而有尊严地回到未出生的世界，那么从来没有一个人不愿意回到未出生的世界。在这个世界上，他通常会留下来，直到他被迫离开为止。但你认为如果他有机会的话，他会同意重生并重新过自己的生活吗？别这么想。如果他能够改变过去，使他根本不应该出现，你不认为他会很乐意这样做吗？

‘What was it that one of their own poets meant, if it was not this, when he cried out upon the day in which he was born, and the night in which it was said there is a man child conceived? ‘For now,’ he says, ‘I should have lain still and been quiet, I should have slept; then had I been at rest with kings and counsellors of the earth, which built desolate places for themselves; or with princes that had gold, who filled their houses with silver; or as an hidden untimely birth, I had not been; as infants which never saw light. There the wicked cease from troubling, and the weary are at rest.’ Be very sure that the guilt of being born carries this punishment at times to all men; but how can they ask for pity, or complain of any mischief that may befall them, having entered open-eyed into the snare?
‘他们自己的一位诗人在他出生的那天和据说怀上一个男孩的那天晚上大声喊叫时，如果不是这个，那是什么意思呢？ “现在，”他说，“我应该安静地躺着，我应该睡觉；那时我就​​可以与世上的君王和谋士一起安息了，他们为自己建造了荒凉的地方。或有金子的王子，他们的房屋里装满了银子；或者说，作为一个隐藏的不合时宜的出生，我并没有；就像从未见过光明的婴儿一样。在那里，恶人不再烦恼，疲倦的人得到安息。”请务必确信，出生时的罪责有时会给所有人带来这种惩罚；但他们既然睁着眼睛落入网罗，又怎能祈求怜悯，或抱怨可能降临在他们身上的任何恶作剧呢？

‘One word more and we have done. If any faint remembrance, as of a dream, flit in some puzzled moment across your brain, and you shall feel that the potion which is to be given you shall not have done its work, and the memory of this existence which you are leaving endeavours vainly to return; we say in such a moment, when you clutch at the dream but it eludes your grasp, and you watch it, as Orpheus watched Eurydice, gliding back again into the twilight kingdom, fly—fly—if you can remember the advice—to the haven of your present and immediate duty, taking shelter incessantly in the work which you have in hand. This much you may perhaps recall; and this, if you will imprint it deeply upon your every faculty, will be most likely to bring you safely and honourably home through the trials that are before you.’ {3}
‘再多说一句话，我们就完成了。如果有任何微弱的记忆，如梦境，在某个困惑的时刻掠过你的大脑，你就会觉得要给你的药水还没有发挥作用，而你正在离开的这个存在的记忆也会努力工作。徒然返回；我们说，在这样的时刻，当你紧紧抓住梦想，但它却逃脱了你的掌控，你看着它，就像俄耳甫斯看着欧律狄刻，再次滑回暮色王国，飞——飞——如果你还记得建议的话——到你当前和直接职责的避风港，不断地在你手头的工作中得到庇护。您可能还记得这么多；如果您将这一点深深地烙印在您的每一个能力中，那么您最有可能通过面前的考验安全而光荣地回家。”{3}

This is the fashion in which they reason with those who would be for leaving them, but it is seldom that they do much good, for none but the unquiet and unreasonable ever think of being born, and those who are foolish enough to think of it are generally foolish enough to do it. Finding, therefore, that they can do no more, the friends follow weeping to the courthouse of the chief magistrate, where the one who wishes to be born declares solemnly and openly that he accepts the conditions attached to his decision. On this he is presented with a potion, which immediately destroys his memory and sense of identity, and dissipates the thin gaseous tenement which he has inhabited: he becomes a bare vital principle, not to be perceived by human senses, nor to be by any chemical test appreciated. He has but one instinct, which is that he is to go to such and such a place, where he will find two persons whom he is to importune till they consent to undertake him; but whether he is to find these persons among the race of Chowbok or the Erewhonians themselves is not for him to choose.
这是他们与那些想要离开他们的人讲道理的方式，但他们很少做太多善事，因为除了不安和不合理的人之外，没有人会想到出生，而那些愚蠢到想到它的人一般都是愚蠢到这么做的。因此，朋友们发现他们无能为力，便哭着来到首席法官的法院，在那里，希望出生的人庄严而公开地宣布，他接受其决定所附加的条件。此时，他得到了一剂药水，它立即摧毁了他的记忆和身份感，并驱散了他所居住的稀薄的气态房屋：他变成了一个赤裸裸的重要原则，不被人类感官感知，也不被任何人所感知。化学测试赞赏。他只有一种本能，那就是他要去某某地方，在那里他会找到两个人，他要强求他们，直到他们同意接受他为止；但他是否要在乔博克人中找到这些人，还是在埃雷洪尼亚人中找到这些人，这不是他可以选择的。

CHAPTER XX: WHAT THEY MEAN BY IT
第二十章：他们的意思

I have given the above mythology at some length, but it is only a small part of what they have upon the subject. My first feeling on reading it was that any amount of folly on the part of the unborn in coming here was justified by a desire to escape from such intolerable prosing. The mythology is obviously an unfair and exaggerated representation of life and things; and had its authors been so minded they could have easily drawn a picture which would err as much on the bright side as this does on the dark. No Erewhonian believes that the world is as black as it has been here painted, but it is one of their peculiarities that they very often do not believe or mean things which they profess to regard as indisputable.
我已经详细地给出了上述神话，但这只是他们关于这个主题的一小部分。读到这本书时，我的第一感觉是，未出生的孩子来这里的任何愚蠢行为都是合理的，因为他们渴望逃离这种令人难以忍受的散文。神话显然是对生活和事物的不公平和夸张的表现；如果它的作者有这样的想法，他们很容易就能画出这样一幅图画，它在光明的一面和在黑暗的一面都会犯同样的错误。没有埃雷洪人相信世界就像这里所描绘的那样黑暗，但他们的特点之一是他们常常不相信或不相信他们自称认为无可争议的事情。

In the present instance their professed views concerning the unborn have arisen from their desire to prove that people have been presented with the gloomiest possible picture of their own prospects before they came here; otherwise, they could hardly say to one whom they are going to punish for an affection of the heart or brain that it is all his own doing. In practice they modify their theory to a considerable extent, and seldom refer to the birth formula except in extreme cases; for the force of habit, or what not, gives many of them a kindly interest even in creatures who have so much wronged them as the unborn have done; and though a man generally hates the unwelcome little stranger for the first twelve months, he is apt to mollify (according to his lights) as time goes on, and sometimes he will become inordinately attached to the beings whom he is pleased to call his children.
在目前的情况下，他们对未出生婴儿的看法源于他们希望证明人们在来到这里之前就已经看到了自己前景最黯淡的景象；否则，他们很难对一个因内心或大脑的感情而受到惩罚的人说，这都是他自己造成的。在实践中，他们对自己的理论进行了相当大的修改，除了极端情况外，很少提及出生公式。因为习惯的力量，或者其他原因，使他们中的许多人对那些像未出生的人那样冤枉过他们的生物产生了善意的兴趣。尽管一个人在最初的十二个月里通常会讨厌不受欢迎的小陌生人，但随着时间的推移，他很容易变得平静（根据他的看法），有时他会变得异常依恋那些他乐于称之为孩子的人。 。

Of course, according to Erewhonian premises, it would serve people right to be punished and scouted for moral and intellectual diseases as much as for physical, and I cannot to this day understand why they should have stopped short half way. Neither, again, can I understand why their having done so should have been, as it certainly was, a matter of so much concern to myself. What could it matter to me how many absurdities the Erewhonians might adopt? Nevertheless I longed to make them think as I did, for the wish to spread those opinions that we hold conducive to our own welfare is so deeply rooted in the English character that few of us can escape its influence. But let this pass.
当然，根据埃雷洪尼亚的前提，人们有权因道德和智力上的疾病而受到惩罚和侦察，就像身体上的疾病一样，我至今无法理解为什么他们应该中途停下来。我也无法理解为什么他们这样做应该是我自己如此关心的事情，事实上确实如此。埃雷洪人可能会采取多少荒谬的做法，这对我来说又有什么关系呢？尽管如此，我还是渴望让他们像我一样思考，因为传播那些我们认为有利于我们自身福祉的观点的愿望深深植根于英国人的性格中，以至于我们中很少有人能够逃脱它的影响。但让这件事过去吧。

In spite of not a few modifications in practice of a theory which is itself revolting, the relations between children and parents in that country are less happy than in Europe. It was rarely that I saw cases of real hearty and intense affection between the old people and the young ones. Here and there I did so, and was quite sure that the children, even at the age of twenty, were fonder of their parents than they were of any one else; and that of their own inclination, being free to choose what company they would, they would often choose that of their father and mother. The straightener’s carriage was rarely seen at the door of those houses. I saw two or three such cases during the time that I remained in the country, and cannot express the pleasure which I derived from a sight suggestive of so much goodness and wisdom and forbearance, so richly rewarded; yet I firmly believe that the same thing would happen in nine families out of ten if the parents were merely to remember how they felt when they were young, and actually to behave towards their children as they would have had their own parents behave towards themselves. But this, which would appear to be so simple and obvious, seems also to be a thing which not one in a hundred thousand is able to put in practice. It is only the very great and good who have any living faith in the simplest axioms; and there are few who are so holy as to feel that 19 and 13 make 32 as certainly as 2 and 2 make 4.
尽管这个本身就令人反感的理论在实践中做了不少修改，但那个国家的孩子和父母之间的关系并不像欧洲那样幸福。我很少见到老人和年轻人之间真正的真挚而深厚的感情。我时不时地这样做过，并且确信孩子们，即使在二十岁的时候，也比其他任何人都更爱他们的父母；他们可以根据自己的喜好自由选择陪伴的对象，通常会选择父母的陪伴。那些房子门口很少见到矫直机的马车。我在乡下的时候，见过两三个这样的例子，看到如此多的善良、智慧和忍耐，并得到如此丰厚的回报，我无法表达我的喜悦之情。但我坚信，如果父母仅仅记住他们年轻时的感受，并真正像对待自己的父母那样对待自己的孩子，那么十个家庭中就有九个会发生同样的事情。但这看似简单明了的事情，似乎也不是十万分之一的人能够付诸实践的。只有非常伟大和善良的人才会对最简单的公理抱有活泼的信念。很少有人如此神圣地认为 19 和 13 等于 32 就像 2 和 2 等于 4 一样。

I am quite sure that if this narrative should ever fall into Erewhonian hands, it will be said that what I have written about the relations between parents and children being seldom satisfactory is an infamous perversion of facts, and that in truth there are few young people who do not feel happier in the society of their nearest relations {4} than in any other. Mr. Nosnibor would be sure to say this. Yet I cannot refrain from expressing an opinion that he would be a good deal embarrassed if his deceased parents were to reappear and propose to pay him a six months’ visit. I doubt whether there are many things which he would regard as a greater infliction. They had died at a ripe old age some twenty years before I came to know him, so the case is an extreme one; but surely if they had treated him with what in his youth he had felt to be true unselfishness, his face would brighten when he thought of them to the end of his life.
我很确定，如果这篇叙述落入埃雷霍尼亚之手，人们会说，我所写的关于父母与孩子之间的关系很少令人满意的内容是对事实的臭名昭著的歪曲，而事实上，很少有年轻人他们在与自己最亲近的亲戚交往的社会中并不比在其他社会中感到更快乐{4}。诺斯尼博尔先生肯定会这么说。但我还是忍不住要表达这样的观点：如果他已故的父母再次出现并提议去拜访他六个月，他会感到非常尴尬。我怀疑是否有很多事情他会认为是更大的痛苦。他们在我认识他之前大约二十年就去世了，所以这是一个极端的例子。但可以肯定的是，如果他们以他年轻时所认为的真正无私的态度对待他，那么当他在生命的最后一刻想起他们时，他的脸色就会变得明亮。

In the one or two cases of true family affection which I met with, I am sure that the young people who were so genuinely fond of their fathers and mothers at eighteen, would at sixty be perfectly delighted were they to get the chance of welcoming them as their guests. There is nothing which could please them better, except perhaps to watch the happiness of their own children and grandchildren.
在我遇到的一两个真正亲情的例子中，我相信那些在十八岁时真心喜爱父母的年轻人，如果有机会在六十岁时受到欢迎，一定会非常高兴。作为他们的客人。没有什么比看到自己的子孙幸福更能让他们高兴的了。

This is how things should be. It is not an impossible ideal; it is one which actually does exist in some few cases, and might exist in almost all, with a little more patience and forbearance upon the parents’ part; but it is rare at present—so rare that they have a proverb which I can only translate in a very roundabout way, but which says that the great happiness of some people in a future state will consist in watching the distress of their parents on returning to eternal companionship with their grandfathers and grandmothers; whilst ‘compulsory affection’ is the idea which lies at the root of their word for the deepest anguish.
事情应该是这样的。这并不是一个不可能实现的理想。这种情况在少数情况下确实存在，而且只要父母多一点耐心和宽容，几乎所有情况都可能存在。但目前这种情况很少见，以至于他们有一句谚语，我只能以一种非常迂回的方式翻译，但它说，有些人在未来的状态中的最大幸福，就是看着父母归来时的痛苦。与祖辈、祖母永远相伴；而“强制性的感情”是他们表达最深痛苦的词的根源。

There is no talisman in the word ‘parent’ which can generate miracles of affection, and I can well believe that my own child might find it less of a calamity to lose both Arowhena and myself when he is six years old, than to find us again when he is sixty—a sentence which I would not pen did I not feel that by doing so I was giving him something like a hostage, or at any rate putting a weapon into his hands against me, should my selfishness exceed reasonable limits.
“父母”这个词没有任何护身符可以产生感情的奇迹，我完全相信，我自己的孩子可能会发现，在他六岁的时候失去阿罗菲娜和我，比找到我们更不那么灾难。当他六十岁的时候，我不会再写这句话，如果我不觉得这样做，我就给了他一个类似人质的东西，或者无论如何，如果我的自私超出了合理的限度，我就会把武器放在他手中来对付我。

Money is at the bottom of all this to a great extent. If the parents would put their children in the way of earning a competence earlier than they do, the children would soon become self- supporting and independent. As it is, under the present system, the young ones get old enough to have all manner of legitimate wants (that is, if they have any ‘go’ about them) before they have learnt the means of earning money to pay for them; hence they must either do without them, or take more money than the parents can be expected to spare. This is due chiefly to the schools of Unreason, where a boy is taught upon hypothetical principles, as I will explain hereafter; spending years in being incapacitated for doing this, that, or the other (he hardly knows what), during all which time he ought to have been actually doing the thing itself, beginning at the lowest grades, picking it up through actual practice, and rising according to the energy which is in him.
金钱在很大程度上是这一切的根源。如果父母比他们更早地让孩子获得能力，孩子很快就会变得自立和独立。事实上，在现行制度下，年轻人在学会赚钱养家糊口的方法之前，就已经足够大了，能够拥有各种合法的需求（也就是说，如果他们有任何“行动”的话）；因此，他们要么不带孩子，要么拿走比父母所能节省的更多的钱。这主要归功于非理性学校，在那里，男孩接受假设性原则的教育，我将在下文中解释这一点。花了很多年的时间，他无法做这个、那个或那个（他几乎不知道做什么），在这段时间里，他本应该真正做这件事本身，从最低年级开始，通过实际练习来掌握它，并且根据他体内的能量而上升。

These schools of Unreason surprised me much. It would be easy to fall into pseudo-utilitarianism, and I would fain believe that the system may be good for the children of very rich parents, or for those who show a natural instinct to acquire hypothetical lore; but the misery was that their Ydgrun-worship required all people with any pretence to respectability to send their children to some one or other of these schools, mulcting them of years of money. It astonished me to see what sacrifices the parents would make in order to render their children as nearly useless as possible; and it was hard to say whether the old suffered most from the expense which they were thus put to, or the young from being deliberately swindled in some of the most important branches of human inquiry, and directed into false channels or left to drift in the great majority of cases.
这些非理性流派让我非常惊讶。很容易陷入伪功利主义，我很愿意相信这个系统可能对非常富有的父母的孩子有好处，或者对那些表现出获得假设知识的自然本能的人有好处；但不幸的是，他们对伊德格林的崇拜要求所有假装受人尊敬的人都将他们的孩子送到这些学校中的一所或另一所，这让他们损失了多年的金钱。令我惊讶的是，父母们为了让自己的孩子尽可能地变得毫无用处而做出了多大的牺牲。很难说，到底是老年人遭受了最大的损失，还是年轻人在人类探究的一些最重要的领域被故意欺骗，被引导到错误的渠道，或者被遗弃在错误的道路上。绝大多数情况下。

I cannot think I am mistaken in believing that the growing tendency to limit families by infanticide—an evil which was causing general alarm throughout the country—was almost entirely due to the way in which education had become a fetish from one end of Erewhon to the other. Granted that provision should be made whereby every child should be taught reading, writing, and arithmetic, but here compulsory state-aided education should end, and the child should begin (with all due precautions to ensure that he is not overworked) to acquire the rudiments of that art whereby he is to earn his living.
我认为我不会错误地相信，通过杀婴来限制家庭的日益增长的趋势——这种罪恶在全国范围内引起了普遍的恐慌——几乎完全是由于教育从埃雷洪一端到另一端变成了一种迷恋。其他。诚然，应该规定每个孩子都应该接受阅读、写作和算术教育，但国家资助的义务教育应该结束，孩子应该开始（采取一切适当的预防措施以确保他不会过度劳累）获得他赖以谋生的艺术的基础。

He cannot acquire these in what we in England call schools of technical education; such schools are cloister life as against the rough and tumble of the world; they unfit, rather than fit for work in the open. An art can only be learned in the workshop of those who are winning their bread by it.
他无法在我们英国人所谓的技术教育学校中获得这些；这样的学校是与世隔绝的隐士生活。他们不适合，而不是适合户外工作。艺术只能在那些靠它赢得面包的人的工作室里学习。

Boys, as a rule, hate the artificial, and delight in the actual; give them the chance of earning, and they will soon earn. When parents find that their children, instead of being made artificially burdensome, will early begin to contribute to the well-being of the family, they will soon leave off killing them, and will seek to have that plenitude of offspring which they now avoid. As things are, the state lays greater burdens on parents than flesh and blood can bear, and then wrings its hands over an evil for which it is itself mainly responsible.
一般来说，男孩子讨厌做作的东西，喜欢现实的东西。给他们赚钱的机会，他们很快就会赚钱。当父母发现他们的孩子不会被人为地成为负担，而是会尽早开始为家庭的福祉做出贡献时，他们很快就会停止杀害孩子，并会寻求拥有他们现在所避免的繁衍后代。事实上，国家给父母带来的负担超出了血肉之躯所能承受的范围，然后又对自己负主要责任的罪恶绞尽脑汁。

With the less well-dressed classes the harm was not so great; for among these, at about ten years old, the child has to begin doing something: if he is capable he makes his way up; if he is not, he is at any rate not made more incapable by what his friends are pleased to call his education. People find their level as a rule; and though they unfortunately sometimes miss it, it is in the main true that those who have valuable qualities are perceived to have them and can sell them. I think that the Erewhonians are beginning to become aware of these things, for there was much talk about putting a tax upon all parents whose children were not earning a competence according to their degrees by the time they were twenty years old. I am sure that if they will have the courage to carry it through they will never regret it; for the parents will take care that the children shall begin earning money (which means ‘doing good’ to society) at an early age; then the children will be independent early, and they will not press on the parents, nor the parents on them, and they will like each other better than they do now.
对于衣着不太考究的阶层来说，伤害并没有那么大。因为在这些人中，大约十岁的时候，孩子就必须开始做一些事情：如果他有能力，他就会向上；如果他有能力，他就会进步；如果他有能力，他就会进步。如果他不是，至少他的朋友们乐于称他的教育并没有使他变得更加无能。人们通常会找到自己的水平；尽管不幸的是，他们有时会错过这一点，但总的来说，那些拥有宝贵品质的人被认为拥有这些品质，并且可以出售它们。我认为埃雷洪人已经开始意识到这些事情，因为有很多人谈论对所有孩子在二十岁时没有根据他们的学位获得能力的父母征税。我相信，如果他们有勇气坚持到底，他们将永远不会后悔；因为父母会照顾孩子从小就开始赚钱（这意味着对社会“做好事”）；那么孩子就会早点独立，他们不会压迫父母，父母也不会压迫他们，他们会比现在更喜欢彼此。

This is the true philanthropy. He who makes a colossal fortune in the hosiery trade, and by his energy has succeeded in reducing the price of woollen goods by the thousandth part of a penny in the pound—this man is worth ten professional philanthropists. So strongly are the Erewhonians impressed with this, that if a man has made a fortune of over 20,000 pounds a year they exempt him from all taxation, considering him as a work of art, and too precious to be meddled with; they say, ‘How very much he must have done for society before society could have been prevailed upon to give him so much money;’ so magnificent an organisation overawes them; they regard it as a thing dropped from heaven.
这才是真正的慈善事业。在袜子贸易中赚得巨额财富，并凭借自己的精力成功地将羊毛制品的价格降低了千分之一便士的人——这个人的价值相当于十个职业慈善家。埃雷洪尼亚人对此印象深刻，如果一个人每年的财富超过 20,000 英镑，他们就免除他的所有税收，认为他是一件艺术品，太珍贵了，不容干涉；他们说：“他必须为社会做出多少贡献，社会才能说服他给他这么多钱。”如此宏伟的组织令他们惊叹不已；他们将其视为从天而降的东西。

‘Money,’ they say, ‘is the symbol of duty, it is the sacrament of having done for mankind that which mankind wanted. Mankind may not be a very good judge, but there is no better.’ This used to shock me at first, when I remembered that it had been said on high authority that they who have riches shall enter hardly into the kingdom of heaven; but the influence of Erewhon had made me begin to see things in a new light, and I could not help thinking that they who have not riches shall enter more hardly still.
他们说，“金钱是责任的象征，是为人类完成人类想要的事情的圣礼。”人类也许不是一个很好的法官，但也没有比这更好的了。”起初，当我想起有权威说过，拥有财富的人很难进天国时，这让我很震惊；但埃雷洪的影响使我开始以新的眼光看待事物，我不禁想到，那些没有财富的人更难进入。

People oppose money to culture, and imply that if a man has spent his time in making money he will not be cultivated—fallacy of fallacies! As though there could be a greater aid to culture than the having earned an honourable independence, and as though any amount of culture will do much for the man who is penniless, except make him feel his position more deeply. The young man who was told to sell all his goods and give to the poor, must have been an entirely exceptional person if the advice was given wisely, either for him or for the poor; how much more often does it happen that we perceive a man to have all sorts of good qualities except money, and feel that his real duty lies in getting every half-penny that he can persuade others to pay him for his services, and becoming rich. It has been said that the love of money is the root of all evil. The want of money is so quite as truly.
人们把金钱与文化对立起来，暗示一个人如果把时间花在了赚钱上，他就没有修养——谬论中的谬论！似乎对文化的帮助可能比赢得光荣的独立更大，似乎任何程度的文化都会对身无分文的人有很大帮助，除了让他更深刻地感受到自己的地位。那个被告知要卖掉所有财产并施舍给穷人的年轻人，如果他的建议是明智的，无论是对他还是对穷人来说，他一定是一个完全不同寻常的人。更有多少时候，我们认为一个人拥有除金钱以外的各种良好品质，并认为他真正的责任在于获得他能说服别人付钱给他的每一分钱，并变得富有。 。有人说，贪财是万恶之源。缺钱是千真万确的。

The above may sound irreverent, but it is conceived in a spirit of the most utter reverence for those things which do alone deserve it—that is, for the things which are, which mould us and fashion us, be they what they may; for the things that have power to punish us, and which will punish us if we do not heed them; for our masters therefore. But I am drifting away from my story.
上述内容可能听起来不敬，但它是本着对那些单独值得尊重的事物最彻底的尊重的精神构思的，也就是说，对那些塑造我们和塑造我们的事物，无论它们是什么；因为那些有能力惩罚我们的事物，如果我们不听从它们，它们就会惩罚我们；因此，对于我们的主人来说。但我正在偏离我的故事。

They have another plan about which they are making a great noise and fuss, much as some are doing with women’s rights in England. A party of extreme radicals have professed themselves unable to decide upon the superiority of age or youth. At present all goes on the supposition that it is desirable to make the young old as soon as possible. Some would have it that this is wrong, and that the object of education should be to keep the old young as long as possible. They say that each age should take it turn in turn about, week by week, one week the old to be topsawyers, and the other the young, drawing the line at thirty-five years of age; but they insist that the young should be allowed to inflict corporal chastisement on the old, without which the old would be quite incorrigible. In any European country this would be out of the question; but it is not so there, for the straighteners are constantly ordering people to be flogged, so that they are familiar with the notion. I do not suppose that the idea will be ever acted upon; but its having been even mooted is enough to show the utter perversion of the Erewhonian mind.
他们还有另一个计划，对此他们大肆喧哗和大惊小怪，就像英国一些人在争取妇女权利方面所做的那样。一群极端激进分子声称自己无法决定年龄和青年的优越性。目前，所有人都认为希望尽快让年轻人变老。有人会认为这是错误的，教育的目的应该是让老的年轻的人尽可能长寿。他们说，每个年龄段都应该轮流轮流，一周一周，一周让老年人当拓宽者，另一周让年轻人当，以三十五岁为界；但他们坚持认为，应该允许年轻人对老年人进行体罚，否则老年人将无可救药。在任何欧洲国家，这都是不可能的。但那里的情况并非如此，因为矫正者经常下令鞭打人们，以便他们熟悉这个概念。我不认为这个想法会被付诸实施。但它的提出就足以表明埃雷洪人思想的彻底扭曲。

CHAPTER XXI: THE COLLEGES OF UNREASON
第二十一章：非理性学院

I had now been a visitor with the Nosnibors for some five or six months, and though I had frequently proposed to leave them and take apartments of my own, they would not hear of my doing so. I suppose they thought I should be more likely to fall in love with Zulora if I remained, but it was my affection for Arowhena that kept me.
我现在已经在诺斯尼伯一家做客了大约五六个月了，尽管我经常提出离开他们并拥有自己的公寓，但他们不会听说我这样做。我想他们认为如果我留下来，我应该更有可能爱上祖罗拉，但正是我对阿罗维娜的感情留住了我。

During all this time both Arowhena and myself had been dreaming, and drifting towards an avowed attachment, but had not dared to face the real difficulties of the position. Gradually, however, matters came to a crisis in spite of ourselves, and we got to see the true state of the case, all too clearly.
在这段时间里，阿罗菲娜和我都一直在做梦，并逐渐走向一种公开的依恋，但却不敢面对这个职位的真正困难。然而，渐渐地，事情不由自主地陷入了危机，我们也看清了案件的真相。

One evening we were sitting in the garden, and I had been trying in every stupid roundabout way to get her to say that she should be at any rate sorry for a man, if he really loved a woman who would not marry him. I had been stammering and blushing, and been as silly as any one could be, and I suppose had pained her by fishing for pity for myself in such a transparent way, and saying nothing about her own need of it; at any rate, she turned all upon me with a sweet sad smile and said, ‘Sorry? I am sorry for myself; I am sorry for you; and I am sorry for every one.’ The words had no sooner crossed her lips than she bowed her head, gave me a look as though I were to make no answer, and left me.
一天晚上，我们坐在花园里，我一直在试图以各种愚蠢的迂回方式让她说，如果一个男人真的爱一个不肯嫁给他的女人，她至少应该为他感到难过。我一直结结巴巴、脸红，像任何人一样愚蠢，我想，我以如此透明的方式为自己寻求怜悯，却只字不提她自己的需要，这让她感到痛苦；无论如何，她把一切转向我，脸上带着甜蜜而悲伤的微笑，说道：“抱歉？”我为自己感到难过；我为你感到难过；我为每个人感到抱歉。”话一出口，她就低下了头，看了我一眼，好像我不想回答，然后就离开了我。

The words were few and simple, but the manner with which they were uttered was ineffable: the scales fell from my eyes, and I felt that I had no right to try and induce her to infringe one of the most inviolable customs of her country, as she needs must do if she were to marry me. I sat for a long while thinking, and when I remembered the sin and shame and misery which an unrighteous marriage—for as such it would be held in Erewhon—would entail, I became thoroughly ashamed of myself for having been so long self- blinded. I write coldly now, but I suffered keenly at the time, and should probably retain a much more vivid recollection of what I felt, had not all ended so happily.
这些话很少而简单，但说话的方式却是难以形容的：天平从我的眼睛里掉下来，我觉得我没有权利试图引导她侵犯她国家最不可侵犯的习俗之一，如果她要嫁给我，她就必须这么做。我坐了很长一段时间思考，当我想起一场不义的婚姻——因为在埃里洪举行这样的婚姻——将带来的罪恶、耻辱和痛苦时，我为自己长期以来的自我蒙蔽感到彻底羞愧。 。我现在写得很冷淡，但当时我很痛苦，也许应该对我的感受保留更生动的回忆，但一切并没有那么幸福地结束。

As for giving up the idea of marrying Arowhena, it never so much as entered my head to do so: the solution must be found in some other direction than this. The idea of waiting till somebody married Zulora was to be no less summarily dismissed. To marry Arowhena at once in Erewhon—this had already been abandoned: there remained therefore but one alternative, and that was to run away with her, and get her with me to Europe, where there would be no bar to our union save my own impecuniosity, a matter which gave me no uneasiness.
至于放弃与阿罗菲娜结婚的想法，我从来没有想到过：必须从其他方向找到解决方案。等到某人与祖洛拉结婚的想法也同样被草率地打消了。立即在埃瑞洪迎娶阿罗希娜——这件事已经被放弃了：因此只剩下一个选择，那就是带着她私奔，带她和我一起去欧洲，在那里，除了我自己的联盟​​之外，我们的结合不会受到任何阻碍。身无分文，这并不让我感到不安。

To this obvious and simple plan I could see but two objections that deserved the name,—the first, that perhaps Arowhena would not come; the second, that it was almost impossible for me to escape even alone, for the king had himself told me that I was to consider myself a prisoner on parole, and that the first sign of my endeavouring to escape would cause me to be sent to one of the hospitals for incurables. Besides, I did not know the geography of the country, and even were I to try and find my way back, I should be discovered long before I had reached the pass over which I had come. How then could I hope to be able to take Arowhena with me? For days and days I turned these difficulties over in my mind, and at last hit upon as wild a plan as was ever suggested by extremity. This was to meet the second difficulty: the first gave me less uneasiness, for when Arowhena and I next met after our interview in the garden I could see that she had suffered not less acutely than myself.
对于这个明显而简单的计划，我只能看到两个名副其实的反对意见：第一，也许阿罗希纳不会来；第二，即使我独自一人逃跑，也几乎不可能，因为国王亲自告诉我，我将被视为假释囚犯，而我一旦试图逃跑，就会被送往监狱。收治不治之症的医院之一。此外，我不了解这个国家的地理，即使我试图找到回去的路，我也会在到达我来时经过的山口之前很久就被发现了。那么我怎么能希望能够带着Arowhena一起呢？日复一日，我在心里反复思索这些困难，最后突然想到了一个极端的计划。这是为了应对第二个困难：第一个困难让我不那么不安，因为当我和阿罗维娜在花园里采访后下次见面时，我可以看到她所遭受的痛苦并不比我少。

I resolved that I would have another interview with her—the last for the present—that I would then leave her, and set to work upon maturing my plan as fast as possible. We got a chance of being alone together, and then I gave myself the loose rein, and told her how passionately and devotedly I loved her. She said little in return, but her tears (which I could not refrain from answering with my own) and the little she did say were quite enough to show me that I should meet with no obstacle from her. Then I asked her whether she would run a terrible risk which we should share in common, if, in case of success, I could take her to my own people, to the home of my mother and sisters, who would welcome her very gladly. At the same time I pointed out that the chances of failure were far greater than those of success, and that the probability was that even though I could get so far as to carry my design into execution, it would end in death to us both.
我决定再一次采访她——目前最后一次——然后我就离开她，并开始尽快完善我的计划。我们有机会单独在一起，然后我放开了自己，告诉她我是多么热情和忠诚地爱她。她没有说什么作为回应，但她的眼泪（我忍不住用自己的泪水回应）和她所说的那一点足以告诉我，我不应该遇到她的任何障碍。然后我问她是否会冒我们共同承担的可怕风险，如果成功的话，我可以带她到我自己的人民那里，到我母亲和姐妹的家里，他们会非常高兴地欢迎她。同时我指出，失败的可能性远大于成功的可能性，而且即使我能够将我的设计付诸实施，也有可能以我们两人的死亡告终。

I was not mistaken in her; she said that she believed I loved her as much as she loved me, and that she would brave anything if I could only assure her that what I proposed would not be thought dishonourable in England; she could not live without me, and would rather die with me than alone; that death was perhaps the best for us both; that I must plan, and that when the hour came I was to send for her, and trust her not to fail me; and so after many tears and embraces, we tore ourselves away.
我没有看错她。她说她相信我爱她就像她爱我一样，只要我能向她保证我的提议在英国不会被认为是不光彩的，她愿意勇敢做任何事。她没有我就活不下去，宁愿和我一起死也不愿孤单。死亡也许对我们俩都是最好的；我必须做好计划，到时候我就派人去找她，相信她不会让我失望。因此，在多次流泪和拥抱之后，我们分手了。

I then left the Nosnibors, took a lodging in the town, and became melancholy to my heart’s content. Arowhena and I used to see each other sometimes, for I had taken to going regularly to the Musical Banks, but Mrs. Nosnibor and Zulora both treated me with considerable coldness. I felt sure that they suspected me. Arowhena looked miserable, and I saw that her purse was now always as full as she could fill it with the Musical Bank money—much fuller than of old. Then the horrible thought occurred to me that her health might break down, and that she might be subjected to a criminal prosecution. Oh! how I hated Erewhon at that time.
然后我就离开了诺斯尼伯一家，在镇上寄宿下来，心里惆怅起来。阿罗维娜和我有时会见面，因为我习惯了定期去音乐银行，但诺斯尼博尔夫人和祖罗拉对我都相当冷淡。我确信他们怀疑我。阿罗维娜看起来很痛苦，我看到她的钱包现在总是装满了音乐银行的钱——比以前装得多。然后我突然想到她的健康可能会崩溃，她可能会受到刑事起诉。哦！那时我多么讨厌Erewhon。

I was still received at court, but my good looks were beginning to fail me, and I was not such an adept at concealing the effects of pain as the Erewhonians are. I could see that my friends began to look concerned about me, and was obliged to take a leaf out of Mahaina’s book, and pretend to have developed a taste for drinking. I even consulted a straightener as though this were so, and submitted to much discomfort. This made matters better for a time, but I could see that my friends thought less highly of my constitution as my flesh began to fall away.
我仍然在法庭上受到接待，但我的美貌开始让我失望，而且我不像埃雷洪人那样善于隐藏痛苦的影响。我看得出来，我的朋友们开始关心我，不得不向马海娜的书学习，假装已经养成了喝酒的习惯。我什至咨询了直发器，好像确实如此，并且感到非常不舒服。这让事情一度好转，但我可以看到，随着我的肉体开始脱落，我的朋友们对我体质的评价降低了。

I was told that the poor made an outcry about my pension, and I saw a stinging article in an anti-ministerial paper, in which the writer went so far as to say that my having light hair reflected little credit upon me, inasmuch as I had been reported to have said that it was a common thing in the country from which I came. I have reason to believe that Mr. Nosnibor himself inspired this article. Presently it came round to me that the king had begun to dwell upon my having been possessed of a watch, and to say that I ought to be treated medicinally for having told him a lie about the balloons. I saw misfortune gathering round me in every direction, and felt that I should have need of all my wits and a good many more, if I was to steer myself and Arowhena to a good conclusion.
有人告诉我，穷人对我的养老金提出强烈抗议，我在一份反部长的报纸上看到了一篇尖刻的文章，其中作者甚至说我的浅色头发并没有给我带来多少荣誉，因为我据报道说，这在我来自的国家是很常见的事情。我有理由相信诺斯尼博尔先生本人启发了这篇文章。不久，我意识到国王开始谈论我拥有一块手表，并说我应该因为对他说了关于气球的谎言而接受治疗。我看到不幸从四面八方聚集在我周围，我觉得如果我想引导自己和阿罗维娜取得一个好的结果，我需要发挥我所有的智慧，甚至更多。
