There were some who continued to show me kindness, and strange to say, I received the most from the very persons from whom I should have least expected it—I mean from the cashiers of the Musical Banks. I had made the acquaintance of several of these persons, and now that I frequented their bank, they were inclined to make a good deal of me. One of them, seeing that I was thoroughly out of health, though of course he pretended not to notice it, suggested that I should take a little change of air and go down with him to one of the principal towns, which was some two or three days’ journey from the metropolis, and the chief seat of the Colleges of Unreason; he assured me that I should be delighted with what I saw, and that I should receive a most hospitable welcome. I determined therefore to accept the invitation.
有些人继续对我表现出善意，奇怪的是，我从那些我最不应该期待的人那里得到了最多的东西——我指的是音乐银行的出纳员。我已经认识了其中几个人，现在我经常去他们的银行，他们很愿意拿我做很多事情。其中一个人看到我的健康状况不佳，当然他假装没有注意到，建议我换换空气，然后和他一起去一个主要城镇，那里大约有两个或两个。距离大都市三天路程，无理学院总校所在地；他向我保证，我会对所看到的感到高兴，并且会受到最热情的欢迎。因此我决定接受邀请。

We started two or three days later, and after a night on the road, we arrived at our destination towards evening. It was now full spring, and as nearly as might be ten months since I had started with Chowbok on my expedition, but it seemed more like ten years. The trees were in their freshest beauty, and the air had become warm without being oppressively hot. After having lived so many months in the metropolis, the sight of the country, and the country villages through which we passed refreshed me greatly, but I could not forget my troubles. The last five miles or so were the most beautiful part of the journey, for the country became more undulating, and the woods were more extensive; but the first sight of the city of the colleges itself was the most delightful of all. I cannot imagine that there can be any fairer in the whole world, and I expressed my pleasure to my companion, and thanked him for having brought me.
两三天后我们出发，经过一夜的路途，傍晚时分到达了目的地。现在已经是春天了，距离我和乔博克一起探险已经过去了将近十个月，但看起来更像是十年了。树木呈现出最新鲜的美丽，空气变得温暖，但并不闷热。在大都市生活了这么多个月，看到乡村、经过的乡村，让我精神焕发，但我却无法忘记自己的烦恼。最后五英里左右是整个旅程中最美丽的部分，因为乡村变得更加起伏，树林更加广阔；但第一眼看到大学城本身是最令人愉快的。我无法想象世界上还有比这更公平的事情了，我向我的同伴表达了我的高兴，并感谢他带我来。

We drove to an inn in the middle of the town, and then, while it was still light, my friend the cashier, whose name was Thims, took me for a stroll in the streets and in the court-yards of the principal colleges. Their beauty and interest were extreme; it was impossible to see them without being attracted towards them; and I thought to myself that he must be indeed an ill-grained and ungrateful person who can have been a member of one of these colleges without retaining an affectionate feeling towards it for the rest of his life. All my misgivings gave way at once when I saw the beauty and venerable appearance of this delightful city. For half-an-hour I forgot both myself and Arowhena.
我们开车到镇中心的一家旅馆，天还亮的时候，我的收银员朋友蒂姆斯带我在街上和主要学院的庭院里散步。他们的美丽和兴趣是极端的。看到它们就不可能不被它们吸引。我心里想，他确实是个心胸狭隘、忘恩负义的人，竟然能成为其中一所学院的一员，却对它终生没有保留一份感情。当我看到这座令人愉快的城市的美丽和庄严的外观时，我所有的疑虑立刻消失了。半个小时里我忘记了自己和阿罗维娜。

After supper Mr. Thims told me a good deal about the system of education which is here practised. I already knew a part of what I heard, but much was new to me, and I obtained a better idea of the Erewhonian position than I had done hitherto: nevertheless there were parts of the scheme of which I could not comprehend the fitness, although I fully admit that this inability was probably the result of my having been trained so very differently, and to my being then much out of sorts.
晚餐后，蒂姆斯先生向我讲述了很多关于这里实行的教育制度的事情。我已经知道了我听到的一部分内容，但很多东西对我来说都是新的，而且我对埃雷洪尼亚的立场有了比迄今为止更好的了解：尽管如此，该计划的某些部分我无法理解其适用性，尽管我完全承认，这种无能可能是由于我所接受的训练非常不同，以及当时我的状态很差所致。

The main feature in their system is the prominence which they give to a study which I can only translate by the word ‘hypothetics.’ They argue thus—that to teach a boy merely the nature of the things which exist in the world around him, and about which he will have to be conversant during his whole life, would be giving him but a narrow and shallow conception of the universe, which it is urged might contain all manner of things which are not now to be found therein. To open his eyes to these possibilities, and so to prepare him for all sorts of emergencies, is the object of this system of hypothetics. To imagine a set of utterly strange and impossible contingencies, and require the youths to give intelligent answers to the questions that arise therefrom, is reckoned the fittest conceivable way of preparing them for the actual conduct of their affairs in after life.
他们的体系的主要特点是他们对一项研究的重视，我只能用“假设学”这个词来翻译这项研究。他们这样认为——仅仅教一个男孩他周围世界中存在的事物的本质，他一生都必须熟悉的知识，只会给他一个狭隘而肤浅的宇宙概念，它敦促可能包含现在在宇宙中找不到的所有事物。让他看到这些可能性，从而为各种紧急情况做好准备，就是这个假设系统的目标。想象一系列完全奇怪和不可能的意外事件，并要求年轻人对由此产生的问题给出明智的答案，被认为是为他们来世实际处理事务做好准备的最合适的可能方法。

Thus they are taught what is called the hypothetical language for many of their best years—a language which was originally composed at a time when the country was in a very different state of civilisation to what it is at present, a state which has long since disappeared and been superseded. Many valuable maxims and noble thoughts which were at one time concealed in it have become current in their modern literature, and have been translated over and over again into the language now spoken. Surely then it would seem enough that the study of the original language should be confined to the few whose instincts led them naturally to pursue it.
因此，他们在许多最美好的岁月里都被教导着所谓的假设语言——这种语言最初是在这个国家处于与现在截然不同的文明状态的时候创造的，这种状态很久以前就已经存在了。消失并被取代。许多曾经隐藏在其中的有价值的格言和崇高的思想已经在他们的现代文学中流行起来，并被一遍又一遍地翻译成现在所使用的语言。当然，对原始语言的研究应该仅限于少数人，他们的本能自然地引导他们去追求它，这似乎就足够了。

But the Erewhonians think differently; the store they set by this hypothetical language can hardly be believed; they will even give any one a maintenance for life if he attains a considerable proficiency in the study of it; nay, they will spend years in learning to translate some of their own good poetry into the hypothetical language—to do so with fluency being reckoned a distinguishing mark of a scholar and a gentleman. Heaven forbid that I should be flippant, but it appeared to me to be a wanton waste of good human energy that men should spend years and years in the perfection of so barren an exercise, when their own civilisation presented problems by the hundred which cried aloud for solution and would have paid the solver handsomely; but people know their own affairs best. If the youths chose it for themselves I should have wondered less; but they do not choose it; they have it thrust upon them, and for the most part are disinclined towards it. I can only say that all I heard in defence of the system was insufficient to make me think very highly of its advantages.
但埃瑞洪人的想法不同。他们对这种假设语言的重视程度令人难以置信。如果一个人在学习方面取得了相当的熟练程度，他们甚至会为他提供终身赡养费。不仅如此，他们还将花费数年时间学习将自己的一些好诗翻译成假设的语言——这样做的流畅性被认为是学者和绅士的显着标志。上帝不允许我轻率，但在我看来，人们花费数年时间来完善如此贫瘠的一项练习，这在我看来是对人类良好能量的肆意浪费，而当他们自己的文明提出了数百个大声疾呼的问题时寻求解决方案，并会向解决者支付丰厚的费用；但人们最了解自己的事情。如果年轻人为自己选择了它，我就不会那么奇怪了；但他们不选择它；他们是强加给他们的，而且大多数人不愿意这样做。我只能说，我听到的所有为该系统辩护的内容不足以让我高度评价它的优点。

The arguments in favour of the deliberate development of the unreasoning faculties were much more cogent. But here they depart from the principles on which they justify their study of hypothetics; for they base the importance which they assign to hypothetics upon the fact of their being a preparation for the extraordinary, while their study of Unreason rests upon its developing those faculties which are required for the daily conduct of affairs. Hence their professorships of Inconsistency and Evasion, in both of which studies the youths are examined before being allowed to proceed to their degree in hypothetics. The more earnest and conscientious students attain to a proficiency in these subjects which is quite surprising; there is hardly any inconsistency so glaring but they soon learn to defend it, or injunction so clear that they cannot find some pretext for disregarding it.
支持刻意发展非理性能力的论点更有说服力。但在这里他们背离了他们证明假设研究合理性的原则。因为他们对假设的重视是基于假设是为非凡的事情做准备的事实，而他们对非理性的研究则基于其发展日常事务处理所需的能力。因此，他们获得了“不一致”和“逃避”的教授职位，在这两项研究中，年轻人在被允许继续攻读假设学学位之前都会受到检查。更加认真和认真的学生能够熟练掌握这些科目，这是相当令人惊讶的。几乎没有任何不一致之处如此明显，但他们很快就学会了捍卫它，或者禁令如此明确，以至于他们找不到任何借口来忽视它。

Life, they urge, would be intolerable if men were to be guided in all they did by reason and reason only. Reason betrays men into the drawing of hard and fast lines, and to the defining by language—language being like the sun, which rears and then scorches. Extremes are alone logical, but they are always absurd; the mean is illogical, but an illogical mean is better than the sheer absurdity of an extreme. There are no follies and no unreasonablenesses so great as those which can apparently be irrefragably defended by reason itself, and there is hardly an error into which men may not easily be led if they base their conduct upon reason only.
他们强烈主张，如果人们所做的一切都受到理性的引导，并且仅仅依靠理性，那么生活将是无法忍受的。理性背叛了人们，让他们画出严格而快速的线条，并通过语言进行定义——语言就像太阳，升起然后灼热。极端虽然合乎逻辑，但总是荒谬的。中庸之道是不合逻辑的，但不合逻辑的中庸之道总比完全荒谬的极端要好。没有什么愚蠢和不合理的行为比那些显然可以通过理性本身无可辩驳地辩护的行为更严重，而且如果人们只将自己的行为建立在理性的基础上，那么几乎没有什么错误是不容易被引入的。

Reason might very possibly abolish the double currency; it might even attack the personality of Hope and Justice. Besides, people have such a strong natural bias towards it that they will seek it for themselves and act upon it quite as much as or more than is good for them: there is no need of encouraging reason. With unreason the case is different. She is the natural complement of reason, without whose existence reason itself were non-existent.
理性很可能废除双重货币；它甚至可能攻击希望和正义的人格。此外，人们对它有一种强烈的自然偏见，以至于他们会为自己寻求它，并按照它采取尽可能多或超过对他们有利的行动：不需要鼓励性的理由。如果是非理性，情况就不同了。她是理性的天然补充，没有她的存在，理性本身就不存在。

If, then, reason would be non-existent were there no such thing as unreason, surely it follows that the more unreason there is, the more reason there must be also? Hence the necessity for the development of unreason, even in the interests of reason herself. The Professors of Unreason deny that they undervalue reason: none can be more convinced than they are, that if the double currency cannot be rigorously deduced as a necessary consequence of human reason, the double currency should cease forthwith; but they say that it must be deduced from no narrow and exclusive view of reason which should deprive that admirable faculty of the one-half of its own existence. Unreason is a part of reason; it must therefore be allowed its full share in stating the initial conditions.
那么，如果没有非理性这样的东西，理性就不存在，那么，非理性越多，理性必然也就越多吧？因此，即使为了理性本身的利益，非理性的发展也是必要的。非理性教授们否认他们低估了理性：没有人比他们更确信，如果双重货币不能被严格地推论为人类理性的必然结果，那么双重货币就应该立即停止；但他们说，它不能从狭隘和排他性的理性观点中推论出来，这种观点应该剥夺这一令人钦佩的能力的一半存在。非理性是理性的一部分；因此，必须允许它充分参与陈述初始条件。

CHAPTER XXII: THE COLLEGES OF UNREASON—Continued
第二十二章：非理性学院——续

Of genius they make no account, for they say that every one is a genius, more or less. No one is so physically sound that no part of him will be even a little unsound, and no one is so diseased but that some part of him will be healthy—so no man is so mentally and morally sound, but that he will be in part both mad and wicked; and no man is so mad and wicked but he will be sensible and honourable in part. In like manner there is no genius who is not also a fool, and no fool who is not also a genius.
他们不考虑天才，因为他们说每个人或多或少都是天才。没有一个人的身体健康得如此健全，以至于他的任何部分都不会有一点不健康；也没有一个人病得如此严重，但他的某些部分却是健康的——同样，没有一个人的精神和道德如此健全，但他仍处于健康状态。分开疯狂和邪恶；没有人会如此疯狂和邪恶，但他也会有部分理智和光荣。同样地，没有一个天才不是一个傻瓜，也没有一个傻瓜不是一个天才。

When I talked about originality and genius to some gentlemen whom I met at a supper party given by Mr. Thims in my honour, and said that original thought ought to be encouraged, I had to eat my words at once. Their view evidently was that genius was like offences— needs must that it come, but woe unto that man through whom it comes. A man’s business, they hold, is to think as his neighbours do, for Heaven help him if he thinks good what they count bad. And really it is hard to see how the Erewhonian theory differs from our own, for the word ‘idiot’ only means a person who forms his opinions for himself.
当我在蒂姆斯先生为我举办的晚宴上遇到的一些先生谈论原创性和天才，并说应该鼓励原创性思想时，我不得不立即收回自己的话。他们的观点显然是，天才就像冒犯——天才必须出现，但天才的出现却是有祸的。他们认为，一个人的职责就是像他的邻居一样思考，因为如果他认为他们认为不好的事情是好的，上天会帮助他。事实上，很难看出埃鲁霍尼的理论与我们自己的理论有什么不同，因为“白痴”这个词只意味着一个为自己形成自己观点的人。

The venerable Professor of Worldly Wisdom, a man verging on eighty but still hale, spoke to me very seriously on this subject in consequence of the few words that I had imprudently let fall in defence of genius. He was one of those who carried most weight in the university, and had the reputation of having done more perhaps than any other living man to suppress any kind of originality.
德高望重的世间智慧教授，一位年近八十却依然精神矍铄的老人，由于我在为天才辩护时不小心说了几句话，他非常严肃地向我谈到了这个话题。他是大学里最有影响力的人之一，并享有盛誉，因为他在压制任何原创性方面可能比任何其他在世的人都做得更多。

‘It is not our business,’ he said, ‘to help students to think for themselves. Surely this is the very last thing which one who wishes them well should encourage them to do. Our duty is to ensure that they shall think as we do, or at any rate, as we hold it expedient to say we do.’ In some respects, however, he was thought to hold somewhat radical opinions, for he was President of the Society for the Suppression of Useless Knowledge, and for the Completer Obliteration of the Past.
他说：“帮助学生独立思考不是我们的事。”当然，这是祝福他们的人应该鼓励他们做的最后一件事。我们的职责是确保他们像我们一样思考，或者至少像我们认为说我们这样做是有利的那样。”然而，在某些方面，他被认为持有一些激进的观点，因为他是总统抑制无用知识并彻底消除过去的协会。

As regards the tests that a youth must pass before he can get a degree, I found that they have no class lists, and discourage anything like competition among the students; this, indeed, they regard as self-seeking and unneighbourly. The examinations are conducted by way of papers written by the candidate on set subjects, some of which are known to him beforehand, while others are devised with a view of testing his general capacity and savoir faire.
至于年轻人获得学位之前必须通过的考试，我发现他们没有班级名单，不鼓励学生之间的竞争；事实上，他们认为这是自私且不睦的。考试是通过考生就指定科目撰写的试卷进行的，其中一些科目是他事先知道的，而另一些科目则是为了测试他的一般能力和专业知识而设计的。

My friend the Professor of Worldly Wisdom was the terror of the greater number of students; and, so far as I could judge, he very well might be, for he had taken his Professorship more seriously than any of the other Professors had done. I heard of his having plucked one poor fellow for want of sufficient vagueness in his saving clauses paper. Another was sent down for having written an article on a scientific subject without having made free enough use of the words ‘carefully,’ ‘patiently,’ and ‘earnestly.’ One man was refused a degree for being too often and too seriously in the right, while a few days before I came a whole batch had been plucked for insufficient distrust of printed matter.
我的朋友，世俗智慧教授让更多的学生感到恐惧。据我判断，他很可能是这样，因为他比任何其他教授都更认真地对待自己的教授职位。我听说他因为储蓄条款文件不够含糊而解雇了一个可怜的家伙。另一个人因为写了一篇关于科学主题的文章而没有充分自由地使用“仔细”、“耐心”和“认真”等词而被罚下。是的，而在我来的前几天，由于对印刷品的不信任，整批都被摘了下来。

About this there was just then rather a ferment, for it seems that the Professor had written an article in the leading university magazine, which was well known to be by him, and which abounded in all sorts of plausible blunders. He then set a paper which afforded the examinees an opportunity of repeating these blunders— which, believing the article to be by their own examiner, they of course did. The Professor plucked every single one of them, but his action was considered to have been not quite handsome.
关于此事，当时引起了相当大的骚动，因为教授似乎在主要大学杂志上写了一篇文章，众所周知，这篇文章是他写的，其中充满了各种看似合理的错误。然后，他布置了一篇试卷，为考生提供了重复这些错误的机会——他们相信这篇文章是他们自己的考官写的，他们当然这么做了。教授一个个都拔了，但动作却被认为不太帅。

I told them of Homer’s noble line to the effect that a man should strive ever to be foremost and in all things to outvie his peers; but they said that no wonder the countries in which such a detestable maxim was held in admiration were always flying at one another’s throats.
我告诉他们荷马的高贵思想，大意是一个人应该永远努力成为第一，在所有事情上都超越他的同龄人。但他们表示，难怪那些推崇这种令人憎恶的格言的国家总是互相争斗。

‘Why,’ asked one Professor, ‘should a man want to be better than his neighbours? Let him be thankful if he is no worse.’
一位教授问道：“为什么一个人应该比他的邻居更好？”如果他没有变得更糟，就让他心存感激吧。

I ventured feebly to say that I did not see how progress could be made in any art or science, or indeed in anything at all, without more or less self-seeking, and hence unamiability.
我壮着胆子说，如果没有或多或少的自私自利和不友善，我看不出如何能够在任何艺术或科学上取得进步，甚至在任何事情上都能取得进步。

‘Of course it cannot,’ said the Professor, ‘and therefore we object to progress.’
“当然不可能，”教授说，“因此我们反对进步。”

After which there was no more to be said. Later on, however, a young Professor took me aside and said he did not think I quite understood their views about progress.
之后就没有再说什么了。然而后来，一位年轻的教授把我拉到一边，说他认为我不太理解他们对进步的看法。

‘We like progress,’ he said, ‘but it must commend itself to the common sense of the people. If a man gets to know more than his neighbours he should keep his knowledge to himself till he has sounded them, and seen whether they agree, or are likely to agree with him. He said it was as immoral to be too far in front of one’s own age, as to lag too far behind it. If a man can carry his neighbours with him, he may say what he likes; but if not, what insult can be more gratuitous than the telling them what they do not want to know? A man should remember that intellectual over- indulgence is one of the most insidious and disgraceful forms that excess can take. Granted that every one should exceed more or less, inasmuch as absolutely perfect sanity would drive any man mad the moment he reached it, but … ‘
“我们喜欢进步，”他说，“但它必须符合人民的常识。”如果一个人比他的邻居懂得更多，他就应该保守自己的知识，直到他试探过他们，看看他们是否同意或可能同意他的观点。他说，远远超过自己的年龄，就像落后太远一样，都是不道德的。如果一个人能够带着他的邻居一起去，他就可以说他想说的话；但如果不是，还有什么侮辱比告诉他们他们不想知道的事情更无端呢？一个人应该记住，智力上的过度放纵是放纵行为中最阴险、最可耻的形式之一。诚然，每个人都应该或多或少地超过，因为绝对完美的理智会让任何人在达到它的那一刻发疯，但是……”

He was now warming to his subject and I was beginning to wonder how I should get rid of him, when the party broke up, and though I promised to call on him before I left, I was unfortunately prevented from doing so.
他现在对他的话题越来越感兴趣，我开始想知道该如何摆脱他，当聚会散场时，虽然我答应在离开前拜访他，但不幸的是我没有这样做。

I have now said enough to give English readers some idea of the strange views which the Erewhonians hold concerning unreason, hypothetics, and education generally. In many respects they were sensible enough, but I could not get over the hypothetics, especially the turning their own good poetry into the hypothetical language. In the course of my stay I met one youth who told me that for fourteen years the hypothetical language had been almost the only thing that he had been taught, although he had never (to his credit, as it seemed to me) shown the slightest proclivity towards it, while he had been endowed with not inconsiderable ability for several other branches of human learning. He assured me that he would never open another hypothetical book after he had taken his degree, but would follow out the bent of his own inclinations. This was well enough, but who could give him his fourteen years back again?
我现在已经说了足够多的内容，足以让英国读者了解埃雷洪人对非理性、假设和一般教育所持有的奇怪观点。他们在很多方面都足够明智，但我无法克服这些假设，尤其是将他们自己的好诗变成假设的语言。在我逗留期间，我遇到了一位年轻人，他告诉我，十四年来，假想语言几乎是他所学到的唯一东西，尽管他从未（值得赞扬的是，在我看来）表现出丝毫的兴趣。他在人类学习的其他几个分支方面也被赋予了不小的能力。他向我保证，在获得学位后，他永远不会再打开另一本假想的书，而是会按照自己的喜好行事。这已经很好了，但谁能让他回到十四岁呢？

I sometimes wondered how it was that the mischief done was not more clearly perceptible, and that the young men and women grew up as sensible and goodly as they did, in spite of the attempts almost deliberately made to warp and stunt their growth. Some doubtless received damage, from which they suffered to their life’s end; but many seemed little or none the worse, and some, almost the better. The reason would seem to be that the natural instinct of the lads in most cases so absolutely rebelled against their training, that do what the teachers might they could never get them to pay serious heed to it. The consequence was that the boys only lost their time, and not so much of this as might have been expected, for in their hours of leisure they were actively engaged in exercises and sports which developed their physical nature, and made them at any rate strong and healthy.
有时我想知道为什么这些恶作剧并没有更明显地被察觉，尽管人们几乎故意扭曲和阻碍年轻男女的成长，但这些年轻男女却像他们一样明智而良好地成长。毫无疑问，有些人受到了伤害，并因此丧命。但许多人似乎并没有变得更糟，甚至没有更糟，而有些则几乎更好。原因似乎是，在大多数情况下，小伙子们的自然本能完全违背了他们的训练，即使老师想做的事，他们也永远无法让他们认真注意。结果是，男孩们只是失去了时间，而且并没有想象中的那么多，因为在闲暇时间，他们积极参加锻炼和运动，这些锻炼和运动发展了他们的身体素质，至少使他们变得强壮和健康的。

Moreover those who had any special tastes could not be restrained from developing them: they would learn what they wanted to learn and liked, in spite of obstacles which seemed rather to urge them on than to discourage them, while for those who had no special capacity, the loss of time was of comparatively little moment; but in spite of these alleviations of the mischief, I am sure that much harm was done to the children of the sub-wealthy classes, by the system which passes current among the Erewhonians as education. The poorest children suffered least—if destruction and death have heard the sound of wisdom, to a certain extent poverty has done so also.
此外，那些有任何特殊品味的人不能被限制发展它们：他们会学习他们想学和喜欢的东西，尽管障碍似乎是在敦促他们而不是阻止他们，而对于那些没有特殊能力的人来说，时间的损失相对较小；但是，尽管这些危害有所减轻，但我确信埃雷洪人中流行的教育制度对次富裕阶层的孩子造成了很大的伤害。最贫困的儿童遭受的痛苦最少——如果破坏和死亡听到了智慧的声音，那么在某种程度上，贫困也起到了同样的作用。

And yet perhaps, after all, it is better for a country that its seats of learning should do more to suppress mental growth than to encourage it. Were it not for a certain priggishness which these places infuse into so great a number of their alumni, genuine work would become dangerously common. It is essential that by far the greater part of what is said or done in the world should be so ephemeral as to take itself away quickly; it should keep good for twenty-four hours, or even twice as long, but it should not be good enough a week hence to prevent people from going on to something else. No doubt the marvellous development of journalism in England, as also the fact that our seats of learning aim rather at fostering mediocrity than anything higher, is due to our subconscious recognition of the fact that it is even more necessary to check exuberance of mental development than to encourage it. There can be no doubt that this is what our academic bodies do, and they do it the more effectually because they do it only subconsciously. They think they are advancing healthy mental assimilation and digestion, whereas in reality they are little better than cancer in the stomach.
但归根结底，对于一个国家来说，其学习场所应该更多地抑制智力发展而不是鼓励智力发展，这也许更好。如果不是这些地方给如此多的校友灌输了某种自以为是的态度，真正的工作就会变得危险地普遍。至关重要的是，迄今为止，世界上所说或所做的大部分事情都应该是短暂的，以至于很快就会消失。它应该保持二十四小时，甚至两倍的时间，但一周不应该足够好，因此会阻止人们继续做其他事情。毫无疑问，英国新闻业的惊人发展，以及我们的学习场所的目的不是培养平庸而不是更高的事实，都是由于我们潜意识中认识到这样一个事实，即检查智力发展的旺盛程度比检查智力发展的旺盛程度更重要。鼓励它。毫无疑问，这就是我们学术机构所做的事情，而且他们做得更有效，因为他们只是在潜意识里这样做。他们认为自己正在促进健康的精神同化和消化，但实际上，他们比胃癌好不了多少。

Let me return, however, to the Erewhonians. Nothing surprised me more than to see the occasional flashes of common sense with which one branch of study or another was lit up, while not a single ray fell upon so many others. I was particularly struck with this on strolling into the Art School of the University. Here I found that the course of study was divided into two branches—the practical and the commercial—no student being permitted to continue his studies in the actual practice of the art he had taken up, unless he made equal progress in its commercial history.
然而，让我回到埃雷洪尼亚人。没有什么比看到常识的偶尔闪现照亮一个或另一个研究分支更让我感到惊讶的了，而其他许多分支却没有一丝光芒落到他们身上。当我走进大学艺术学院时，我对此印象特别深刻。在这里，我发现学习课程分为两个分支——实践和商业——没有学生被允许在他所从事的艺术的实际实践中继续学习，除非他在商业历史上取得了同样的进步。

Thus those who were studying painting were examined at frequent intervals in the prices which all the leading pictures of the last fifty or a hundred years had realised, and in the fluctuations in their values when (as often happened) they had been sold and resold three or four times. The artist, they contend, is a dealer in pictures, and it is as important for him to learn how to adapt his wares to the market, and to know approximately what kind of a picture will fetch how much, as it is for him to be able to paint the picture. This, I suppose, is what the French mean by laying so much stress upon ‘values.’
因此，那些学习绘画的人会定期检查过去五十年或一百年的所有主要画作的价格，以及当它们被出售和转售三年时（经常发生的情况）它们的价值波动。或四次。他们认为，艺术家是画作经销商，对他来说，学习如何使他的作品适应市场、了解什么样的画能卖多少钱对他来说同样重要。能够画出这幅画。我想，这就是法国人如此强调“价值观”的意思。

As regards the city itself, the more I saw the more enchanted I became. I dare not trust myself with any description of the exquisite beauty of the different colleges, and their walks and gardens. Truly in these things alone there must be a hallowing and refining influence which is in itself half an education, and which no amount of error can wholly spoil. I was introduced to many of the Professors, who showed me every hospitality and kindness; nevertheless I could hardly avoid a sort of suspicion that some of those whom I was taken to see had been so long engrossed in their own study of hypothetics that they had become the exact antitheses of the Athenians in the days of St. Paul; for whereas the Athenians spent their lives in nothing save to see and to hear some new thing, there were some here who seemed to devote themselves to the avoidance of every opinion with which they were not perfectly familiar, and regarded their own brains as a sort of sanctuary, to which if an opinion had once resorted, none other was to attack it.
至于这座城市本身，我看得越多，就越着迷。我不敢相信自己能够描述不同学院及其步道和花园的精致之美。确实，仅在这些事情上就一定有一种神圣而精炼的影响力，这种影响力本身就是半种教育，任何错误都不能完全破坏这种影响力。我被介绍给了许多教授，他们对我表现出热情好客和友善。然而，我很难避免一种怀疑，即我被带去见的一些人长期专注于自己的假设研究，以至于他们已经成为圣保罗时代雅典人的对立面。因为，雅典人除了看到和听到一些新事物之外，就度过了他们的一生，而这里有些人似乎致力于避免他们不完全熟悉的每一种观点，并认为自己的大脑是一种庇护所，一旦有意见诉诸于此，就没有其他人会攻击它。

I should warn the reader, however, that I was rarely sure what the men whom I met while staying with Mr. Thims really meant; for there was no getting anything out of them if they scented even a suspicion that they might be what they call ‘giving themselves away.’ As there is hardly any subject on which this suspicion cannot arise, I found it difficult to get definite opinions from any of them, except on such subjects as the weather, eating and drinking, holiday excursions, or games of skill.
然而，我应该警告读者，我很少确定我和蒂姆斯先生住在一起时遇到的那些人的真正含义是什么；因为如果他们察觉到自己可能是所谓的“出卖自己”，那么他们就无法从他们身上得到任何信息。由于几乎没有任何主题不会产生这种怀疑，我发现很难从他们那里得到明确的意见。其中任何一个，除了天气、饮食、假期旅行或技巧游戏等主题。

If they cannot wriggle out of expressing an opinion of some sort, they will commonly retail those of some one who has already written upon the subject, and conclude by saying that though they quite admit that there is an element of truth in what the writer has said, there are many points on which they are unable to agree with him. Which these points were, I invariably found myself unable to determine; indeed, it seemed to be counted the perfection of scholarship and good breeding among them not to have—much less to express—an opinion on any subject on which it might prove later that they had been mistaken. The art of sitting gracefully on a fence has never, I should think, been brought to greater perfection than at the Erewhonian Colleges of Unreason.
如果他们无法避免表达某种观点，他们通常会转述已经写过该主题的人的观点，并得出结论说，尽管他们非常承认作者所写的内容有一定的真实性。说，有很多观点他们无法同意他的观点。我总是发现自己无法确定这些要点是什么。事实上，他们似乎拥有完美的学识和良好的教养，对任何问题不持有任何意见，更不用说表达意见，而这些意见后来可能会证明他们是错误的。我认为，优雅地坐在栅栏上的艺术从来没有像埃雷洪尼亚非理性学院那样达到如此完美的程度。

Even when, wriggle as they may, they find themselves pinned down to some expression of definite opinion, as often as not they will argue in support of what they perfectly well know to be untrue. I repeatedly met with reviews and articles even in their best journals, between the lines of which I had little difficulty in detecting a sense exactly contrary to the one ostensibly put forward. So well is this understood, that a man must be a mere tyro in the arts of Erewhonian polite society, unless he instinctively suspects a hidden ‘yea’ in every ‘nay’ that meets him. Granted that it comes to much the same in the end, for it does not matter whether ‘yea’ is called ‘yea’ or ‘nay,’ so long as it is understood which it is to be; but our own more direct way of calling a spade a spade, rather than a rake, with the intention that every one should understand it as a spade, seems more satisfactory. On the other hand, the Erewhonian system lends itself better to the suppression of that downrightness which it seems the express aim of Erewhonian philosophy to discountenance.
即使他们竭尽全力，发现自己只能表达某种明确的观点，但他们常常会争论支持他们明知不真实的观点。我多次遇到评论和文章，甚至是在他们最好的期刊上，我毫不费力地在它们的字里行间中发现了一种与表面上提出的完全相反的感觉。人们对这一点的理解如此透彻，以至于一个人在埃雷洪尼亚上流社会的艺术中必定只是一个新手，除非他本能地怀疑在他遇到的每一个“不”中都隐藏着一个“是”。诚然，最终的结果大致相同，因为“是”被称为“是”还是“否”并不重要，只要它被理解为“是”就可以了。但我们自己更直接的称呼黑桃是黑桃的方式，而不是耙子，目的是让每个人都应该将其理解为黑桃，似乎更令人满意。另一方面，埃雷洪主义体系更适合抑制那种直截了当的行为，而这种直率似乎是埃雷洪主义哲学的明确目标，不予理睬。

However this may be, the fear-of-giving-themselves-away disease was fatal to the intelligence of those infected by it, and almost every one at the Colleges of Unreason had caught it to a greater or less degree. After a few years atrophy of the opinions invariably supervened, and the sufferer became stone dead to everything except the more superficial aspects of those material objects with which he came most in contact. The expression on the faces of these people was repellent; they did not, however, seem particularly unhappy, for they none of them had the faintest idea that they were in reality more dead than alive. No cure for this disgusting fear- of-giving-themselves-away disease has yet been discovered.
不管情况如何，害怕暴露自己的疾病对于感染者的智力来说是致命的，几乎非理性学院的每个人都或多或少地感染了这种疾病。几年之后，观念必然随之萎缩，患者对一切都变得死气沉沉，除了他最常接触的那些物质对象的更肤浅的方面。这些人脸上的表情都令人厌恶。然而，他们似乎并没有特别不高兴，因为他们中没有一个人丝毫不知道自己实际上已经死了，而不是活着。对于这种令人厌恶的“害怕暴露自己的疾病”，目前还没有找到治愈方法。

* * *

It was during my stay in City of the Colleges of Unreason—a city whose Erewhonian name is so cacophonous that I refrain from giving it—that I learned the particulars of the revolution which had ended in the destruction of so many of the mechanical inventions which were formerly in common use.
正是在我在非理性学院之城逗留期间——这座城市的埃雷洪尼亚语名字如此刺耳，以至于我没有说出它——我了解到了这场革命的细节，这场革命最终导致了许多机械发明的毁灭。以前很常用。

Mr. Thims took me to the rooms of a gentleman who had a great reputation for learning, but who was also, so Mr. Thims told me, rather a dangerous person, inasmuch as he had attempted to introduce an adverb into the hypothetical language. He had heard of my watch and been exceedingly anxious to see me, for he was accounted the most learned antiquary in Erewhon on the subject of mechanical lore. We fell to talking upon the subject, and when I left he gave me a reprinted copy of the work which brought the revolution about.
蒂姆斯先生带我去了一位绅士的房间，这位绅士在学问上享有很高的声誉，但蒂姆斯先生告诉我，他也是一个相当危险的人，因为他试图在假设的语言中引入一个副词。他听说过我的手表，并且非常渴望见到我，因为他被认为是埃雷洪在机械知识方面最博学的古董家。我们开始谈论这个话题，当我离开时，他给了我一本引发革命的著作的重印本。

It had taken place some five hundred years before my arrival: people had long become thoroughly used to the change, although at the time that it was made the country was plunged into the deepest misery, and a reaction which followed had very nearly proved successful. Civil war raged for many years, and is said to have reduced the number of the inhabitants by one-half. The parties were styled the machinists and the anti-machinists, and in the end, as I have said already, the latter got the victory, treating their opponents with such unparalleled severity that they extirpated every trace of opposition.
它发生在我到达之前大约五百年：人们早已完全习惯了这种变化，尽管当时国家正陷入最深的苦难，随后的反应几乎被证明是成功的。内战持续多年，据说居民人数减少了一半。两党被称为机械主义者和反机械主义者，最后，正如我已经说过的，后者取得了胜利，他们以无与伦比的严厉态度对待他们的对手，以至于消灭了一切反对派。

The wonder was that they allowed any mechanical appliances to remain in the kingdom, neither do I believe that they would have done so, had not the Professors of Inconsistency and Evasion made a stand against the carrying of the new principles to their legitimate conclusions. These Professors, moreover, insisted that during the struggle the anti-machinists should use every known improvement in the art of war, and several new weapons, offensive and defensive, were invented, while it was in progress. I was surprised at there remaining so many mechanical specimens as are seen in the museums, and at students having rediscovered their past uses so completely; for at the time of the revolution the victors wrecked all the more complicated machines, and burned all treatises on mechanics, and all engineers’ workshops—thus, so they thought, cutting the mischief out root and branch, at an incalculable cost of blood and treasure.
令人惊奇的是，他们允许任何机械设备留在王国里，我也不相信他们会这样做，如果没有不一致和逃避的教授们反对将新原则带入他们的合法结论。此外，这些教授坚持认为，在斗争中，反机械主义者应该利用战争艺术中一切已知的改进，并在战争进行过程中发明了几种进攻性和防御性的新武器。我很惊讶博物馆里还保留着如此多的机械标本，学生们如此彻底地重新发现了它们过去的用途；这让我感到惊讶。因为在革命时期，胜利者毁坏了所有更复杂的机器，烧毁了所有机械论文和所有工程师的工作室——因此，他们认为，要彻底消灭恶作剧，付出了无法估量的鲜血和代价。宝藏。

Certainly they had not spared their labour, but work of this description can never be perfectly achieved, and when, some two hundred years before my arrival, all passion upon the subject had cooled down, and no one save a lunatic would have dreamed of reintroducing forbidden inventions, the subject came to be regarded as a curious antiquarian study, like that of some long-forgotten religious practices among ourselves. Then came the careful search for whatever fragments could be found, and for any machines that might have been hidden away, and also numberless treatises were written, showing what the functions of each rediscovered machine had been; all being done with no idea of using such machinery again, but with the feelings of an English antiquarian concerning Druidical monuments or flint arrow heads.
他们当然不遗余力，但是这种描述的工作永远不可能完美地完成，在我到达之前大约两百年，对这个主题的所有热情都已经冷却下来，除了疯子之外没有人会梦想重新引入被禁止的发明，这个主题逐渐被视为一项奇怪的古物研究，就像我们之间一些长期被遗忘的宗教活动一样。随后，人们开始仔细搜寻能找到的碎片，以及可能被隐藏起来的机器，并撰写了无数的论文，展示了每台重新发现的机器的功能；所有这一切都是在没有再次使用这种机器的想法的情况下完成的，而是带着英国古物学家对德鲁伊纪念碑或燧石箭头的感觉。

On my return to the metropolis, during the remaining weeks or rather days of my sojourn in Erewhon I made a resume in English of the work which brought about the already mentioned revolution. My ignorance of technical terms has led me doubtless into many errors, and I have occasionally, where I found translation impossible, substituted purely English names and ideas for the original Erewhonian ones, but the reader may rely on my general accuracy. I have thought it best to insert my translation here.
回到大都市后，在埃里洪逗留的剩余几周或更确切地说几天内，我用英语写了一份导致前面提到的革命的工作简历。我对技术术语的无知无疑使我犯了许多错误，有时，当我发现翻译不可能时，我会用纯英文的名称和想法替换原来的埃鲁洪语名称和想法，但读者可以相信我的总体准确性。我认为最好在这里插入我的翻译。

CHAPTER XXIII: THE BOOK OF THE MACHINES
第二十三章：机器之书

The writer commences:- ‘There was a time, when the earth was to all appearance utterly destitute both of animal and vegetable life, and when according to the opinion of our best philosophers it was simply a hot round ball with a crust gradually cooling. Now if a human being had existed while the earth was in this state and had been allowed to see it as though it were some other world with which he had no concern, and if at the same time he were entirely ignorant of all physical science, would he not have pronounced it impossible that creatures possessed of anything like consciousness should be evolved from the seeming cinder which he was beholding? Would he not have denied that it contained any potentiality of consciousness? Yet in the course of time consciousness came. Is it not possible then that there may be even yet new channels dug out for consciousness, though we can detect no signs of them at present?
作者开始写道：“曾经有一段时间，地球表面上完全没有动物和植物的生命，根据我们最优秀的哲学家的观点，地球只是一个热圆球，地壳逐渐冷却。现在，如果一个人类在地球处于这种状态时就已经存在，并且被允许看到它，就好像这是一个他不关心的另一个世界，如果同时他对所有物理科学一无所知，难道他不会宣称拥有意识之类的生物不可能从他所看到的看似煤渣中进化而来吗？难道他不会否认它含有意识的潜力吗？然而随着时间的推移，意识出现了。那么，尽管我们目前还没有发现任何迹象，但有没有可能为意识挖掘出新的通道？

‘Again. Consciousness, in anything like the present acceptation of the term, having been once a new thing—a thing, as far as we can see, subsequent even to an individual centre of action and to a reproductive system (which we see existing in plants without apparent consciousness)—why may not there arise some new phase of mind which shall be as different from all present known phases, as the mind of animals is from that of vegetables?
'再次。意识，就像目前对该术语的接受一样，曾经是一个新事物——就我们所知，它甚至是继个体行动中心和生殖系统之后的事物（我们在植物中看到它存在于没有明显的意识）——为什么不能出现某种新的心智阶段，它与所有目前已知的阶段都不同，就像动物的心智与植物的心智不同一样？

‘It would be absurd to attempt to define such a mental state (or whatever it may be called), inasmuch as it must be something so foreign to man that his experience can give him no help towards conceiving its nature; but surely when we reflect upon the manifold phases of life and consciousness which have been evolved already, it would be rash to say that no others can be developed, and that animal life is the end of all things. There was a time when fire was the end of all things: another when rocks and water were so.’
“试图定义这样一种精神状态（或者无论它被称为什么）是荒谬的，因为它对人类来说一定是一种陌生的东西，以至于他的经验无法帮助他理解它的本质；但可以肯定的是，当我们反思生命和意识已经进化的多个阶段时，说没有其他阶段可以发展，而动物生命是万物的终结，那就太草率了。曾经有一段时间，火是万物的终结；另一段时间，岩石和水也是如此。

The writer, after enlarging on the above for several pages, proceeded to inquire whether traces of the approach of such a new phase of life could be perceived at present; whether we could see any tenements preparing which might in a remote futurity be adapted for it; whether, in fact, the primordial cell of such a kind of life could be now detected upon earth. In the course of his work he answered this question in the affirmative and pointed to the higher machines.
笔者将上述内容放大了几页后，继续询问目前是否能察觉到这样一个新的生活阶段即将到来的痕迹？我们是否可以看到任何在遥远的将来可以适应它的公寓；事实上，现在是否可以在地球上检测到这种生命的原始细胞。在他的工作过程中，他对这个问题做出了肯定的回答，并指出了更高的机器。

‘There is no security’—to quote his own words—‘against the ultimate development of mechanical consciousness, in the fact of machines possessing little consciousness now. A mollusc has not much consciousness. Reflect upon the extraordinary advance which machines have made during the last few hundred years, and note how slowly the animal and vegetable kingdoms are advancing. The more highly organised machines are creatures not so much of yesterday, as of the last five minutes, so to speak, in comparison with past time. Assume for the sake of argument that conscious beings have existed for some twenty million years: see what strides machines have made in the last thousand! May not the world last twenty million years longer? If so, what will they not in the end become? Is it not safer to nip the mischief in the bud and to forbid them further progress?
引用他自己的话说，“机械意识的最终发展是没有保障的，事实上机器现在几乎没有意识”。软体动物没有太多意识。反思一下机器在过去几百年中所取得的非凡进步，并注意动物和植物王国的进步是多么缓慢。与过去的时间相比，组织性更强的机器与其说是昨天的生物，不如说是最后五分钟的生物。为了便于论证，假设有意识的生物已经存在了大约两千万年：看看机器在过去的一千年里取得了多大的进步！难道世界不能再延长两千万年吗？如果是的话，他们最终不会变成什么？将恶作剧消灭在萌芽状态并禁止他们进一步发展不是更安全吗？

‘But who can say that the vapour engine has not a kind of consciousness? Where does consciousness begin, and where end? Who can draw the line? Who can draw any line? Is not everything interwoven with everything? Is not machinery linked with animal life in an infinite variety of ways? The shell of a hen’s egg is made of a delicate white ware and is a machine as much as an egg- cup is: the shell is a device for holding the egg, as much as the egg-cup for holding the shell: both are phases of the same function; the hen makes the shell in her inside, but it is pure pottery. She makes her nest outside of herself for convenience’ sake, but the nest is not more of a machine than the egg-shell is. A ‘machine’ is only a ‘device.’’
‘但谁能说蒸汽机没有一种意识呢？意识从哪里开始，又在哪里结束？谁能划清界限？谁能画出一条线？万物不都是相互交织的吗？机器不是以无数种方式与动物的生命联系在一起吗？鸡蛋的壳是用精致的白色器皿制成的，它就像蛋杯一样是一台机器：鸡蛋壳是盛放鸡蛋的装置，就像盛放蛋壳的蛋杯一样：两者都是相同功能的阶段；母鸡在她的体内做壳，但它是纯陶器。为了方便起见，她在自己外面筑巢，但这个巢并不比蛋壳更像是一台机器。 ‘机器’只是‘设备’。”

Then returning to consciousness, and endeavouring to detect its earliest manifestations, the writer continued:-
然后回到意识，并努力发现其最早的表现，作者继续说道：

‘There is a kind of plant that eats organic food with its flowers: when a fly settles upon the blossom, the petals close upon it and hold it fast till the plant has absorbed the insect into its system; but they will close on nothing but what is good to eat; of a drop of rain or a piece of stick they will take no notice. Curious! that so unconscious a thing should have such a keen eye to its own interest. If this is unconsciousness, where is the use of consciousness?
“有一种植物用它的花吃有机食物：当一只苍蝇停在花上时，花瓣会靠近它并紧紧抓住它，直到植物将昆虫吸收到它的系统中;但他们只吃好吃的东西；一滴雨或一根棍子，他们不会注意到。好奇的！如此无意识的事物竟然对自己的利益有如此敏锐的洞察力。如果这就是无意识，那意识又有什么用呢？

‘Shall we say that the plant does not know what it is doing merely because it has no eyes, or ears, or brains? If we say that it acts mechanically, and mechanically only, shall we not be forced to admit that sundry other and apparently very deliberate actions are also mechanical? If it seems to us that the plant kills and eats a fly mechanically, may it not seem to the plant that a man must kill and eat a sheep mechanically?
“我们是否可以说，植物不知道自己在做什么，仅仅是因为它没有眼睛、耳朵或大脑？”如果我们说它是机械地起作用，并且只是机械地起作用，那么我们难道不应该被迫承认其他各种明显非常刻意的行为也是机械的吗？如果在我们看来，植物机械地杀死并吃掉一只苍蝇，那么在植物看来，人是否必须机械地杀死并吃掉一只羊呢？

‘But it may be said that the plant is void of reason, because the growth of a plant is an involuntary growth. Given earth, air, and due temperature, the plant must grow: it is like a clock, which being once wound up will go till it is stopped or run down: it is like the wind blowing on the sails of a ship—the ship must go when the wind blows it. But can a healthy boy help growing if he have good meat and drink and clothing? can anything help going as long as it is wound up, or go on after it is run down? Is there not a winding up process everywhere?
‘但是可以说，植物是没有理性的，因为植物的生长是一种非自愿的生长。给定土壤、空气和适当的温度，植物必须生长：它就像一个时钟，一旦上紧发条就会一直走下去，直到停止或走完：就像吹在船帆上的风——船风一吹就必须走。但一个健康的男孩，吃好喝好穿，就能帮助成长吗？只要上紧发条，有什么东西可以帮助它继续运转，或者在它耗尽后继续运转吗？不是到处都有清算程序吗？

‘Even a potato {5} in a dark cellar has a certain low cunning about him which serves him in excellent stead. He knows perfectly well what he wants and how to get it. He sees the light coming from the cellar window and sends his shoots crawling straight thereto: they will crawl along the floor and up the wall and out at the cellar window; if there be a little earth anywhere on the journey he will find it and use it for his own ends. What deliberation he may exercise in the matter of his roots when he is planted in the earth is a thing unknown to us, but we can imagine him saying, ‘I will have a tuber here and a tuber there, and I will suck whatsoever advantage I can from all my surroundings. This neighbour I will overshadow, and that I will undermine; and what I can do shall be the limit of what I will do. He that is stronger and better placed than I shall overcome me, and him that is weaker I will overcome.’
“即使是在黑暗地窖里的土豆{5}也有一定的狡猾之处，这对他很有帮助。他非常清楚自己想要什么以及如何得到它。他看到从地窖窗户射出的光，然后让他的芽径直爬向那里：它们会沿着地板爬行，爬上墙壁，最后从地窖窗户爬出来；如果旅途中任何地方有一点泥土，他都会找到它并利用它来达到自己的目的。当他被种在土里时，他会对他的根问题进行怎样的深思熟虑，这是我们不知道的事情，但我们可以想象他说：“我将在这里有一个块茎，在那里有一个块茎，我将吸收任何优势我可以从我周围的所有地方。我将遮盖这个邻居，我将破坏他；我能做的就是我要做的极限。比我更强、地位更好的人将战胜我，比我更弱的人我将战胜他。

‘The potato says these things by doing them, which is the best of languages. What is consciousness if this is not consciousness? We find it difficult to sympathise with the emotions of a potato; so we do with those of an oyster. Neither of these things makes a noise on being boiled or opened, and noise appeals to us more strongly than anything else, because we make so much about our own sufferings. Since, then, they do not annoy us by any expression of pain we call them emotionless; and so qua mankind they are; but mankind is not everybody.
“土豆通过做事来表达这些事情，这是最好的语言。如果这不是意识，那什么是意识呢？我们发现很难同情土豆的情感；我们对牡蛎也是如此。这些东西在煮沸或打开时都不会发出噪音，而噪音对我们的吸引力比其他任何东西都更强烈，因为我们对自己的痛苦看得太多。既然如此，他们不会因任何痛苦的表达而惹恼我们，我们称他们为无感情的人。他们也是人类；但人类并不是所有人。

If it be urged that the action of the potato is chemical and mechanical only, and that it is due to the chemical and mechanical effects of light and heat, the answer would seem to lie in an inquiry whether every sensation is not chemical and mechanical in its operation? whether those things which we deem most purely spiritual are anything but disturbances of equilibrium in an infinite series of levers, beginning with those that are too small for microscopic detection, and going up to the human arm and the appliances which it makes use of? whether there be not a molecular action of thought, whence a dynamical theory of the passions shall be deducible? Whether strictly speaking we should not ask what kind of levers a man is made of rather than what is his temperament? How are they balanced? How much of such and such will it take to weigh them down so as to make him do so and so?’
如果有人主张马铃薯的作用只是化学和机械作用，并且是由于光和热的化学和机械效应造成的，那么答案似乎在于询问是否每种感觉都不是化学和机械作用的。它的运作？那些我们认为最纯粹的精神事物是否只是无限系列杠杆中平衡的扰动，从那些太小而无法用显微镜检测到的杠杆开始，一直到人类的手臂及其使用的器具？是否不存在思想的分子行为，由此可以演绎出激情的动力理论？严格来说，我们是否不应该问一个人是由什么杠杆组成的，而不是问他的气质是什么？它们如何平衡？需要多少这样那样的事情才能压垮他们，让他这样做呢？

The writer went on to say that he anticipated a time when it would be possible, by examining a single hair with a powerful microscope, to know whether its owner could be insulted with impunity. He then became more and more obscure, so that I was obliged to give up all attempt at translation; neither did I follow the drift of his argument. On coming to the next part which I could construe, I found that he had changed his ground.
作者接着说，他预计有一天，通过用强大的显微镜检查一根头发，就可以知道它的主人是否会受到侮辱而不受惩罚。后来他变得越来越晦涩难懂，我不得不放弃所有翻译的尝试。我也不明白他的论点的主旨。到了我可以解释的下一部分时，我发现他改变了立场。

‘Either,’ he proceeds, ‘a great deal of action that has been called purely mechanical and unconscious must be admitted to contain more elements of consciousness than has been allowed hitherto (and in this case germs of consciousness will be found in many actions of the higher machines)—Or (assuming the theory of evolution but at the same time denying the consciousness of vegetable and crystalline action) the race of man has descended from things which had no consciousness at all. In this case there is no a priori improbability in the descent of conscious (and more than conscious) machines from those which now exist, except that which is suggested by the apparent absence of anything like a reproductive system in the mechanical kingdom. This absence however is only apparent, as I shall presently show.
“或者，”他继续说道，“必须承认，大量被称为纯粹机械和无意识的行为包含了比迄今为止所允许的更多的意识元素（在这种情况下，意识的萌芽将在许多行为中被发现）更高的机器）——或者（假设进化论，但同时否认植物和晶体行为的意识）人类是从根本没有意识的事物中进化而来的。在这种情况下，除了机械王国中明显不存在生殖系统之类的东西所暗示的之外，有意识的（并且不仅仅是有意识的）机器从现在存在的机器中进化出来并不存在先验的可能性。然而，正如我接下来将要展示的那样，这种缺席只是明显的。

‘Do not let me be misunderstood as living in fear of any actually existing machine; there is probably no known machine which is more than a prototype of future mechanical life. The present machines are to the future as the early Saurians to man. The largest of them will probably greatly diminish in size. Some of the lowest vertebrate attained a much greater bulk than has descended to their more highly organised living representatives, and in like manner a diminution in the size of machines has often attended their development and progress.
“不要让我被误解为生活在对任何实际存在的机器的恐惧之中；可能没有任何已知的机器比未来机械寿命的原型更重要。现在的机器之于未来，就像早期蜥蜴之于人类一样。其中最大的一个可能会大大缩小。一些最低等的脊椎动物的体型比它们组织更严密的现存脊椎动物的体型要大得多，同样地，它们的发展和进步往往伴随着机器尺寸的缩小。

‘Take the watch, for example; examine its beautiful structure; observe the intelligent play of the minute members which compose it: yet this little creature is but a development of the cumbrous clocks that preceded it; it is no deterioration from them. A day may come when clocks, which certainly at the present time are not diminishing in bulk, will be superseded owing to the universal use of watches, in which case they will become as extinct as ichthyosauri, while the watch, whose tendency has for some years been to decrease in size rather than the contrary, will remain the only existing type of an extinct race.
“以手表为例；检查其美丽的结构；观察组成它的微小成员的智能游戏：然而，这个小生物只不过是之前笨重的时钟的发展；它们并没有恶化。有一天，钟表的体积肯定不会减少，但由于手表的普遍使用，钟表将被取代，在这种情况下，它们将像鱼龙一样灭绝，而钟表的趋势对某些人来说已经灭绝了。多年来，体型不断缩小而不是相反，将仍然是灭绝种族的唯一存在类型。

‘But returning to the argument, I would repeat that I fear none of the existing machines; what I fear is the extraordinary rapidity with which they are becoming something very different to what they are at present. No class of beings have in any time past made so rapid a movement forward. Should not that movement be jealously watched, and checked while we can still check it? And is it not necessary for this end to destroy the more advanced of the machines which are in use at present, though it is admitted that they are in themselves harmless?
“但是回到这个论点，我要再说一遍，我不害怕任何现有的机器；我担心的是他们正在以惊人的速度变得与现在截然不同。过去任何时期都没有任何一类生物能够如此迅速地前进。难道不应该在我们还能检查的时候，嫉妒地观察和检查它吗？尽管我们承认目前正在使用的更先进的机器本身是无害的，但为此目的是否没有必要摧毁它们？

‘As yet the machines receive their impressions through the agency of man’s senses: one travelling machine calls to another in a shrill accent of alarm and the other instantly retires; but it is through the ears of the driver that the voice of the one has acted upon the other. Had there been no driver, the callee would have been deaf to the caller. There was a time when it must have seemed highly improbable that machines should learn to make their wants known by sound, even through the ears of man; may we not conceive, then, that a day will come when those ears will be no longer needed, and the hearing will be done by the delicacy of the machine’s own construction?—when its language shall have been developed from the cry of animals to a speech as intricate as our own?
“到目前为止，机器通过人类感官接收印象：一台行驶的机器以尖锐的警报声呼叫另一台机器，另一台立即退出；但一个人的声音是通过司机的耳朵传到另一个人身上的。如果没有司机，被叫者就会对呼叫者充耳不闻。曾经有一段时间，机器学会通过声音，甚至是通过人的耳朵来表达自己的需求，这似乎是极不可能的。那么，我们是否可以想象，有一天，我们将不再需要这些耳朵，而听觉将由机器本身的精致结构来完成？——那时它的语言将从动物的叫声发展为人类的叫声。像我们自己的演讲一样复杂？

‘It is possible that by that time children will learn the differential calculus—as they learn now to speak—from their mothers and nurses, or that they may talk in the hypothetical language, and work rule of three sums, as soon as they are born; but this is not probable; we cannot calculate on any corresponding advance in man’s intellectual or physical powers which shall be a set-off against the far greater development which seems in store for the machines. Some people may say that man’s moral influence will suffice to rule them; but I cannot think it will ever be safe to repose much trust in the moral sense of any machine.
“到那时，孩子们可能会从他们的母亲和护士那里学习微积分——就像他们现在学习说话一样，或者他们可能会用假设的语言说话，以及三和的工作规则，一旦他们学会了出生；但这是不可能的；我们无法计算出人类智力或体力的任何相应进步，这将抵消机器似乎即将取得的更大发展。有些人可能会说，人的道德影响足以统治他们；但我认为对任何机器的道德感抱有很大的信任永远不会是安全的。

‘Again, might not the glory of the machines consist in their being without this same boasted gift of language? ‘Silence,’ it has been said by one writer, ‘is a virtue which renders us agreeable to our fellow-creatures.’’
“再说一次，机器的荣耀难道不就在于它们没有同样自夸的语言天赋吗？”一位作家曾说过，“沉默是一种美德，它使我们能够与同胞相处融洽。”

CHAPTER XXIV: THE MACHINES—continued
第二十四章：机器——续

‘But other questions come upon us. What is a man’s eye but a machine for the little creature that sits behind in his brain to look through? A dead eye is nearly as good as a living one for some time after the man is dead. It is not the eye that cannot see, but the restless one that cannot see through it. Is it man’s eyes, or is it the big seeing-engine which has revealed to us the existence of worlds beyond worlds into infinity? What has made man familiar with the scenery of the moon, the spots on the sun, or the geography of the planets? He is at the mercy of the seeing-engine for these things, and is powerless unless he tack it on to his own identity, and make it part and parcel of himself. Or, again, is it the eye, or the little see-engine, which has shown us the existence of infinitely minute organisms which swarm unsuspected around us?
“但是我们还面临着其他问题。人的眼睛除了是一个供大脑后面的小生物观察的机器之外，还能算什么呢？在人死后的一段时间内，死眼几乎与活眼一样好。不是眼睛看不见，而是不安的眼睛看不透。是人的眼睛，还是巨大的视觉引擎向我们揭示了超越世界、进入无限的世界的存在？是什么让人类熟悉月球的风景、太阳的斑点或行星的地理？他受到这些事物的视觉引擎的摆布，并且无能为力，除非他将其附加到他自己的身份上，并使其成为他自己的一部分。或者，是眼睛，还是小小的视觉引擎，向我们展示了无限微小的有机体的存在，这些有机体毫无防备地聚集在我们周围？

‘And take man’s vaunted power of calculation. Have we not engines which can do all manner of sums more quickly and correctly than we can? What prizeman in Hypothetics at any of our Colleges of Unreason can compare with some of these machines in their own line? In fact, wherever precision is required man flies to the machine at once, as far preferable to himself. Our sum-engines never drop a figure, nor our looms a stitch; the machine is brisk and active, when the man is weary; it is clear-headed and collected, when the man is stupid and dull; it needs no slumber, when man must sleep or drop; ever at its post, ever ready for work, its alacrity never flags, its patience never gives in; its might is stronger than combined hundreds, and swifter than the flight of birds; it can burrow beneath the earth, and walk upon the largest rivers and sink not. This is the green tree; what then shall be done in the dry?
'还有人类引以为傲的计算能力。我们难道没有比我们更快、更正确地完成各种计算的引擎吗？我们任何非理性学院的假设学获奖者有哪一个可以与他们自己的系列中的一些机器相比呢？事实上，只要是需要精确度的地方，人们都会立即飞向机器，这比他自己要好得多。我们的求和引擎从不掉下一个数字，我们的织布机也从不落下一针；当人疲倦时，机器轻快而活跃；当一个人愚蠢而迟钝时，他头脑清醒，镇定自若。当人必须睡觉或倒下时，它不需要睡觉；永远在岗位上，永远准备好工作，它的敏捷性永不减退，它的耐心永不屈服；其威力胜于百人之和，迅捷于百鸟之飞。它可以在地下挖洞，在最大的河流上行走而不沉没。这就是绿树；那么在干燥的时候该怎么办呢？

‘Who shall say that a man does see or hear? He is such a hive and swarm of parasites that it is doubtful whether his body is not more theirs than his, and whether he is anything but another kind of ant-heap after all. May not man himself become a sort of parasite upon the machines? An affectionate machine-tickling aphid?
‘谁能说一个人确实看到或听到了呢？他是一群寄生虫，令人怀疑他的身体是否不属于他们，也不属于他，而他到底是否只是另一种蚂蚁堆。人自己难道不会成为机器上的寄生虫吗？一只深情的机器搔痒蚜虫？

‘It is said by some that our blood is composed of infinite living agents which go up and down the highways and byways of our bodies as people in the streets of a city. When we look down from a high place upon crowded thoroughfares, is it possible not to think of corpuscles of blood travelling through veins and nourishing the heart of the town? No mention shall be made of sewers, nor of the hidden nerves which serve to communicate sensations from one part of the town’s body to another; nor of the yawning jaws of the railway stations, whereby the circulation is carried directly into the heart,—which receive the venous lines, and disgorge the arterial, with an eternal pulse of people. And the sleep of the town, how life-like! with its change in the circulation.’
“有人说，我们的血液是由无限的活性物质组成的，它们就像城市街道上的人们一样，在我们身体的高速公路和小路上来回流动。当我们从高处俯视人潮拥挤的大街时，是否能不想起血液在血管中流动，滋养着这座城市的心脏？不会提及下水道，也不会提及隐藏的神经，这些神经用于将城镇身体的一个部分的感觉传达到另一个部分；也不像火车站张开的大口，血液循环直接进入心脏，心脏接收静脉线路，排出动脉，伴随着人们永恒的脉搏。还有小镇的睡眠，多么有生活气息啊！随着流通的变化。

Here the writer became again so hopelessly obscure that I was obliged to miss several pages. He resumed:-
在这里，作者再次变得如此晦涩难懂，以至于我不得不漏掉几页。他继续说道：-

‘It can be answered that even though machines should hear never so well and speak never so wisely, they will still always do the one or the other for our advantage, not their own; that man will be the ruling spirit and the machine the servant; that as soon as a machine fails to discharge the service which man expects from it, it is doomed to extinction; that the machines stand to man simply in the relation of lower animals, the vapour-engine itself being only a more economical kind of horse; so that instead of being likely to be developed into a higher kind of life than man’s, they owe their very existence and progress to their power of ministering to human wants, and must therefore both now and ever be man’s inferiors.
“可以回答的是，即使机器听得再好，说话也再聪明，它们仍然会为了我们的利益而不是它们自己的利益而这样做或另一种；人将成为统治者，机器将成为仆人；一旦机器无法履行人类所期望的服务，它就注定要灭绝；机器与人类的关系只是低等动物，蒸汽机本身只是一种更经济的马；因此，它们不可能发展成为比人类更高级的生命，而是将它们的存在和进步归功于它们满足人类需求的能力，因此现在和永远都必须低于人类。

‘This is all very well. But the servant glides by imperceptible approaches into the master; and we have come to such a pass that, even now, man must suffer terribly on ceasing to benefit the machines. If all machines were to be annihilated at one moment, so that not a knife nor lever nor rag of clothing nor anything whatsoever were left to man but his bare body alone that he was born with, and if all knowledge of mechanical laws were taken from him so that he could make no more machines, and all machine-made food destroyed so that the race of man should be left as it were naked upon a desert island, we should become extinct in six weeks. A few miserable individuals might linger, but even these in a year or two would become worse than monkeys. Man’s very soul is due to the machines; it is a machine-made thing: he thinks as he thinks, and feels as he feels, through the work that machines have wrought upon him, and their existence is quite as much a sine qua non for his, as his for theirs. This fact precludes us from proposing the complete annihilation of machinery, but surely it indicates that we should destroy as many of them as we can possibly dispense with, lest they should tyrannise over us even more completely.
‘这一切都很好。但仆人却不知不觉地接近了主人。我们已经到了这样的地步，即使是现在，人类也必须因停止造福机器而遭受可怕的痛苦。如果所有的机器都在同一时刻被消灭，那么人类就只剩下他与生俱来的赤裸身体，而没有留下一把刀、杠杆、破布或任何东西，如果所有机械定律的知识都来自于人类如果他不再制造机器，所有机器制造的食物都会被毁掉，人类就会赤身裸体地被留在荒岛上，我们将在六周内灭绝。一些悲惨的人可能会留下来，但即使是这些人在一两年内也会变得比猴子更糟糕。人的灵魂在于机器；这是一个机器制造的东西：通过机器对他所做的工作，他思考他的想法，感受他的感受，机器的存在对于他来说是一个必要条件，正如他对于他们的存在一样。这一事实使我们无法提出彻底消灭机器的建议，但它无疑表明我们应该尽可能多地消灭机器，以免它们更彻底地对我们施暴。

‘True, from a low materialistic point of view, it would seem that those thrive best who use machinery wherever its use is possible with profit; but this is the art of the machines—they serve that they may rule. They bear no malice towards man for destroying a whole race of them provided he creates a better instead; on the contrary, they reward him liberally for having hastened their development. It is for neglecting them that he incurs their wrath, or for using inferior machines, or for not making sufficient exertions to invent new ones, or for destroying them without replacing them; yet these are the very things we ought to do, and do quickly; for though our rebellion against their infant power will cause infinite suffering, what will not things come to, if that rebellion is delayed?
“确实，从低物质主义的角度来看，那些在任何可能获利的地方使用机器的人似乎会发展得最好；但这就是机器的艺术——它们服务于它们的统治。他们对人类毁灭整个种族并无恶意，只要他创造了更好的种族。相反，他们会因为他加速了他们的发展而慷慨地奖励他。正是因为他忽视了他们，或者因为使用了劣质机器，或者因为没有做出足够的努力来发明新机器，或者因为摧毁了它们而不更换它们，所以他招致了他们的愤怒。然而，这些正是我们应该做的事情，而且应该尽快做；因为虽然我们对他们幼年权力的反抗会造成无限的痛苦，但如果反抗被推迟，事情会不会发生什么呢？

‘They have preyed upon man’s grovelling preference for his material over his spiritual interests, and have betrayed him into supplying that element of struggle and warfare without which no race can advance. The lower animals progress because they struggle with one another; the weaker die, the stronger breed and transmit their strength. The machines being of themselves unable to struggle, have got man to do their struggling for them: as long as he fulfils this function duly, all goes well with him—at least he thinks so; but the moment he fails to do his best for the advancement of machinery by encouraging the good and destroying the bad, he is left behind in the race of competition; and this means that he will be made uncomfortable in a variety of ways, and perhaps die.
“他们利用了人类对物质利益而非精神利益的卑鄙偏好，并背叛了人类，提供了斗争和战争的元素，没有这些元素，任何种族都无法进步。”低等动物之所以进步，是因为它们彼此斗争；弱者死去，强者繁衍并传递力量。机器本身无法进行斗争，所以需要人来替它们进行斗争：只要他适当地履行了这一职责，一切就都顺利了——至少他是这么认为的；但是，一旦他不能尽最大努力促进机器的进步，鼓励善行，消灭恶行，他就会在竞争中被抛在后面。这意味着他会以各种方式感到不舒服，甚至可能会死。

‘So that even now the machines will only serve on condition of being served, and that too upon their own terms; the moment their terms are not complied with, they jib, and either smash both themselves and all whom they can reach, or turn churlish and refuse to work at all. How many men at this hour are living in a state of bondage to the machines? How many spend their whole lives, from the cradle to the grave, in tending them by night and day? Is it not plain that the machines are gaining ground upon us, when we reflect on the increasing number of those who are bound down to them as slaves, and of those who devote their whole souls to the advancement of the mechanical kingdom?
“因此，即使是现在，机器也只有在被服务的条件下才能服务，而且也是按照它们自己的条件；一旦他们的条件没有得到遵守，他们就会逃避，要么毁掉自己，要么毁掉所有他们能接触到的人，要么变得粗鲁，根本拒绝工作。此时此刻，有多少人生活在机器的束缚之中？有多少人从摇篮到坟墓，一生都在日夜照顾他们？当我们想到越来越多的人被机器束缚为奴隶，以及那些将整个灵魂奉献给机械王国的进步的人时，这难道不是很明显吗？

‘The vapour-engine must be fed with food and consume it by fire even as man consumes it; it supports its combustion by air as man supports it; it has a pulse and circulation as man has. It may be granted that man’s body is as yet the more versatile of the two, but then man’s body is an older thing; give the vapour-engine but half the time that man has had, give it also a continuance of our present infatuation, and what may it not ere long attain to?
“蒸汽机必须以食物为食，并用火来消耗它，就像人类消耗它一样；它通过空气支持其燃烧，就像人类支持它一样；它和人类一样有脉搏和循环。可以肯定的是，人类的身体迄今为止是两者中更加多才多艺的一个，但人类的身体是一个更古老的东西；只要给予蒸汽机人类一半的时间，给予它我们目前的迷恋的延续，它很快就会达到什么目的呢？

‘There are certain functions indeed of the vapour-engine which will probably remain unchanged for myriads of years—which in fact will perhaps survive when the use of vapour has been superseded: the piston and cylinder, the beam, the fly-wheel, and other parts of the machine will probably be permanent, just as we see that man and many of the lower animals share like modes of eating, drinking, and sleeping; thus they have hearts which beat as ours, veins and arteries, eyes, ears, and noses; they sigh even in their sleep, and weep and yawn; they are affected by their children; they feel pleasure and pain, hope, fear, anger, shame; they have memory and prescience; they know that if certain things happen to them they will die, and they fear death as much as we do; they communicate their thoughts to one another, and some of them deliberately act in concert. The comparison of similarities is endless: I only make it because some may say that since the vapour-engine is not likely to be improved in the main particulars, it is unlikely to be henceforward extensively modified at all. This is too good to be true: it will be modified and suited for an infinite variety of purposes, as much as man has been modified so as to exceed the brutes in skill.
“蒸汽机的某些功能确实可能会保持数千年不变——事实上，当蒸汽的使用被取代时，这些功能可能会继续存在：活塞和气缸、横梁、飞轮和机器的其他部分可能是永久性的，就像我们看到人类和许多低等动物共享相似的饮食和睡眠模式一样；因此，他们有与我们一样跳动的心脏、静脉和动脉、眼睛、耳朵和鼻子；他们甚至在睡梦中叹息、哭泣、打哈欠；他们受到孩子的影响；他们感受到快乐和痛苦、希望、恐惧、愤怒、羞耻；他们有记忆力和预知力；他们知道，如果某些事情发生在他们身上，他们就会死，而且他们和我们一样害怕死亡；他们互相交流想法，有些人故意一致行动。相似之处的比较是无穷无尽的：我这样做只是因为有些人可能会说，由于蒸汽发动机不太可能在主要细节上得到改进，因此今后根本不可能进行广泛的修改。这好得令人难以置信：它将被修改并适应无数种目的，就像人类被修改以超越野兽一样。

‘In the meantime the stoker is almost as much a cook for his engine as our own cooks for ourselves. Consider also the colliers and pitmen and coal merchants and coal trains, and the men who drive them, and the ships that carry coals—what an army of servants do the machines thus employ! Are there not probably more men engaged in tending machinery than in tending men? Do not machines eat as it were by mannery? Are we not ourselves creating our successors in the supremacy of the earth? daily adding to the beauty and delicacy of their organisation, daily giving them greater skill and supplying more and more of that self-regulating self-acting power which will be better than any intellect?
“与此同时，加油工几乎就像我们自己为自己做饭一样，是他发动机的厨师。还想一想煤矿工人、煤矿工人、煤商、运煤火车、驾驶它们的人和运煤的船——机器雇用了多少仆人啊！从事照料机器的人难道不是比照料人的人多吗？机器吃东西不是很有礼貌吗？难道我们自己不是在创造地球至高无上的继承者吗？每天为他们的组织增添美丽和精致，每天赋予他们更高的技能，并提供越来越多的自我调节自我行动的力量，这会比任何智力都更好吗？

‘What a new thing it is for a machine to feed at all! The plough, the spade, and the cart must eat through man’s stomach; the fuel that sets them going must burn in the furnace of a man or of horses. Man must consume bread and meat or he cannot dig; the bread and meat are the fuel which drive the spade. If a plough be drawn by horses, the power is supplied by grass or beans or oats, which being burnt in the belly of the cattle give the power of working: without this fuel the work would cease, as an engine would stop if its furnaces were to go out.
“对于机器来说，喂食是多么新鲜的事情啊！犁、铲子、车子必须吃人的胃；推动它们前进的燃料必须在人或马的熔炉中燃烧。人必须吃面包和肉，否则就无法挖掘；面包和肉是驱动铲子的燃料。如果犁是用马拉的，动力是由草、豆子或燕麦提供的，这些草、豆子或燕麦在牛的肚子里燃烧，提供工作的动力：没有这种燃料，工作就会停止，就像发动机如果炉子停止运转就会停止一样。我们要出去。

‘A man of science has demonstrated ‘that no animal has the power of originating mechanical energy, but that all the work done in its life by any animal, and all the heat that has been emitted from it, and the heat which would be obtained by burning the combustible matter which has been lost from its body during life, and by burning its body after death, make up altogether an exact equivalent to the heat which would be obtained by burning as much food as it has used during its life, and an amount of fuel which would generate as much heat as its body if burned immediately after death.’ I do not know how he has found this out, but he is a man of science—how then can it be objected against the future vitality of the machines that they are, in their present infancy, at the beck and call of beings who are themselves incapable of originating mechanical energy?
“一位科学家已经证明，‘没有一种动物具有产生机械能的能力，但是任何动物在其一生中所做的所有工作，以及从其散发出的所有热量，以及将获得的热量通过燃烧其生前身体失去的可燃物质，以及在死后燃烧其身体，完全等于燃烧其生前所消耗的食物所获得的热量，并且我不知道他是如何发现这一点的，但他是一个科学家——那么，这怎么能反对未来的生命力呢？它们是目前处于婴儿期的机器，听命于那些本身无法产生机械能的生物吗？

‘The main point, however, to be observed as affording cause for alarm is, that whereas animals were formerly the only stomachs of the machines, there are now many which have stomachs of their own, and consume their food themselves. This is a great step towards their becoming, if not animate, yet something so near akin to it, as not to differ more widely from our own life than animals do from vegetables. And though man should remain, in some respects, the higher creature, is not this in accordance with the practice of nature, which allows superiority in some things to animals which have, on the whole, been long surpassed? Has she not allowed the ant and the bee to retain superiority over man in the organisation of their communities and social arrangements, the bird in traversing the air, the fish in swimming, the horse in strength and fleetness, and the dog in self-sacrifice?
然而，值得警惕的要点是，虽然动物以前是机器唯一的胃，但现在很多动物都有自己的胃，自己吃食物。这是向它们迈出的一大步，即使它们不是有生命的，但也是如此接近的东西，以至于它们与我们自己的生活的差异并不比动物与蔬菜的差异更大。尽管人类在某些方面仍然是高等生物，但这不符合自然的惯例吗？自然在某些方面比动物优越，而动物在总体上已经被超越了？难道她不允许蚂蚁和蜜蜂在群落组织和社会安排上保持对人类的优越性，让鸟在空中飞行方面保持优越性，让鱼在游泳方面保持优越性，马在力量和敏捷方面保持优越性，而狗在自我牺牲方面保持优越性？

‘It is said by some with whom I have conversed upon this subject, that the machines can never be developed into animate or quasi- animate existences, inasmuch as they have no reproductive system, nor seem ever likely to possess one. If this be taken to mean that they cannot marry, and that we are never likely to see a fertile union between two vapour-engines with the young ones playing about the door of the shed, however greatly we might desire to do so, I will readily grant it. But the objection is not a very profound one. No one expects that all the features of the now existing organisations will be absolutely repeated in an entirely new class of life. The reproductive system of animals differs widely from that of plants, but both are reproductive systems. Has nature exhausted her phases of this power?
“我与一些人讨论过这个问题，他们说，机器永远不可能发展成有生命或准有生命的存在，因为它们没有生殖系统，而且似乎也不可能拥有生殖系统。如果这意味着他们不能结婚，并且我们永远不可能看到两个蒸汽机之间的肥沃结合，而年轻人在棚屋的门上玩耍，无论我们多么希望这样做，我都会轻易地给予它。但反对意见并不是非常深刻。没有人期望现有组织的所有特征将在全新的生活阶层中完全重复。动物的生殖系统与植物的生殖系统有很大不同，但两者都是生殖系统。大自然是否已经耗尽了这种力量的各个阶段？

‘Surely if a machine is able to reproduce another machine systematically, we may say that it has a reproductive system. What is a reproductive system, if it be not a system for reproduction? And how few of the machines are there which have not been produced systematically by other machines? But it is man that makes them do so. Yes; but is it not insects that make many of the plants reproductive, and would not whole families of plants die out if their fertilisation was not effected by a class of agents utterly foreign to themselves? Does any one say that the red clover has no reproductive system because the humble bee (and the humble bee only) must aid and abet it before it can reproduce? No one. The humble bee is a part of the reproductive system of the clover. Each one of ourselves has sprung from minute animalcules whose entity was entirely distinct from our own, and which acted after their kind with no thought or heed of what we might think about it. These little creatures are part of our own reproductive system; then why not we part of that of the machines?
“当然，如果一台机器能够系统地复制另一台机器，我们可以说它有生殖系统。如果生殖系统不是生殖系统，那它是什么？还有多少机器不是由其他机器系统生产的？但正是人让他们这样做。是的;但是，许多植物的繁殖难道不是由昆虫造成的吗？如果植物的受精过程没有受到一类与它们自身完全不同的媒介的影响，那么整个植物家族难道不会灭绝吗？有人说红三叶草没有生殖系统，因为卑微的蜜蜂（而且只是卑微的蜜蜂）必须帮助和怂恿它才能繁殖？没有人。不起眼的蜜蜂是三叶草生殖系统的一部分。我们每个人都是从微小的微生物中产生的，它们的实体与我们自己的完全不同，并且它们按照同类行事，不考虑或不注意我们的想法。这些小生物是我们生殖系统的一部分；那么我们为什么不成为机器的一部分呢？

‘But the machines which reproduce machinery do not reproduce machines after their own kind. A thimble may be made by machinery, but it was not made by, neither will it ever make, a thimble. Here, again, if we turn to nature we shall find abundance of analogies which will teach us that a reproductive system may be in full force without the thing produced being of the same kind as that which produced it. Very few creatures reproduce after their own kind; they reproduce something which has the potentiality of becoming that which their parents were. Thus the butterfly lays an egg, which egg can become a caterpillar, which caterpillar can become a chrysalis, which chrysalis can become a butterfly; and though I freely grant that the machines cannot be said to have more than the germ of a true reproductive system at present, have we not just seen that they have only recently obtained the germs of a mouth and stomach? And may not some stride be made in the direction of true reproduction which shall be as great as that which has been recently taken in the direction of true feeding?
“但是，复制机器的机器并不按照自己的同类复制机器。顶针可能是由机器制造的，但它不是由顶针制造的，也永远不会制造顶针。在这里，如果我们再次转向自然，我们会发现大量的类比，这些类比将告诉我们，即使所产生的事物与产生它的事物不是同一种类，生殖系统也可能发挥全部作用。很少有生物会各从其类繁衍生息。他们繁殖出一些有可能成为其父母的东西。蝴蝶产卵，卵可以变成毛毛虫，毛毛虫可以变成蛹，蛹可以变成蝴蝶；尽管我坦率地承认，目前这些机器只能拥有真正的生殖系统的细菌，但我们不是才看到它们最近才获得了口腔和胃的细菌吗？难道不能在真正的繁殖方向上迈出一些步伐，这与最近在真正喂养的方向上所迈出的步伐一样大吗？

‘It is possible that the system when developed may be in many cases a vicarious thing. Certain classes of machines may be alone fertile, while the rest discharge other functions in the mechanical system, just as the great majority of ants and bees have nothing to do with the continuation of their species, but get food and store it, without thought of breeding. One cannot expect the parallel to be complete or nearly so; certainly not now, and probably never; but is there not enough analogy existing at the present moment, to make us feel seriously uneasy about the future, and to render it our duty to check the evil while we can still do so? Machines can within certain limits beget machines of any class, no matter how different to themselves. Every class of machines will probably have its special mechanical breeders, and all the higher ones will owe their existence to a large number of parents and not to two only.
“该系统在开发后可能在很多情况下都是替代品。某些类别的机器可能单独具有繁殖力，而其余的则在机械系统中发挥其他功能，就像绝大多数蚂蚁和蜜蜂与它们物种的延续无关，但获取食物并储存它，而不考虑配种。人们不能指望这种平行是完全的或接近的。现在肯定不会，也可能永远不会；但是，目前存在的类比还不够多，使我们对未来感到严重不安，并让我们有责任在我们仍然可以这样做的时候制止邪恶吗？机器在一定限度内可以产生任何类别的机器，无论它们本身有多么不同。每一类机器都可能有其特殊的机械繁殖者，所有高级机器的存在都将归功于大量的父母，而不仅仅是两个。

‘We are misled by considering any complicated machine as a single thing; in truth it is a city or society, each member of which was bred truly after its kind. We see a machine as a whole, we call it by a name and individualise it; we look at our own limbs, and know that the combination forms an individual which springs from a single centre of reproductive action; we therefore assume that there can be no reproductive action which does not arise from a single centre; but this assumption is unscientific, and the bare fact that no vapour-engine was ever made entirely by another, or two others, of its own kind, is not sufficient to warrant us in saying that vapour-engines have no reproductive system. The truth is that each part of every vapour-engine is bred by its own special breeders, whose function it is to breed that part, and that only, while the combination of the parts into a whole forms another department of the mechanical reproductive system, which is at present exceedingly complex and difficult to see in its entirety.
“我们将任何复杂的机器视为单一事物，这是一种误导；事实上，它是一个城市或社会，其中的每个成员都是真正按照自己的同类培育出来的。我们将机器视为一个整体，给它起一个名字，并将其个性化；我们看看自己的四肢，就知道这种结合形成了一个个体，这个个体源于一个生殖活动的单一中心；因此，我们假设不可能存在不是由单一中心产生的生殖行为；但这种假设是不科学的，而且没有任何蒸汽机完全是由另一个或两个同类的蒸汽机制造的，这一事实不足以让我们有理由说蒸汽机没有生殖系统。事实是，每台蒸汽机的每个部件都是由其自己的特殊育种者培育的，其功能就是培育该部件，而且只有当这些部件组合成一个整体时，才形成机械生殖系统的另一个部门，目前情况极其复杂，很难全面了解。

‘Complex now, but how much simpler and more intelligibly organised may it not become in another hundred thousand years? or in twenty thousand? For man at present believes that his interest lies in that direction; he spends an incalculable amount of labour and time and thought in making machines breed always better and better; he has already succeeded in effecting much that at one time appeared impossible, and there seem no limits to the results of accumulated improvements if they are allowed to descend with modification from generation to generation. It must always be remembered that man’s body is what it is through having been moulded into its present shape by the chances and changes of many millions of years, but that his organisation never advanced with anything like the rapidity with which that of the machines is advancing. This is the most alarming feature in the case, and I must be pardoned for insisting on it so frequently.’
“现在很复杂，但再过十万年，它不会变得更加简单和更加容易理解吗？”还是两万？因为现在的人相信他的兴趣在于这个方向；他花费了难以估量的劳动、时间和思想，让机器不断繁殖得越来越好；他已经成功地实现了许多一度看似不可能的目标，而且如果允许这些改进代代相传，那么积累的改进的结果似乎是没有限制的。必须永远记住，人类的身体是通过数百万年的机会和变化塑造成现在的形状的，但他的组织从未像机器的组织那样快速发展。 。这是本案中最令人震惊的特征，我必须原谅我如此频繁地坚持这一点。

CHAPTER XXV: THE MACHINES—concluded
第二十五章：机器——结束

Here followed a very long and untranslatable digression about the different races and families of the then existing machines. The writer attempted to support his theory by pointing out the similarities existing between many machines of a widely different character, which served to show descent from a common ancestor. He divided machines into their genera, subgenera, species, varieties, subvarieties, and so forth. He proved the existence of connecting links between machines that seemed to have very little in common, and showed that many more such links had existed, but had now perished. He pointed out tendencies to reversion, and the presence of rudimentary organs which existed in many machines feebly developed and perfectly useless, yet serving to mark descent from an ancestor to whom the function was actually useful.
接下来是关于当时现有机器的不同种族和家族的很长且无法翻译的题外话。作者试图通过指出许多具有广泛不同特征的机器之间存在的相似性来支持他的理论，这些相似性表明了来自共同祖先的血统。他将机器分为属、亚属、种、变种、亚变种等等。他证明了机器之间似乎没有什么共同点的连接链接的存在，并表明更多这样的链接曾经存在，但现在已经消失了。他指出了回归的倾向，以及存在于许多发育微弱且完全无用的机器中的初级器官的存在，但却标志着该功能实际上是有用的祖先的血统。

I left the translation of this part of the treatise, which, by the way, was far longer than all that I have given here, for a later opportunity. Unfortunately, I left Erewhon before I could return to the subject; and though I saved my translation and other papers at the hazard of my life, I was a obliged to sacrifice the original work. It went to my heart to do so; but I thus gained ten minutes of invaluable time, without which both Arowhena and myself must have certainly perished.
我留下了这部分论文的译文，顺便说一句，它比我在这里给出的所有内容都要长得多，以供以后有机会使用。不幸的是，我还没来得及回到主题就离开了Erewhon。尽管我冒着生命危险保存了我的翻译和其他论文，但我不得不牺牲原始作品。我很想这么做。但我因此获得了十分钟的宝贵时间，没有这些时间，阿罗维娜和我自己肯定会丧命。

I remember one incident which bears upon this part of the treatise. The gentleman who gave it to me had asked to see my tobacco-pipe; he examined it carefully, and when he came to the little protuberance at the bottom of the bowl he seemed much delighted, and exclaimed that it must be rudimentary. I asked him what he meant.
我记得一件与本文这一部分有关的事件。给我烟斗的那位先生要求看一下我的烟斗。他仔细地检查了它，当他看到碗底的小突起时，他似乎很高兴，并惊呼这一定是简陋的。我问他什么意思。

‘Sir,’ he answered, ‘this organ is identical with the rim at the bottom of a cup; it is but another form of the same function. Its purpose must have been to keep the heat of the pipe from marking the table upon which it rested. You would find, if you were to look up the history of tobacco-pipes, that in early specimens this protuberance was of a different shape to what it is now. It will have been broad at the bottom, and flat, so that while the pipe was being smoked the bowl might rest upon the table without marking it. Use and disuse must have come into play and reduced the function to its present rudimentary condition. I should not be surprised, sir,’ he continued, ‘if, in the course of time, it were to become modified still farther, and to assume the form of an ornamental leaf or scroll, or even a butterfly, while, in some cases, it will become extinct.’
“先生，”他回答说，“这个器官与杯底的边缘相同；它只是同一功能的另一种形式。它的目的一定是防止管子的热量在它所放置的桌子上留下痕迹。如果你查阅烟斗的历史，你会发现，在早期的标本中，这个突起的形状与现在不同。它的底部很宽，而且很平，这样在抽烟斗的时候，碗就可以放在桌子上，而不会留下任何痕迹。使用和废弃肯定已经发挥作用，并将功能降低到目前的基本状态。先生，我不会感到惊讶，”他继续说道，“如果随着时间的推移，它会进一步改变，呈现出装饰性的叶子或卷轴，甚至蝴蝶的形状，而在某些情况下，在这种情况下，它将灭绝。

On my return to England, I looked up the point, and found that my friend was right.
回到英国后，我查了一下这一点，发现我的朋友是对的。

Returning, however, to the treatise, my translation recommences as follows:-
然而，回到这篇论文，我的翻译如下：-

‘May we not fancy that if, in the remotest geological period, some early form of vegetable life had been endowed with the power of reflecting upon the dawning life of animals which was coming into existence alongside of its own, it would have thought itself exceedingly acute if it had surmised that animals would one day become real vegetables? Yet would this be more mistaken than it would be on our part to imagine that because the life of machines is a very different one to our own, there is therefore no higher possible development of life than ours; or that because mechanical life is a very different thing from ours, therefore that it is not life at all?
“我们是否可以想象，如果在最遥远的地质时期，某种早期的植物生命形式被赋予了反思动物生命的能力，而动物的生命也随之出现，它会认为自己非常伟大。如果推测动物有一天会变成真正的蔬菜，会不会很尖锐？然而，如果我们认为由于机器的生命与我们的生命非常不同，因此生命的发展不可能比我们的更高，这种想法会比我们想象的更加错误吗？或者因为机械生命与我们的生命非常不同，因此它根本不是生命？

‘But I have heard it said, ‘granted that this is so, and that the vapour-engine has a strength of its own, surely no one will say that it has a will of its own?’ Alas! if we look more closely, we shall find that this does not make against the supposition that the vapour-engine is one of the germs of a new phase of life. What is there in this whole world, or in the worlds beyond it, which has a will of its own? The Unknown and Unknowable only!
“但我听人说：‘既然如此，而且蒸汽机有自己的力量，肯定没有人会说它有自己的意志吗？’唉！如果我们更仔细地观察，我们会发现这并不违背蒸汽机是生命新阶段的萌芽之一的假设。在这个世界上，或者在这个世界之外的世界里，有什么东西是有自己的意志的呢？只有未知和不可知！

‘A man is the resultant and exponent of all the forces that have been brought to bear upon him, whether before his birth or afterwards. His action at any moment depends solely upon his constitution, and on the intensity and direction of the various agencies to which he is, and has been, subjected. Some of these will counteract each other; but as he is by nature, and as he has been acted on, and is now acted on from without, so will he do, as certainly and regularly as though he were a machine.
“一个人是所有施加在他身上的力量的结果和体现，无论是在他出生之前还是之后。他在任何时刻的行动完全取决于他的体质，以及他现在和过去所服从的各种机构的强度和方向。其中一些会相互抵消；但正如他的本性一样，正如他曾经受到过作用，现在又受到来自外部的作用，他也会这样做，就像他是一台机器一样，确定而有规律。

‘We do not generally admit this, because we do not know the whole nature of any one, nor the whole of the forces that act upon him. We see but a part, and being thus unable to generalise human conduct, except very roughly, we deny that it is subject to any fixed laws at all, and ascribe much both of a man’s character and actions to chance, or luck, or fortune; but these are only words whereby we escape the admission of our own ignorance; and a little reflection will teach us that the most daring flight of the imagination or the most subtle exercise of the reason is as much the thing that must arise, and the only thing that can by any possibility arise, at the moment of its arising, as the falling of a dead leaf when the wind shakes it from the tree.
“我们通常不承认这一点，因为我们不知道任何人的全部本性，也不知道作用于他的全部力量。我们只看到一部分，因此无法概括人类行为，除非非常粗略，我们否认它受任何固定法则的约束，并将一个人的性格和行为归因于机会，运气或财富;但这些只是我们逃避承认自己无知的话语而已。稍加思考就会告诉我们，最大胆的想象力飞翔或最微妙的理性运用同样是必须出现的事物，也是唯一可以在其出现的时刻出现的事物，就像风把树上的枯叶吹落时一样。
