‘For the future depends upon the present, and the present (whose existence is only one of those minor compromises of which human life is full—for it lives only on sufferance of the past and future) depends upon the past, and the past is unalterable. The only reason why we cannot see the future as plainly as the past, is because we know too little of the actual past and actual present; these things are too great for us, otherwise the future, in its minutest details, would lie spread out before our eyes, and we should lose our sense of time present by reason of the clearness with which we should see the past and future; perhaps we should not be even able to distinguish time at all; but that is foreign. What we do know is, that the more the past and present are known, the more the future can be predicted; and that no one dreams of doubting the fixity of the future in cases where he is fully cognisant of both past and present, and has had experience of the consequences that followed from such a past and such a present on previous occasions. He perfectly well knows what will happen, and will stake his whole fortune thereon.
“因为未来取决于现在，而现在（其存在只是人类生命充实的那些微小妥协之一——因为它仅靠对过去和未来的忍受而生活）取决于过去，而过去是不可改变的。我们之所以不能像过去一样清楚地看到未来，唯一的原因是我们对实际的过去和实际的现在了解得太少；这些事情对我们来说太伟大了，否则未来的最微小的细节就会展现在我们眼前，我们会因为清楚地看到过去和未来而失去对当下的时间感；或许我们根本就无法区分时间；但这是外国的。我们所知道的是，对过去和现在了解得越多，就越能预测未来；如果一个人充分认识到过去和现在，并且在以前的情况下经历过这样的过去和这样的现在所带来的后果，那么没有人会梦想怀疑未来的确定性。他完全知道将会发生什么，并将把自己的全部财产押在上面。

‘And this is a great blessing; for it is the foundation on which morality and science are built. The assurance that the future is no arbitrary and changeable thing, but that like futures will invariably follow like presents, is the groundwork on which we lay all our plans—the faith on which we do every conscious action of our lives. If this were not so we should be without a guide; we should have no confidence in acting, and hence we should never act, for there would be no knowing that the results which will follow now will be the same as those which followed before.
‘这是一个伟大的祝福；因为它是道德和科学的基础。确信未来不是任意的、可变的事物，而是像未来一样，总是会像现在一样随之而来，这是我们制定所有计划的基础，也是我们在生活中采取每一个有意识的行动的信念。如果不是这样，我们就没有向导了。我们对行动不应该有信心，因此我们永远不应该行动，因为不知道现在的结果会和以前的结果一样。

‘Who would plough or sow if he disbelieved in the fixity of the future? Who would throw water on a blazing house if the action of water upon fire were uncertain? Men will only do their utmost when they feel certain that the future will discover itself against them if their utmost has not been done. The feeling of such a certainty is a constituent part of the sum of the forces at work upon them, and will act most powerfully on the best and most moral men. Those who are most firmly persuaded that the future is immutably bound up with the present in which their work is lying, will best husband their present, and till it with the greatest care. The future must be a lottery to those who think that the same combinations can sometimes precede one set of results, and sometimes another. If their belief is sincere they will speculate instead of working: these ought to be the immoral men; the others have the strongest spur to exertion and morality, if their belief is a living one.
“如果他不相信未来的确定性，谁还会犁地或播种呢？如果水对火的作用不确定，谁会向着火的房子泼水呢？只有当人们确信，如果不竭尽全力，未来就会对他们不利时，他们才会竭尽全力。这种确定性的感觉是作用在他们身上的力量总和的一个组成部分，并且会对最优秀和最有道德的人产生最有力的作用。那些坚信未来与他们的工作所在的现在不可分割地联系在一起的人，将最好地珍惜他们的现在，并以最大的谨慎对待它。对于那些认为相同的组合有时会出现一组结果，有时会出现另一组结果的人来说，未来一定是一场彩票。如果他们的信仰是真诚的，他们就会投机而不是工作：这些人应该是不道德的人；其他人如果他们的信仰是活生生的，那么他们对努力和道德的激励是最强烈的。

‘The bearing of all this upon the machines is not immediately apparent, but will become so presently. In the meantime I must deal with friends who tell me that, though the future is fixed as regards inorganic matter, and in some respects with regard to man, yet that there are many ways in which it cannot be considered as fixed. Thus, they say that fire applied to dry shavings, and well fed with oxygen gas, will always produce a blaze, but that a coward brought into contact with a terrifying object will not always result in a man running away. Nevertheless, if there be two cowards perfectly similar in every respect, and if they be subjected in a perfectly similar way to two terrifying agents, which are themselves perfectly similar, there are few who will not expect a perfect similarity in the running away, even though a thousand years intervene between the original combination and its being repeated.
“所有这一切对机器的影响并不是立即显而易见的，但很快就会变得如此。与此同时，我必须与朋友们打交道，他们告诉我，虽然未来对于无机物以及对于人类来说在某些方面是固定的，但在很多方面它不能被认为是固定的。因此，他们说，对干刨花施火并充分供给氧气，总是会产生火焰，但胆小鬼接触到可怕的物体并不总是会导致一个人逃跑。然而，如果有两个胆小鬼在各方面都完全相似，如果他们以完全相似的方式受到两个可怕的代理人的攻击，而这两个代理人本身又完全相似，那么很少有人会期望逃跑的过程完全相似，即使是在逃跑的过程中。尽管最初的组合和它的重复之间间隔了一千年。

‘The apparently greater regularity in the results of chemical than of human combinations arises from our inability to perceive the subtle differences in human combinations—combinations which are never identically repeated. Fire we know, and shavings we know, but no two men ever were or ever will be exactly alike; and the smallest difference may change the whole conditions of the problem. Our registry of results must be infinite before we could arrive at a full forecast of future combinations; the wonder is that there is as much certainty concerning human action as there is; and assuredly the older we grow the more certain we feel as to what such and such a kind of person will do in given circumstances; but this could never be the case unless human conduct were under the influence of laws, with the working of which we become more and more familiar through experience.
“化学结果的规律性显然比人类组合的规律性更大，这是因为我们无法察觉人类组合中的细微差别——这些组合永远不会完全相同地重复。”我们知道火，我们也知道刨花，但没有两个人曾经或将来是完全相同的。最小的差异可能会改变问题的整体情况。在我们能够对未来组合进行全面预测之前，我们的结果记录必须是无限的；令人惊奇的是，人类的行为有如此多的确定性。当然，我们年纪越大，我们就越能确定这样那样的人在特定情况下会做什么。但是，除非人类行为受到法律的影响，否则情况永远不会如此，而且我们通过经验越来越熟悉法律的运作。

‘If the above is sound, it follows that the regularity with which machinery acts is no proof of the absence of vitality, or at least of germs which may be developed into a new phase of life. At first sight it would indeed appear that a vapour-engine cannot help going when set upon a line of rails with the steam up and the machinery in full play; whereas the man whose business it is to drive it can help doing so at any moment that he pleases; so that the first has no spontaneity, and is not possessed of any sort of free will, while the second has and is.
“如果上述说法正确，那么机器运转的规律性并不能证明缺乏活力，或者至少不能证明缺乏可能发展成生命新阶段的细菌。”乍一看，蒸汽机确实会在蒸汽升起且机械充分发挥作用的情况下放在一条铁轨上时无法控制地运转。而以驾驶为己任的人可以在他愿意的任何时候帮助这样做；因此，前者没有自发性，也不具有任何形式的自由意志，而后者则具有并且存在。

‘This is true up to a certain point; the driver can stop the engine at any moment that he pleases, but he can only please to do so at certain points which have been fixed for him by others, or in the case of unexpected obstructions which force him to please to do so. His pleasure is not spontaneous; there is an unseen choir of influences around him, which make it impossible for him to act in any other way than one. It is known beforehand how much strength must be given to these influences, just as it is known beforehand how much coal and water are necessary for the vapour-engine itself; and curiously enough it will be found that the influences brought to bear upon the driver are of the same kind as those brought to bear upon the engine—that is to say, food and warmth. The driver is obedient to his masters, because he gets food and warmth from them, and if these are withheld or given in insufficient quantities he will cease to drive; in like manner the engine will cease to work if it is insufficiently fed. The only difference is, that the man is conscious about his wants, and the engine (beyond refusing to work) does not seem to be so; but this is temporary, and has been dealt with above.
“在某种程度上，这是正确的；驾驶员可以在他愿意的任何时刻停止发动机，但他只能在其他人为他固定的某些点上这样做，或者在出现意外障碍迫使他这样做的情况下。他的快乐不是自发的，而是自发的。他周围有一群看不见的影响力，这使得他不可能以任何其他方式行事。事先知道必须给予这些影响多大的强度，就像事先知道蒸汽机本身需要多少煤和水一样；奇怪的是，我们会发现对驾驶员的影响与对发动机的影响是同一类——也就是说，食物和温暖。司机服从主人，因为他从他们那里得到食物和温暖，如果这些东西被扣留或给予不足，他就会停止驾驶；同样，如果供油不足，发动机将停止工作。唯一的区别是，这个人意识到自己的需求，而引擎（除了拒绝工作）似乎并没有意识到；但这是暂时的，上面已经处理过。

‘Accordingly, the requisite strength being given to the motives that are to drive the driver, there has never, or hardly ever, been an instance of a man stopping his engine through wantonness. But such a case might occur; yes, and it might occur that the engine should break down: but if the train is stopped from some trivial motive it will be found either that the strength of the necessary influences has been miscalculated, or that the man has been miscalculated, in the same way as an engine may break down from an unsuspected flaw; but even in such a case there will have been no spontaneity; the action will have had its true parental causes: spontaneity is only a term for man’s ignorance of the gods.
“因此，在驱动驾驶员的动机得到了必要的力量的情况下，从来没有或几乎没有一个人肆意地停止发动机的例子。但这样的情况也有可能发生；是的，并且可能会出现引擎故障的情况：但是，如果火车因某种微不足道的动机而停下来，就会发现，要么是必要影响的强度被误算了，要么是那个人被误判了，同样地，发动机可能会因意想不到的缺陷而发生故障；但即使在这种情况下，也不会有自发性。这种行为有其真正的根源：自发性只是人类对神的无知的一个术语。

‘Is there, then, no spontaneity on the part of those who drive the driver?’
“那么，开车的人就没有自发性吗？”

Here followed an obscure argument upon this subject, which I have thought it best to omit. The writer resumes:- ‘After all then it comes to this, that the difference between the life of a man and that of a machine is one rather of degree than of kind, though differences in kind are not wanting. An animal has more provision for emergency than a machine. The machine is less versatile; its range of action is narrow; its strength and accuracy in its own sphere are superhuman, but it shows badly in a dilemma; sometimes when its normal action is disturbed, it will lose its head, and go from bad to worse like a lunatic in a raging frenzy: but here, again, we are met by the same consideration as before, namely, that the machines are still in their infancy; they are mere skeletons without muscles and flesh.
接下来是关于这个主题的一个晦涩的论证，我认为最好省略它。作者继续说道：“毕竟，人的生命与机器的生命之间的差异是程度的差异，而不是种类的差异，尽管种类上的差异并不缺乏。动物比机器有更多的应对紧急情况的能力。机器的通用性较差；其作用范围较窄；它的力量和准确性在它自己的领域是超人的，但它在困境中表现得很糟糕；有时，当它的正常动作受到干扰时，它会失去理智，像一个疯狂的疯子一样变得越来越糟：但在这里，我们再次遇到了与以前相同的考虑，即机器仍然处于静止状态。在他们的婴儿期；他们只是骷髅，没有肌肉和血肉。

‘For how many emergencies is an oyster adapted? For as many as are likely to happen to it, and no more. So are the machines; and so is man himself. The list of casualties that daily occur to man through his want of adaptability is probably as great as that occurring to the machines; and every day gives them some greater provision for the unforeseen. Let any one examine the wonderful self-regulating and self-adjusting contrivances which are now incorporated with the vapour-engine, let him watch the way in which it supplies itself with oil; in which it indicates its wants to those who tend it; in which, by the governor, it regulates its application of its own strength; let him look at that store-house of inertia and momentum the fly-wheel, or at the buffers on a railway carriage; let him see how those improvements are being selected for perpetuity which contain provision against the emergencies that may arise to harass the machines, and then let him think of a hundred thousand years, and the accumulated progress which they will bring unless man can be awakened to a sense of his situation, and of the doom which he is preparing for himself. {6}
“一只牡蛎能应对多少种紧急情况？对于尽可能多的可能发生的事情，仅此而已。机器也是如此；人本身也是如此。人类因缺乏适应能力而每天遭受的伤亡可能与机器所遭受的伤亡一样多。每一天都会为他们提供更多的准备，以应对不可预见的情况。让任何人都检查一下现在与蒸汽机结合在一起的奇妙的自我调节和自我调节装置，让他观察一下它如何为自己提供油；它向照料它的人表明它的需要；其中，由总督管理其自身力量的运用；让他看看惯性和动量的仓库——飞轮，或者火车车厢的缓冲器；让他看看这些改进是如何被永久选择的，其中包含针对可能出现的骚扰机器的紧急情况的规定，然后让他想想十万年，以及它们将带来的累积进步，除非人类能够被唤醒对他的处境以及他正在为自己准备的厄运的感觉。 {6}

‘The misery is that man has been blind so long already. In his reliance upon the use of steam he has been betrayed into increasing and multiplying. To withdraw steam power suddenly will not have the effect of reducing us to the state in which we were before its introduction; there will be a general break-up and time of anarchy such as has never been known; it will be as though our population were suddenly doubled, with no additional means of feeding the increased number. The air we breathe is hardly more necessary for our animal life than the use of any machine, on the strength of which we have increased our numbers, is to our civilisation; it is the machines which act upon man and make him man, as much as man who has acted upon and made the machines; but we must choose between the alternative of undergoing much present suffering, or seeing ourselves gradually superseded by our own creatures, till we rank no higher in comparison with them, than the beasts of the field with ourselves.
‘可悲的是，人类已经盲目了这么久。在他对蒸汽的依赖中，他已经被背叛而增加和繁殖。突然撤走蒸汽动力不会使我们回到蒸汽动力引入之前的状态；将会出现前所未有的全面分裂和无政府状态；就好像我们的人口突然增加了一倍，却没有其他办法来养活增加的人口。我们呼吸的空气对于我们的动物生命来说并不比任何机器的使用对于我们的文明更重要，借助机器我们增加了我们的数量。是机器作用于人并使人成为人，就像人作用于机器并创造了机器一样。但是我们必须在两种选择之间做出选择：要么承受目前的许多痛苦，要么看到我们自己逐渐被我们自己的生物所取代，直到我们与他们相比，就像野外的野兽与我们自己相比一样。

‘Herein lies our danger. For many seem inclined to acquiesce in so dishonourable a future. They say that although man should become to the machines what the horse and dog are to us, yet that he will continue to exist, and will probably be better off in a state of domestication under the beneficent rule of the machines than in his present wild condition. We treat our domestic animals with much kindness. We give them whatever we believe to be the best for them; and there can be no doubt that our use of meat has increased their happiness rather than detracted from it. In like manner there is reason to hope that the machines will use us kindly, for their existence will be in a great measure dependent upon ours; they will rule us with a rod of iron, but they will not eat us; they will not only require our services in the reproduction and education of their young, but also in waiting upon them as servants; in gathering food for them, and feeding them; in restoring them to health when they are sick; and in either burying their dead or working up their deceased members into new forms of mechanical existence.
‘这就是我们的危险。因为许多人似乎倾向于默许如此不光彩的未来。他们说，虽然人之于机器就像马和狗之于我们，但他将继续存在，并且在机器仁慈统治下的驯化状态中可能会比在目前的野生状态中过得更好。健康）状况。我们非常友善地对待我们的家畜。我们为他们提供我们认为对他们最好的一切；毫无疑问，我们对肉类的使用增加了而不是降低了他们的幸福感。同样，我们有理由希望机器能够善待我们，因为它们的存在在很大程度上取决于我们的存在。他们会用铁杖统治我们，但不会吃我们；它们不仅需要我们为它们的后代提供繁殖和教育方面的服务，而且还需要我们像仆人一样伺候它们；为他们收集食物并喂养他们；当他们生病时使他们恢复健康；或者埋葬他们的死者，或者让他们死去的成员进入新的机械存在形式。

‘The very nature of the motive power which works the advancement of the machines precludes the possibility of man’s life being rendered miserable as well as enslaved. Slaves are tolerably happy if they have good masters, and the revolution will not occur in our time, nor hardly in ten thousand years, or ten times that. Is it wise to be uneasy about a contingency which is so remote? Man is not a sentimental animal where his material interests are concerned, and though here and there some ardent soul may look upon himself and curse his fate that he was not born a vapour-engine, yet the mass of mankind will acquiesce in any arrangement which gives them better food and clothing at a cheaper rate, and will refrain from yielding to unreasonable jealousy merely because there are other destinies more glorious than their own.
“推动机器进步的原动力的本质排除了人类生活变得悲惨和被奴役的可能性。如果奴隶有好主人，他们就还算幸福，而革命不会发生在我们这个时代，一万年或十倍之内也不会发生。对如此遥远的意外事件感到不安是否明智？就物质利益而言，人不是感性的动物，虽然时不时会有一些热心的灵魂审视自己，咒骂自己的命运，说他生来不是一台蒸汽机，但人类大众会默许任何安排以更便宜的价格给他们更好的食物和衣服，并且不会仅仅因为有其他命运比自己更光荣而屈服于无理的嫉妒。

‘The power of custom is enormous, and so gradual will be the change, that man’s sense of what is due to himself will be at no time rudely shocked; our bondage will steal upon us noiselessly and by imperceptible approaches; nor will there ever be such a clashing of desires between man and the machines as will lead to an encounter between them. Among themselves the machines will war eternally, but they will still require man as the being through whose agency the struggle will be principally conducted. In point of fact there is no occasion for anxiety about the future happiness of man so long as he continues to be in any way profitable to the machines; he may become the inferior race, but he will be infinitely better off than he is now. Is it not then both absurd and unreasonable to be envious of our benefactors? And should we not be guilty of consummate folly if we were to reject advantages which we cannot obtain otherwise, merely because they involve a greater gain to others than to ourselves?
“习惯的力量是巨大的，而且这种变化是渐进的，人们对自己应得的东西的感觉永远不会受到粗鲁的震惊；我们的束缚会悄无声息地、不知不觉地降临到我们身上；人与机器之间的欲望冲突也不会导致它们之间的相遇。机器之间将永远进行战争，但它们仍然需要人作为主要通过其代理进行斗争的存在。事实上，只要人类继续以任何方式为机器带来利润，就没有必要担心人类未来的幸福。他可能会成为劣等种族，但他会比现在过得无限好。那么，嫉妒我们的恩人不是既荒谬又不合理吗？如果我们仅仅因为别人获得的利益比我们自己获得的利益更大而拒绝通过其他方式无法获得的利益，我们难道不应该犯下极大的愚蠢吗？

‘With those who can argue in this way I have nothing in common. I shrink with as much horror from believing that my race can ever be superseded or surpassed, as I should do from believing that even at the remotest period my ancestors were other than human beings. Could I believe that ten hundred thousand years ago a single one of my ancestors was another kind of being to myself, I should lose all self-respect, and take no further pleasure or interest in life. I have the same feeling with regard to my descendants, and believe it to be one that will be felt so generally that the country will resolve upon putting an immediate stop to all further mechanical progress, and upon destroying all improvements that have been made for the last three hundred years. I would not urge more than this. We may trust ourselves to deal with those that remain, and though I should prefer to have seen the destruction include another two hundred years, I am aware of the necessity for compromising, and would so far sacrifice my own individual convictions as to be content with three hundred. Less than this will be insufficient.’
“我与那些能以这种方式争论的人没有任何共同点。我害怕相信我的种族可以被取代或超越，就像我相信即使在最遥远的时期我的祖先也不是人类一样。如果我相信十万年前我的祖先对我来说是另一种存在，我就会失去所有的自尊，对生活不再有任何乐趣或兴趣。我对我的后代也有同样的感觉，并且相信这种感觉会如此普遍，以至于国家将决心立即停止所有进一步的机械进步，并摧毁为机械化所做的所有改进。过去三百年。我不会敦促更多。我们可以相信自己能够处理剩下的那些，虽然我更希望看到毁灭再持续两百年，但我意识到妥协的必要性，并且到目前为止会牺牲我自己的个人信念，以满足三百。少于这个是不够的。

This was the conclusion of the attack which led to the destruction of machinery throughout Erewhon. There was only one serious attempt to answer it. Its author said that machines were to be regarded as a part of man’s own physical nature, being really nothing but extra-corporeal limbs. Man, he said, was a machinate mammal. The lower animals keep all their limbs at home in their own bodies, but many of man’s are loose, and lie about detached, now here and now there, in various parts of the world—some being kept always handy for contingent use, and others being occasionally hundreds of miles away. A machine is merely a supplementary limb; this is the be all and end all of machinery. We do not use our own limbs other than as machines; and a leg is only a much better wooden leg than any one can manufacture.
这就是这次袭击的结论，这次袭击导致整个埃瑞翁的机械被毁。只有一次认真的尝试来回答这个问题。它的作者说，机器应该被视为人类自身身体本质的一部分，实际上只不过是体外的肢体。他说，人类是一种精明的哺乳动物。低等动物把所有的四肢都藏在自己的身体里，但人类的许多四肢都是松散的，分离地躺在世界各地，时而在这里，时而那里——有些总是放在手边以备不时之需。有时距离数百英里。机器只是一个辅助肢体；这是机械的全部和最终目的。我们不会将自己的四肢用作机器以外的用途；腿只是比任何人都能制造的更好的木腿。

‘Observe a man digging with a spade; his right fore-arm has become artificially lengthened, and his hand has become a joint. The handle of the spade is like the knob at the end of the humerus; the shaft is the additional bone, and the oblong iron plate is the new form of the hand which enables its possessor to disturb the earth in a way to which his original hand was unequal. Having thus modified himself, not as other animals are modified, by circumstances over which they have had not even the appearance of control, but having, as it were, taken forethought and added a cubit to his stature, civilisation began to dawn upon the race, the social good offices, the genial companionship of friends, the art of unreason, and all those habits of mind which most elevate man above the lower animals, in the course of time ensued.
‘观察一个人用铁锹挖掘；他的右前臂被人为延长，手也变成了关节。铲子的手柄就像肱骨末端的旋钮；轴是额外的骨头，而椭圆形铁板是手的新形式，它使持有者能够以他原来的手无法比拟的方式扰动地球。这样改变了自己，不像其他动物那样，被他们甚至无法控制的环境所改变，而是经过深思熟虑，将自己的身材增加了一肘，文明开始在这个种族中显现出来。随着时间的推移，社会斡旋、朋友的友善陪伴、非理性的艺术以及所有那些最能将人类提升到低等动物之上的思维习惯都随之而来。

‘Thus civilisation and mechanical progress advanced hand in hand, each developing and being developed by the other, the earliest accidental use of the stick having set the ball rolling, and the prospect of advantage keeping it in motion. In fact, machines are to be regarded as the mode of development by which human organism is now especially advancing, every past invention being an addition to the resources of the human body. Even community of limbs is thus rendered possible to those who have so much community of soul as to own money enough to pay a railway fare; for a train is only a seven-leagued foot that five hundred may own at once.’
“因此，文明和机械进步齐头并进，彼此发展并相互发展，最早偶然使用棍子使球滚动起来，而优势的前景则使其继续运转。事实上，机器被视为人类有机体现在特别进步的发展模式，过去的每一项发明都是对人体资源的补充。对于那些拥有如此多的灵魂共同体以至于拥有足够的钱来支付火车票的人来说，甚至四肢的共同体也成为可能；因为一列火车只不过是五百人同时拥有的七联盟英尺。

The one serious danger which this writer apprehended was that the machines would so equalise men’s powers, and so lessen the severity of competition, that many persons of inferior physique would escape detection and transmit their inferiority to their descendants. He feared that the removal of the present pressure might cause a degeneracy of the human race, and indeed that the whole body might become purely rudimentary, the man himself being nothing but soul and mechanism, an intelligent but passionless principle of mechanical action.
笔者所担心的一个严重危险是，机器将使人类的力量变得平等，从而减轻竞争的严重性，以至于许多体质较差的人会逃避检测，并将其劣势遗传给他们的后代。他担心，消除当前的压力可能会导致人类的退化，甚至整个身体可能会变得纯粹初级，人本身只不过是灵魂和机械，是一种聪明但无激情的机械行动原理。

‘How greatly,’ he wrote, ‘do we not now live with our external limbs? We vary our physique with the seasons, with age, with advancing or decreasing wealth. If it is wet we are furnished with an organ commonly called an umbrella, and which is designed for the purpose of protecting our clothes or our skins from the injurious effects of rain. Man has now many extra-corporeal members, which are of more importance to him than a good deal of his hair, or at any rate than his whiskers. His memory goes in his pocket-book. He becomes more and more complex as he grows older; he will then be seen with see-engines, or perhaps with artificial teeth and hair: if he be a really well-developed specimen of his race, he will be furnished with a large box upon wheels, two horses, and a coachman.’
“我们现在不是靠外肢生活吗？”他写道。我们的体质随着季节、年龄、财富的增减而变化。如果天气潮湿，我们会配备一种通常称为雨伞的器官，其设计目的是保护我们的衣服或皮肤免受雨水的伤害。人现在有许多体外成员，这些成员对他来说比他的大量头发更重要，或者至少比他的胡须更重要。他的记忆就在他的皮夹里。随着年龄的增长，他变得越来越复杂；然后人们会看到他带着看见引擎，或者也许带着人造牙齿和头发：如果他是他的种族中真正发育良好的标本，他将配备一个带轮子的大箱子、两匹马和一名车夫。

It was this writer who originated the custom of classifying men by their horse-power, and who divided them into genera, species, varieties, and subvarieties, giving them names from the hypothetical language which expressed the number of limbs which they could command at any moment. He showed that men became more highly and delicately organised the more nearly they approached the summit of opulence, and that none but millionaires possessed the full complement of limbs with which mankind could become incorporate.
正是这位作家首创了按照马力对人类进行分类的习惯，并将它们分为属、种、变种和亚变种，并根据假设的语言给它们命名，该语言表示它们在任何情况下都能指挥的肢体数量。片刻。他表明，人类越接近富裕的顶峰，他们的组织性就越高，除了百万富翁之外，没有人拥有人类可以融入的完整四肢。

‘Those mighty organisms,’ he continued, ‘our leading bankers and merchants, speak to their congeners through the length and breadth of the land in a second of time; their rich and subtle souls can defy all material impediment, whereas the souls of the poor are clogged and hampered by matter, which sticks fast about them as treacle to the wings of a fly, or as one struggling in a quicksand: their dull ears must take days or weeks to hear what another would tell them from a distance, instead of hearing it in a second as is done by the more highly organised classes. Who shall deny that one who can tack on a special train to his identity, and go wheresoever he will whensoever he pleases, is more highly organised than he who, should he wish for the same power, might wish for the wings of a bird with an equal chance of getting them; and whose legs are his only means of locomotion? That old philosophic enemy, matter, the inherently and essentially evil, still hangs about the neck of the poor and strangles him: but to the rich, matter is immaterial; the elaborate organisation of his extra-corporeal system has freed his soul.
“那些强大的有机体，”他继续说道，“我们的主要银行家和商人，在一秒钟的时间里通过土地的长度和广度与他们的同类交谈；他们丰富而微妙的灵魂可以克服一切物质障碍，而穷人的灵魂则被物质所堵塞和阻碍，物质紧紧地粘在他们周围，就像苍蝇翅膀上的糖蜜，或者像在流沙中挣扎的人一样：他们迟钝的耳朵必须需要几天或几周的时间才能听到别人从远处告诉他们什么，而不是像组织更严密的班级那样在一秒钟内听到。谁会否认，一个人可以根据自己的身份搭上一趟专列，随时随地去任何他想去的地方，他比那些希望拥有同样力量的人更有组织性，如果他希望获得同样的力量，他可能希望拥有一只鸟的翅膀获得它们的机会均等；谁的腿是他唯一的移动手段？那个古老的哲学敌人，物质，本质上的邪恶，仍然挂在穷人的脖子上并勒死他们：但对富人来说，物质是非物质的；对于富人来说，物质是非物质的。他的体外系统的精心组织解放了他的灵魂。

‘This is the secret of the homage which we see rich men receive from those who are poorer than themselves: it would be a grave error to suppose that this deference proceeds from motives which we need be ashamed of: it is the natural respect which all living creatures pay to those whom they recognise as higher than themselves in the scale of animal life, and is analogous to the veneration which a dog feels for man. Among savage races it is deemed highly honourable to be the possessor of a gun, and throughout all known time there has been a feeling that those who are worth most are the worthiest.’
“这就是我们看到富人从比自己更穷的人那里得到敬意的秘密：如果认为这种敬意是出于我们需要感到羞耻的动机，那将是一个严重的错误：这是所有人都自然而然的尊重。生物会向那些它们认为在动物生命等级上比自己高的人付出代价，这类似于狗对人类的尊敬。在野蛮种族中，拥有一把枪被认为是非常光荣的，并且在整个已知的时间里，人们一直有一种感觉，即那些最有价值的人是最有价值的。

And so he went on at considerable length, attempting to show what changes in the distribution of animal and vegetable life throughout the kingdom had been caused by this and that of man’s inventions, and in what way each was connected with the moral and intellectual development of the human species: he even allotted to some the share which they had had in the creation and modification of man’s body, and that which they would hereafter have in its destruction; but the other writer was considered to have the best of it, and in the end succeeded in destroying all the inventions that had been discovered for the preceding 271 years, a period which was agreed upon by all parties after several years of wrangling as to whether a certain kind of mangle which was much in use among washerwomen should be saved or no. It was at last ruled to be dangerous, and was just excluded by the limit of 271 years. Then came the reactionary civil wars which nearly ruined the country, but which it would be beyond my present scope to describe.
因此，他继续用相当长的篇幅，试图表明人类的这一或另一项发明引起了整个王国动植物生命分布的哪些变化，以及每一项发明与人类的道德和智力发展有何联系。人类：他甚至将他们在人类身体的创造和改造中所拥有的份额，以及他们在人类身体的毁灭中所拥有的份额分配给了一些人；但另一位作家被认为拥有最好的，并最终成功地摧毁了过去 271 年中发现的所有发明，这一时期是各方经过数年争论后达成的共识。洗衣女工常用的某种熨布机是否应该保留或不保留。最后被判定为危险，只是被排除在271年的期限之外。然后是反动内战，几乎毁掉了这个国家，但这超出了我目前的范围。

CHAPTER XXVI: THE VIEWS OF AN EREWHONIAN PROPHET CONCERNING THE
第二十六章：一位埃雷沃尼安先知关于

RIGHTS OF ANIMALS
动物的权利

It will be seen from the foregoing chapters that the Erewhonians are a meek and long-suffering people, easily led by the nose, and quick to offer up common sense at the shrine of logic, when a philosopher arises among them, who carries them away through his reputation for especial learning, or by convincing them that their existing institutions are not based on the strictest principles of morality.
从前面的章节可以看出，埃雷洪尼亚人是一个温顺、忍耐的民族，很容易被牵着鼻子走，当他们中间出现一位哲学家，把他们带走时，他们很快就会在逻辑圣殿前奉献常识。通过他在特殊学问方面的声誉，或者通过让他们相信他们现有的机构并不是基于最严格的道德原则。

The series of revolutions on which I shall now briefly touch shows this even more plainly than the way (already dealt with) in which at a later date they cut their throats in the matter of machinery; for if the second of the two reformers of whom I am about to speak had had his way—or rather the way that he professed to have—the whole race would have died of starvation within a twelve-month. Happily common sense, though she is by nature the gentlest creature living, when she feels the knife at her throat, is apt to develop unexpected powers of resistance, and to send doctrinaires flying, even when they have bound her down and think they have her at their mercy. What happened, so far as I could collect it from the best authorities, was as follows:-
我现在要简要讨论的一系列革命比后来他们在机械问题上割断喉咙的方式（已经讨论过）更清楚地表明了这一点。因为，如果我要谈到的两位改革家中的第二位按照他自己的方式——或者更确切地说是他自称的方式——整个人类就会在十二个月内死于饥饿。令人高兴的是，虽然她本质上是最温柔的生物，但当她感到喉咙上有刀时，很容易产生意想不到的抵抗力量，并让教条主义者飞走，即使他们已经束缚了她并认为他们拥有了她任凭他们摆布。据我从最权威的机构收集到的信息，发生的事情如下：-

Some two thousand five hundred years ago the Erewhonians were still uncivilised, and lived by hunting, fishing, a rude system of agriculture, and plundering such few other nations as they had not yet completely conquered. They had no schools or systems of philosophy, but by a kind of dog-knowledge did that which was right in their own eyes and in those of their neighbours; the common sense, therefore, of the public being as yet unvitiated, crime and disease were looked upon much as they are in other countries.
大约两千五百年前，埃雷洪尼亚人还没有开化，他们靠狩猎、捕鱼、原始的农业制度以及掠夺他们尚未完全征服的少数其他国家为生。他们没有哲学流派或体系，但通过一种狗的知识去做他们自己和邻居眼中正确的事情。因此，人们对公众尚未受到损害的常识、犯罪和疾病的看法与其他国家的情况大致相同。

But with the gradual advance of civilisation and increase in material prosperity, people began to ask questions about things that they had hitherto taken as matters of course, and one old gentleman, who had great influence over them by reason of the sanctity of his life, and his supposed inspiration by an unseen power, whose existence was now beginning to be felt, took it into his head to disquiet himself about the rights of animals—a question that so far had disturbed nobody.
但随着文明的逐步进步和物质繁荣的增加，人们开始对他们迄今为止视为理所当然的事情提出疑问，一位老先生因其生命的神圣性而对他们产生了巨大的影响，他所谓的灵感来源于一种看不见的力量，现在人们开始感觉到这种力量的存在，这让他对动物的权利感到不安——这个问题到目前为止还没有困扰过任何人。

All prophets are more or less fussy, and this old gentleman seems to have been one of the more fussy ones. Being maintained at the public expense, he had ample leisure, and not content with limiting his attention to the rights of animals, he wanted to reduce right and wrong to rules, to consider the foundations of duty and of good and evil, and otherwise to put all sorts of matters on a logical basis, which people whose time is money are content to accept on no basis at all.
所有的先知都或多或少地挑剔，而这位老先生似乎是其中最挑剔的一位。他靠公费维持生活，有充足的闲暇，他不满足于将注意力限制在动物的权利上，他想减少规则的是非，考虑义务和善恶的基础，并以其他方式把各种事情放在逻辑的基础上，时间就是金钱的人会在没有任何基础的情况下满意地接受。

As a matter of course, the basis on which he decided that duty could alone rest was one that afforded no standing-room for many of the old-established habits of the people. These, he assured them, were all wrong, and whenever any one ventured to differ from him, he referred the matter to the unseen power with which he alone was in direct communication, and the unseen power invariably assured him that he was right. As regards the rights of animals he taught as follows:-
当然，他决定只靠责任的基础是，人民的许多旧习惯没有立足之地。他向他们保证，这些都是错误的，每当有人敢于与他提出不同意见时，他都会将此事交给与他单独直接沟通的看不见的力量，而看不见的力量总是向他保证他是对的。关于动物的权利，他教导如下：-

‘You know, he said, ‘how wicked it is of you to kill one another. Once upon a time your fore-fathers made no scruple about not only killing, but also eating their relations. No one would now go back to such detestable practices, for it is notorious that we have lived much more happily since they were abandoned. From this increased prosperity we may confidently deduce the maxim that we should not kill and eat our fellow-creatures. I have consulted the higher power by whom you know that I am inspired, and he has assured me that this conclusion is irrefragable.
“你知道，”他说，“你们互相残杀是多么邪恶。”从前，你们的祖先不仅肆无忌惮地杀戮，而且还吃掉他们的亲人。现在没有人会再回到这种可憎的做法，因为众所周知，自从它们被抛弃以来，我们生活得更加幸福。从这种日益繁荣的情况中，我们可以自信地推断出我们不应该杀死和吃掉我们的同胞的格言。我已经咨询了更高的力量，你知道我是受到他的启发，他向我保证这个结论是无可辩驳的。

‘Now it cannot be denied that sheep, cattle, deer, birds, and fishes are our fellow-creatures. They differ from us in some respects, but those in which they differ are few and secondary, while those that they have in common with us are many and essential. My friends, if it was wrong of you to kill and eat your fellow-men, it is wrong also to kill and eat fish, flesh, and fowl. Birds, beasts, and fishes, have as full a right to live as long as they can unmolested by man, as man has to live unmolested by his neighbours. These words, let me again assure you, are not mine, but those of the higher power which inspires me.
“现在不可否认的是，羊、牛、鹿、鸟和鱼是我们的同胞。他们在某些方面与我们不同，但他们的不同之处是很少的、次要的，而他们与我们的共同点却是很多且重要的。我的朋友们，如果你们杀害和吃你们的同胞是错误的，那么杀害和吃鱼、肉和家禽也是错误的。鸟类、野兽和鱼类，只要不受人类干扰，就拥有充分的生存权，就像人类必须在不受邻居干扰的情况下生存一样。让我再次向你们保证，这些话不是我的，而是激励我的更高力量的话语。

‘I grant,’ he continued, ‘that animals molest one another, and that some of them go so far as to molest man, but I have yet to learn that we should model our conduct on that of the lower animals. We should endeavour, rather, to instruct them, and bring them to a better mind. To kill a tiger, for example, who has lived on the flesh of men and women whom he has killed, is to reduce ourselves to the level of the tiger, and is unworthy of people who seek to be guided by the highest principles in all, both their thoughts and actions.
“我承认，”他继续说道，“动物们互相骚扰，有些动物甚至骚扰人类，但我还不知道我们应该效仿低等动物的行为。相反，我们应该努力指导他们，让他们有更好的思想。例如，杀死一只老虎，它以被它所杀死的男人和女人的肉为生，就是把我们自己降低到老虎的水平，不配那些寻求遵循一切最高原则的人。 ，他们的想法和行动。

‘The unseen power who has revealed himself to me alone among you, has told me to tell you that you ought by this time to have outgrown the barbarous habits of your ancestors. If, as you believe, you know better than they, you should do better. He commands you, therefore, to refrain from killing any living being for the sake of eating it. The only animal food that you may eat, is the flesh of any birds, beasts, or fishes that you may come upon as having died a natural death, or any that may have been born prematurely, or so deformed that it is a mercy to put them out of their pain; you may also eat all such animals as have committed suicide. As regards vegetables you may eat all those that will let you eat them with impunity.’
“在你们中间，有一种无形的力量向我独自显现，它告诉我，你们现在应该已经摆脱了你们祖先的野蛮习惯。如果你相信，你比他们更了解，你就应该做得更好。因此，他命令你们不要为了吃而杀死任何生物。你唯一可以吃的动物食物是任何鸟类、野兽或鱼类的肉，你可能会遇到自然死亡的动物，或者任何可能早产的动物，或者畸形得可怜的动物。让他们摆脱痛苦；你也可以吃所有自杀的动物。至于蔬菜，你可以吃所有能让你不受惩罚地吃的蔬菜。

So wisely and so well did the old prophet argue, and so terrible were the threats he hurled at those who should disobey him, that in the end he carried the more highly educated part of the people with him, and presently the poorer classes followed suit, or professed to do so. Having seen the triumph of his principles, he was gathered to his fathers, and no doubt entered at once into full communion with that unseen power whose favour he had already so pre-eminently enjoyed.
这位老先知的论点是如此明智和出色，他对那些不服从他的人发出的威胁是如此可怕，以至于最终他带着受过高等教育的那部分人跟随他，不久，较贫穷的阶级也效仿了。 ，或声称这样做。在看到自己的原则取得了胜利之后，他被聚集到他的祖先那里，毫无疑问，他立即与那股看不见的力量完全融为一体，而他已经非常享受这种力量的青睐。

He had not, however, been dead very long, before some of his more ardent disciples took it upon them to better the instruction of their master. The old prophet had allowed the use of eggs and milk, but his disciples decided that to eat a fresh egg was to destroy a potential chicken, and that this came to much the same as murdering a live one. Stale eggs, if it was quite certain that they were too far gone to be able to be hatched, were grudgingly permitted, but all eggs offered for sale had to be submitted to an inspector, who, on being satisfied that they were addled, would label them ‘Laid not less than three months’ from the date, whatever it might happen to be. These eggs, I need hardly say, were only used in puddings, and as a medicine in certain cases where an emetic was urgently required. Milk was forbidden inasmuch as it could not be obtained without robbing some calf of its natural sustenance, and thus endangering its life.
然而，他死后不久，他的一些更热心的弟子就开始承担起更好地指导他们老师的责任。老先知允许使用鸡蛋和牛奶，但他的弟子们认为，吃一个新鲜的鸡蛋就是消灭一只潜在的鸡，这与谋杀一只活鸡没有什么区别。不新鲜的鸡蛋，如果确信它们已经过时而无法孵化，则勉强允许，但所有出售的鸡蛋都必须提交给检查员，检查员在确认这些鸡蛋已变质后，将无论发生什么情况，都将其标记为“自日期起不少于三个月内放置”。不用说，这些鸡蛋只用于布丁，以及在某些急需催吐的情况下作为药物。牛奶是被禁止的，因为获得牛奶会剥夺小牛的天然营养，从而危及其生命。

It will be easily believed that at first there were many who gave the new rules outward observance, but embraced every opportunity of indulging secretly in those flesh-pots to which they had been accustomed. It was found that animals were continually dying natural deaths under more or less suspicious circumstances. Suicidal mania, again, which had hitherto been confined exclusively to donkeys, became alarmingly prevalent even among such for the most part self-respecting creatures as sheep and cattle. It was astonishing how some of these unfortunate animals would scent out a butcher’s knife if there was one within a mile of them, and run right up against it if the butcher did not get it out of their way in time.
人们很容易相信，一开始有很多人表面上遵守新规则，但他们抓住一切机会偷偷地沉迷于他们已经习惯的肉锅里。人们发现，动物不断地在或多或少可疑的情况下自然死亡。迄今为止，自杀狂潮还仅限于驴子，现在甚至在像羊和牛这样大多数自尊的动物中也变得惊人地普遍。令人惊讶的是，如果这些不幸的动物在一英里之内有一把屠刀，一些动物会闻到一把屠刀的气味，如果屠夫没有及时把它移开，它们就会直接跑向它。

Dogs, again, that had been quite law-abiding as regards domestic poultry, tame rabbits, sucking pigs, or sheep and lambs, suddenly took to breaking beyond the control of their masters, and killing anything that they were told not to touch. It was held that any animal killed by a dog had died a natural death, for it was the dog’s nature to kill things, and he had only refrained from molesting farmyard creatures hitherto because his nature had been tampered with. Unfortunately the more these unruly tendencies became developed, the more the common people seemed to delight in breeding the very animals that would put temptation in the dog’s way. There is little doubt, in fact, that they were deliberately evading the law; but whether this was so or no they sold or ate everything their dogs had killed.
狗，对于家禽、驯服的兔子、乳猪、绵羊和羔羊来说，一直很守法，突然变得不受主人的控制，杀死任何被告知不要碰的东西。人们认为，任何被狗杀死的动物都属于自然死亡，因为狗的本性就是杀戮，而他至今没有骚扰农家的生物，只是因为他的本性被篡改了。不幸的是，这些不守规矩的倾向越发展，普通人似乎就越喜欢饲养那些能够对狗施加诱惑的动物。事实上，毫无疑问，他们是故意逃避法律。但无论事实是否如此，他们都会卖掉或吃掉他们的狗杀死的所有东西。

Evasion was more difficult in the case of the larger animals, for the magistrates could not wink at all the pretended suicides of pigs, sheep, and cattle that were brought before them. Sometimes they had to convict, and a few convictions had a very terrorising effect—whereas in the case of animals killed by a dog, the marks of the dog’s teeth could be seen, and it was practically impossible to prove malice on the part of the owner of the dog.
对于较大的动物来说，逃避更加困难，因为地方官员对所有被带到他们面前的假装自杀的猪、羊和牛都无法眨眼。有时他们必须定罪，有的定罪会产生非常恐怖的效果——而在狗杀死动物的情况下，可以看到狗的牙齿痕迹，几乎不可能证明狗有恶意。狗的主人。

Another fertile source of disobedience to the law was furnished by a decision of one of the judges that raised a great outcry among the more fervent disciples of the old prophet. The judge held that it was lawful to kill any animal in self-defence, and that such conduct was so natural on the part of a man who found himself attacked, that the attacking creature should be held to have died a natural death. The High Vegetarians had indeed good reason to be alarmed, for hardly had this decision become generally known before a number of animals, hitherto harmless, took to attacking their owners with such ferocity, that it became necessary to put them to a natural death. Again, it was quite common at that time to see the carcase of a calf, lamb, or kid exposed for sale with a label from the inspector certifying that it had been killed in self- defence. Sometimes even the carcase of a lamb or calf was exposed as ‘warranted still-born,’ when it presented every appearance of having enjoyed at least a month of life.
不遵守法律的另一个丰富根源是一位法官的一项决定，该决定在老先知的更热心的门徒中引起了强烈抗议。法官认为，出于自卫而杀死任何动物是合法的，而且对于发现自己受到攻击的人来说，这种行为是很自然的，因此攻击动物应该被视为自然死亡。高级素食者确实有充分的理由感到震惊，因为这一决定还没有被广泛知晓，许多迄今为止无害的动物就开始以如此凶猛的方式攻击它们的主人，以至于有必要让它们自然死亡。同样，当时很常见看到小牛、羔羊或小山羊的尸体暴露在外出售，并附有检查员的标签，证明其是出于自卫而被杀害的。有时，甚至羔羊或小牛的尸体也会被暴露为“死产”，因为它看起来已经享受了至少一个月的生活。

As for the flesh of animals that had bona fide died a natural death, the permission to eat it was nugatory, for it was generally eaten by some other animal before man got hold of it; or failing this it was often poisonous, so that practically people were forced to evade the law by some of the means above spoken of, or to become vegetarians. This last alternative was so little to the taste of the Erewhonians, that the laws against killing animals were falling into desuetude, and would very likely have been repealed, but for the breaking out of a pestilence, which was ascribed by the priests and prophets of the day to the lawlessness of the people in the matter of eating forbidden flesh. On this, there was a reaction; stringent laws were passed, forbidding the use of meat in any form or shape, and permitting no food but grain, fruits, and vegetables to be sold in shops and markets. These laws were enacted about two hundred years after the death of the old prophet who had first unsettled people’s minds about the rights of animals; but they had hardly been passed before people again began to break them.
至于真正自然死亡的动物的肉，食用它的许可是无效的，因为在人类获得它之前，它通常已经被其他动物吃掉了。如果做不到这一点，它通常是有毒的，因此实际上人们被迫通过上述某些手段来逃避法律，或者成为素食主义者。这最后的选择太不符合埃雷洪人的口味，以至于禁止宰杀动物的法律已经废止，而且很可能被废除，除非爆发了瘟疫，这是由祭司和先知所归咎的。人民在吃禁肉问题上无法无天的日子。对此，有人做出了反应；通过了严格的法律，禁止使用任何形式或形状的肉类，并不允许商店和市场上出售除谷物、水果和蔬菜外的任何食物。这些法律是在这位老先知去世大约两百年后颁布的，他首先动摇了人们对动物权利的认识。但它们刚被通过，人们又开始破坏它们。

I was told that the most painful consequence of all this folly did not lie in the fact that law-abiding people had to go without animal food—many nations do this and seem none the worse, and even in flesh-eating countries such as Italy, Spain, and Greece, the poor seldom see meat from year’s end to year’s end. The mischief lay in the jar which undue prohibition gave to the consciences of all but those who were strong enough to know that though conscience as a rule boons, it can also bane. The awakened conscience of an individual will often lead him to do things in haste that he had better have left undone, but the conscience of a nation awakened by a respectable old gentleman who has an unseen power up his sleeve will pave hell with a vengeance.
有人告诉我，所有这些愚蠢行为最痛苦的后果并不在于守法的人们必须不吃动物食品——许多国家都这样做，而且看起来并没有变得更糟，甚至在意大利这样的食肉国家也是如此。 、西班牙、希腊，穷人从年到年都很少见到肉。恶作剧就在不适当的禁令给所有人的良心带来的伤害中，除了那些足够强大的人知道，虽然良心通常是有益的，但它也可能是祸害。一个人的良心觉醒，常常会导致他匆忙做一些他最好不做的事情，但一个国家的良心被一位可敬的老绅士唤醒，他拥有一种看不见的力量，他会以复仇铺平地狱。

Young people were told that it was a sin to do what their fathers had done unhurt for centuries; those, moreover, who preached to them about the enormity of eating meat, were an unattractive academic folk, and though they over-awed all but the bolder youths, there were few who did not in their hearts dislike them. However much the young person might be shielded, he soon got to know that men and women of the world—often far nicer people than the prophets who preached abstention—continually spoke sneeringly of the new doctrinaire laws, and were believed to set them aside in secret, though they dared not do so openly. Small wonder, then, that the more human among the student classes were provoked by the touch-not, taste-not, handle-not precepts of their rulers, into questioning much that they would otherwise have unhesitatingly accepted.
年轻人被告知，做他们的父辈几个世纪以来所做的事情而不受伤害是一种罪过。此外，那些向他们鼓吹吃肉的可怕性的人都是毫无吸引力的学术人士，尽管他们让除了大胆的年轻人之外的所有人都感到敬畏，但很少有人心里不喜欢他们。无论这个年轻人可能受到多大的保护，他很快就知道世界上的男男女女——通常比宣扬禁欲的先知要好得多——不断地嘲笑新的教条主义法律，并被认为将它们搁置在一边。秘密，虽然他们不敢公开这样做。因此，毫不奇怪，学生阶层中更人性化的人会被统治者的“不碰、不尝、不把手”的戒律激怒，对他们本来会毫不犹豫地接受的许多问题提出质疑。

One sad story is on record about a young man of promising amiable disposition, but cursed with more conscience than brains, who had been told by his doctor (for as I have above said disease was not yet held to be criminal) that he ought to eat meat, law or no law. He was much shocked and for some time refused to comply with what he deemed the unrighteous advice given him by his doctor; at last, however, finding that he grew weaker and weaker, he stole secretly on a dark night into one of those dens in which meat was surreptitiously sold, and bought a pound of prime steak. He took it home, cooked it in his bedroom when every one in the house had gone to rest, ate it, and though he could hardly sleep for remorse and shame, felt so much better next morning that he hardly knew himself.
有一个悲伤的故事被记录在案，讲述的是一位性格温和的年轻人，但他的医生告诉他，他应该吃肉，有法或无法。他非常震惊，有一段时间拒绝遵守他认为医生给他的不公正的建议。但最后，他发现自己越来越虚弱，就在一个漆黑的夜晚偷偷溜进一个卖肉的窝点，买了一磅上等牛排。他把它带回家，在家里的每个人都休息的时候在卧室里煮了它，吃了它，尽管他因悔恨和羞愧而几乎无法入睡，但第二天早上感觉好多了，他几乎不知道自己。

Three or four days later, he again found himself irresistibly drawn to this same den. Again he bought a pound of steak, again he cooked and ate it, and again, in spite of much mental torture, on the following morning felt himself a different man. To cut the story short, though he never went beyond the bounds of moderation, it preyed upon his mind that he should be drifting, as he certainly was, into the ranks of the habitual law-breakers.
三四天后，他再次发现自己不可抗拒地被这个同一个巢穴所吸引。他又买了一磅牛排，又煮了吃，尽管精神上受到了很大的折磨，第二天早上他还是感觉自己变了一个人。总而言之，尽管他从未超越过节制的界限，但他的思想却在不断地变化，他确实是这样，已经跻身于惯犯的行列了。

All the time his health kept on improving, and though he felt sure that he owed this to the beefsteaks, the better he became in body, the more his conscience gave him no rest; two voices were for ever ringing in his ears—the one saying, ‘I am Common Sense and Nature; heed me, and I will reward you as I rewarded your fathers before you.’ But the other voice said: ‘Let not that plausible spirit lure you to your ruin. I am Duty; heed me, and I will reward you as I rewarded your fathers before you.’
他的健康状况一直在不断好转，虽然他确信这要归功于牛排，但他的身体越好，他的良心就越不安宁；有两个声音永远在他耳边响起——一个说：“我是常识和自然；另一个是：我是常识和自然”。听我说，我会奖赏你，就像我奖赏你的祖先一样。”但是另一个声音说：“不要让那个看似合理的精神引诱你走向灭亡。我是责任；听我说，我会奖赏你，就像我奖赏你的祖先一样。”

Sometimes he even seemed to see the faces of the speakers. Common Sense looked so easy, genial, and serene, so frank and fearless, that do what he might he could not mistrust her; but as he was on the point of following her, he would be checked by the austere face of Duty, so grave, but yet so kindly; and it cut him to the heart that from time to time he should see her turn pitying away from him as he followed after her rival.
有时他甚至似乎能看到说话者的脸。常识看起来那么轻松、和蔼、平静、坦率、无所畏惧，无论他做什么，他都不会不信任她。但当他正要跟着她时，他会被义务那张严肃的脸所制止，他是那么严肃，但又那么和蔼可亲。当他追随她的情敌时，他时不时会看到她对他表示同情，而他的心却感到刺痛。

The poor boy continually thought of the better class of his fellow- students, and tried to model his conduct on what he thought was theirs. ‘They,’ he said to himself, ‘eat a beefsteak? Never.’ But they most of them ate one now and again, unless it was a mutton chop that tempted them. And they used him for a model much as he did them. ‘He,’ they would say to themselves, ‘eat a mutton chop? Never.’ One night, however, he was followed by one of the authorities, who was always prowling about in search of law- breakers, and was caught coming out of the den with half a shoulder of mutton concealed about his person. On this, even though he had not been put in prison, he would have been sent away with his prospects in life irretrievably ruined; he therefore hanged himself as soon as he got home.
这个可怜的男孩不断地想着他的同学中更好的班级，并试图以他认为是他们的行为为榜样。 “他们，”他自言自语道，“吃牛排？从来没有。”但他们中的大多数人时不时地吃一块，除非是羊排吸引了他们。他们把他当作模特，就像他为他们做模特一样。 ‘他，’他们会自言自语地说，‘吃羊排？然而，一天晚上，他被一位一直在四处寻找违法者的当局跟踪，并在他身上藏着半块羊肩肉从窝里出来时被发现。这样一来，即使他不被关进监狱，他也会被送走，他的人生前途将无可挽回地毁掉；因此，他一回到家就上吊自杀了。

CHAPTER XXVII: THE VIEWS OF AN EREWHONIAN PHILOSOPHER CONCERNING
第二十七章：一位埃雷霍尼安哲学家的观点

THE RIGHTS OF VEGETABLES
蔬菜的权利

Let me leave this unhappy story, and return to the course of events among the Erewhonians at large. No matter how many laws they passed increasing the severity of the punishments inflicted on those who ate meat in secret, the people found means of setting them aside as fast as they were made. At times, indeed, they would become almost obsolete, but when they were on the point of being repealed, some national disaster or the preaching of some fanatic would reawaken the conscience of the nation, and people were imprisoned by the thousand for illicitly selling and buying animal food.
让我离开这个不幸的故事，回到整个埃雷洪尼亚人的事件过程。不管他们通过了多少法律，加重了对偷吃肉的人的惩罚，人们总是想方设法将其废除。确实，有时它们几乎已经过时了，但当它们即将被废除时，一些国家灾难或一些狂热分子的鼓吹会重新唤醒民族的良知，成千上万的人因非法出售和非法销售而被监禁。购买动物食品。

About six or seven hundred years, however, after the death of the old prophet, a philosopher appeared, who, though he did not claim to have any communication with an unseen power, laid down the law with as much confidence as if such a power had inspired him. Many think that this philosopher did not believe his own teaching, and, being in secret a great meat-eater, had no other end in view than reducing the prohibition against eating animal food to an absurdity, greater even than an Erewhonian Puritan would be able to stand.
然而，在老先知死后大约六七百年，出现了一位哲学家，虽然他没有声称自己与一种看不见的力量有任何联系，但他却充满信心地制定了法律，就好像这种力量一样启发了他。许多人认为这位哲学家不相信自己的教义，而且，作为一个秘密的肉食者，除了将禁止吃动物性食品的禁令降低到荒谬之外别无他法，甚至比埃雷洪清教徒所能做到的还要伟大。站起来。

Those who take this view hold that he knew how impossible it would be to get the nation to accept legislation that it held to be sinful; he knew also how hopeless it would be to convince people that it was not wicked to kill a sheep and eat it, unless he could show them that they must either sin to a certain extent, or die. He, therefore, it is believed, made the monstrous proposals of which I will now speak.
持这种观点的人认为，他知道让国家接受被认为是有罪的立法是多么不可能。他也知道要让人们相信杀羊并吃它并不邪恶是多么无望，除非他能向人们表明，他们要么犯罪到一定程度，要么就死。因此，据信他提出了我现在要谈到的可怕建议。

He began by paying a tribute of profound respect to the old prophet, whose advocacy of the rights of animals, he admitted, had done much to soften the national character, and enlarge its views about the sanctity of life in general. But he urged that times had now changed; the lesson of which the country had stood in need had been sufficiently learnt, while as regards vegetables much had become known that was not even suspected formerly, and which, if the nation was to persevere in that strict adherence to the highest moral principles which had been the secret of its prosperity hitherto, must necessitate a radical change in its attitude towards them.
他首先向这位老先知表示深深的敬意，他承认，这位老先知对动物权利的倡导极大地软化了国民性格，并扩大了人们对生命神圣性的看法。但他强调，时代已经变了。这个国家所需要的教训已经得到了充分的吸取，而关于蔬菜，许多以前甚至没有被怀疑过的知识已经变得众所周知，如果这个国家坚持严格遵守最高的道德原则，那么这些原则就已经得到了充分的认识。迄今为止，这一直是其繁荣的秘密，因此必须彻底改变对它们的态度。

It was indeed true that much was now known that had not been suspected formerly, for the people had had no foreign enemies, and, being both quick-witted and inquisitive into the mysteries of nature, had made extraordinary progress in all the many branches of art and science. In the chief Erewhonian museum I was shown a microscope of considerable power, that was ascribed by the authorities to a date much about that of the philosopher of whom I am now speaking, and was even supposed by some to have been the instrument with which he had actually worked.
确实，现在已经知道了许多以前未曾怀疑过的事情，因为人民没有外敌，而且对自然的奥秘既机智又好奇，在科学的各个领域都取得了非凡的进步。艺术和科学。在埃雷洪尼亚主要博物馆里，我看到了一台具有相当大功率的显微镜，当局认为这台显微镜的年代与我现在所说的这位哲学家的年代相当，甚至有些人认为它是他使用的工具。实际上已经起作用了。

This philosopher was Professor of botany in the chief seat of learning then in Erewhon, and whether with the help of the microscope still preserved, or with another, had arrived at a conclusion now universally accepted among ourselves—I mean, that all, both animals and plants, have had a common ancestry, and that hence the second should be deemed as much alive as the first. He contended, therefore, that animals and plants were cousins, and would have been seen to be so, all along, if people had not made an arbitrary and unreasonable division between what they chose to call the animal and vegetable kingdoms.
这位哲学家是埃里洪当时主要学府的植物学教授，无论是借助仍然保存下来的显微镜，还是借助其他显微镜，他都得出了现在我们普遍接受的结论——我的意思是，所有动物，包括动物和植物都有共同的祖先，因此第二个应该被认为与第一个一样有生命力。因此，他认为，动物和植物是近亲，如果人们没有在他们选择的动物界和植物界之间进行武断和不合理的划分，那么人们一直都会认为动物和植物是表亲。

He declared, and demonstrated to the satisfaction of all those who were able to form an opinion upon the subject, that there is no difference appreciable either by the eye, or by any other test, between a germ that will develop into an oak, a vine, a rose, and one that (given its accustomed surroundings) will become a mouse, an elephant, or a man.
他宣称，并让所有能够就这个问题形成意见的人都满意地证明，无论是通过肉眼还是通过任何其他测试，在将发育成橡树的胚芽与将要发育成橡树的胚芽之间都没有明显的区别。藤蔓，一朵玫瑰，还有一朵（考虑到它习惯的环境）会变成一只老鼠、一头大象或一个人。

He contended that the course of any germ’s development was dictated by the habits of the germs from which it was descended and of whose identity it had once formed part. If a germ found itself placed as the germs in the line of its ancestry were placed, it would do as its ancestors had done, and grow up into the same kind of organism as theirs. If it found the circumstances only a little different, it would make shift (successfully or unsuccessfully) to modify its development accordingly; if the circumstances were widely different, it would die, probably without an effort at self- adaptation. This, he argued, applied equally to the germs of plants and of animals.
他认为，任何细菌的发育过程都是由它所起源的细菌的习性决定的，并且它曾经是细菌身份的一部分。如果一个细菌发现自己的位置与它祖先谱系中的细菌的位置相同，它就会像它的祖先所做的那样，成长为与祖先相同的有机体。如果它发现情况只有一点点不同，它就会做出相应的转变（成功或不成功）来修改其发展；如果环境差异很大，它可能会死亡，可能不需要自我适应的努力。他认为，这同样适用于植物和动物的细菌。

He therefore connected all, both animal and vegetable development, with intelligence, either spent and now unconscious, or still unspent and conscious; and in support of his view as regards vegetable life, he pointed to the way in which all plants have adapted themselves to their habitual environment. Granting that vegetable intelligence at first sight appears to differ materially from animal, yet, he urged, it is like it in the one essential fact that though it has evidently busied itself about matters that are vital to the well-being of the organism that possesses it, it has never shown the slightest tendency to occupy itself with anything else. This, he insisted, is as great a proof of intelligence as any living being can give.
因此，他将一切，无论是动物还是植物的发育，都与智力联系起来，无论是已消耗的、现在无意识的，还是尚未消耗的、有意识的。为了支持他关于植物生命的观点，他指出了所有植物适应其惯常环境的方式。乍一看，植物的智力似乎与动物有本质上的不同，然而，他敦促说，在一个基本事实上，植物的智力与动物是相似的，即尽管它显然忙于那些对拥有该智力的有机体的福祉至关重要的事情。它从来没有表现出丝毫忙于其他事情的倾向。他坚持认为，这是任何生物所能提供的最有力的智力证明。

‘Plants,’ said he, ‘show no sign of interesting themselves in human affairs. We shall never get a rose to understand that five times seven are thirty-five, and there is no use in talking to an oak about fluctuations in the price of stocks. Hence we say that the oak and the rose are unintelligent, and on finding that they do not understand our business conclude that they do not understand their own. But what can a creature who talks in this way know about intelligence? Which shows greater signs of intelligence? He, or the rose and oak?
“植物，”他说，“没有表现出对人类事务感兴趣的迹象。我们永远不会让玫瑰明白五乘七等于三十五，与橡树谈论股票价格的波动是没有用的。因此，我们说橡树和玫瑰是不聪明的，当发现它们不理解我们的事情时，就得出结论，它们不理解自己的事情。但以这种方式说话的生物能了解什么智慧呢？哪个显示出更大的智力迹象？他，还是玫瑰和橡树？

‘And when we call plants stupid for not understanding our business, how capable do we show ourselves of understanding theirs? Can we form even the faintest conception of the way in which a seed from a rose-tree turns earth, air, warmth and water into a rose full- blown? Where does it get its colour from? From the earth, air, &c.? Yes—but how? Those petals of such ineffable texture—that hue that outvies the cheek of a child—that scent again? Look at earth, air, and water—these are all the raw material that the rose has got to work with; does it show any sign of want of intelligence in the alchemy with which it turns mud into rose-leaves? What chemist can do anything comparable? Why does no one try? Simply because every one knows that no human intelligence is equal to the task. We give it up. It is the rose’s department; let the rose attend to it—and be dubbed unintelligent because it baffles us by the miracles it works, and the unconcerned business-like way in which it works them.
“当我们称植物不了解我们的业务而愚蠢时，我们有多大能力了解它们的业务？我们能否对玫瑰树上的一颗种子如何将泥土、空气、温暖和水变成一朵盛开的玫瑰产生哪怕是最微弱的概念？它的颜色从何而来？来自地球、空气等等？是的，但如何？那些花瓣有着难以形容的质感——那种颜色胜过了孩子的脸颊——又是那种香味？看看地球、空气和水——这些都是玫瑰必须使用的原材料；它是否表现出在将泥土变成玫瑰叶的炼金术方面缺乏智慧的迹象？哪个化学家可以做出类似的事情？为什么没有人尝试？原因很简单，因为每个人都知道没有任何人类智慧能够胜任这项任务。我们放弃它。这是玫瑰的部门；让玫瑰来处理它——并被称为“不聪明”，因为它所创造的奇迹以及它所表现出的冷漠的公事方式让我们感到困惑。

‘See what pains, again, plants take to protect themselves against their enemies. They scratch, cut, sting, make bad smells, secrete the most dreadful poisons (which Heaven only knows how they contrive to make), cover their precious seeds with spines like those of a hedgehog, frighten insects with delicate nervous systems by assuming portentous shapes, hide themselves, grow in inaccessible places, and tell lies so plausibly as to deceive even their subtlest foes.
“再看看植物为了保护自己免受敌人侵害而付出了多大的努力。它们抓伤、割伤、蜇人，发出难闻的气味，分泌最可怕的毒药（只有天知道它们是如何制造的），用像刺猬一样的刺覆盖珍贵的种子，通过呈现不祥的形状来吓唬神经系统脆弱的昆虫，隐藏自己，生长在人迹罕至的地方，并且说谎得如此振聋发聩，甚至可以欺骗最狡猾的敌人。

‘They lay traps smeared with bird-lime, to catch insects, and persuade them to drown themselves in pitchers which they have made of their leaves, and fill with water; others make themselves, as it were, into living rat-traps, which close with a spring on any insect that settles upon them; others make their flowers into the shape of a certain fly that is a great pillager of honey, so that when the real fly comes it thinks that the flowers are bespoke, and goes on elsewhere. Some are so clever as even to overreach themselves, like the horse-radish, which gets pulled up and eaten for the sake of that pungency with which it protects itself against underground enemies. If, on the other hand, they think that any insect can be of service to them, see how pretty they make themselves.
“他们设置了涂有粘鸟胶的陷阱来捕捉昆虫，并说服它们把自己淹死在用叶子制成的水罐里，并装满水；其他人则把自己变成了活生生的捕鼠器，用弹簧将任何落在其上的昆虫封闭起来。有些人把花做成某种苍蝇的形状，这种苍蝇是蜂蜜的大掠夺者，所以当真正的苍蝇来时，它认为这些花是定制的，然后去别处。有些人很聪明，甚至超出了自己的范围，就像辣根一样，人们把辣根拔出来吃掉，因为它的辛辣味可以保护自己免受地下敌人的侵害。另一方面，如果他们认为任何昆虫都可以为他们服务，看看他们把自己打扮得多么漂亮。

‘What is to be intelligent if to know how to do what one wants to do, and to do it repeatedly, is not to be intelligent? Some say that the rose-seed does not want to grow into a rose-bush. Why, then, in the name of all that is reasonable, does it grow? Likely enough it is unaware of the want that is spurring it on to action. We have no reason to suppose that a human embryo knows that it wants to grow into a baby, or a baby into a man. Nothing ever shows signs of knowing what it is either wanting or doing, when its convictions both as to what it wants, and how to get it, have been settled beyond further power of question. The less signs living creatures give of knowing what they do, provided they do it, and do it repeatedly and well, the greater proof they give that in reality they know how to do it, and have done it already on an infinite number of past occasions.
“如果知道如何做自己想做的事，并且不断地做，这不是聪明吗？”有人说玫瑰种子不想长成玫瑰丛。那么，以一切合理的名义，为什么它会增长呢？它很可能没有意识到促使其采取行动的需求。我们没有理由假设人类胚胎知道它想要成长为婴儿，或者婴儿想要成长为男人。当它对于自己想要什么以及如何得到它的信念已经确定，超出了进一步质疑的范围时，就没有任何迹象表明它知道它想要什么或正在做什么。生物体表现出的知道自己在做什么的迹象越少，只要它们这样做，并且反复地做得很好，它们就越能证明它们实际上知道如何做，并且已经在过去无数次中做到了这一点。场合。

‘Some one may say,’ he continued, ‘‘What do you mean by talking about an infinite number of past occasions? When did a rose-seed make itself into a rose-bush on any past occasion?’
“有人可能会说，”他继续说道，“你谈论无数的过去事件是什么意思？过去什么时候玫瑰种子会长成玫瑰丛？

‘I answer this question with another. ‘Did the rose-seed ever form part of the identity of the rose-bush on which it grew?’ Who can say that it did not? Again I ask: ‘Was this rose-bush ever linked by all those links that we commonly consider as constituting personal identity, with the seed from which it in its turn grew?’ Who can say that it was not?
‘我用另一个问题来回答这个问题。 “玫瑰种子是否曾经构成它所生长的玫瑰丛的身份的一部分？”谁能说它没有呢？我再次问：“这朵玫瑰花丛是否曾被我们通常认为构成个人身份的所有联系所联系在一起，以及它所生长的种子？”谁能说不是呢？

‘Then, if rose-seed number two is a continuation of the personality of its parent rose-bush, and if that rose-bush is a continuation of the personality of the rose-seed from which it sprang, rose-seed number two must also be a continuation of the personality of the earlier rose-seed. And this rose-seed must be a continuation of the personality of the preceding rose-seed—and so back and back ad infinitum. Hence it is impossible to deny continued personality between any existing rose-seed and the earliest seed that can be called a rose-seed at all.
“那么，如果二号玫瑰种子是其亲本玫瑰丛的个性的延续，并且如果该玫瑰丛是它所发芽的玫瑰种子的个性的延续，那么二号玫瑰种子必须也是早期玫瑰种子个性的延续。而这颗玫瑰种子必定是前一颗玫瑰种子的个性的延续—​​—如此循环往复，无穷无尽。因此，不可能否认任何现有的玫瑰种子和最早的可以称为玫瑰种子的种子之间存在连续的个性。

‘The answer, then, to our objector is not far to seek. The rose- seed did what it now does in the persons of its ancestors—to whom it has been so linked as to be able to remember what those ancestors did when they were placed as the rose-seed now is. Each stage of development brings back the recollection of the course taken in the preceding stage, and the development has been so often repeated, that all doubt—and with all doubt, all consciousness of action—is suspended.
“那么，对于我们的反对者来说，答案并不遥远。玫瑰种子在其祖先身上做了现在所做的事情——它与祖先的联系如此紧密，以至于能够记住那些祖先在被放置为现在的玫瑰种子时所做的事情。发展的每一个阶段都会带回对前一阶段所经历的过程的回忆，而且这种发展经常被重复，以至于所有的怀疑——以及所有的怀疑，所有的行动意识——都被悬置了。

‘But an objector may still say, ‘Granted that the linking between all successive generations has been so close and unbroken, that each one of them may be conceived as able to remember what it did in the persons of its ancestors—how do you show that it actually did remember?’
“但是反对者仍然可能会说，‘假设所有连续几代人之间的联系是如此紧密和不间断，以至于他们中的每一个人都可以被认为能够记住它在其祖先身上所做的事情——你如何表明它真的记得吗？

‘The answer is: ‘By the action which each generation takes—an action which repeats all the phenomena that we commonly associate with memory—which is explicable on the supposition that it has been guided by memory—and which has neither been explained, nor seems ever likely to be explained on any other theory than the supposition that there is an abiding memory between successive generations.’
答案是：“通过每一代人所采取的行动——重复我们通常与记忆联系在一起的所有现象的行动——这是可以解释的，假设它是由记忆引导的——而且既没有被解释，也没有被解释。除了连续几代人之间存在持久记忆的假设之外，似乎任何其他理论都可以解释这一点。

‘Will any one bring an example of any living creature whose action we can understand, performing an ineffably difficult and intricate action, time after time, with invariable success, and yet not knowing how to do it, and never having done it before? Show me the example and I will say no more, but until it is shown me, I shall credit action where I cannot watch it, with being controlled by the same laws as when it is within our ken. It will become unconscious as soon as the skill that directs it has become perfected. Neither rose-seed, therefore, nor embryo should be expected to show signs of knowing that they know what they know—if they showed such signs the fact of their knowing what they want, and how to get it, might more reasonably be doubted.’
“有人能举出一个我们可以理解其行为的生物的例子吗？它一次又一次地执行一种难以形容的困难和复杂的行为，并且总是成功，但不知道如何去做，而且以前从未做过吗？”给我看这个例子，我不会再多说了，但在它向我展示之前，我将相信我看不到的行动，与在我们的知识范围内时受到相同法律的控制。一旦指挥它的技能变得完善，它就会变得无意识。因此，无论是玫瑰种子还是胚胎，都不应该表现出知道自己知道什么的迹象——如果它们表现出这样的迹象，那么他们知道自己想要什么以及如何得到它的事实可能会更合理地受到怀疑。 '

Some of the passages already given in Chapter XXIII were obviously inspired by the one just quoted. As I read it, in a reprint shown me by a Professor who had edited much of the early literature on the subject, I could not but remember the one in which our Lord tells His disciples to consider the lilies of the field, who neither toil nor spin, but whose raiment surpasses even that of Solomon in all his glory.
第二十三章中已经给出的一些段落显然是受到刚才引用的段落的启发。当我读到这本书时，在一位编辑过许多关于这个主题的早期文献的教授给我看的重印本中，我不禁想起我们的主在其中告诉他的门徒要考虑田野里的百合花，他们既不劳苦，也不劳苦。也不纺纱，但他的衣饰甚至胜过所罗门的荣耀。

‘They toil not, neither do they spin?’ Is that so? ‘Toil not?’ Perhaps not, now that the method of procedure is so well known as to admit of no further question—but it is not likely that lilies came to make themselves so beautifully without having ever taken any pains about the matter. ‘Neither do they spin?’ Not with a spinning-wheel; but is there no textile fabric in a leaf?
“它们不劳作，也不纺纱？”是这样吗？ “不辛苦吗？”也许不是，既然程序方法已经众所周知，不容再提出任何进一步的问题，但百合花不太可能在没有付出任何努力的情况下使自己变得如此美丽。 “它们也不旋转？” 不是用纺车；但叶子里没有纺织物吗？

What would the lilies of the field say if they heard one of us declaring that they neither toil nor spin? They would say, I take it, much what we should if we were to hear of their preaching humility on the text of Solomons, and saying, ‘Consider the Solomons in all their glory, they toil not neither do they spin.’ We should say that the lilies were talking about things that they did not understand, and that though the Solomons do not toil nor spin, yet there had been no lack of either toiling or spinning before they came to be arrayed so gorgeously.
如果田野里的百合花听到我们中的一个人宣称它们既不劳作也不纺纱，它们会怎么说呢？他们会说，我想，如果我们听到他们在所罗门书的经文中谦卑地宣讲，并说：“想想所罗门王的一切荣耀，他们不劳苦，也不纺织。”我们应该这样说。说百合花在谈论它们不明白的事情，虽然所罗门人不劳作也不纺纱，但在他们打扮得如此华丽之前，也不乏劳作或纺纱。

Let me now return to the Professor. I have said enough to show the general drift of the arguments on which he relied in order to show that vegetables are only animals under another name, but have not stated his case in anything like the fullness with which he laid it before the public. The conclusion he drew, or pretended to draw, was that if it was sinful to kill and eat animals, it was not less sinful to do the like by vegetables, or their seeds. None such, he said, should be eaten, save what had died a natural death, such as fruit that was lying on the ground and about to rot, or cabbage- leaves that had turned yellow in late autumn. These and other like garbage he declared to be the only food that might be eaten with a clear conscience. Even so the eater must plant the pips of any apples or pears that he may have eaten, or any plum-stones, cherry- stones, and the like, or he would come near to incurring the guilt of infanticide. The grain of cereals, according to him, was out of the question, for every such grain had a living soul as much as man had, and had as good a right as man to possess that soul in peace.
现在让我回到教授身上。我已经说了足够多的内容来表明他所依据的论点的总体倾向，以证明蔬菜只是动物的另一个名称，但还没有像他向公众展示时那样充分地阐述他的观点。他得出的结论，或者假装得出的结论是，如果杀死和吃动物是有罪的，那么用蔬菜或其种子做同样的事情也同样有罪。他说，这样的东西不应该吃，除非自然死亡的东西，比如躺在地上即将腐烂的水果，或者深秋变黄的卷心菜叶子。他宣称这些和其他垃圾一样是唯一可以问心无愧地食用的食物。即便如此，食用者也必须种植他可能吃过的任何苹果或梨的果核，或者任何李子核、樱桃核等，否则他将几乎犯下杀婴罪。在他看来，谷物是不可能的，因为每一种谷物都像人一样有一个活生生的灵魂，并且和人一样有权利平静地拥有这个灵魂。

Having thus driven his fellow countrymen into a corner at the point of a logical bayonet from which they felt that there was no escape, he proposed that the question what was to be done should be referred to an oracle in which the whole country had the greatest confidence, and to which recourse was always had in times of special perplexity. It was whispered that a near relation of the philosopher’s was lady’s-maid to the priestess who delivered the oracle, and the Puritan party declared that the strangely unequivocal answer of the oracle was obtained by backstairs influence; but whether this was so or no, the response as nearly as I can translate it was as follows:-
就这样，他的同胞们被逼入了一个逻辑刺刀的角落，他们感到无处可逃，他建议，应该做什么的问题应该交给一个神谕，在这个神谕中，整个国家都拥有最伟大的知识。信心，在特别困惑的时候总是可以求助于信心。据传，这位哲学家的近亲是那位发表神谕的女祭司的女仆，而清教徒则宣称，神谕的奇怪而明确的答案是通过幕后影响力获得的。但无论事实是否如此，我所能翻译的答复如下：-

‘He who sins aught Sins more than he ought; But he who sins nought Has much to be taught. Beat or be beaten, Eat or be eaten, Be killed or kill; Choose which you will.’
‘凡犯罪者，其罪过过重；但那些无罪的人却有很多值得教导的地方。打还是被打，吃还是被吃，被杀还是被杀；选择你愿意的。

It was clear that this response sanctioned at any rate the destruction of vegetable life when wanted as food by man; and so forcibly had the philosopher shown that what was sauce for vegetables was so also for animals, that, though the Puritan party made a furious outcry, the acts forbidding the use of meat were repealed by a considerable majority. Thus, after several hundred years of wandering in the wilderness of philosophy, the country reached the conclusions that common sense had long since arrived at. Even the Puritans after a vain attempt to subsist on a kind of jam made of apples and yellow cabbage leaves, succumbed to the inevitable, and resigned themselves to a diet of roast beef and mutton, with all the usual adjuncts of a modern dinner-table.
很明显，这种反应无论如何都允许在人类想要作为食物时破坏植物生命。这位哲学家如此有力地表明，蔬菜的酱汁也适用于动物，因此，尽管清教徒党提出了强烈的抗议，但禁止使用肉类的法案还是被相当多的人废除了。于是，在哲学的荒野中徘徊了数百年之后，这个国家得出了常识早已得出的结论。即使是清教徒，在徒劳地尝试靠苹果和黄甘蓝叶制成的果酱维持生计后，也屈服于不可避免的事实，只吃烤牛肉和烤羊肉，以及现代餐桌上所有常见的佐料。 。

One would have thought that the dance they had been led by the old prophet, and that still madder dance which the Professor of botany had gravely, but as I believe insidiously, proposed to lead them, would have made the Erewhonians for a long time suspicious of prophets whether they professed to have communications with an unseen power or no; but so engrained in the human heart is the desire to believe that some people really do know what they say they know, and can thus save them from the trouble of thinking for themselves, that in a short time would-be philosophers and faddists became more powerful than ever, and gradually led their countrymen to accept all those absurd views of life, some account of which I have given in my earlier chapters. Indeed I can see no hope for the Erewhonians till they have got to understand that reason uncorrected by instinct is as bad as instinct uncorrected by reason.
人们可能会认为，他们由老先知领导的舞蹈，以及植物学教授严肃地、但我相信是阴险地提议领导他们的、仍然更疯狂的舞蹈，会让埃雷洪尼亚人在很长一段时间内产生怀疑。先知是否声称与看不见的力量有联系；但是，人们内心根深蒂固地渴望相信，有些人确实知道他们所说的知道的事情，从而可以使他们免于自己思考的麻烦，因此在很短的时间内，未来的哲学家和时尚主义者就变得更加坚定。比以往任何时候都更强大，并逐渐引导他们的同胞接受所有这些荒谬的人生观，我在前面的章节中对此进行了一些描述。事实上，我看不到埃雷洪人有任何希望，除非他们明白未经本能纠正的理性与未经理性纠正的本能一样糟糕。

CHAPTER XXVIII: ESCAPE
第二十八章：逃跑

Though busily engaged in translating the extracts given in the last five chapters, I was also laying matters in train for my escape with Arowhena. And indeed it was high time, for I received an intimation from one of the cashiers of the Musical Banks, that I was to be prosecuted in a criminal court ostensibly for measles, but really for having owned a watch, and attempted the reintroduction of machinery.
虽然我忙着翻译最后五章的摘录，但我也在为我和阿罗菲娜的逃跑做准备。事实上，现在正是时候，因为我收到音乐银行收银员的暗示，我将在刑事法庭受到起诉，表面上是因为麻疹，但实际上是因为拥有一块手表，并试图重新引入机械。

I asked why measles? and was told that there was a fear lest extenuating circumstances should prevent a jury from convicting me, if I were indicted for typhus or small-pox, but that a verdict would probably be obtained for measles, a disease which could be sufficiently punished in a person of my age. I was given to understand that unless some unexpected change should come over the mind of his Majesty, I might expect the blow to be struck within a very few days.
我问为什么会得麻疹？并被告知，如果我因斑疹伤寒或天花被起诉，陪审团可能会因情有可原的情况而无法对我定罪，但可能会因麻疹而做出判决，麻疹是一种可以在刑事案件中受到充分惩罚的疾病。与我同龄的人。我被告知，除非陛下的想法发生了一些意想不到的变化，否则我可能会在几天之内受到打击。

My plan was this—that Arowhena and I should escape in a balloon together. I fear that the reader will disbelieve this part of my story, yet in no other have I endeavoured to adhere more conscientiously to facts, and can only throw myself upon his charity.
我的计划是这样的——阿罗维娜和我一起乘气球逃走。我担心读者会不相信我故事的这一部分，但在其他故事中我并没有努力更认真地坚持事实，只能依靠他的慈善。

I had already gained the ear of the Queen, and had so worked upon her curiosity that she promised to get leave for me to have a balloon made and inflated; I pointed out to her that no complicated machinery would be wanted—nothing, in fact, but a large quantity of oiled silk, a car, a few ropes, &c., &c., and some light kind of gas, such as the antiquarians who were acquainted with the means employed by the ancients for the production of the lighter gases could easily instruct her workmen how to provide. Her eagerness to see so strange a sight as the ascent of a human being into the sky overcame any scruples of conscience that she might have otherwise felt, and she set the antiquarians about showing her workmen how to make the gas, and sent her maids to buy, and oil, a very large quantity of silk (for I was determined that the balloon should be a big one) even before she began to try and gain the King’s permission; this, however, she now set herself to do, for I had sent her word that my prosecution was imminent.
我已经引起了女王的注意，并且充分激发了她的好奇心，以至于她答应让我制作一个气球并为其充气。我向她指出，不需要复杂的机械——事实上，什么都不需要，只是大量的涂油丝绸、一辆汽车、几根绳子等等，以及一些轻质气体，例如古物。熟悉古人用来生产打火机气体的方法的人可以轻松地指导她的工人如何提供。她渴望看到人类升入天空这样奇怪的景象，克服了她原本可能感受到的任何良心顾虑，她让古物学家向她的工人们展示如何制造气体，并派她的女仆去甚至在她开始尝试获得国王的许可之前，就购买了大量的丝绸并上油（因为我决定气球应该很大）；然而，她现在决定这样做，因为我已经向她传达了我即将被起诉的消息。

As for myself, I need hardly say that I knew nothing about balloons; nor did I see my way to smuggling Arowhena into the car; nevertheless, knowing that we had no other chance of getting away from Erewhon, I drew inspiration from the extremity in which we were placed, and made a pattern from which the Queen’s workmen were able to work successfully. Meanwhile the Queen’s carriage-builders set about making the car, and it was with the attachments of this to the balloon that I had the greatest difficulty; I doubt, indeed, whether I should have succeeded here, but for the great intelligence of a foreman, who threw himself heart and soul into the matter, and often both foresaw requirements, the necessity for which had escaped me, and suggested the means of providing for them.
至于我自己，不用说我对气球一无所知。我也没有找到将阿罗菲娜偷偷塞进车里的方法。尽管如此，我知道我们没有其他机会离开埃瑞翁，所以我从我们所处的绝境中汲取了灵感，并制作了一个模型，女王的工人能够根据这个模型成功地工作。与此同时，女王的马车制造商开始制造汽车，而我遇到最大的困难是将其固定在气球上。事实上，我怀疑我是否会在这里取得成功，如果没有一位工头的伟大智慧，他全心全意地投入到这件事中，并且常常预见到我没有意识到的必要性，并提出了解决问题的方法。为他们提供服务。

It happened that there had been a long drought, during the latter part of which prayers had been vainly offered up in all the temples of the air god. When I first told her Majesty that I wanted a balloon, I said my intention was to go up into the sky and prevail upon the air god by means of a personal interview. I own that this proposition bordered on the idolatrous, but I have long since repented of it, and am little likely ever to repeat the offence. Moreover the deceit, serious though it was, will probably lead to the conversion of the whole country.
恰巧发生了一场长期的干旱，干旱的后期，所有的空气神殿都祈祷无果。当我第一次告诉女王陛下我想要一个气球时，我说我的目的是飞上天空，通过个人采访的方式征服空中之神。我承认这个主张近乎偶像崇拜，但我早已为此悔改，并且不太可能重蹈覆辙。此外，这种欺骗虽然很严重，但很可能会导致整个国家的转变。

When the Queen told his Majesty of my proposal, he at first not only ridiculed it, but was inclined to veto it. Being, however, a very uxorious husband, he at length consented—as he eventually always did to everything on which the Queen had set her heart. He yielded all the more readily now, because he did not believe in the possibility of my ascent; he was convinced that even though the balloon should mount a few feet into the air, it would collapse immediately, whereon I should fall and break my neck, and he should be rid of me. He demonstrated this to her so convincingly, that she was alarmed, and tried to talk me into giving up the idea, but on finding that I persisted in my wish to have the balloon made, she produced an order from the King to the effect that all facilities I might require should be afforded me.
当女王将我的提议告诉国王陛下时，他起初不仅嘲笑它，而且倾向于否决它。然而，作为一个非常奢侈的丈夫，他最终同意了——正如他最终总是对女王所下定决心的一切所做的那样。他现在更加屈服了，因为他不相信我有上升的可能性。他确信，即使气球升到空中几英尺，它也会立即塌陷，我就会掉下来，折断脖子，他就应该摆脱我。他如此令人信服地向她展示了这一点，令她感到震惊，并试图说服我放弃这个想法，但当她发现我坚持制作气球的愿望时，她出示了国王的命令，大意是：我应该提供我可能需要的所有设施。

At the same time her Majesty told me that my attempted ascent would be made an article of impeachment against me in case I did not succeed in prevailing on the air god to stop the drought. Neither King nor Queen had any idea that I meant going right away if I could get the wind to take me, nor had he any conception of the existence of a certain steady upper current of air which was always setting in one direction, as could be seen by the shape of the higher clouds, which pointed invariably from south-east to north- west. I had myself long noticed this peculiarity in the climate, and attributed it, I believe justly, to a trade-wind which was constant at a few thousand feet above the earth, but was disturbed by local influences at lower elevations.
与此同时，女王陛下告诉我，如果我不能成功说服空中之神来阻止干旱，我的登顶尝试将成为对我的弹劾条款。国王和王后都不知道我的意思是如果我能让风带我就立即出发，他也不知道存在某种稳定的上层气流，这种气流总是朝一个方向流动，就像可能的那样。从较高云层的形状可以看出，这些云层总是从东南指向西北。我自己很早就注意到了气候的这种特殊性，并将其归因于信风，我相信这是公正的，信风在距地球数千英尺的地方持续存在，但在较低海拔处受到当地影响的干扰。

My next business was to break the plan to Arowhena, and to devise the means for getting her into the car. I felt sure that she would come with me, but had made up my mind that if her courage failed her, the whole thing should come to nothing. Arowhena and I had been in constant communication through her maid, but I had thought it best not to tell her the details of my scheme till everything was settled. The time had now arrived, and I arranged with the maid that I should be admitted by a private door into Mr. Nosnibor’s garden at about dusk on the following evening.
我的下一个任务是打破阿罗菲娜的计划，并想出办法让她上车。我确信她会和我一起去，但我已经下定决心，如果她失去了勇气，那么整个事情就会失败。阿罗维娜和我一直通过她的女仆保持着联系，但我认为在一切都解决之前最好不要告诉她我计划的细节。现在时间已经到了，我和女仆约定，第二天晚上黄昏时分，我可以从一扇私人门进入诺斯尼伯先生的花园。

I came at the appointed time; the girl let me into the garden and bade me wait in a secluded alley until Arowhena should come. It was now early summer, and the leaves were so thick upon the trees that even though some one else had entered the garden I could have easily hidden myself. The night was one of extreme beauty; the sun had long set, but there was still a rosy gleam in the sky over the ruins of the railway station; below me was the city already twinkling with lights, while beyond it stretched the plains for many a league until they blended with the sky. I just noted these things, but I could not heed them. I could heed nothing, till, as I peered into the darkness of the alley, I perceived a white figure gliding swiftly towards me. I bounded towards it, and ere thought could either prompt or check, I had caught Arowhena to my heart and covered her unresisting cheek with kisses.
我按照约定的时间来了；女孩让我进入花园，并让我在一条僻静的小巷里等待，直到阿罗菲娜到来。现在是初夏，树上的叶子很厚，即使有人进入花园，我也可以轻松隐藏自己。夜晚极其美丽。太阳早已落山了，但火车站废墟上空的天空仍然闪烁着玫瑰色的光芒。在我下方，这座城市已经闪烁着灯光，而在它之外，平原绵延数里，直到与天空融为一体。我只是注意到这些事情，但我无法留意它们。我什么也没有注意到，直到当我凝视着小巷的黑暗时，我发现一个白色的人影迅速向我滑来。我跳向它，还没来得及思考或阻止，我就抓住了阿罗芙娜的心，亲吻了她毫无抵抗力的脸颊。

So overjoyed were we that we knew not how to speak; indeed I do not know when we should have found words and come to our senses, if the maid had not gone off into a fit of hysterics, and awakened us to the necessity of self-control; then, briefly and plainly, I unfolded what I proposed; I showed her the darkest side, for I felt sure that the darker the prospect the more likely she was to come. I told her that my plan would probably end in death for both of us, and that I dared not press it—that at a word from her it should be abandoned; still that there was just a possibility of our escaping together to some part of the world where there would be no bar to our getting married, and that I could see no other hope.
我们高兴得不知如何言语。事实上，如果女仆没有歇斯底里，唤醒我们认识到自我控制的必要性，我真不知道我们什么时候才能找到言语并清醒过来。然后，我简单明了地阐述了我的提议；我向她展示了最黑暗的一面，因为我确信前景越黑暗，她就越有可能来。我告诉她，我的计划很可能会导致我们双双死亡，而且我不敢强求——只要她一句话，就应该放弃；尽管如此，我们还是有可能一起逃到世界上某个地方，在那里我们的结婚不会受到任何阻碍，而且我看不到其他希望。

She made no resistance, not a sign or hint of doubt or hesitation. She would do all I told her, and come whenever I was ready; so I bade her send her maid to meet me nightly—told her that she must put a good face on, look as bright and happy as she could, so as to make her father and mother and Zulora think that she was forgetting me—and be ready at a moment’s notice to come to the Queen’s workshops, and be concealed among the ballast and under rugs in the car of the balloon; and so we parted.
她没有做出任何抵抗，没有任何怀疑或犹豫的迹象或暗示。她会做我告诉她的一切，只要我准备好就来。于是我吩咐她派她的女仆每晚来见我——告诉她一定要摆出一副好脸色，尽量让自己看起来开朗快乐，这样才能让她的爸爸、妈妈和祖罗拉以为她把我忘了——然后立即准备好前往女王的工作室，并隐藏在热气球车内的镇流器和地毯下；于是我们分手了。

I hurried my preparations forward, for I feared rain, and also that the King might change his mind; but the weather continued dry, and in another week the Queen’s workmen had finished the balloon and car, while the gas was ready to be turned on into the balloon at any moment. All being now prepared I was to ascend on the following morning. I had stipulated for being allowed to take abundance of rugs and wrappings as protection from the cold of the upper atmosphere, and also ten or a dozen good-sized bags of ballast.
我加快了准备工作，因为我担心下雨，也担心国王会改变主意。但天气仍然干燥，又过了一周，女王的工人就完成了气球和汽车，同时也准备好随时向气球中通气。现在一切准备就绪，我将在第二天早上登顶。我规定可以携带大量的地毯和包装材料来抵御高层大气的寒冷，还有十袋或一打大袋的镇重物。
