I had nearly a quarter’s pension in hand, and with this I fee’d Arowhena’s maid, and bribed the Queen’s foreman—who would, I believe, have given me assistance even without a bribe. He helped me to secrete food and wine in the bags of ballast, and on the morning of my ascent he kept the other workmen out of the way while I got Arowhena into the car. She came with early dawn, muffled up, and in her maid’s dress. She was supposed to be gone to an early performance at one of the Musical Banks, and told me that she should not be missed till breakfast, but that her absence must then be discovered. I arranged the ballast about her so that it should conceal her as she lay at the bottom of the car, and covered her with wrappings. Although it still wanted some hours of the time fixed for my ascent, I could not trust myself one moment from the car, so I got into it at once, and watched the gradual inflation of the balloon. Luggage I had none, save the provisions hidden in the ballast bags, the books of mythology, and the treatises on the machines, with my own manuscript diaries and translations.
我手里有近四分之一的养老金，用这笔钱我招待了阿罗维娜的女仆，并贿赂了女王的工头——我相信，即使没有贿赂，他也会给我帮助。他帮助我将食物和酒装入压舱物袋中，在我攀登的那天早上，当我把阿罗维娜带进车时，他让其他工人不碍事。她天刚蒙蒙亮就来了，穿着女仆装，裹得严严实实的。她本来应该去一家音乐银行观看一场早场演出，并告诉我早餐前不要错过她，但必须在那时发现她的缺席。我把镇流器放在她周围，这样当她躺在车底时，镇流器就能遮住她，并用包裹物盖住她。虽然还需要几个小时的固定时间让我上升，但我在车上一刻都不敢相信自己，所以我立刻钻了进去，看着气球逐渐膨胀。我什么行李都没有，除了压载袋里藏着的给养、神话书籍、机器论文、我自己的手稿日记和翻译。

I sat quietly, and awaited the hour fixed for my departure—quiet outwardly, but inwardly I was in an agony of suspense lest Arowhena’s absence should be discovered before the arrival of the King and Queen, who were to witness my ascent. They were not due yet for another two hours, and during this time a hundred things might happen, any one of which would undo me.
我安静地坐着，等待着出发的时间——表面上很安静，但内心却充满了悬念，唯恐在国王和王后到来之前发现阿罗维娜不在，他们将见证我的升天。还有两个小时他们就到期了，在这段时间里可能会发生一百件事，其中任何一件都会让我崩溃。

At last the balloon was full; the pipe which had filled it was removed, the escape of the gas having been first carefully precluded. Nothing remained to hinder the balloon from ascending but the hands and weight of those who were holding on to it with ropes. I strained my eyes for the coming of the King and Queen, but could see no sign of their approach. I looked in the direction of Mr. Nosnibor’s house—there was nothing to indicate disturbance, but it was not yet breakfast time. The crowd began to gather; they were aware that I was under the displeasure of the court, but I could detect no signs of my being unpopular. On the contrary, I received many kindly expressions of regard and encouragement, with good wishes as to the result of my journey.
气球终于满了。填充它的管道被移开，首先小心地阻止了气体的逸出。除了那些用绳子抓住气球的人的手和重量之外，没有什么能阻止气球上升。我睁大眼睛等待国王和王后的到来，但没有看到他们靠近的迹象。我朝诺斯尼伯先生家的方向看去——没有任何迹象表明有骚乱，但现在还不到早餐时间。人群开始聚集。他们知道我受到法庭的不满，但我看不出我不受欢迎的迹象。相反，我收到了许多善意的关心和鼓励，并对我的旅程的结果表示良好的祝愿。

I was speaking to one gentleman of my acquaintance, and telling him the substance of what I intended to do when I had got into the presence of the air god (what he thought of me I cannot guess, for I am sure that he did not believe in the objective existence of the air god, nor that I myself believed in it), when I became aware of a small crowd of people running as fast as they could from Mr. Nosnibor’s house towards the Queen’s workshops. For the moment my pulse ceased beating, and then, knowing that the time had come when I must either do or die, I called vehemently to those who were holding the ropes (some thirty men) to let go at once, and made gestures signifying danger, and that there would be mischief if they held on longer. Many obeyed; the rest were too weak to hold on to the ropes, and were forced to let them go. On this the balloon bounded suddenly upwards, but my own feeling was that the earth had dropped off from me, and was sinking fast into the open space beneath.
我正在和一位熟人交谈，告诉他当我来到空气之神面前时我打算做什么（我无法猜测他对我的看法，因为我确信他没有当我意识到一小群人以最快的速度从诺斯尼伯先生的房子向女王的工作室跑去时，我相信空气神的客观存在，我自己也不相信。就在我的脉搏停止跳动的那一刻，我知道我要么做，要么死，我猛烈地叫那些拉着绳子的人（大约三十个人）立即放开，并做出了手势。危险，如果他们坚持得更久，就会有恶果。许多人服从了；其余的人都太虚弱了，抓不住绳子，只好松开绳子。气球突然向上弹起，但我自己的感觉是地球已经从我身边掉下来，并且正在快速下沉到下面的空地中。

This happened at the very moment that the attention of the crowd was divided, the one half paying heed to the eager gestures of those coming from Mr. Nosnibor’s house, and the other to the exclamations from myself. A minute more and Arowhena would doubtless have been discovered, but before that minute was over, I was at such a height above the city that nothing could harm me, and every second both the town and the crowd became smaller and more confused. In an incredibly short time, I could see little but a vast wall of blue plains rising up against me, towards whichever side I looked.
这件事发生的时候，人群的注意力已经被分散了，一半人注意着从诺斯尼博尔先生家里传来的热切的手势，另一半人则注意着我自己的惊呼。再过一分钟，阿罗维纳无疑就会被发现，但在那一分钟结束之前，我已经处于城市上方的高度，没有任何东西可以伤害我，每一秒，城镇和人群都变得更小，更混乱。在非常短的时间内，无论我朝哪一边看，我都只能看到一堵巨大的蓝色平原墙在我面前升起。

At first, the balloon mounted vertically upwards, but after about five minutes, when we had already attained a very great elevation, I fancied that the objects on the plain beneath began to move from under me. I did not feel so much as a breath of wind, and could not suppose that the balloon itself was travelling. I was, therefore, wondering what this strange movement of fixed objects could mean, when it struck me that people in a balloon do not feel the wind inasmuch as they travel with it and offer it no resistance. Then I was happy in thinking that I must now have reached the invariable trade wind of the upper air, and that I should be very possibly wafted for hundreds or even thousands of miles, far from Erewhon and the Erewhonians.
起初，气球垂直向上升起，但大约五分钟后，当我们已经达到一个非常高的高度时，我觉得下面平原上的物体开始从我下面移动。我连一丝风的感觉都没有，也无法想象气球本身正在飞行。因此，我想知道固定物体的这种奇怪运动可能意味着什么，当我突然意识到，气球里的人感觉不到风，因为他们随风飞行，并且没有给风带来任何阻力。然后我很高兴地想到，我现在一定已经到达了高空不变的信风，而且我很可能会被吹到数百甚至数千英里之外，远离埃雷洪和埃雷洪人。

Already I had removed the wrappings and freed Arowhena; but I soon covered her up with them again, for it was already very cold, and she was half stupefied with the strangeness of her position.
我已经拆掉了包裹并释放了阿罗菲娜。但我很快又给她盖上，因为天气已经很冷了，她因为自己位置的奇怪而惊呆了。

And now began a time, dream-like and delirious, of which I do not suppose that I shall ever recover a distinct recollection. Some things I can recall—as that we were ere long enveloped in vapour which froze upon my moustache and whiskers; then comes a memory of sitting for hours and hours in a thick fog, hearing no sound but my own breathing and Arowhena’s (for we hardly spoke) and seeing no sight but the car beneath us and beside us, and the dark balloon above.
现在开始了一段如梦似幻、神志不清的时光，我想我永远不会恢复清晰的记忆。有些事情我还记得——比如我们不久就被蒸汽包围了，这些蒸汽冻结在我的小胡子和胡须上；然后是我在浓雾中坐了几个小时的记忆，除了我自己和阿罗维纳的呼吸（因为我们几乎不说话）之外听不到任何声音，除了我们下面和旁边的汽车以及上面的黑色气球之外，什么也看不见。

Perhaps the most painful feeling when the earth was hidden was that the balloon was motionless, though our only hope lay in our going forward with an extreme of speed. From time to time through a rift in the clouds I caught a glimpse of earth, and was thankful to perceive that we must be flying forward faster than in an express train; but no sooner was the rift closed than the old conviction of our being stationary returned in full force, and was not to be reasoned with: there was another feeling also which was nearly as bad; for as a child that fears it has gone blind in a long tunnel if there is no light, so ere the earth had been many minutes hidden, I became half frightened lest we might not have broken away from it clean and for ever. Now and again, I ate and gave food to Arowhena, but by guess-work as regards time. Then came darkness, a dreadful dreary time, without even the moon to cheer us.
也许当地球被隐藏时最痛苦的感觉就是气球一动不动，尽管我们唯一的希望就是以极快的速度前进。我时不时地透过云层的裂缝瞥见地球，并庆幸地意识到我们一定比乘坐特快列车更快地向前飞行；但裂痕一闭合，我们静止不动的旧信念就全力回归，这是不合理的：还有另一种感觉，几乎同样糟糕；因为当我还是个孩子的时候，我担心如果没有光，我会在一条长长的隧道里失明，所以在地球被隐藏了很多分钟之前，我变得有些害怕，生怕我们可能无法彻底地、永远地脱离它。我时不时地给阿罗时娜吃东西，但只是猜测时间。然后黑暗降临了，那是一段可怕而沉闷的时光，甚至连月亮都没有给我们带来欢乐。

With dawn the scene was changed: the clouds were gone and morning stars were shining; the rising of the splendid sun remains still impressed upon me as the most glorious that I have ever seen; beneath us there was an embossed chain of mountains with snow fresh fallen upon them; but we were far above them; we both of us felt our breathing seriously affected, but I would not allow the balloon to descend a single inch, not knowing for how long we might not need all the buoyancy which we could command; indeed I was thankful to find that, after nearly four-and-twenty hours, we were still at so great a height above the earth.
黎明时分，景色发生了变化：乌云散去，晨星闪耀；灿烂的太阳的升起仍然给我留下了深刻的印象，这是我所见过的最辉煌的太阳。我们脚下是一连串的山脉，上面刚落过雪。但我们远远高于他们；我们俩都感到呼吸受到严重影响，但我不允许气球下降一英寸，不知道我们可能需要多长时间不需要我们可以控制的所有浮力；事实上，我很庆幸地发现，在将近四个小时和二十个小时之后，我们仍然处于距地球如此高的高度。

In a couple of hours we had passed the ranges, which must have been some hundred and fifty miles across, and again I saw a tract of level plain extending far away to the horizon. I knew not where we were, and dared not descend, lest I should waste the power of the balloon, but I was half hopeful that we might be above the country from which I had originally started. I looked anxiously for any sign by which I could recognise it, but could see nothing, and feared that we might be above some distant part of Erewhon, or a country inhabited by savages. While I was still in doubt, the balloon was again wrapped in clouds, and we were left to blank space and to conjectures.
几个小时后，我们就穿过了山脉，山脉肯定有一百五十英里宽，我再次看到了一大片平坦的平原，一直延伸到地平线。我不知道我们在哪里，也不敢下降，以免浪费气球的力量，但我对我们可能在我最初出发的国家上方抱有一半的希望。我焦急地寻找任何可以认出它的迹象，但什么也看不见，我担心我们可能在埃雷洪的某个遥远的地方，或者是一个野蛮人居住的国家之上。当我还在犹豫的时候，气球又被云层包裹住了，我们只剩下一片空白和猜测。

The weary time dragged on. How I longed for my unhappy watch! I felt as though not even time was moving, so dumb and spell-bound were our surroundings. Sometimes I would feel my pulse, and count its beats for half-an-hour together; anything to mark the time—to prove that it was there, and to assure myself that we were within the blessed range of its influence, and not gone adrift into the timelessness of eternity.
疲惫的时间一拖再拖。我多么渴望看到那只不快乐的手表啊！我觉得时间仿佛都没有流动，我们的周围是如此的愚蠢和令人着迷。有时我会摸脉搏，一起数半个小时；任何可以标记时间的事情——证明它就在那里，并向自己保证我们处于它的影响范围之内，而不是漂流到永恒的永恒之中。

I had been doing this for the twentieth or thirtieth time, and had fallen into a light sleep: I dreamed wildly of a journey in an express train, and of arriving at a railway station where the air was full of the sound of locomotive engines blowing off steam with a horrible and tremendous hissing; I woke frightened and uneasy, but the hissing and crashing noises pursued me now that I was awake, and forced me to own that they were real. What they were I knew not, but they grew gradually fainter and fainter, and after a time were lost. In a few hours the clouds broke, and I saw beneath me that which made the chilled blood run colder in my veins. I saw the sea, and nothing but the sea; in the main black, but flecked with white heads of storm-tossed, angry waves.
我已经这样做了第二十次或第三十次了，进入了浅睡：我疯狂地梦想着乘坐特快列车旅行，到达火车站，空气中充满了机车引擎的轰鸣声。失去动力，发出可怕而巨大的嘶嘶声；我醒来时感到害怕和不安，但嘶嘶声和撞击声在我醒来后追着我，迫使我承认它们是真实的。我不知道它们是什么，但它们逐渐变得越来越淡，过了一段时间就消失了。几个小时后，云层散去，我看到了脚下的东西，这让我血管里冰冷的血液变得更加寒冷。我看到了大海，除了大海什么也没有；主体是黑色的，但点缀着暴风雨翻腾的愤怒波浪的白色头部。

Arowhena was sleeping quietly at the bottom of the car, and as I looked at her sweet and saintly beauty, I groaned, and cursed myself for the misery into which I had brought her; but there was nothing for it now.
阿罗芙娜正在车底安静地睡着，当我看着她甜美而圣洁的美丽时，我呻吟着，咒骂自己让她陷入了痛苦之中；但现在已经没有办法了。

I sat and waited for the worst, and presently I saw signs as though that worst were soon to be at hand, for the balloon had begun to sink. On first seeing the sea I had been impressed with the idea that we must have been falling, but now there could be no mistake, we were sinking, and that fast. I threw out a bag of ballast, and for a time we rose again, but in the course of a few hours the sinking recommenced, and I threw out another bag.
我坐下来等待最坏的情况发生，不久我就看到了迹象，似乎最坏的情况即将到来，因为气球已经开始下沉。第一次看到大海时，我印象深刻，我们一定是在下落，但现在毫无疑问，我们正在下沉，而且速度那么快。我扔掉了一袋压舱物，有一段时间我们又上升了，但几个小时后又开始下沉，我扔掉了另一袋。

Then the battle commenced in earnest. It lasted all that afternoon and through the night until the following evening. I had seen never a sail nor a sign of a sail, though I had half blinded myself with straining my eyes incessantly in every direction; we had parted with everything but the clothes which we had upon our backs; food and water were gone, all thrown out to the wheeling albatrosses, in order to save us a few hours or even minutes from the sea. I did not throw away the books till we were within a few feet of the water, and clung to my manuscripts to the very last. Hope there seemed none whatever—yet, strangely enough we were neither of us utterly hopeless, and even when the evil that we dreaded was upon us, and that which we greatly feared had come, we sat in the car of the balloon with the waters up to our middle, and still smiled with a ghastly hopefulness to one another.
然后战斗就正式开始了。它持续了整个下午和整个晚上，直到第二天晚上。我从来没有见过帆，也没有见过帆的迹象，尽管我不断地向各个方向看去，眼睛已经半瞎了。除了背上的衣服，我们什么都舍弃了。食物和水都没有了，全都被扔给了旋转的信天翁，以便我们能在离开大海的时候节省几个小时甚至几分钟的时间。直到我们离水只有几英尺的时候，我才把书扔掉，直到最后一刻我都紧紧抓住我的手稿。似乎没有任何希望——然而，奇怪的是，我们俩都没有完全绝望，即使我们害怕的邪恶降临到我们身上，我们非常害怕的事情已经到来，我们还是坐在气球的车厢里，水里有水。直到我们中间，仍然彼此微笑，带着可怕的希望。

* * *

He who has crossed the St. Gothard will remember that below Andermatt there is one of those Alpine gorges which reach the very utmost limits of the sublime and terrible. The feelings of the traveller have become more and more highly wrought at every step, until at last the naked and overhanging precipices seem to close above his head, as he crosses a bridge hung in mid-air over a roaring waterfall, and enters on the darkness of a tunnel, hewn out of the rock.
穿越过圣哥特哈德河的人都会记得，在安德马特下面有一个阿尔卑斯峡谷，它达到了崇高和可怕的极限。旅行者的感情每走一步都变得越来越强烈，直到最后，当他跨过一座悬在半空中的桥，悬在咆哮的瀑布上时，裸露的、悬垂的悬崖似乎在他的头顶上闭合了。从岩石中凿出的黑暗隧道。

What can be in store for him on emerging? Surely something even wilder and more desolate than that which he has seen already; yet his imagination is paralysed, and can suggest no fancy or vision of anything to surpass the reality which he had just witnessed. Awed and breathless he advances; when lo! the light of the afternoon sun welcomes him as he leaves the tunnel, and behold a smiling valley— a babbling brook, a village with tall belfries, and meadows of brilliant green—these are the things which greet him, and he smiles to himself as the terror passes away and in another moment is forgotten.
崭露头角后他会面临什么？肯定有比他已​​经看到的更荒凉、更荒凉的东西。然而他的想象力却是瘫痪的，无法提出任何超越他刚刚目睹的现实的幻想或愿景。他满怀敬畏，气喘吁吁地向前走；当瞧！当他离开隧道时，午后的阳光迎接着他，看到一个微笑的山谷——一条潺潺的小溪，一个有着高高钟楼的村庄，还有翠绿的草地——这些都是迎接他的东西，他对自己微笑恐惧消失了，转眼间就被遗忘了。

So fared it now with ourselves. We had been in the water some two or three hours, and the night had come upon us. We had said farewell for the hundredth time, and had resigned ourselves to meet the end; indeed I was myself battling with a drowsiness from which it was only too probable that I should never wake; when suddenly, Arowhena touched me on the shoulder, and pointed to a light and to a dark mass which was bearing right upon us. A cry for help—loud and clear and shrill—broke forth from both of us at once; and in another five minutes we were carried by kind and tender hands on to the deck of an Italian vessel.
我们自己现在就这样了。我们在水里待了大约两三个小时，夜幕降临了。我们已经第一百次告别了，已经听天由命地迎接最后的结局了。事实上，我自己也在与困倦作斗争，很可能我永远都醒不过来。突然，阿罗维娜拍了拍我的肩膀，指着我们面前的一团光和一团黑团。我们俩同时发出一声响亮、清晰、尖锐的求救声。又过了五分钟，我们被友善而温柔的双手带到了一艘意大利船只的甲板上。

CHAPTER XXIX: CONCLUSION
第二十九章：结论

The ship was the Principe Umberto, bound from Callao to Genoa; she had carried a number of emigrants to Rio, had gone thence to Callao, where she had taken in a cargo of guano, and was now on her way home. The captain was a certain Giovanni Gianni, a native of Sestri; he has kindly allowed me to refer to him in case the truth of my story should be disputed; but I grieve to say that I suffered him to mislead himself in some important particulars. I should add that when we were picked up we were a thousand miles from land.
这艘船是“Principe Umberto”号，从卡亚俄开往热那亚。她载着一些移民到里约热内卢，从那里前往卡亚俄，在那里装了一批鸟粪，现在正在回家的路上。船长是乔瓦尼·贾尼（Giovanni Gianni），塞斯特里人。他好心地允许我向他求助，以防我的故事的真实性受到争议。但我很遗憾地说，我让他在一些重要的细节上误导了自己。我应该补充一点，当我们被接走时，我们距离陆地有一千英里。

As soon as we were on board, the captain began questioning us about the siege of Paris, from which city he had assumed that we must have come, notwithstanding our immense distance from Europe. As may be supposed, I had not heard a syllable about the war between France and Germany, and was too ill to do more than assent to all that he chose to put into my mouth. My knowledge of Italian is very imperfect, and I gathered little from anything that he said; but I was glad to conceal the true point of our departure, and resolved to take any cue that he chose to give me.
我们一上船，船长就开始向我们询问巴黎被围困的情况，他认为我们一定是从巴黎来的，尽管我们距离欧洲很远。可以想象，我没有听到关于法国和德国之间战争的任何一个音节，而且病得太重，只能同意他选择放入我嘴里的所有内容。我对意大利语的了解很不全面，我从他所说的任何事情中都听不到什么。但我很高兴隐瞒了我们出发的真正目的，并决定接受他选择给我的任何暗示。

The line that thus suggested itself was that there had been ten or twelve others in the balloon, that I was an English Milord, and Arowhena a Russian Countess; that all the others had been drowned, and that the despatches which we had carried were lost. I came afterwards to learn that this story would not have been credible, had not the captain been for some weeks at sea, for I found that when we were picked up, the Germans had already long been masters of Paris. As it was, the captain settled the whole story for me, and I was well content.
由此暗示的台词是，气球里还有十到十二个人，我是一位英国贵族，阿罗维娜是一位俄罗斯伯爵夫人；其他人都被淹死了，我们携带的信件也丢失了。后来我才知道，如果船长不是在海上呆了几个星期，这个故事就不可信，因为我发现当我们被接上来时，德国人早已成为巴黎的主人了。事实如此，船长给我解决了整个事情，我也很满足了。

In a few days we sighted an English vessel bound from Melbourne to London with wool. At my earnest request, in spite of stormy weather which rendered it dangerous for a boat to take us from one ship to the other, the captain consented to signal the English vessel, and we were received on board, but we were transferred with such difficulty that no communication took place as to the manner of our being found. I did indeed hear the Italian mate who was in charge of the boat shout out something in French to the effect that we had been picked up from a balloon, but the noise of the wind was so great, and the captain understood so little French that he caught nothing of the truth, and it was assumed that we were two persons who had been saved from shipwreck. When the captain asked me in what ship I had been wrecked, I said that a party of us had been carried out to sea in a pleasure-boat by a strong current, and that Arowhena (whom I described as a Peruvian lady) and I were alone saved.
几天后，我们看到一艘英国船只从墨尔本开往伦敦，满载羊毛。在我的恳切请求下，尽管暴风雨天气使船只将我们从一艘船带到另一艘船变得危险，但船长同意向英国船发出信号，我们被接上船，但我们转移得很困难没有就我们被发现的方式进行任何沟通。我确实听到负责这艘船的意大利大副用法语大喊了一句，大意是我们是从气球上接起来的，但是风的噪音太大了，船长不懂法语，他没有了解到真相，并认为我们是从海难中获救的两个人。当船长问我在哪艘船上失事时，我说我们一行人乘坐一艘游船被强劲的水流冲到了海上，而阿罗菲娜（我将她描述为一位秘鲁女士）和我独自得救。

There were several passengers, whose goodness towards us we can never repay. I grieve to think that they cannot fail to discover that we did not take them fully into our confidence; but had we told them all, they would not have believed us, and I was determined that no one should hear of Erewhon, or have the chance of getting there before me, as long as I could prevent it. Indeed, the recollection of the many falsehoods which I was then obliged to tell, would render my life miserable were I not sustained by the consolations of my religion. Among the passengers there was a most estimable clergyman, by whom Arowhena and I were married within a very few days of our coming on board.
有几个乘客对我们的恩情我们永远无法报答。我悲伤地想到，他们一定会发现我们并没有完全信任他们。但如果我们把一切都告诉他们，他们就不会相信我们，而且我下定决心，只要我能阻止，就不应该让任何人听说埃里洪，或者有机会在我之前到达那里。事实上，如果我没有得到宗教的安慰，回想起当时我不得不说出的许多谎言，我的生活将会变得悲惨。乘客中有一位最值得尊敬的牧师，我和阿罗维娜上船后没几天就在他的主持下结婚了。

After a prosperous voyage of about two months, we sighted the Land’s End, and in another week we were landed at London. A liberal subscription was made for us on board the ship, so that we found ourselves in no immediate difficulty about money. I accordingly took Arowhena down into Somersetshire, where my mother and sisters had resided when I last heard of them. To my great sorrow I found that my mother was dead, and that her death had been accelerated by the report of my having been killed, which had been brought to my employer’s station by Chowbok. It appeared that he must have waited for a few days to see whether I returned, that he then considered it safe to assume that I should never do so, and had accordingly made up a story about my having fallen into a whirlpool of seething waters while coming down the gorge homeward. Search was made for my body, but the rascal had chosen to drown me in a place where there would be no chance of its ever being recovered.
经过大约两个月的顺利航行，我们看到了天涯海角，又一周后，我们在伦敦登陆。船上为我们提供了慷慨的捐款，因此我们发现自己在金钱方面没有立即遇到困难。于是，我带着阿罗维娜去了萨默塞特郡，当我最后一次听说我的母亲和姐妹时，她们就住在那里。令我非常悲痛的是，我发现我的母亲已经死了，而且乔博克把我被杀的消息带到我雇主的驻地，加速了她的死亡。看来他一定等了几天，看我是否回来，然后他认为我永远不应该回来，因此编造了一个关于我在沸腾的水漩涡中的故事。沿着峡谷回家。人们搜寻了我的尸体，但这个流氓却选择把我淹死在一个永远不可能被找到的地方。

My sisters were both married, but neither of their husbands was rich. No one seemed overjoyed on my return; and I soon discovered that when a man’s relations have once mourned for him as dead, they seldom like the prospect of having to mourn for him a second time.
我的姐妹们都已结婚，但她们的丈夫都不富有。似乎没有人对我的回归感到欣喜若狂。我很快发现，当一个人的亲人为他的死者哀悼一次后，他们就很少愿意为他第二次哀悼。

Accordingly I returned to London with my wife, and through the assistance of an old friend supported myself by writing good little stories for the magazines, and for a tract society. I was well paid; and I trust that I may not be considered presumptuous in saying that some of the most popular of the brochures which are distributed in the streets, and which are to be found in the waiting-rooms of the railway stations, have proceeded from my pen. During the time that I could spare, I arranged my notes and diary till they assumed their present shape. There remains nothing for me to add, save to unfold the scheme which I propose for the conversion of Erewhon.
因此，我和妻子回到了伦敦，在一位老朋友的帮助下，通过为杂志和小册子写一些好的小故事来养活自己。我的薪水很高；我相信，如果我说一些在街道上分发的、在火车站候车室里可以找到的最受欢迎的小册子是出自我的笔下，这不会被认为是自以为是。在空闲的时间里，我整理笔记和日记，直到它们呈现出现在的形状。除了展开我为改造埃里洪而提出的计划外，我没有什么可补充的了。

That scheme has only been quite recently decided upon as the one which seems most likely to be successful.
该计划直到最近才被确定为最有可能成功的计划。

It will be seen at once that it would be madness for me to go with ten or a dozen subordinate missionaries by the same way as that which led me to discover Erewhon. I should be imprisoned for typhus, besides being handed over to the straighteners for having run away with Arowhena: an even darker fate, to which I dare hardly again allude, would be reserved for my devoted fellow- labourers. It is plain, therefore, that some other way must be found for getting at the Erewhonians, and I am thankful to say that such another way is not wanting. One of the rivers which descends from the Snowy Mountains, and passes through Erewhon, is known to be navigable for several hundred miles from its mouth. Its upper waters have never yet been explored, but I feel little doubt that it will be found possible to take a light gunboat (for we must protect ourselves) to the outskirts of the Erewhonian country.
很快我们就会发现，如果我带着十个或十几名下级传教士走上发现埃瑞翁的同样道路，那简直就是疯狂。我应该因斑疹伤寒入狱，除了因与阿罗维娜私奔而被移交给矫正者之外：我几乎不敢再次提及的更黑暗的命运将留给我忠诚的工友。因此，很明显，必须找到其他方法来攻击埃雷洪尼亚人，而且我很庆幸地说，这种其他方法并不需要。其中一条河流发源于雪山，流经埃雷洪，距河口数百英里可通航。它的上游水域尚未被探索过，但我毫不怀疑，有可能乘坐轻型炮艇（因为我们必须保护自己）前往埃雷洪尼亚国家的郊区。

I propose, therefore, that one of those associations should be formed in which the risk of each of the members is confined to the amount of his stake in the concern. The first step would be to draw up a prospectus. In this I would advise that no mention should be made of the fact that the Erewhonians are the lost tribes. The discovery is one of absorbing interest to myself, but it is of a sentimental rather than commercial value, and business is business. The capital to be raised should not be less than fifty thousand pounds, and might be either in five or ten pound shares as hereafter determined. This should be amply sufficient for the expenses of an experimental voyage.
因此，我建议成立这样一个协会，其中每个成员的风险仅限于其在该公司的股份数额。第一步是起草招股说明书。在此，我建议不要提及埃雷洪尼亚人是失落部落这一事实。这一发现对我来说很有趣，但它具有情感价值而不是商业价值，而且生意就是生意。筹集的资金不应少于五万英镑，并且可以是五英镑或十英镑的股份，具体情况将在下文确定。这对于一次实验航行的费用来说应该是足够的了。

When the money had been subscribed, it would be our duty to charter a steamer of some twelve or fourteen hundred tons burden, and with accommodation for a cargo of steerage passengers. She should carry two or three guns in case of her being attacked by savages at the mouth of the river. Boats of considerable size should be also provided, and I think it would be desirable that these also should carry two or three six-pounders. The ship should be taken up the river as far as was considered safe, and a picked party should then ascend in the boats. The presence both of Arowhena and myself would be necessary at this stage, inasmuch as our knowledge of the language would disarm suspicion, and facilitate negotiations.
当这笔钱被认购后，我们的责任就是租一艘大约十二或一千四百吨的轮船，并为全舱乘客提供住宿。她应该携带两三把枪，以防在河口遭到野人的袭击。还应该提供相当大的船只，我认为这些船只也应该携带两到三艘六磅炮是可取的。在认为安全的情况下，应将船带到河上，然后由选定的人员乘船上升。在这个阶段，阿罗维纳和我本人都必须在场，因为我们的语言知识可以消除怀疑并促进谈判。

We should begin by representing the advantages afforded to labour in the colony of Queensland, and point out to the Erewhonians that by emigrating thither, they would be able to amass, each and all of them, enormous fortunes—a fact which would be easily provable by a reference to statistics. I have no doubt that a very great number might be thus induced to come back with us in the larger boats, and that we could fill our vessel with emigrants in three or four journeys.
我们应该首先阐述昆士兰殖民地为劳工提供的优势，并向埃雷洪人指出，通过移民到那里，他们每个人都能够积累巨额财富——这一事实很容易证明通过参考统计数据。我毫不怀疑，可能会吸引很多人乘坐更大的船只与我们一起返回，并且我们可以在三到四趟旅程中将移民装满我们的船只。

Should we be attacked, our course would be even simpler, for the Erewhonians have no gunpowder, and would be so surprised with its effects that we should be able to capture as many as we chose; in this case we should feel able to engage them on more advantageous terms, for they would be prisoners of war. But even though we were to meet with no violence, I doubt not that a cargo of seven or eight hundred Erewhonians could be induced, when they were once on board the vessel, to sign an agreement which should be mutually advantageous both to us and them.
如果我们受到攻击，我们的路线会更简单，因为埃雷洪尼亚人没有火药，而且会对其效果感到惊讶，我们应该能够捕获我们选择的尽可能多的人；在这种情况下，我们应该感到能够以更有利的条件与他们交战，因为他们将成为战俘。但即使我们没有发生暴力冲突，我也不怀疑七八百名埃雷洪人一旦登上船只，就能被诱使签署一项对我们和他们双方都有利的协议。 。

We should then proceed to Queensland, and dispose of our engagement with the Erewhonians to the sugar-growers of that settlement, who are in great want of labour; it is believed that the money thus realised would enable us to declare a handsome dividend, and leave a considerable balance, which might be spent in repeating our operations and bringing over other cargoes of Erewhonians, with fresh consequent profits. In fact we could go backwards and forwards as long as there was a demand for labour in Queensland, or indeed in any other Christian colony, for the supply of Erewhonians would be unlimited, and they could be packed closely and fed at a very reasonable cost.
然后我们应该前往昆士兰，把我们与埃雷洪尼亚人的接触交给该定居点的糖种植者，因为他们非常需要劳动力；据信，由此实现的资金将使我们能够宣布可观的股息，并留下可观的余额，这些余额可用于重复我们的业务并运送埃鲁洪人的其他货物，从而带来新的利润。事实上，只要昆士兰，或者任何其他基督教殖民地有劳动力需求，我们就可以来回走动，因为埃雷洪尼亚人的供应是无限的，他们可以紧密地包装在一起，并以非常合理的成本喂养。 。

It would be my duty and Arowhena’s to see that our emigrants should be boarded and lodged in the households of religious sugar-growers; these persons would give them the benefit of that instruction whereof they stand so greatly in need. Each day, as soon as they could be spared from their work in the plantations, they would be assembled for praise, and be thoroughly grounded in the Church Catechism, while the whole of every Sabbath should be devoted to singing psalms and church-going.
我和阿罗维纳的职责是确保我们的移民能够在宗教糖农的家庭中得到寄宿。这些人将使他们受益于他们非常需要的指导。每天，只要他们能从种植园的工作中解脱出来，他们就会聚集在一起接受赞美，并彻底扎根于教会教义问答，而每个安息日的整个时间都应该用来唱诗篇和去教堂。

This must be insisted upon, both in order to put a stop to any uneasy feeling which might show itself either in Queensland or in the mother country as to the means whereby the Erewhonians had been obtained, and also because it would give our own shareholders the comfort of reflecting that they were saving souls and filling their own pockets at one and the same moment. By the time the emigrants had got too old for work they would have become thoroughly instructed in religion; they could then be shipped back to Erewhon and carry the good seed with them.
必须坚持这一点，既是为了制止昆士兰州或母国可能对获得埃雷洪尼亚人的方式表现出的任何不安情绪，也是因为这将使我们自己的股东想到他们在拯救灵魂的同时又充实了自己的口袋，这让他们感到很安慰。当移民到了不能工作的年龄时，他们就会接受彻底的宗教教育。然后，他们可以被运回埃里洪并随身携带好种子。

I can see no hitch nor difficulty about the matter, and trust that this book will sufficiently advertise the scheme to insure the subscription of the necessary capital; as soon as this is forthcoming I will guarantee that I convert the Erewhonians not only into good Christians but into a source of considerable profit to the shareholders.
我认为这件事没有任何障碍或困难，并相信这本书将充分宣传该计划，以确保认购必要的资本；一旦这一切到来，我将保证我不仅将埃雷洪人转变为优秀的基督徒，而且将其转变为股东可观利润的来源。

I should add that I cannot claim the credit for having originated the above scheme. I had been for months at my wit’s end, forming plan after plan for the evangelisation of Erewhon, when by one of those special interpositions which should be a sufficient answer to the sceptic, and make even the most confirmed rationalist irrational, my eye was directed to the following paragraph in the Times newspaper, of one of the first days in January 1872:-
我应该补充一点，我不能声称自己发起了上述计划。几个月来，我一直束手无策，为埃里翁传福音制定了一个又一个的计划，当通过其中一个特殊的干预措施时，我的眼睛被引导了，这些干预措施应该足以回答怀疑论者，甚至使最坚定的理性主义者变得非理性。 《泰晤士报》中 1872 年 1 月头一天的以下一段话：

‘POLYNESIANS IN QUEENSLAND.—The Marquis of Normanby, the new Governor of Queensland, has completed his inspection of the northern districts of the colony. It is stated that at Mackay, one of the best sugar-growing districts, his Excellency saw a good deal of the Polynesians. In the course of a speech to those who entertained him there, the Marquis said:- ‘I have been told that the means by which Polynesians were obtained were not legitimate, but I have failed to perceive this, in so far at least as Queensland is concerned; and, if one can judge by the countenances and manners of the Polynesians, they experience no regret at their position.’ But his Excellency pointed out the advantage of giving them religious instruction. It would tend to set at rest an uneasy feeling which at present existed in the country to know that they were inclined to retain the Polynesians, and teach them religion.’
昆士兰州的波利尼西亚人——昆士兰州新任总督诺曼比侯爵已完成对殖民地北部地区的视察。据说，在最好的糖产区之一麦凯，阁下见到了很多波利尼西亚人。侯爵在向在那里招待他的人发表讲话时说：“有人告诉我，获得波利尼西亚人的方式是不合法的，但我没有意识到这一点，至少在昆士兰州是如此。”被关注到; “如果人们能从波利尼西亚人的面容和举止来判断，他们不会对自己的处境感到遗憾。”但阁下指出了给予他们宗教教育的好处。如果知道他们倾向于保留波利尼西亚人并教导他们宗教，这往往会平息该国目前存在的一种不安情绪。

I feel that comment is unnecessary, and will therefore conclude with one word of thanks to the reader who may have had the patience to follow me through my adventures without losing his temper; but with two, for any who may write at once to the Secretary of the Erewhon Evangelisation Company, limited (at the address which shall hereafter be advertised), and request to have his name put down as a shareholder.
我觉得评论是不必要的，因此我想对读者说一声感谢，感谢他们耐心地跟随我经历了我的冒险而不发脾气；但有两个，任何人可以立即写信给 Erewhon Evangelization Company, Limited 的秘书（地址将在下文中公布），并要求将其姓名写为股东。

P.S.—I had just received and corrected the last proof of the foregoing volume, and was walking down the Strand from Temple Bar to Charing Cross, when on passing Exeter Hall I saw a number of devout-looking people crowding into the building with faces full of interested and complacent anticipation. I stopped, and saw an announcement that a missionary meeting was to be held forthwith, and that the native missionary, the Rev. William Habakkuk, from— (the colony from which I had started on my adventures), would be introduced, and make a short address. After some little difficulty I obtained admission, and heard two or three speeches, which were prefatory to the introduction of Mr. Habakkuk. One of these struck me as perhaps the most presumptuous that I had ever heard. The speaker said that the races of whom Mr. Habakkuk was a specimen, were in all probability the lost ten tribes of Israel. I dared not contradict him then, but I felt angry and injured at hearing the speaker jump to so preposterous a conclusion upon such insufficient grounds. The discovery of the ten tribes was mine, and mine only. I was still in the very height of indignation, when there was a murmur of expectation in the hall, and Mr. Habakkuk was brought forward. The reader may judge of my surprise at finding that he was none other than my old friend Chowbok!
P.S.——我刚刚收到并改正了上一卷的最后一份校样，正沿着斯特​​兰德街从圣殿酒吧步行到查令十字街，经过埃克塞特大厅时，我看到许多虔诚的人们满脸满脸地涌进大楼。充满兴趣和自满的期待。我停下来，看到一个布告，即将召开传教士会议，来自——（我开始冒险的殖民地）的本土传教士威廉·哈巴谷牧师将被介绍，并让一个简短的地址。经过一些小困难后，我获得了入场许可，并听到了两三场演讲，这些演讲是介绍哈巴谷先生的序言。其中之一让我觉得也许是我听过的最自以为是的。演讲者说，以哈巴谷先生为样本的种族很可能就是以色列失落的十个支派。当时我不敢反驳他，但听到演讲者在如此不充分的理由下得出如此荒谬的结论，我感到愤怒和受伤。十个部落的发现是我的，也只是我的。正当我义愤填膺时，大厅里响起一片期待的低语声，哈巴谷先生被带上前来。读者可能会判断我对发现他正是我的老朋友乔博克的惊讶！

My jaw dropped, and my eyes almost started out of my head with astonishment. The poor fellow was dreadfully frightened, and the storm of applause which greeted his introduction seemed only to add to his confusion. I dare not trust myself to report his speech— indeed I could hardly listen to it, for I was nearly choked with trying to suppress my feelings. I am sure that I caught the words ‘Adelaide, the Queen Dowager,’ and I thought that I heard ‘Mary Magdalene’ shortly afterwards, but I had then to leave the hall for fear of being turned out. While on the staircase, I heard another burst of prolonged and rapturous applause, so I suppose the audience were satisfied.
我惊得下巴都掉下来了，眼睛都快要瞪出来了。这个可怜的家伙被吓坏了，迎接他的介绍所引发的暴风雨般的掌声似乎只会让他更加困惑。我不敢相信自己去报道他的演讲——事实上，我几乎听不进去，因为我几乎因为压抑自己的感情而窒息。我确信我听到了“阿德莱德，太后”这个词，我以为不久之后我听到了“抹大拉的玛丽亚”，但我不得不离开大厅，因为担心被赶出去。在楼梯上，我又听到了一阵持久而热烈的掌声，所以我想观众们都很满意。

The feelings that came uppermost in my mind were hardly of a very solemn character, but I thought of my first acquaintance with Chowbok, of the scene in the woodshed, of the innumerable lies he had told me, of his repeated attempts upon the brandy, and of many an incident which I have not thought it worth while to dwell upon; and I could not but derive some satisfaction from the hope that my own efforts might have contributed to the change which had been doubtless wrought upon him, and that the rite which I had performed, however unprofessionally, on that wild upland river-bed, had not been wholly without effect. I trust that what I have written about him in the earlier part of my book may not be libellous, and that it may do him no harm with his employers. He was then unregenerate. I must certainly find him out and have a talk with him; but before I shall have time to do so these pages will be in the hands of the public.
我脑海中浮现出的最强烈的感觉并不是一种非常庄严的性格，但我想起了我第一次认识乔博克，想起了柴棚里的场景，想起了他对我说过的无数谎言，想起了他反复尝试喝白兰地，还有许多我认为不值得细想的事件；我不得不从希望中得到一些满足，希望我自己的努力可能有助于改变他身上无疑发生的变化，而且我在那个荒凉的高地河床上举行的仪式，无论多么不专业，已经并非完全没有影响。我相信我在书的前半部分所写的关于他的内容可能不是诽谤性的，而且这也不会对他的雇主造成伤害。那时他还没有重生。我一定要找到他，跟他谈谈；但在我有时间这样做之前，这些页面将交到公众手中。

At the last moment I see a probability of a complication which causes me much uneasiness. Please subscribe quickly. Address to the Mansion-House, care of the Lord Mayor, whom I will instruct to receive names and subscriptions for me until I can organise a committee.
在最后一刻，我看到了可能发生的并发症，这让我感到非常不安。请速速订阅。向官邸致辞，由市长大人负责，我将指示他为我接收姓名和捐款，直到我可以组织一个委员会。

脚注

{1} The last part of Chapter XXIII.
{1} 第二十三章的最后部分。

{2} See Handel’s compositions for the harpsichord, published by Litolf, p. 78.
{2}参见亨德尔的羽管键琴作品，由 Litolf 出版，第 14 页。 78.

{3} The myth above alluded to exists in Erewhon with changed names, and considerable modifications. I have taken the liberty of referring to the story as familiar to ourselves.
{3}上面提到的神话存在于 Erewhon，但名称已更改，并且进行了相当大的修改。我冒昧地提到了这个我们所熟悉的故事。

{4} What a SAFE word ‘relation’ is; how little it predicates! yet it has overgrown ‘kinsman.’
{4}“关系”是一个多么安全的词啊？它的谓词是多么少啊！但它已经过度生长“亲戚”。

{5} The root alluded to is not the potato of our own gardens, but a plant so near akin to it that I have ventured to translate it thus. Apropos of its intelligence, had the writer known Butler he would probably have said -
{5}所提到的根不是我们自己花园里的马铃薯，而是一种与它非常相似的植物，因此我冒昧地这样翻译它。就其情报而言，如果作者认识巴特勒，他可能会说——

“He knows what’s what, and that’s as high,
“他知道什么是什么，那就是高，

As metaphysic wit can fly.’
正如形而上学的智慧可以飞翔一样。

{6} Since my return to England, I have been told that those who are conversant about machines use many terms concerning them which show that their vitality is here recognised, and that a collection of expressions in use among those who attend on steam engines would be no less startling than instructive. I am also informed, that almost all machines have their own tricks and idiosyncrasies; that they know their drivers and keepers; and that they will play pranks upon a stranger. It is my intention, on a future occasion, to bring together examples both of the expressions in common use among mechanicians, and of any extraordinary exhibitions of mechanical sagacity and eccentricity that I can meet with—not as believing in the Erewhonian Professor’s theory, but from the interest of the subject.
{6}自从我回到英国后，有人告诉我，那些熟悉机器的人使用了许多与机器有关的术语，这表明它们的生命力在这里得到了认可，并且在那些关注蒸汽机的人中使用的一系列表达方式将既令人震惊，又具有启发性。我还了解到，几乎所有机器都有自己的技巧和特性；他们了解自己的司机和饲养员；他们会对陌生人恶作剧。我的目的是，在未来的某个场合，将机械师常用的表达方式以及我能遇到的任何机械智慧和怪异的非凡表现的例子汇集在一起​​——不是相信埃里洪尼亚教授的理论，而是从主题的兴趣出发。
